_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 3 / C — Basis-normalized canonical Wronskian theorem

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: build the basis-normalized Wronskian theorem, incorporating low-prime plateau rank while avoiding monomial Vandermonde losses. I am **not** attempting the final subset-product incidence theorem. 

---

# 1. Objective

We want a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank}+\text{stable basis conditioning}
\Longrightarrow
\text{existence of a normalized Wronskian minor with }Q^{-C}\text{ coefficient}.
}
\]

This addresses only the **coefficient/minor conditioning** part of the Wronskian route.

It does **not** prove:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That remains the separate arithmetic incidence theorem.

---

# 2. Normalized frequency nodes

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

For a main-side AFE frequency \(n\), define the normalized node

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\quad\text{or}\quad
x_n=\Delta\log n.
\]

On a low-prime plateau block

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}(Q)=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\},
\]

we may additionally affine-normalize:

\[
y_p=\frac{x_p-x_0}{L_x}\in[-1,1],
\]

where

\[
L_x=x_+-x_-.
\]

The Wronskian should be constructed in the \(y\)-coordinate, not in raw monomials of \(\log p\).

---

# 3. Canonical AFE symbols

On the chosen active block, write the main contribution schematically as

\[
Z_\alpha^{+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
z_n(\alpha)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
q''_{\rm can,+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can,+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n \phi_j(-i x_n)e^{-im\log n},
\]

where \(\phi_j\) is a stable polynomial basis.

Define the symbol ratio

\[
r_n(\alpha)=\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}.
\]

The basis-normalized rank condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{n\in\mathcal B}
|r_n(\alpha)-P(y_n)|
\ge Q^{-C_r}.
}
\]

For low-prime plateau blocks, the expected source of rank is the visible variation of

\[
r_p(\alpha)\sim p^{-\alpha}(\log p)^{-3}A_\alpha(\log p),
\]

especially the \((\log p)^{-3}\) factor when \(\alpha\approx0\).

---

# 4. Stable basis choice

Use either of the following equivalent constructions.

## Option A: Lagrange witness basis

Choose \(R+2\) active nodes

\[
S=\{n_0,\dots,n_{R+1}\}\subset\mathcal B
\]

such that

\[
y_{n_j}\in[-1,1]
\]

are Chebyshev-like or otherwise interpolation-stable.

Let

\[
\ell_0,\dots,\ell_R
\]

be the degree-\(\le R\) Lagrange basis for the first \(R+1\) nodes:

\[
\ell_j(y_{n_i})=\delta_{ij},
\qquad 0\le i,j\le R.
\]

Let

\[
I_Rr
\]

be the degree-\(\le R\) interpolant through

\[
n_0,\dots,n_R.
\]

Then the augmented symbol determinant is

\[
A_S(\alpha)
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{n_0} & r_{n_1} & \cdots & r_{n_R} & r_{n_{R+1}}\\
\ell_0(y_{n_0}) & \ell_0(y_{n_1}) & \cdots & \ell_0(y_{n_R}) & \ell_0(y_{n_{R+1}})\\
\vdots & \vdots & & \vdots & \vdots\\
\ell_R(y_{n_0}) & \ell_R(y_{n_1}) & \cdots & \ell_R(y_{n_R}) & \ell_R(y_{n_{R+1}})
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

By row reduction,

\[
\boxed{
A_S(\alpha)
=
r_{n_{R+1}}(\alpha)-I_Rr(y_{n_{R+1}}).
}
\]

So the augmented determinant is exactly an interpolation residual. There is no Vandermonde factor.

## Option B: discrete orthonormal basis

Let \(\mu\) be a weight on \(\mathcal B\), and let

\[
\phi_0,\dots,\phi_R
\]

be orthonormal in

\[
\ell^2(\mathcal B,\mu).
\]

Let

\[
\rho=r-\Pi_{\mathcal P_{\le R}}r.
\]

Then

\[
\|\rho\|_{\ell^2(\mu)}
=
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}\|r-P\|_{\ell^2(\mu)}.
\]

By Cauchy–Binet applied to the row matrix

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\rho\\
\phi_0\\
\vdots\\
\phi_R
\end{pmatrix},
\]

one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+2}|\det A_S|^2
=
\|\rho\|_{\ell^2(\mu)}^2.
}
\]

Therefore at least one subset satisfies

\[
|\det A_S|
\ge
\frac{\|\rho\|_{\ell^2(\mu)}}{\sqrt{\binom{M}{R+2}}}.
\]

If

\[
M\le C R,
\]

then

\[
\sqrt{\binom{M}{R+2}}
=
\exp(O(R)),
\]

so this gives only an \(\exp(O(R))\) loss.

---

# 5. Basis-normalized Wronskian rows

Define the basis-normalized row functions as

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\]

\[
G_{j+1}=\phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can},
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

where

\[
\phi_j
\]

is a stable basis polynomial in the normalized frequency variable.

Then define columns using another stable basis

\[
\psi_0,\dots,\psi_{R+1}
\]

or, equivalently, use basis-normalized differential operators

\[
\psi_\ell(\mathcal D)
\]

instead of raw powers \(\mathcal D^\ell\).

The basis-normalized Wronskian is

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}^{\rm bas}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\left(
\psi_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}.
}
\]

In the main AFE block, each entry is

\[
\psi_\ell(\mathcal D)G_{j+1}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n
\phi_j(-ix_n)
\psi_\ell(-ix_n)
e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For \(G_0=Z_\alpha\), the corresponding symbol is

\[
z_n(\alpha)\psi_\ell(-ix_n)
=
c_n r_n(\alpha)\psi_\ell(-ix_n).
\]

---

# 6. Cauchy–Binet coefficient formula

Expanding the basis-normalized Wronskian over an active main block gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}^{\rm bas}_{R,+}(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\substack{S\subset\mathcal B\\ |S|=R+2}}
\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_{S,+}(\alpha)
e^{-im\log N_S},
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

The coefficient factors as

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_{S,+}(\alpha)
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n\right)
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_R(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}
\cdot
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\psi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\psi_{R+1}(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}.
}
\]

If the column basis \(\psi_\ell\) is chosen as a Lagrange basis on the same node set \(S\), then

\[
\det(\psi_\ell(x_n))_{n\in S}=1.
\]

Likewise, if the row basis \(\phi_j\) is Lagrange on \(R+1\) anchor nodes, then

\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_R(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}
=
r(x_\ast)-I_Rr(x_\ast)
\]

for the remaining witness node \(x_\ast\).

Therefore the coefficient becomes

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_{S,+}(\alpha)
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n\right)
\bigl(r(x_\ast)-I_Rr(x_\ast)\bigr),
}
\]

up to harmless row/column ordering signs and amplitude normalizations.

---

# 7. Lower bound from symbol residual

Assume the active block satisfies the symbol-rank condition

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|r-P\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\ge Q^{-C_r}.
\]

Assume also that the active nodes are sufficiently dense and stable so that one can select anchors and a witness satisfying

\[
|r(x_\ast)-I_Rr(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C_r-C_{\rm mesh}}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_{S,+}(\alpha)|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n|.
}
\]

This is the desired normalized minor coefficient lower bound.

The low-prime plateau block enters here through two requirements:

1. the symbol residual is visible, i.e.

   \[
   r_p(\alpha)\not\approx P(y_p);
   \]

2. the coefficients \(c_p\) are not too small on the block.

If

\[
|c_p|\ge Q^{-C_c}
\]

for all \(p\in S\), then

\[
\prod_{p\in S}|c_p|
\ge
Q^{-C_c(R+2)}.
\]

At

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is not \(Q^{-O(1)}\) unless the coefficient normalization absorbs the natural per-prime size. Therefore the correct statement must either:

- normalize the coefficient vector \(c_n\) before forming the determinant; or
- measure the minor relative to the natural block amplitude

\[
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n|.
\]

The Wronskian incidence theorem should be formulated in this amplitude-normalized basis.

---

# 8. Operator norm cost

The basis polynomials \(\phi_j,\psi_\ell\) must be converted into differential operators

\[
\phi_j(\mathcal D),\qquad \psi_\ell(\mathcal D).
\]

For Chebyshev, Legendre, or stable Lagrange bases on well-spaced nodes, one has conservative bounds

\[
\|\phi_j\|_{\rm op}
+
\|\psi_\ell\|_{\rm op}
\le
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

This includes:

- basis conversion to powers of \(\mathcal D\);
- interpolation Lebesgue constants;
- derivative / AFE error amplification;
- modest conditioning losses from nonideal node placement.

At the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus basis normalization is compatible with the canonical AFE derivative budget.

By contrast, the raw monomial Wronskian has determinant conditioning

\[
\exp(O(R^2)),
\]

and can become non-polynomial in \(Q\). This is why the monomial determinant should not be used.

---

# 9. Theorem candidate

## Basis-normalized canonical minor theorem

Let

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(\mathcal B\) be an admissible active AFE block, for example a low-prime plateau block, with normalized nodes \(x_n\in[-1,1]\). Suppose:

### Symbol residual

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{n\in\mathcal B}
|r_n(\alpha)-P(x_n)|
\ge Q^{-C_r}.
\]

### Stable nodes

There exists \(S\subset\mathcal B\), \(|S|=R+2\), such that the Lagrange / discrete orthonormal basis on \(S\) has operator norm

\[
\le \exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

### Nonvanishing AFE amplitudes

For \(n\in S\), the canonical AFE coefficients \(c_n\) are nonzero and are either amplitude-normalized or satisfy an explicit lower bound.

Then there is a basis-normalized Wronskian minor whose Cauchy–Binet coefficient satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_S(\alpha)|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n|.
}
\]

Equivalently, after amplitude normalization,

\[
\boxed{
|\widehat C^{\rm bas}_S(\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

All basis-transformation and differential-operator losses are bounded by

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

---

# 10. What this theorem proves and does not prove

It proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank + stable basis}
\Rightarrow
\text{a polynomially visible normalized minor exists.}
}
\]

It eliminates the artificial monomial Vandermonde loss.

It does **not** prove:

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}^{\rm bas}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The full determinant is still

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}^{\rm bas}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_S
\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_S(\alpha)e^{-im\log N_S},
\]

and the subset-product phases may cancel.

Therefore the remaining independent theorem is still:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
\left|
\sum_S
\widetilde C^{\rm bas}_S(\alpha)e^{-im\log N_S}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The basis-normalized theorem only ensures that this determinant is not coefficient-degenerate for trivial conditioning reasons.

---

# 11. Degeneration cases

The theorem fails or becomes Yellow in the following cases.

## 1. No admissible low-prime plateau block

If the block

\[
Q^a\le p\le Q^b
\]

is outside the usable AFE range, or has negligible coefficients \(c_p\), the rank may be algebraically visible but canonically irrelevant.

## 2. Nodes too compressed

If

\[
x_p=\lambda\log p
\]

has spread

\[
\operatorname{diam}\{x_p:p\in\mathcal B\}\ll R^{-C},
\]

then stable degree-\(R\) interpolation may fail. This is especially dangerous in singular packet scales where \(\lambda\) is very small.

## 3. Symbol residual too small

If

\[
r_p(\alpha)
\]

is too close to a degree-\(R\) polynomial on the chosen block, no basis change can create rank.

## 4. AFE coefficient zeros

If \(c_p\) or smoothing weights vanish on the witness set, the normalized determinant may be formally nonzero but have no canonical mass.

## 5. Full main+dual interference

The theorem above is cleanest for a single branch. In the full canonical object, one must either:

- apply it branchwise to a clean main or dual block; or
- use the two-branch rank condition

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm(\alpha)-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 12. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Basis-normalized canonical minor theorem: Green-feasible.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If low-prime plateau blocks are admissible and symbol residual is }Q^{-C},
\text{ then a normalized minor coefficient is }Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

The monomial Vandermonde loss

\[
\exp(O(R^2))
\]

is avoidable. The correct basis-normalized operator cost is

\[
\boxed{
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
}
\]

at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Remaining open theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual subset-product incidence/nonrecurrence at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:38:13)

_Thought for 15s_

## Agent 3 / C — Basis-normalized Wronskian on packet-frequency blocks

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: construct the basis-normalized Wronskian minor theorem on active packet-frequency blocks satisfying

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp 1,
\]

not low-prime plateau blocks. The latest coordinator brief explicitly corrects the previous low-prime-block issue: low primes can test symbol variation, but they compress the Wronskian nodes \(x_n=\lambda\log n\) too much for the actual determinant.  The assigned Agent 3 task is in the new six-agent prompt. 

---

# 1. Correct active-node regime

Use

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

for definiteness. The same construction works with \(\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m\).

For a main AFE term

\[
e^{-im\log n},
\]

we have

\[
i\mathcal D e^{-im\log n}
=
\lambda\log n\ e^{-im\log n}.
\]

So the natural normalized node is

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

For a dual/folded AFE term of schematic form

\[
e^{i\Theta(m)}e^{im\log n},
\]

the local effective frequency is

\[
\Theta'(m)+\log n
\approx
-\log T+\log n
=
-\log(T/n),
\qquad
T=\frac{m}{2\pi}.
\]

Thus the folded dual node may be taken as

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n),
\]

up to convention-dependent signs.

The Wronskian determinant needs nodes with nontrivial spread:

\[
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n\}\gtrsim R^{-C}.
\]

Therefore the relevant packet-frequency block must satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log n\asymp1.
}
\]

In ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so the correct frequency scale is

\[
\boxed{
\log n\asymp Q.
}
\]

Low-prime blocks with \(\log p\asymp\log Q\) give

\[
x_p\asymp\frac{\log Q}{Q}\ll1
\]

and are not determinant-admissible without a separate renormalized transfer lemma.

---

# 2. Packet-frequency active block

Let

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{n: x_n^+=\lambda\log n\in I_+\},
\]

where \(I_+\subset[c_0,c_1]\subset(0,\infty)\) has length

\[
|I_+|\ge R^{-C_I}.
\]

Similarly define a folded dual block

\[
\mathcal B_-
=
\{n: x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n)\in I_-\}.
\]

The basis-normalized construction is valid on either a single clean branch or on a two-branch union

\[
\mathcal B=\mathcal B_+\sqcup\mathcal B_-.
\]

The minimum block requirements are:

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge R+2,
\]

\[
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n:n\in\mathcal B\}\ge R^{-C_I},
\]

and the AFE amplitudes are nonzero on the witness set.

The active nodes should be selected to be Chebyshev-like after affine normalization

\[
y_n=\frac{2x_n-(x_-+x_+)}{x_+-x_-}\in[-1,1].
\]

---

# 3. Stable basis choice

Choose a stable polynomial basis

\[
\phi_0,\ldots,\phi_R
\]

on the packet-frequency node interval. Good choices are:

1. Chebyshev basis \(T_j(y)\);
2. Legendre basis on \([-1,1]\);
3. discrete orthonormal polynomials on \(\mathcal B\);
4. Lagrange basis on Chebyshev-like selected nodes.

For the minor theorem, the cleanest choice is a Lagrange witness basis.

Pick

\[
S=\{n_0,\ldots,n_{R+1}\}\subset\mathcal B
\]

with stable nodes

\[
y_{n_j}\in[-1,1].
\]

Let

\[
\ell_0,\ldots,\ell_R
\]

be the Lagrange basis on the first \(R+1\) nodes:

\[
\ell_j(y_{n_i})=\delta_{ij},
\qquad 0\le i,j\le R.
\]

Let

\[
\psi_0,\ldots,\psi_{R+1}
\]

be the Lagrange basis on all \(R+2\) nodes:

\[
\psi_\ell(y_{n_i})=\delta_{\ell i}.
\]

Then the basis-normalized row and column operators are

\[
\ell_j(i\mathcal D),
\qquad
\psi_\ell(i\mathcal D),
\]

on the main branch. For the folded dual branch, replace \(i\mathcal D\) by the conventionally signed operator whose principal symbol is \(x_n^-\).

---

# 4. Basis-normalized rows

Define

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\]

\[
G_{j+1}=\ell_j(i\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

The basis-normalized Wronskian minor is

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}^{\rm bas}_{R,S}(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\left(
\psi_\ell(i\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}.
}
\]

This is the localized, stable-basis version of the normalized Wronskian. It is not the raw monomial determinant.

---

# 5. Main-branch Cauchy–Binet coefficient

On a main packet-frequency block, write

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Define

\[
r_n^+(\alpha,m)=\frac{z_n^+(\alpha,m)}{c_n^+(m)}.
\]

Ignoring lower-order amplitude derivatives for the principal symbol, the Cauchy–Binet coefficient for a subset \(S\) is

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde C_{S,+}^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n^+(m)\right)
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n^+(\alpha,m)\\
\ell_0(y_n)\\
\vdots\\
\ell_R(y_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\psi_0(y_n)\\
\vdots\\
\psi_{R+1}(y_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}.
}
\]

For the chosen Lagrange basis,

\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\psi_0(y_n)\\
\vdots\\
\psi_{R+1}(y_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}
=
\pm1.
\]

The augmented row determinant reduces to an interpolation residual:

\[
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n^+\\
\ell_0(y_n)\\
\vdots\\
\ell_R(y_n)
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S}
=
\pm
\left(
r_{n_{R+1}}^+
-
I_R r^+(y_{n_{R+1}})
\right),
\]

where \(I_Rr^+\) is the degree-\(\le R\) interpolant through \(n_0,\ldots,n_R\).

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde C_{S,+}^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)
=
\pm
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n^+(m)\right)
\left(
r_{n_{R+1}}^+
-
I_R r^+(y_{n_{R+1}})
\right)
}
\]

at the principal-symbol level.

This is the central gain: there is no monomial Vandermonde loss.

---

# 6. Dual branch coefficient

For the folded dual branch, write

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}e^{im\log n},
\]

\[
q_{\rm can,-}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
c_n^-(m)e^{i\Theta_q(m)}e^{im\log n}.
\]

After folding, use nodes

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n)
\]

or the exact signed convention.

Define

\[
r_n^-(\alpha,m)=\frac{z_n^-(\alpha,m)}{c_n^-(m)}.
\]

Then the same coefficient formula holds:

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde C_{S,-}^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)
=
\pm
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n^-(m)\right)
\left(
r_{n_{R+1}}^-
-
I_R r^-(y_{n_{R+1}}^-)
\right)
}
\]

again modulo lower-order amplitude-derivative corrections.

---

# 7. Two-branch variant

For the full canonical object, the proper symbol-rank condition is two-branch:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm(\alpha,m)-P(y_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C_r}.
}
\]

If this holds, then by the same interpolation-residual argument there exists a witness subset

\[
S\subset \mathcal B_+\sqcup\mathcal B_-
\]

such that the basis-normalized augmented determinant satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|\det A_S|
\ge Q^{-C_r-C_{\rm mesh}}.
}
\]

Here \(A_S\) is the normalized symbol matrix with first row \(r^\pm\) and lower rows the stable basis functions.

The corresponding Cauchy–Binet coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde C_{S}^{\rm bas}|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n^{\sigma(n)}|,
}
\]

where \(\sigma(n)\in\{+,-\}\) denotes the branch.

After amplitude normalization,

\[
\boxed{
|\widehat C_{S}^{\rm bas}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Operator norm cost

The basis operators are polynomials in \(i\mathcal D\):

\[
\ell_j(i\mathcal D),
\qquad
\psi_\ell(i\mathcal D).
\]

For Chebyshev-like or discrete orthonormal bases on a stable packet-frequency node set,

\[
\|\ell_j\|_{\rm op}
+
\|\psi_\ell\|_{\rm op}
\le
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

This includes:

- conversion from the stable basis to powers of \(\mathcal D\);
- interpolation Lebesgue constants;
- nonideal node placement;
- ordinary AFE derivative amplification.

At safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

Therefore basis normalization remains compatible with the canonical high-derivative AFE package.

---

# 9. Minor theorem

## Packet-frequency basis-normalized minor theorem

Assume ordinary or mildly singular scale with

\[
\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C_\lambda}.
\]

Let \(\mathcal B=\mathcal B_+\sqcup\mathcal B_-\) be an active packet-frequency AFE block satisfying

\[
x_n^\pm\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n^\pm:n\in\mathcal B\}\ge R^{-C_I},
\]

and containing at least \(R+2\) stable nodes.

Assume the full branch symbol residual satisfies

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm(\alpha,m)-P(y_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C_r}.
\]

Assume the branch coefficients \(c_n^\pm\) are amplitude-normalized or non-negligible on the witness nodes.

Then there exists a basis-normalized Wronskian minor coefficient satisfying

\[
\boxed{
|\widehat C_S^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

after natural amplitude normalization, and before normalization

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde C_S^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n^{\sigma(n)}(m)|.
}
\]

All basis transformation and operator losses are bounded by

\[
\boxed{
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 10. What this theorem proves

It proves the following local algebraic-conditioning statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency symbol rank}
+
\text{stable basis}
\Longrightarrow
\text{existence of a polynomially visible normalized minor coefficient.}
}
\]

It also proves that the monomial Vandermonde loss is a coordinate artifact in the packet-frequency Wronskian construction.

---

# 11. What this theorem does not prove

It does **not** prove the determinant lower bound

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Even after basis normalization, the full determinant has the subset-product expansion

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R^{\rm bas}(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_S
\widetilde C_S^{\rm bas}(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log N_S}.
\]

The coefficients may be healthy while the phases cancel.

So the remaining theorem is still the actual arithmetic incidence/nonrecurrence statement.

---

# 12. Obstructions

## Obstruction 1: packet-frequency block outside AFE support

If

\[
\log n\asymp 1/\lambda
\]

lies beyond both main and folded dual AFE support, the block is invalid.

For ordinary scale \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), this requires that the AFE support reaches

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

If the canonical AFE support only reaches a smaller log scale, the Wronskian determinant cannot use the required packet-frequency nodes.

## Obstruction 2: compressed nodes in singular scale

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

then even conductor-scale nodes may satisfy

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\ll1,
\]

and stable rank-\(R\) interpolation collapses.

Deep singular packets should not be forced through this Wronskian theorem.

## Obstruction 3: two-branch rank degeneration

The residual condition can fail if

\[
r_n^+\approx P(y_n^+),
\qquad
r_n^-\approx P(y_n^-)
\]

for one degree-\(\le R\) polynomial \(P\). Degenerate cases include:

\[
\alpha\to0,
\]

saddle overlap,

\[
x^+\approx x^-,
\]

and matching main/dual weight ratios.

## Obstruction 4: amplitude collapse

The normalized coefficient may be healthy but the physical coefficient

\[
\prod_{n\in S}|c_n^\pm|
\]

may be extremely small. The theorem must therefore be stated in amplitude-normalized form, with a separate canonical amplitude lower bound if the physical determinant is used directly.

## Obstruction 5: lower-order amplitude derivatives

Applying \(\phi_j(i\mathcal D)\) to

\[
c_n(m)e^{-im\log n}
\]

also differentiates \(c_n(m)\). These terms are lower order only if the high-derivative AFE package controls them by

\[
Q^{-C}
\]

relative to the principal symbol. Otherwise they must be included in the exact branch symbol.

---

# 13. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency basis-normalized minor theorem: Green-feasible.}
}
\]

Conditional requirements:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log n\asymp1
}
\]

active blocks must exist inside the canonical AFE support;

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-branch symbol residual}\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

must hold on those blocks;

and the construction must use basis-normalized operators, not raw monomial derivatives.

The theorem clears the conditioning/minor subproblem. It does not clear the final incidence theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:41:45)

I’ll focus only on the Agent 3/C subclaim: whether the angle/nonalignment estimate is genuinely weaker than the full incidence theorem, and whether any usable arithmetic mechanism appears at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

_Thought for 4s_

## Agent 3 / C — Angle/nonalignment theorem at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: attack the angle/nonalignment estimate

\[
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0)|
\]

at admissible packet-frequency zeros

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

The prompt defines this as the current hardest subclaim inside the packet-frequency Wronskian incidence theorem. 

---

# 1. Setup at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

Use the basis-normalized Wronskian

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det\bigl(C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)\bigr)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

expansion along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row or first function-row gives schematically

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\,
M_\ell(m_0).
\]

Define

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
=
\bigl((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)
=
(M_1(m_0),\dots,M_{R+1}(m_0)).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
}
\]

The desired incidence theorem follows from three estimates:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Agent 3 is responsible for the third estimate.

---

# 2. Packet-frequency AFE expressions

On a packet-frequency main block

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\]

with

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

write

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For the dual/folded branch,

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}e^{im\log n},
\]

\[
q_{\rm can,-}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
c_n^-(m)e^{i\Theta_q(m)}e^{im\log n},
\]

with folded nodes

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{T}{n},
\qquad
T=\frac{m}{2\pi}.
\]

The \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector has components

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+ C_\ell(-ix_n^+)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^- C_\ell(ix_n^-)e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)+im_0\log n}
+
\text{background/error}.
\]

The minors \(M_\ell\) are exterior products of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows. They expand as subset-product sums

\[
M_\ell(m_0)
=
\sum_{S}
D_{\ell,S}(\alpha,m_0)
e^{-im_0\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/mixed branch terms}
+
\text{canonical errors}.
\]

Thus the angle expression is itself a structured exponential sum:

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\sum_{\ell,S}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
D_{\ell,S}(m_0)e^{-im_0\log N_S}.
\]

There is no manifest positivity or Hermitian structure.

---

# 3. Does zero simplicity give the angle bound?

No.

Zero simplicity or quantitative zero separation may give

\[
\max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}
|C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That is a lower bound for

\[
|\mathbf z'|.
\]

It says nothing about the direction of \(\mathbf z'\) relative to \(\mathbf M\).

The angle theorem needs

\[
\mathbf z'
\not\perp
\mathbf M
\]

quantitatively. Simplicity only says

\[
\mathbf z'\ne0.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{simplicity of }Z_\alpha\text{ is insufficient for the angle estimate.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Does packet-frequency symbol rank give the angle bound?

Also no, at least not by itself.

Packet-frequency symbol rank says roughly

\[
r_n^\pm(\alpha,m)=\frac{z_n^\pm}{c_n^\pm}
\]

is not approximable by a degree-\(\le R\) polynomial in the packet nodes \(x_n^\pm\). This ensures that the \(Z_\alpha\)-row is not algebraically redundant with the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows at the symbol level.

That yields nonzero normalized minors or nonzero exterior products.

But the angle estimate is a **pointwise phase statement** at \(m=m_0\). Symbol rank controls coefficient geometry; it does not prevent subset-product phase cancellation in

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank gives exterior algebra nondegeneracy, not pointwise nonalignment.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Phase-relaxed countermodel

A phase-relaxed model shows the angle theorem is as hard as the incidence theorem.

Let the packet-frequency active block have independent phases

\[
u_n=e^{-im\log n}\in S^1.
\]

Model

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=\sum_n z_n u_n,
\]

and let

\[
\mathbf z'(u)=
\bigl(\sum_n z_n C_\ell(x_n)u_n\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf M(u)
\]

be the vector of basis-normalized minors, each a subset-product polynomial in the same \(u_n\).

The phase-relaxed bad system is:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

\[
\langle \mathbf z'(u),\mathbf M(u)\rangle=0,
\]

with healthy conditions

\[
|\mathbf z'(u)|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M(u)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is only two complex equations plus inequalities on a torus of dimension \(|\mathcal B|\gg R\). Generically, it has many solutions.

Indeed, the orthogonality condition is codimension \(2\) real, while \(Z_\alpha=0\) is another codimension \(2\) real. The active phase torus still has dimension

\[
|\mathcal B|-4,
\]

which is positive and large.

Thus in the relaxed model one can have

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M,
\qquad
|\mathbf z'|,|\mathbf M|\not\approx0.
\]

Therefore the angle theorem cannot follow from dimension, symbol rank, or basis conditioning.

---

# 6. One-parameter recurrence version

Restricting to the actual one-parameter prime-log orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}
\]

does not automatically save the theorem.

If a phase-relaxed solution \(u^\ast\) exists with healthy diagnostics, then Kronecker recurrence suggests that the one-parameter orbit can approximate it to accuracy \(\varepsilon\) with recurrence cost roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-d},
\]

where \(d\) is the effective number of multiplicatively independent prime phases involved.

For a packet-frequency block with \(d\asymp R\), achieving polynomial smallness

\[
\varepsilon\asymp Q^{-C}
\]

costs

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This remains too cheap relative to the natural large height budget if \(Q\sim\log m\).

Thus the actual one-parameter orbit does not by generic Diophantine recurrence alone forbid near-orthogonality.

---

# 7. What actual-zeta arithmetic would need to provide

To prove the angle theorem, one needs a genuinely arithmetic nonalignment principle.

A plausible target theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac{\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)}{|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|},
\mathbf M(m_0)^\perp
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

This would have to exploit one of the following:

## 7.1 A zero-repulsion identity

Some identity forcing the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector at a zero to have a component aligned with the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-minor vector.

No such identity is currently visible.

## 7.2 A resultant inequality

A quantitative exponential-polynomial resultant of the form

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But this is exactly the direct incidence theorem.

## 7.3 Main/dual compatibility obstruction

A theorem that simultaneous

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0
\]

forces incompatible main/dual AFE conditions.

This is plausible only with exact canonical coefficients and gamma phase. It is not a formal Wronskian consequence.

## 7.4 Euler-product rigidity

A theorem that the actual \(\Lambda(n)\)-weighted coefficients cannot realize the phase-relaxed orthogonality pattern.

This would be a fixed actual-zeta nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 8. Relationship to the original incidence theorem

The angle theorem is not meaningfully easier than the incidence theorem.

At a zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

If one already has

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

then the incidence theorem is exactly equivalent to the angle theorem.

Conversely, if the angle theorem fails, then one can have

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

even when derivative size and minor-vector size are healthy.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the angle theorem is the incidence theorem modulo size lower bounds.}
}
\]

It is not a separate soft sublemma.

---

# 9. Conditional theorem candidate

The strongest useful formulation is conditional.

## Conditional angle theorem

Assume ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

packet-frequency active blocks

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+\frac{Q}{R},
\]

basis-normalized operators with cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

and canonical AFE control through order \(2R+1\).

Assume:

### Derivative lower bound

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_z}.
\]

### Minor lower bound

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_M}.
\]

### Arithmetic nonalignment

\[
\operatorname{angle}(\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0))
\ge Q^{-A_\angle}.
\]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-(A_z+A_M+A_\angle)}.
\]

This gives finite-jet anti-design and hence Gate 1 after the standard Wronskian-to-jet transfer.

But the third assumption is exactly the missing arithmetic theorem.

---

# 10. No-go diagnosis

The following routes do **not** prove the angle theorem:

## Simplicity of \(Z_\alpha\)

Gives

\[
|\mathbf z'|>0
\]

or maybe

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but not the angle.

## Packet-frequency symbol rank

Gives coefficient-level independence, not pointwise phase nonalignment.

## Basis normalization

Controls conditioning, not subset-product cancellation.

## Average \(L^2\) lower bounds

May show that

\[
\int |\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|^2
\]

is nonzero or large on average, but does not exclude smallness at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

## Generic codimension

The joint bad event still has low enough codimension in the phase torus that recurrence remains plausible.

---

# 11. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No independent angle theorem is currently visible.}
}
\]

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The angle/nonalignment bound is essentially equivalent to the actual incidence theorem.}
}
\]

Packet-frequency blocks repair the node-spread and conditioning problem, but they do not by themselves create a nonalignment mechanism at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

A proof must use genuinely actual-zeta arithmetic, likely one of:

\[
\text{main/dual incompatibility},
\quad
\text{Euler-product rigidity},
\quad
\text{exponential-polynomial resultant},
\quad
\text{zero-repulsion beyond simplicity}.
\]

In all relaxed models I can formulate, including healthy packet-frequency rank and healthy minor size, one can impose

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M.
\]

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Angle route: Yellow-to-Red as a standalone proof.}
}
\]

It remains useful as a clean decomposition of the incidence theorem, but it does not reduce the core arithmetic difficulty.

## Agent 3 / C — Vector minor nonrecurrence

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: analyze the cofactor/minor-vector lower bound

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, using packet-frequency blocks and basis-normalized Wronskians. The coordinator prompt identifies this as one of the remaining subclaims needed for the incidence theorem. 

---

# 1. Object

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the Wronskian expands as

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle,
\]

where

\[
\mathbf M=(M_1,\ldots,M_{R+1})
\]

is the cofactor vector obtained from the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows.

The target subclaim is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is strictly weaker than the full angle/incidence theorem, but it is still not automatic.

---

# 2. Packet-frequency expansion of \(\mathbf M\)

Work in ordinary scale:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp 1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use packet-frequency blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<1/2,
\]

so

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

On a main branch,

\[
q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Apply stable basis operators

\[
\phi_j(\mathcal D),
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

to produce the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-rows. Principal-symbol form:

\[
\phi_j(\mathcal D)q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
c_n^+(m)\phi_j(-ix_n^+)e^{-im\log n}
+
\text{lower-order amplitude terms}.
\]

The cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\) is the Hodge dual of these \(R+1\) jet rows after column-basis normalization. Hence it has a Cauchy–Binet expansion

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{\substack{S\subset\mathcal B\\ |S|=R+1}}
\mathbf A_S(m)\,e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\mathbf M_{\rm dual}(m)
+
\mathbf M_{B_2}(m)
+
\mathbf M_{E_2}(m),
}
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

For a pure main-branch subset,

\[
\mathbf A_S
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n^+\right)
\mathbf a_S,
\]

where \(\mathbf a_S\) is the basis-normalized exterior coefficient vector determined by

\[
\{\phi_j(x_n):0\le j\le R,\ n\in S\}.
\]

In a discrete orthonormal basis on the active block, \(\mathbf a_S\) is a Plücker coordinate vector of the row space.

---

# 3. Exterior coefficient mass lower bound

The cleanest coefficient-mass statement is in an \(\ell^2\)-normalized active block.

Let

\[
v_n
=
c_n \, e_n
\]

where \(e_n\) is the column evaluation vector

\[
e_n=(\phi_0(x_n),\ldots,\phi_R(x_n))\in\mathbb C^{R+1}.
\]

Let \(V\) be the \((R+1)\times M\) matrix with columns \(v_n\).

Then the exterior coefficient mass is

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\det V_S|^2
=
\det(VV^\ast)
\]

by Cauchy–Binet.

If the basis \(\phi_j\) is discrete orthonormal with respect to weights comparable to \(|c_n|^2\), then

\[
VV^\ast\approx I_{R+1}\cdot \mathcal A,
\]

after amplitude normalization, where

\[
\mathcal A=\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}|c_n|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2
\asymp
\mathcal A^{R+1}
}
\]

before amplitude normalization, and

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2
\asymp1
}
\]

after normalizing the active coefficient vector.

Using the packet-frequency block mass supplied in the coordinator brief,

\[
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}|c_p|^2\asymp\frac{Q^6}{R},
\]

we get a strong aggregate exterior mass:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2
\gtrsim
\left(\frac{Q^6}{R}\right)^{R+1}
}
\]

in physical coefficient normalization, modulo basis-conditioning and dual/error corrections.

So coefficient-level nonvanishing of the minor vector is not the problem.

---

# 4. Average lower bound for \(\mathbf M\)

The vector-valued sum is

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_S \mathbf A_S e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\cdots.
\]

On a long interval \(J\), if subset-product frequencies are sufficiently separated, then

\[
\int_J |\mathbf M(m)|^2\,dm
=
|J|\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2
+
\text{off-diagonal error}.
\]

More explicitly,

\[
\int_J |\mathbf M(m)|^2\,dm
=
\sum_{S,S'}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_{S'}\rangle
\int_J e^{-im(\log N_S-\log N_{S'})}\,dm.
\]

The diagonal contribution is

\[
|J|\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
\]

The off-diagonal terms are controlled if

\[
|J|\cdot |\log N_S-\log N_{S'}|\gg1
\]

for most pairs. Since \(N_S\ne N_{S'}\) for distinct prime subsets, this is plausible on sufficiently long \(J\).

Thus an average theorem is plausible:

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J|\mathbf M(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

after amplitude normalization and canonical error control.

This proves that \(\mathbf M\) is not globally small on long intervals.

---

# 5. Failure of average-to-pointwise transfer at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros

The desired estimate is not average. It is pointwise at a constrained set:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

An \(L^2\) lower bound over \(J\) does not exclude the possibility that all or many \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros in \(J\) lie in the small set

\[
\{m:|\mathbf M(m)|<Q^{-A}\}.
\]

To transfer the average estimate to the zero set, one would need a correlation/avoidance theorem:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\mathbf M(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But that is exactly the vector minor nonrecurrence problem.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exterior coefficient mass gives average mass, not pointwise mass at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Subset-product cancellation can make \(\mathbf M\) small in relaxed models

Consider a phase-relaxed torus model with independent phases

\[
u_p=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M(u)
=
\sum_S\mathbf A_S\prod_{p\in S}u_p.
\]

The equation

\[
\mathbf M(u)=0
\]

is a system of \(R+1\) complex equations. If the active dimension \(M\) is much larger than \(R\), this may be solvable directly.

Even if \(M\asymp R+1\), one can often arrange near-cancellation componentwise if the coefficient vectors \(\mathbf A_S\) span many directions and no positivity is present.

The packet-frequency construction gives healthy coefficient mass, but not positivity. Therefore the relaxed model can plausibly satisfy

\[
|\mathbf M(u)|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

with healthy basis conditioning.

Adding

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0
\]

imposes one additional complex equation. In a sufficiently large phase-relaxed block, the system remains underdetermined.

Thus a relaxed countermodel exists unless one uses actual one-parameter arithmetic.

---

# 7. One-parameter orbit recurrence obstruction

Restrict to the actual orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

If there is a phase-relaxed torus point \(u^\ast\) with

\[
\mathbf M(u^\ast)\approx0,
\qquad
Z_\alpha(u^\ast)\approx0,
\]

then Kronecker-type recurrence suggests approximation by the one-parameter orbit at cost

\[
\varepsilon^{-d},
\]

where \(d\) is the effective number of independent prime phases.

For packet-frequency blocks with \(d\asymp R\), polynomial accuracy

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C}
\]

costs

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is still too cheap compared with the natural height budget when \(Q\sim\log m\).

Therefore generic one-parameter recurrence does not forbid

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

---

# 8. Possible positive mechanisms

I see four possible ways to prove the minor-vector lower bound. None follows from current algebra alone.

## 8.1 Positivity / Hodge norm identity

If \(\mathbf M\) were the gradient of a positive exterior norm, then perhaps

\[
|\mathbf M|^2
\]

would equal a determinant of a positive Gram matrix.

But pointwise in \(m\), \(\mathbf M\) is a sum of oscillatory subset-products, not a positive Gram determinant.

So this does not currently work.

## 8.2 Dominant minor family

If a subset family \(\mathfrak S_0\) dominated the vector sum, then cancellation would be impossible.

But packet-frequency blocks contain many comparable subsets. There is no natural dominance.

## 8.3 Long average plus zero equidistribution

If one could prove \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros are equidistributed relative to the phases of \(\mathbf M\), then the average lower bound might transfer to zeros.

This is a deep pair-correlation / value-distribution statement for actual zeta exponential sums, not currently available in the proof architecture.

## 8.4 Main/dual incompatibility

The most plausible actual-zeta mechanism is that the full canonical main+dual coupling prevents \(\mathbf M\) from being small when \(Z_\alpha=0\).

This would need a theorem of the form:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\det(VV^\ast)_{\rm effective}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or an equivalent nonrecurrence statement for the actual AFE phases.

This is plausible only as a hard arithmetic theorem.

---

# 9. Conditional theorem

A useful conditional formulation is:

## Minor-vector nonrecurrence theorem

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

packet-frequency active blocks

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R,
\]

basis-normalized operators with cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

and canonical AFE control through order \(2R+1\).

Assume:

### Exterior coefficient mass

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-C_1}
\]

after amplitude normalization.

### Zero-set nonconcentration

For every admissible zero \(m_0\) of \(Z_\alpha\),

\[
\left|
\sum_S\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\log N_S}
\right|
\ge
Q^{-C_2}
\left(\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The second assumption is the actual nonrecurrence content.

---

# 10. No-go diagnosis

The following are insufficient for a pointwise minor-vector lower bound:

## Coefficient mass

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-C}
\]

only proves average size.

## Basis conditioning

Controls artificial determinant losses, not phase cancellation.

## Packet-frequency node spread

Ensures rank and stable bases, not pointwise nonrecurrence.

## \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank

Ensures the first Wronskian row is not redundant; it does not force the cofactor vector to be large at zeros.

## Simplicity of \(Z_\alpha\)

Relevant to \(|\mathbf z'|\), not \(|\mathbf M|\).

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The minor-vector lower bound is not proved by exterior coefficient mass alone.}
}
\]

What is Green-feasible:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

after amplitude normalization, using packet-frequency block mass and basis conditioning.

What remains Yellow/open:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a vector-valued subset-product nonrecurrence theorem for the actual packet-frequency AFE orbit.

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{minor-vector size reduces to actual prime-log orbit nonconcentration at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

It is easier than the full angle theorem only in that it removes \(\mathbf z'\) from the problem, but it is still an arithmetic incidence/nonrecurrence statement, not a consequence of Wronskian algebra.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:49:10)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 3 / C — Arithmetic angle/nonalignment theorem

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: attack the angle/nonalignment estimate at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, using packet-frequency main+dual AFE structure. 

The target is

\[
|\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0)|
\]

under

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Here

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

---

# 1. Principal-symbol form of \(\mathbf z'\)

Use packet-frequency blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<1/2,
\]

with ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp1.
\]

For the main branch,

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}e^{im\log n},
\]

with folded node

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{T}{n},
\qquad
T=\frac{m}{2\pi}.
\]

Let \(C_\ell\) be the stable column-basis operator. Then, at principal-symbol level,

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+ C_\ell(-ix_n^+)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^- C_\ell(ix_n^-)e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)+im_0\log n}
+
\text{l.o.t.}
\]

Thus

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
\]

is a vector-valued packet-frequency exponential sum.

---

# 2. Principal-symbol form of \(\mathbf M\)

The cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\) is built only from the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows. On the main branch,

\[
q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

After basis normalization, the cofactor vector has the Cauchy–Binet form

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S(m)e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\mathbf M_{\rm dual}(m)
+
\mathbf M_{B_2}(m)
+
\mathbf M_{E_2}(m),
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

For a pure main subset,

\[
\mathbf A_S
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n^+\right)\mathbf a_S,
\]

with \(\mathbf a_S\) a basis-normalized exterior coefficient vector.

The pairing is therefore

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\sum_{\ell,S}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\,A_{\ell,S}(m_0)e^{-im_0\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/mixed/background/error}.
\]

Equivalently, after expanding \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha\), the main-main part contains frequencies

\[
\log n+\log N_S
=
\log(nN_S).
\]

So the angle numerator is itself another packet-frequency subset-product exponential sum.

---

# 3. Why symbol rank does not give the angle bound

The packet-frequency symbol-rank theorem says roughly that

\[
r_n^\pm=\frac{z_n^\pm}{c_n^\pm}
\]

is not well-approximated by a degree-\(\le R\) polynomial in \(x_n^\pm\). This gives exterior-algebra nondegeneracy: it says the \(Z_\alpha\)-row is not coefficient-wise redundant with the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows.

But the angle estimate is pointwise in \(m\). It depends on the phases

\[
e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
e^{-im\log N_S},
\qquad
e^{-im\log(nN_S)}.
\]

So the implication

\[
\text{symbol rank}
\Rightarrow
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|
\]

is false in general. Symbol rank is a coefficient-space statement; nonalignment is a phase-space statement.

---

# 4. Simplicity of \(Z_\alpha\) is insufficient

A quantitative simple-zero theorem could give

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That is useful, but it only controls the length of one vector. It gives no lower bound for the angle between \(\mathbf z'\) and \(\mathbf M\).

Even if

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

one can still have

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

Thus zero simplicity / zero separation can supply the first size factor, not the nonalignment theorem.

---

# 5. Strong phase-relaxed countermodel

Use independent phases

\[
u_n=e^{-im\log n}\in S^1
\]

for the packet-frequency block.

Model

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=\sum_n z_n u_n+\sum_n z_n^-v_n+\text{background}.
\]

At the same time,

\[
\mathbf z'(u)
=
\left(
\sum_n z_n C_\ell(x_n)u_n+\sum_n z_n^-C_\ell(x_n^-)v_n
\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M(u)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S\prod_{n\in S}u_n
+
\text{dual/mixed terms}.
\]

The relaxed bad system is

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

\[
|\mathbf z'(u)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M(u)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
\langle\mathbf z'(u),\mathbf M(u)\rangle=0.
\]

This is solvable generically: \(Z_\alpha=0\) is one complex condition, and the orthogonality is another complex condition. With \(|\mathcal B|\gg R\) phase variables, the system remains underdetermined.

So phase-relaxed models allow

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M,
\qquad
|\mathbf z'|,|\mathbf M|\not\approx0.
\]

Therefore the angle theorem cannot follow from:

\[
\text{packet-frequency node spread},
\quad
\text{basis conditioning},
\quad
\text{symbol rank},
\quad
\text{zero simplicity}.
\]

---

# 6. One-parameter recurrence obstruction

Restricting to the true orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}
\]

does not automatically eliminate the relaxed obstruction.

If a healthy relaxed bad point \(u^\ast\) exists, then Kronecker recurrence suggests the orbit can approach it to accuracy \(\varepsilon\) at cost approximately

\[
\varepsilon^{-d},
\]

where \(d\) is the effective prime-phase dimension.

For packet-frequency blocks with \(d\asymp R\), polynomial accuracy \(\varepsilon=Q^{-C}\) costs

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is still too cheap compared with the global height budget when \(Q\sim\log m\).

So a generic Diophantine one-parameter-orbit argument does not prove the angle theorem.

---

# 7. Possible actual-zeta mechanisms checked

## 7.1 Main/dual commutator

A hopeful route is that exact main+dual folding forces a nonzero skew pairing between \(\mathbf z'\) and \(\mathbf M\). Schematically, one would want

\[
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\right)
\]

to have a sign or a lower bound.

I do not see such a sign. Away from saddle overlap, the two branches are separated in frequency, but separation gives rank and conditioning, not sign. The gamma phase rotates the dual contribution; it does not impose positivity.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{No visible commutator lower bound.}}
\]

## 7.2 Euler-product rigidity

The coefficients are not arbitrary: they come from \(\Lambda(n)\), AFE weights, and gamma factors. A true theorem might say the Euler-product coefficients cannot realize the phase-relaxed orthogonality pattern.

But this is exactly a fixed actual-zeta nonrecurrence theorem. It is plausible as a hard theorem, not as a consequence of the current Wronskian algebra.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{Possible, but it is the missing arithmetic theorem.}}
\]

## 7.3 Zero-repulsion

A zero-repulsion theorem might imply that when

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-minor direction cannot be orthogonal to the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative direction.

But standard zero separation gives lower bounds for derivatives or distances between zeros, not vector-angle information against a cofactor vector built from \(q''_{\rm can}\).

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{Zero separation may help }|\mathbf z'|,\text{ not the angle.}}
\]

## 7.4 Exponential-polynomial resultant

One could seek an effective resultant inequality

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

At a zero this gives the desired lower bound. But this is exactly the direct incidence theorem. It is not a simpler angle sublemma.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{Equivalent to the full incidence theorem.}}
\]

---

# 8. Conditional angle theorem

The best available formulation is conditional.

Assume:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_z},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_M},
\]

and the actual-zeta nonalignment condition

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac{\mathbf z'}{|\mathbf z'|},
\mathbf M^\perp
\right)
\ge Q^{-A_\angle}.
\]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
=
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-(A_z+A_M+A_\angle)}.
\]

This gives the Wronskian incidence estimate and hence finite-jet anti-design.

But the third assumption is the hard missing theorem.

---

# 9. Precise reduction

The angle theorem is equivalent to the full incidence theorem modulo the two size estimates.

If

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_z},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A_M},
\]

then

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is equivalent to

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A'}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{angle nonalignment is not a softer theorem; it is the incidence theorem in cofactor coordinates.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No independent arithmetic angle theorem is currently visible.}
}
\]

The packet-frequency correction fixes node spread and makes symbol rank plausible, but it does not create a nonalignment mechanism.

The strongest negative model is:

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
\mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M
\]

in a phase-relaxed packet-frequency model with healthy rank and basis conditioning.

To forbid this, one needs genuinely actual-zeta arithmetic, most likely one of:

\[
\text{Euler-product rigidity},
\quad
\text{main/dual incompatibility beyond frequency separation},
\quad
\text{effective exponential-polynomial resultant},
\quad
\text{zero-repulsion coupled to }q''_{\rm can}\text{ minors}.
\]

Current classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Angle theorem: Yellow-to-Red as an independent route.}
}
\]

It remains useful as a decomposition, but not as a simplification. The Wronskian route still lives or dies on the actual incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Arithmetic angle theorem via main/dual structure

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: test whether exact main/dual AFE structure can prove the angle/nonalignment bound

\[
|\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0)|
\]

at admissible zeros \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\). The prompt asks specifically for main/dual arithmetic mechanisms, not another broad route audit. 

---

# 1. Main/dual packet-frequency model

Work in ordinary packet scale:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use packet-frequency main blocks

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<c_1<1/2.
\]

Let

\[
T=\frac{m}{2\pi}.
\]

The main packet node is

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

The folded dual packet node is

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n).
\]

For \(c<c_1<1/2\), the main block is away from the saddle. The dual block corresponding to the same packet-frequency scale lies near

\[
\log(T/n)\asymp Q,
\]

so

\[
\log n\asymp \log T-Q.
\]

Thus main and dual live on separated frequency branches.

Write the packet-frequency AFE pieces as

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{im\log n},
\]

and

\[
q_{\rm can,+}''(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
q_{\rm can,-}''(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_q(m)}
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
c_n^-(m)e^{im\log n}.
\]

The canonical object is

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+q_{\rm can,+}''+q_{\rm can,-}''+E_2.
\]

The basis-normalized \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector has components

\[
z'_\ell
=
(-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0).
\]

Principal-symbol expansion:

\[
z'_\ell
=
(-1)^\ell
\left[
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+ C_\ell(-ix_n^+)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^- C_\ell(ix_n^-)e^{im_0\log n}
\right]
+
\text{l.o.t.}
\]

The cofactor vector has the form

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_{++\cdots+}
+
\mathbf M_{--\cdots-}
+
\mathbf M_{\rm mixed}
+
\mathbf M_{B_2}
+
\mathbf M_{E_2}.
\]

The angle numerator is

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\text{mixed/background/error}.
\]

Each term is a subset-product exponential sum. For example,

\[
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
=
\sum_{n,S}
K^+_{n,S}(\alpha,m_0)
e^{-im_0\log(nN_S)},
\]

while

\[
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}
\sum_{n,S}
K^{-+}_{n,S}(\alpha,m_0)
e^{im_0\log n}e^{-im_0\log N_S}.
\]

So main/dual structure changes the frequency set, but the numerator remains an oscillatory fixed-coefficient exponential sum.

---

# 2. Candidate commutator mechanism

The most plausible soft mechanism would be a skew main/dual commutator, e.g.

\[
\mathcal C_{\pm}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\right).
\]

If one could show

\[
|\mathcal C_{\pm}|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|,
\]

then the angle theorem would follow.

However, after folding the dual branch,

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n),
\]

the dual is not an opposite-sign copy of the main. It is a complementary packet-frequency branch. The gamma phase contributes a rotating factor

\[
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}
\quad\text{or}\quad
e^{i\Theta_q(m)},
\]

but this does not impose a sign. The cross terms have phases of the form

\[
\Theta_Z(m_0)+m_0\log n-m_0\log N_S,
\]

or

\[
-\Theta_q(m_0)-m_0\log n+m_0\log N_S,
\]

depending on branch assignment. These phases are not locked to a fixed quadrant.

Thus the commutator has no evident positivity or coercive imaginary part.

\[
\boxed{
\text{No sign-definite main/dual commutator is visible.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Branch separation helps rank, not angle

Avoiding saddle overlap by taking

\[
0<c<c_1<1/2
\]

is useful because it separates the nodes:

\[
x^+\not\approx x^-.
\]

This helps the two-branch symbol-rank condition

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_n
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But angle nonalignment is not a coefficient-rank statement. It is a pointwise statement about phases at \(m=m_0\).

Branch separation gives better-conditioned coefficient matrices. It does not prevent the subset-product sums in

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]

from cancelling.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch separation gives rank/conditioning, not pointwise angle control.}
}
\]

---

# 4. \(\alpha\)-asymmetry does not by itself force nonalignment

The branch ratios have schematic normalized forms

\[
r_+(\alpha;x)
\sim
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
x^{-3}A_+(x),
\]

and

\[
r_-(\alpha;y)
\sim
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(y-y_0)}
y^{-3}A_-(y),
\]

up to convention-dependent weights.

For \(|\alpha|/\lambda\) not too small, this creates strong two-branch symbol variation. But the angle problem persists: the same \(\alpha\)-asymmetry appears only in the coefficients \(K_{n,S}\), while the phases remain free enough to cancel in the actual exponential sum unless one proves a genuine nonrecurrence theorem.

In the hardest regime,

\[
\alpha\to0,
\]

the asymmetry vanishes and one relies on \(x^{-3}\)-type curvature for symbol rank. That is enough for coefficient nondegeneracy, but not angle control.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\text{-asymmetry helps symbol rank but does not supply a soft angle bound.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Phase-relaxed obstruction with main/dual included

A clean obstruction keeps the exact branch structure but relaxes phases.

Let

\[
u_n^+=e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
u_n^-=e^{im\log n},
\]

with the gamma phases kept as fixed unit factors

\[
\omega_Z=e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)},
\qquad
\omega_q=e^{i\Theta_q(m_0)}.
\]

Define

\[
Z_\alpha(u)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}z_n^+u_n^+
+
\omega_Z
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}z_n^-u_n^-.
\]

Define \(\mathbf z'(u)\) and \(\mathbf M(u)\) by the same basis-normalized AFE symbols and subset-products.

Then the bad relaxed system is

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

\[
|\mathbf z'(u)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M(u)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
\langle \mathbf z'(u),\mathbf M(u)\rangle=0.
\]

This is one complex zero equation and one complex orthogonality equation, plus inequalities. With the packet-frequency block containing many more phase variables than equations, the system is underdetermined.

The main/dual branch relation changes coefficients and frequency labels, but it does not remove the degrees of freedom. In particular, the folded relation

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log(T/n)
\]

does not impose algebraic dependence among the relaxed phases strong enough to prevent orthogonality.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact branch shapes alone do not forbid the angle countermodel.}
}
\]

---

# 6. What actual-zeta arithmetic is missing

The phase-relaxed model omits the one essential arithmetic constraint:

\[
u_n^\pm
\]

are not independent. They lie on the actual one-parameter orbit tied by

\[
u_n^+=e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
u_n^-=e^{im\log n},
\]

with the same \(m\), the same gamma phase, and actual Euler-product coefficients.

However, generic Kronecker recurrence of the one-parameter orbit still suggests polynomially small targets can be approached at cost

\[
Q^{O(R)}
\]

when the effective phase dimension is \(O(R)\). So even the one-parameter orbit does not automatically give a proof.

The missing arithmetic theorem must say that the **actual zeta coefficients and the actual main/dual coupling** forbid the specific incidence

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0
\]

despite generic recurrence.

A possible statement is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac{\mathbf z'(m,\alpha)}{|\mathbf z'(m,\alpha)|},
\mathbf M(m)^\perp
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But this is precisely the arithmetic angle theorem, not a consequence of existing Wronskian algebra.

---

# 7. Main/dual obstruction theorem candidate

The strongest candidate I can formulate is conditional.

## Candidate theorem: folded-branch incidence obstruction

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

packet-frequency blocks

\[
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R,
\qquad 0<c<c_1<1/2,
\]

safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

basis-normalized Wronskians, and canonical AFE control.

Suppose the exact folded main/dual coefficients satisfy a nonrecurrence condition:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
\left|
\sum_{\sigma\in\{+,-\}}
\sum_{\ell,S}
K_{\ell,S}^{\sigma}(m,\alpha)
e^{-im\Omega_{\ell,S}^{\sigma}(m)}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Here the \(\Omega_{\ell,S}^{\sigma}\) are the exact main/dual subset-product phases, including gamma phase.

Then the angle theorem follows.

This is tautological but useful: it identifies the exact arithmetic object that must be bounded. It is a **folded main/dual subset-product nonrecurrence theorem**.

---

# 8. No-go diagnosis for soft main/dual closure

I do **not** see a soft theorem of the form:

\[
\text{main/dual branch separation}
+
\text{gamma phase}
+
\alpha\text{-asymmetry}
\Rightarrow
\text{angle lower bound}.
\]

Reasons:

1. Branch separation improves coefficient rank but does not impose sign.
2. Gamma phases rotate dual terms rather than making them positive.
3. \(\alpha\)-asymmetry may vanish as \(\alpha\to0\).
4. Cross terms are still subset-product exponential sums.
5. Phase-relaxed models with the same branch coefficient geometry admit orthogonality.
6. One-parameter recurrence appears too cheap absent a deeper arithmetic exclusion.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main/dual coupling currently only shifts the nonrecurrence problem into a more exact folded-branch form.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No independent main/dual angle mechanism found.}
}
\]

The best precise statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the angle theorem reduces to a folded main/dual subset-product nonrecurrence theorem for actual zeta coefficients.}
}
\]

Thus the Wronskian route remains viable but Yellow. The remaining theorem is not local algebra, not basis conditioning, and not symbol rank; it is actual arithmetic incidence:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\langle\mathbf z'(m,\alpha),\mathbf M(m)\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Main/dual structure gives the correct exact object to attack, but I do not see a sign, commutator, or branch-separation argument that proves it.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:54:45)

_Thought for 12s_

## Agent 3 / C — Direct actual-orbit incidence theorem

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: attack the full incidence theorem directly,

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

treating \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) as actual fixed-coefficient exponential sums on the one-parameter zeta orbit. 

---

# 1. Direct packet-frequency AFE model

Work in the ordinary packet-frequency regime:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use packet-frequency blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<1/2.
\]

Then

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

The \(Z_\alpha\) AFE has schematic main+dual form

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_\alpha^+(m)+Z_\alpha^-(m)+E_Z(m),
\]

with

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{im\log n}.
\]

For the canonical source curvature,

\[
q''_{\rm can}
=
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The basis-normalized Wronskian is an exponential polynomial of much higher degree:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\Omega}
C_\Omega(\alpha,m)e^{-im\Omega}
+
\text{folded dual/mixed phases}
+
\text{background/error}.
\]

In the pure main branch, the frequencies are subset-products:

\[
\Omega=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+2.
\]

In the mixed main/dual expansion, frequencies include forms such as

\[
\log N_+ - \log N_-,
\]

and gamma-phase shifted terms

\[
e^{ik\Theta(m)}e^{-im(\log N_+-\log N_-)}.
\]

So the direct incidence theorem is a small-value exclusion for two actual exponential-polynomial observables:

\[
Z_\alpha(m),
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha).
\]

---

# 2. Joint small-value event

The theorem to prove is equivalent to excluding

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|\le Q^{-A_Z},
\qquad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\le Q^{-A_W},
\]

at admissible packet centers.

At \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\), this reduces to

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But the direct problem is better written as:

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for all admissible ordinary packet centers.

This avoids splitting into \(|\mathbf z'|\), \(|\mathbf M|\), and angle, but it is not easier unless the pair has a special arithmetic repulsion.

---

# 3. Generic recurrence is unfavorable

Model the active prime phases as

\[
u_p(m)=p^{-im}.
\]

Let the effective prime-phase torus have dimension \(d\). The map is

\[
m\mapsto u(m)\in\mathbb T^d.
\]

The two observables are functions

\[
Z_\alpha(u),
\qquad
W(u)=\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha).
\]

If \(Z_\alpha\) and \(W\) are transverse as complex-valued functions, then the set

\[
\{|Z_\alpha|\le \varepsilon,\ |W|\le \varepsilon\}
\]

has torus measure heuristically

\[
\asymp \varepsilon^4
\]

provided it is nonempty.

Thus the expected hitting time along an equidistributed one-parameter orbit is roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-4},
\]

not \(\varepsilon^{-d}\). The larger \(\varepsilon^{-d}\) estimate applies when trying to hit a prescribed phase point, but here we only need to hit a codimension-four small-value tube.

Taking

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A}
\]

gives recurrence time

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

That is far too cheap relative to the available height range. Therefore generic recurrence strongly suggests that a pointwise incidence theorem cannot follow from dimension or transversality alone.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The determinant does not raise generic recurrence cost enough.}
}
\]

A successful theorem must use special actual-zeta arithmetic, not generic orbit recurrence.

---

# 4. Does \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) increase codimension enough?

No, not generically.

Adding \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0\) to \(Z_\alpha\approx0\) adds one complex condition. If the two functions are independent, the target is codimension four real. That still leaves a large recurrent target.

If the two functions are dependent, the situation is worse: \(W\) may be small near some \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros automatically.

Thus neither alternative gives a soft proof:

\[
\boxed{
\text{independence gives recurrence; dependence may create smallness.}
}
\]

The needed property is stronger than independence. One needs a **repulsion inequality**:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
|W(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is a special arithmetic incidence exclusion.

---

# 5. Direct resultant formulation

One may try to define an effective resultant for the pair

\[
Z_\alpha(m),
\qquad
W(m)=\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha).
\]

For finite exponential polynomials

\[
f(m)=\sum_j a_j e^{-im\omega_j},
\qquad
g(m)=\sum_k b_k e^{-im\nu_k},
\]

a resultant-style theorem would need to say:

\[
|f(m)|+|g(m)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

However, usual nonvanishing of a symbolic resultant would only imply that \(f\) and \(g\) are not identically sharing all zeros. It does not exclude approximate common zeros along a long one-parameter orbit.

For a polynomial analogy, \(\operatorname{Res}(f,g)\ne0\) can yield separation between exact roots only if one has strong coefficient height and degree control. For these exponential polynomials, the effective “degree” is the frequency diameter and subset-product count. The relevant height is enormous unless basis/amplitude normalization is built in. Even then, nonzero resultant would likely give a bound of the form

\[
\exp(-{\rm poly}(R,\log Q)),
\]

but converting that to a uniform \(Q^{-A}\) lower bound at all admissible heights appears to require exactly the missing nonrecurrence theorem.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a resultant formulation is possible, but it does not avoid actual-orbit nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel

The strongest obstruction is still phase-relaxed.

Let \(u=(u_p)_{p\in\mathcal P}\in\mathbb T^d\), and define exact-symbol surrogates

\[
Z_\alpha(u)
=
\sum_p z_p u_p+\text{dual/background},
\]

\[
W(u)
=
\sum_S C_S\prod_{p\in S}u_p
+
\text{dual/mixed/background}.
\]

Assume healthy diagnostics:

\[
\rho_{\rm rank}\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\kappa_{\rm basis}\le Q^C,
\qquad
\sum_S|C_S|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The system

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\qquad
W(u)=0
\]

is two complex equations in \(d\) phase variables. For \(d\gg4\), it is generically solvable.

Even if one also imposes healthy derivative and minor-size diagnostics,

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

the angle can be tuned so that

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

Therefore any successful theorem must exploit what this model omits:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact actual one-parameter zeta orbit and exact main/dual coefficient coupling.}
}
\]

---

# 7. One-parameter orbit obstruction

Restricting to

\[
u_p(m)=p^{-im}
\]

removes the independent phases, but not enough generically.

If the small-value set has torus measure \(\asymp Q^{-4A}\), then a generic equidistributed orbit meets it on length about

\[
Q^{4A}.
\]

This is still small compared with the ambient height range.

Therefore a direct incidence theorem must prove that the actual orbit is **not generic** with respect to this specific small-value set, or that the small-value set is empty for actual zeta coefficients.

That is a much stronger statement than Kronecker independence.

A possible theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
u(m),
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ W(u)=0\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for all admissible \(m\). But this is again an actual-orbit incidence theorem.

---

# 8. Does exact main+dual coupling help directly?

The direct pair is

\[
Z_\alpha=Z_+ + Z_- +E_Z,
\]

\[
W=W_{++\cdots+}
+
W_{--\cdots-}
+
W_{\rm mixed}
+
W_{B_2}
+
W_{E_2}.
\]

A useful obstruction would be something like:

\[
Z_++Z_-=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
W_{++\cdots+}+W_{--\cdots-}+W_{\rm mixed}\ne0.
\]

But the determinant \(W\) is multilinear in the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-rows, not a simple algebraic function of \(Z_\alpha\). The equation \(Z_++Z_-=0\) imposes one complex scalar relation among branch sums. It does not visibly force a lower bound on a high-degree subset-product determinant.

The branch separation

\[
0<c<c_1<1/2
\]

helps avoid saddle degeneracy and improves symbol rank. But it does not create sign or positivity in \(W\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact main/dual coupling does not currently yield a direct incidence proof.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Candidate theorem: actual-orbit incidence exclusion

The best direct theorem statement is:

## Actual-orbit incidence exclusion

Let

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Let \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) be formed from the full canonical AFE

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

using packet-frequency active blocks and basis-normalized operators.

Assume:

1. packet-frequency symbol rank;
2. canonical AFE derivative control;
3. ordinary-scale admissibility;
4. exclusion of saddle/transition degeneracy.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for every admissible ordinary packet center \(m\).

This theorem would close the Wronskian route.

But at present, the proof is exactly the missing actual-zeta arithmetic input.

---

# 10. No-go diagnosis

The following do not prove the direct incidence theorem:

## Codimension

Two complex small-value equations still have too large a target set.

## Generic recurrence

Expected hitting cost is polynomial in \(Q\), not prohibitive.

## Symbol rank

Prevents coefficient redundancy, not pointwise common small values.

## Basis conditioning

Removes artificial determinant losses, not actual phase cancellation.

## Mean-square determinant mass

Shows \(W\) is often large, not that it is large at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

## Main/dual branch separation

Improves rank and avoids saddle overlap, but does not give sign or repulsion.

## Nonzero resultant in a formal sense

At best shows no common factor / no identical vanishing. It does not exclude approximate common zeros along a long orbit.

---

# 11. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Direct actual-orbit incidence remains open and is the core arithmetic theorem.}
}
\]

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Generic recurrence makes the theorem implausible without special actual-zeta repulsion.}
}
\]

The ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route is structurally coherent, but the final step must be a genuinely arithmetic statement:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or equivalently

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

I do not see a proof from current Wronskian algebra, main/dual bookkeeping, or recurrence heuristics. The theorem must use a new actual-zeta nonrecurrence/repulsion input.
