## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:46:14)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 3 / C — Cell-sum non-cancellation via explicit formula / prime statistics

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: recast the multiblock cell-sum theorem as an explicit-formula / prime-statistic lower-bound problem. The current shared target is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

with multiblock packet-frequency support

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+\frac{KQ}{R},
\qquad K\ge 8.
\]

This is now the smallest concrete arithmetic unlock for proving \(|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}\). 

---

# 1. Cell projections as packet-frequency test functions

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

On the main packet-frequency branch,

\[
F^+(t)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_K^+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-itx_n^+},
\]

where

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

Let \(\chi_r(x)\) be a smooth partition of unity on the multiblock packet-frequency interval. Define

\[
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_n
\chi_r(x_n^+)
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Similarly, for the folded dual branch,

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-(m_0)
=
\sum_n
\chi_r(x_n^-)
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The full cell sum is

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Thus \((B_r)_r\) is the vector of smooth packet-frequency projections of \(Z_\alpha\)’s AFE coefficients.

---

# 2. Prime-statistic form of the cell mass

The cell mass is

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2.
\]

Ignoring dual/background/error for the moment, the main-main part is

\[
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{n,n'}
\chi_r(x_n)\chi_r(x_{n'})
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0(\log n-\log n')}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2
=
\sum_{n,n'}
W(x_n,x_{n'})
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')},
}
\]

where

\[
W(x,x')=\sum_r\chi_r(x)\chi_r(x').
\]

The diagonal contribution is

\[
\sum_n W(x_n,x_n)|z_n|^2
\asymp
\sum_n |z_n|^2.
\]

The off-diagonal contribution is

\[
\sum_{n\ne n'}
W(x_n,x_{n'})
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

So the desired lower bound is a **localized bilinear prime/AFE statistic**:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{n,n'}
W(x_n,x_{n'})
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

For the full main+dual object, one gets four terms:

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2
=
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2
+
\sum_r|B_r^-|^2
+
2\Re\left(e^{-i\Theta_Z}\sum_rB_r^+\overline{B_r^-}\right)
+
\text{bg/error}.
\]

The hard term is the main-dual cross term:

\[
2\Re\left(e^{-i\Theta_Z}\sum_rB_r^+\overline{B_r^-}\right).
\]

A sufficient theorem is:

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2+\sum_r|B_r^-|^2
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\left|
\sum_rB_r^+\overline{B_r^-}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A'})
\left(\sum_r|B_r^+|^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\sum_r|B_r^-|^2\right)^{1/2},
\]

unless one branch is already dominant.

---

# 3. Explicit-formula interpretation

Each cell projection is a Dirichlet-polynomial statistic with a packet-frequency cutoff:

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_n
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)
\chi_r(\lambda\log n)
n^{-im_0}.
\]

This can be viewed as the prime-side transform of a test function whose Fourier transform is localized near the cell \(I_r\).

Formally, if \(h_r\) is a test function satisfying

\[
\widehat h_r(\lambda\log n)\approx \chi_r(\lambda\log n),
\]

then the explicit formula gives a zero-side statistic of the form

\[
\sum_\rho h_r(\gamma_\rho-m_0)
=
\text{gamma/trivial terms}
-
2\Re\sum_n
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-im_0}
\widehat h_r(\log n)
+
\text{tail/error}.
\]

The cell sum \(B_r\) is not literally \(\Lambda(n)n^{-1/2}\)-weighted unless \(Z_\alpha\)’s AFE coefficients match the explicit-formula coefficients, but it is the same structural object: a localized prime-frequency projection.

Therefore the cell-sum theorem is equivalent to saying:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\text{ cannot make every packet-frequency prime projection }B_r
\text{ small.}
}
\]

In zero-side language, this is a statement that the zero condition does not annihilate the whole packet-frequency response vector.

---

# 4. Diagonal lower bound and off-diagonal obstruction

The optimistic second-moment calculation is:

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2
=
\sum_n|z_n|^2
+
\text{off-diagonal}.
\]

If the off-diagonal were small, we would get immediately

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2\gg \sum_n|z_n|^2.
\]

The problem is that \(m_0\) is not averaged. It is fixed and conditioned by

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

The zero condition is

\[
\sum_r B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}\sum_r B_r^-
+
B^{\rm bg}
+
B^E
\approx0.
\]

This cancels only the total sum over cells, but in a phase-relaxed model one can impose all cell sums small:

\[
B_r\approx0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

Thus the off-diagonal obstruction is exactly actual prime-log recurrence inside each cell.

A sufficient lower-bound theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{n\in I_r}
z_n e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_n|z_n|^2
}
\]

for all admissible \(m_0\) satisfying \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\).

This is a **cellwise Dirichlet-polynomial large-sieve lower bound at a fixed point**.

---

# 5. Can the explicit formula provide the lower bound?

A plausible route is to square and sum the cell projections:

\[
\mathcal C(m_0)=\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2.
\]

Then try to express \(\mathcal C\) by the explicit formula or by a mollified second moment.

The diagonal part is positive. The off-diagonal part has frequencies

\[
\log(n/n').
\]

If one had an average over \(m_0\), the off-diagonal would be small. But the theorem is pointwise at a zero of \(Z_\alpha\).

To use the explicit formula, one would need either:

1. an argument-principle sampling over \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros;
2. a zero-set large sieve for the cell projections;
3. a positivity identity for \(\sum_r|B_r|^2\) at a zero;
4. or a main/dual obstruction preventing all cells from cancelling.

None is currently available as a soft consequence.

So the explicit formula does not close the theorem by itself. It reformulates the target as a localized prime-vector nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 6. Relation to the zero-set large sieve for \(\mathbf M\)

The cell-sum theorem and the \(\mathbf M\)-large-sieve theorem have a common form, but different frequency complexity.

## Cell-sum problem

Frequencies:

\[
\omega_n=\log n.
\]

Cell projections group the linear frequencies into packet-frequency cells.

## \(\mathbf M\) problem

Frequencies:

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S=\sum_{n\in S}\log n,
\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

These are subset-product frequencies.

Thus the cell-sum theorem is the **degree-one** version of the zero-set spectral problem, while the \(\mathbf M\)-large-sieve theorem is the **degree-\(R+1\)** exterior-product version.

This makes the cell-sum theorem substantially narrower.

A possible unifying theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zeros of }Z_\alpha
\text{ are spectrally nonconcentrated for packet-frequency polynomial lifts up to degree }R+1.
}
\]

But proving the degree-one case first is the reasonable next target.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed no-go

In a relaxed model, choose independent phases inside each cell. Then for each \(r\), one can solve

\[
B_r
=
\sum_{x_n\in I_r} z_n e^{-i\theta_n}
=0
\]

provided the cell contains enough terms and no single coefficient dominates.

This gives

\[
B_r=0
\quad\forall r,
\]

and hence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=\sum_rB_r=0.
\]

Therefore the theorem is false in the phase-relaxed model.

The actual theorem must use the one-parameter constraint:

\[
\theta_n=m_0\log n,
\]

with fixed actual logarithms and coefficients.

Thus the core missing arithmetic is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the one-parameter prime-log orbit cannot hit the product of cellwise cancellation sets at a }Z_\alpha\text{-zero.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Recurrence cost for the cell-flat variety

Let there be \(M\) cells. Requiring

\[
B_r\approx0
\qquad 1\le r\le M
\]

is \(M\) complex conditions. This is much higher codimension than the scalar zero condition.

This is why the multiblock formulation is promising.

If \(M\asymp K\) with \(K=8\), then the target has real codimension about

\[
2M\asymp16,
\]

rather than \(2\). A generic orbit hitting cost becomes

\[
\varepsilon^{-2M},
\]

which can be meaningfully larger.

This is a key distinction from the full incidence theorem, where adding one determinant condition only gave codimension four. The multiblock cell theorem may genuinely raise recurrence cost.

However, this heuristic only helps if:

1. the cells are genuinely independent;
2. the one-parameter orbit sees them as independent enough;
3. the cell-flat set is not enlarged by main/dual dependencies;
4. \(K\) is large enough that \(\varepsilon^{-2K}\) exceeds the admissible height budget.

So the cell theorem is more promising than the full incidence theorem as a first arithmetic target.

---

# 9. Candidate theorem

## Multiblock cell-sum nonrecurrence theorem

Let

\[
\mathcal B_K=\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+KQ/R\},
\qquad K\ge8,
\]

and partition

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

into \(M\asymp K\) cells of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\).

Let

\[
B_r(m)
=
B_r^+(m)
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}B_r^-(m)
+
B_r^{\rm bg}(m)
+
B_r^E(m).
\]

Assume:

1. no cell coefficient dominance;
2. each cell has coefficient mass \(\ge Q^{-C}\);
3. AFE bg/error terms are \(Q^{-C}\)-controlled;
4. main/dual folded contributions do not perfectly pairwise cancel cell-by-cell.

Then for every admissible ordinary \(Z_\alpha\)-zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{r=1}^{M}|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This implies polylog-local amplitude and hence

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

The nontrivial input is the actual one-parameter nonrecurrence against the product of cell-flat constraints.

---

# 10. What an explicit-formula proof would need

An explicit-formula proof should produce a positive statistic

\[
\mathcal C(m)=\sum_r|B_r(m)|^2
\]

and show that at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros,

\[
\mathcal C(m)\not\approx0.
\]

A sufficient zero-set averaged version is:

\[
\sum_{Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}\mathcal C(m_j)
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}.
\]

Using the argument principle, this becomes

\[
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int
\mathcal C(s)
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
\]

The diagonal of \(\mathcal C\) should be positive. The off-diagonal requires control of sums involving

\[
e^{-is\log(n/n')}\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s).
\]

This is a concrete explicit-formula/zero-statistics problem. It is likely easier than the subset-product \(\mathbf M\) version because the frequencies are only \(\log(n/n')\), not \(\log(N_S/N_T)\).

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The cell-sum theorem can be recast as a degree-one zero-set large-sieve / prime-statistic lower bound.}
}
\]

This is meaningfully narrower than the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve and the full Wronskian incidence theorem.

But it is still not automatic. In phase-relaxed models, all cell sums can be made zero. Therefore the proof must use actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.

The most promising theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
B_r^+(m_0)+e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B_r^-(m_0)
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently: the scalar zero condition may cancel the total packet sum, but actual zeta arithmetic prevents simultaneous cancellation in all multiblock packet-frequency cells.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:49:06)

_Thought for a few seconds_

## Agent 3 / C — Phase-relaxed and one-parameter adversarial analysis

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: try to break the fixed-width multiblock cell-sum theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

using phase-relaxed and one-parameter adversarial models. The current prompt identifies this theorem as the smallest ordinary-route unlock for proving \(|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}\). 

---

# 1. Target failure

Use fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Then

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\in[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2),
\]

and cells have width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Thus

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

The bad event is

\[
B_r(m_0)\approx0
\qquad
\text{for every }r,
\]

where

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Since

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=\sum_r B_r(m_0),
\]

cell-flatness is much stronger than the scalar zero condition.

---

# 2. Phase-relaxed construction

In the phase-relaxed model, assign independent phases

\[
u_n=e^{-i\theta_n}
\]

inside each cell. The main-branch cell sum is

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{n\in I_r}
z_n^+u_n.
\]

If a cell contains at least two comparable terms and no coefficient dominates the sum of the others, then one can choose phases so that

\[
B_r^+=0.
\]

More generally, the polygon condition suffices:

\[
\max_{n\in I_r}|z_n^+|
\le
\sum_{n'\in I_r,\ n'\ne n}|z_{n'}^+|.
\]

On fixed-width packet-frequency support, each cell contains many terms, so this condition should hold generically.

Therefore, in the phase-relaxed main-only model,

\[
B_r^+=0
\quad\forall r
\]

is feasible.

This gives

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2=0,
\]

and hence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=\sum_rB_r^+=0.
\]

So the theorem is false in the phase-relaxed model.

This confirms the expected conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any proof must use actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Adding reflected/folded dual constraints

Now include the full cell sum

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

In a phase-relaxed two-branch model, with independent main and dual phases, each cell equation is

\[
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-=0.
\]

This is even easier to satisfy: one can choose \(B_r^+\) and \(B_r^-\) to cancel cellwise.

If main and dual magnitudes are imbalanced in some cell, the larger branch alone may not be exactly cancellable by the smaller, but each branch has internal phase freedom. Unless one branch has a single dominant coefficient, the cellwise vector polygon remains flexible.

Thus reflected/folded dual structure does **not** rescue the theorem in the relaxed model.

\[
\boxed{
\text{main+dual relaxed cell-flatness is feasible.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Imposing actual one-parameter phases

The real constraint is

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Now each cell condition is one complex equation:

\[
B_r(m)
=
\sum_{n\in I_r}
z_n e^{-im\log n}
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}
\sum_{n\in I_r^-}
z_n^-e^{+im\log n}
+
\cdots
\approx0.
\]

For

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

cells, the cell-flat target has approximately

\[
2M_{\rm cell}\asymp 2R
\]

real scalar conditions.

This is a much higher codimension target than the scalar zero condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0,
\]

which is only two real conditions.

A generic recurrence estimate for hitting

\[
|B_r(m)|\le \varepsilon
\quad\forall r
\]

is roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-2M_{\rm cell}}.
\]

Taking

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

the hitting cost is

\[
Q^{A\cdot 2R}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is much more expensive than direct incidence codimension-four recurrence, which cost only \(Q^{O(1)}\).

Thus the cell-sum theorem is substantially more plausible than the full Wronskian incidence theorem as a first arithmetic target.

---

# 5. Comparison with direct jet-flatness

The direct jet-flat event is

\[
F^{(k)}(0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le k\le R+1.
\]

In packet-frequency variables,

\[
F^{(k)}(0)
=
(-i)^k\sum_n b_n x_n^k.
\]

This is \(R+2\) complex moment conditions, or roughly

\[
2R+4
\]

real conditions.

The cell-flat event with

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

also imposes

\[
2R
\]

real conditions.

So direct jet-flatness and multiblock cell-flatness have comparable codimension.

However, cell-flatness has two advantages:

1. It is geometrically localized in frequency cells.
2. It is directly connected to local \(L^2\) amplitude.

Jet-flatness has one advantage:

1. It is exactly the derivative vector condition.

In a relaxed model, both can be forced. On the actual one-parameter orbit, both are high-codimension nonrecurrence problems.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell-sum non-cancellation is comparable to direct jet nonflatness, but more analyzable.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Comparison with full Wronskian incidence

Full Wronskian incidence asks for exclusion of

\[
Z_\alpha(m)\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

This is only two complex small-value constraints:

\[
\text{codimension }4.
\]

Generic recurrence cost:

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

By contrast, cell-flatness imposes roughly \(R\) complex constraints:

\[
B_r(m)\approx0
\quad
1\le r\le M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

Generic recurrence cost:

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

So the cell theorem is **strictly easier to believe** than the final incidence theorem, because its bad set is much thinner.

This matches the numerical evidence: the optimizer could force \(Z_\alpha\) very small, but not cell-mass collapse.

---

# 7. Is the recurrence cost high enough?

This depends on the admissible height budget.

If the relevant search height is exponentially large in \(Q\), e.g.

\[
m\le e^Q,
\]

then

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right)
\]

is still much smaller than \(e^Q\).

So a purely generic recurrence-cost argument may still not prove the theorem globally.

But the cell-flat target is much smaller than the scalar-zero target, and the actual one-parameter phases are not arbitrary independent cell variables. A proof still needs actual arithmetic, but the theorem is plausibly closer.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{recurrence heuristics support cell-sum theorem as easier, but do not prove it.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Strongest actual-orbit adversary

The strongest possible countermechanism would be:

1. Choose \(m\) so that within each cell,

   \[
   \sum_{n\in I_r}z_ne^{-im\log n}\approx0.
   \]

2. Simultaneously match the folded dual phase so

   \[
   B_r^++e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-\approx0.
   \]

3. Keep \(m>50\), avoid \(m=0\) artifacts, and remain in the AFE plateau.

This is a system of \(R\)-many cell equations for one variable \(m\). Generic recurrence says such points may exist at very large heights, but the packet-frequency determinant tests did not find them in the tested ranges.

To make this into a real counterexample, one would need exhibit a sequence \(m_j\) such that the actual prime-log orbit approaches the product cell-flat variety to polynomial precision in \(Q\). I do not see such a construction.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no credible actual-orbit countermechanism is currently visible.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Theorem candidate

A reasonable theorem target is:

## Multiblock cell-sum nonrecurrence

Let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

and partition

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

into

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

cells of width

\[
\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define

\[
B_r(m)
=
B_r^+(m)
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}B_r^-(m)
+
B_r^{\rm bg}(m)
+
B_r^E(m).
\]

Then for every admissible ordinary \(Z_\alpha\)-zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{r=1}^{M_{\rm cell}}|B_r(m_0)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the actual one-parameter zeta orbit avoids the product cell-flat variety

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:B_r(u)=0\ \forall r\}
\]

to polynomial accuracy at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed cell-flatness is easy, but actual-orbit cell-flatness is high-codimension and currently unbroken.}
}
\]

The multiblock cell theorem is:

- false in phase-relaxed models;
- not proved by generic recurrence;
- much thinner than full Wronskian incidence;
- comparable to direct \(R\)-jet nonflatness;
- empirically supported by the K=8 multiblock runs;
- currently the most plausible first arithmetic theorem to attack.

Final classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-orbit cell-sum theorem: plausible Yellow, not Green.}
}
\]

It is the right next target for proving

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]
## User (2026-04-27 06:51:32)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:51:38)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 3 / C — Same-cell off-diagonal control

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: attack the fixed-width multiblock cell theorem through the expansion of same-cell diagonal and off-diagonal terms. The target theorem is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The current prompt frames this as the smallest ordinary-route arithmetic unlock for proving \(|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}\). 

---

# 1. Main-branch expansion

Use fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
x_n^+\in[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2),
\]

and partition into cells

\[
I_r,\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

The main-branch cell sum is

\[
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n,n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

Split this as

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2
=
D_+
+
O_+,
}
\]

where

\[
D_+
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}|z_n^+|^2
\]

is the positive diagonal and

\[
O_+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\]

is the same-cell off-diagonal.

A sufficient main-only theorem is

\[
|O_+|\le (1-Q^{-C})D_+,
\]

which would imply

\[
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2\ge Q^{-C}D_+.
\]

The physical scale of \(D_+\) depends on the AFE normalization, but after amplitude normalization the desired lower bound is

\[
D_+\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 2. Dual and main-dual terms

The folded dual cell sum is

\[
B_r^-(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n},
\]

with

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}.
\]

The full canonical cell sum is

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Ignoring background/error temporarily,

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2
=
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2
+
\sum_r|B_r^-|^2
+
2\Re\left(
e^{-i\Theta_Z}
\sum_r B_r^+\overline{B_r^-}
\right).
\]

Define

\[
D_-=\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}|z_n^-|^2,
\]

\[
O_-=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^-,x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^-\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{+im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_r|B_r^-|^2=D_-+O_-.
\]

The main-dual cross term is

\[
C_{+-}
=
\sum_r B_r^+\overline{B_r^-}
\]

or explicitly

\[
C_{+-}
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-im_0\log n'}.
\]

The full expansion is therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r|^2
=
D_++D_-
+
O_++O_-
+
2\Re(e^{-i\Theta_Z}C_{+-})
+
\text{bg/error}.
}
\]

A sufficient full theorem is

\[
O_++O_-+2\Re(e^{-i\Theta_Z}C_{+-})
\ge
-(1-Q^{-C})(D_++D_-),
\]

with background/error controlled by

\[
\sum_r|B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E|^2
+
2\sum_r|B_r^++B_r^-|\,|B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E|
\le Q^{-C}(D_++D_-).
\]

---

# 3. Can \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) force every off-diagonal to cancel the diagonal?

The scalar zero condition is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_r B_r(m_0)
\approx0.
\]

This is one complex condition:

\[
\sum_r B_r=0.
\]

It does **not** algebraically imply

\[
B_r\approx0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

For the off-diagonal terms to cancel the diagonal in every cell, one needs approximately

\[
|B_r|^2\ll Q^{-A}
\qquad\forall r,
\]

which means

\[
B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^- \approx0
\]

cell by cell. This is \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\) complex constraints.

Thus the obstruction is not algebraic. It is arithmetic/dynamical:

\[
m_0\mapsto
\left(B_r(m_0)\right)_{r=1}^{M_{\rm cell}}
\]

must hit a high-codimension cell-flat variety while also satisfying

\[
\sum_rB_r(m_0)=0.
\]

That is much thinner than the scalar zero condition.

---

# 4. Fixed-\(m_0\) same-cell large-sieve theorem candidate

The desired theorem can be formulated as a fixed-point lower frame inequality.

## Same-cell large-sieve candidate

Let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q\},
\]

and let \(I_r\) be cells of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\) in \(x=\lambda\log n\). Define

\[
B_r(m)
=
B_r^+(m)
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m)}B_r^-(m)
+
B_r^{\rm bg}(m)
+
B_r^E(m).
\]

Assume:

1. AFE plateau support, away from saddle:
   \[
   0<c_-<c_+<1/2.
   \]

2. Cell mass nondegeneracy:
   \[
   D_r^+ + D_r^- :=
   \sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}|z_n^+|^2
   +
   \sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}|z_n^-|^2
   \ge Q^{-C}D_{\rm avg}
   \]
   for most cells.

3. No cell-dominant coefficient:
   \[
   \max_{x_n\in I_r}|z_n^\pm|^2
   \le Q^{-C}
   \sum_{x_n\in I_r}|z_n^\pm|^2.
   \]

4. Canonical background/error:
   \[
   \sum_r|B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E|^2\le Q^{-C}.
   \]

Then for every admissible \(m_0\) with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is exactly the fixed-\(m_0\) same-cell large-sieve lower bound needed.

But the actual proof must control

\[
O_++O_-+2\Re(e^{-i\Theta_Z}C_{+-}).
\]

---

# 5. Why ordinary large sieve does not immediately apply

A standard large sieve gives bounds after averaging over \(m\):

\[
\int_J
\sum_r|B_r(m)|^2\,dm
\]

or after averaging over a family of phases.

But here \(m=m_0\) is fixed and constrained by

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

At one fixed point, the off-diagonal terms

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\]

can in principle align adversarially. The condition \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) only controls the global sum, not the same-cell off-diagonal phases.

Therefore a proof needs a nonrecurrence statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual prime-log phases cannot make all same-cell sums small at a }Z_\alpha\text{-zero}.
}
\]

This is not a standard large sieve.

---

# 6. Same-cell off-diagonal obstruction

For one cell \(I_r\), define

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{n\in I_r} a_n e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
|B_r^+|^2
=
\sum_{n\in I_r}|a_n|^2
+
\sum_{n\ne n'\in I_r}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

The off-diagonal can cancel the diagonal exactly if the vector sum closes polygonally:

\[
\sum_{n\in I_r} a_n e^{-im_0\log n}=0.
\]

In a phase-relaxed model this is easy.

With actual phases, cancellation in one cell is one complex condition. Cancellation in all \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\) cells is \(R\) complex conditions. This is the key high-codimension feature.

Thus a recurrence heuristic says cell-flatness is far less likely than scalar zero:

\[
\text{scalar zero: codim }2,
\]

\[
\text{cell flat: codim }2R.
\]

But recurrence heuristic is not a proof.

---

# 7. Main-dual cross term as the hard obstruction

Even if we prove

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sum_r|B_r^-|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

the full cell mass can be small if

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-
\]

as vectors in \(\ell^2_r\).

So one needs either:

## Branch dominance

\[
\|B^+\|_2
\ge
(1+Q^{-C})\|B^-\|_2
\]

or vice versa; then

\[
\|B^++e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge Q^{-C}\max(\|B^+\|_2,\|B^-\|_2).
\]

## Branch nonalignment

\[
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-C})\|B^+\|_2\|B^-\|_2.
\]

The hard regime is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

where branch weights are most symmetric. In that regime, branch dominance is unlikely. One needs branch nonalignment.

This is a folded main/dual cell-vector nonrecurrence theorem, but it is still easier than full Wronskian incidence because it concerns degree-one cell vectors, not degree-\(R+1\) subset-products.

---

# 8. Candidate two-stage theorem

A useful decomposition is:

## Stage 1: branch cell mass

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

## Stage 2: branch nonalignment

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
(\|B^+\|_2+\|B^-\|_2).
}
\]

Together they imply

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Stage 1 is same-branch nonrecurrence.  
Stage 2 is main-dual cellwise nonalignment.

Both are degree-one actual-orbit statements.

---

# 9. What would prove Stage 1?

Stage 1 would follow if, for at least one branch,

\[
\sum_r|B_r^\pm|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A sufficient condition is:

\[
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n^\pm\in I_r}
z_n^\pm e^{\mp im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is equivalent to saying the actual one-parameter orbit avoids the product of branch-cell cancellation sets.

Generic recurrence cost:

\[
Q^{O(R)}.
\]

No soft proof is visible, but this is the narrowed arithmetic statement.

---

# 10. What would prove Stage 2?

Stage 2 would follow from a cell-vector angle bound:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})\|B^+\|_2\|B^-\|_2.
}
\]

In expanded form,

\[
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-im_0\log n'}.
\]

This is a folded main/dual bilinear exponential sum. Branch separation helps because \(x^+\) and \(x^-\) come from separated regions of the conductor, but it does not automatically give orthogonality at one fixed \(m_0\).

Again, this is actual prime-log nonrecurrence.

---

# 11. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-cell off-diagonal control reduces to degree-one actual-orbit nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

What we can say positively:

1. The diagonal terms are robust:
   \[
   D_++D_-\ge Q^{-C}
   \]
   after normalization.

2. Scalar zero only imposes:
   \[
   \sum_rB_r=0,
   \]
   not \(B_r=0\) cellwise.

3. Cell-flatness imposes \(R\)-many complex constraints and is much thinner than scalar zero or full Wronskian codimension-four incidence.

4. The target is therefore much more plausible than the final angle theorem.

What remains open:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove the actual prime-log orbit avoids simultaneous same-cell cancellation at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

A good theorem target is the two-stage statement:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}(\|B^+\|_2+\|B^-\|_2).
\]

Together they prove the fixed-width multiblock cell-sum theorem and hence the \(|\mathbf z'|\) lower bound.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:54:18)

_Thought for 4s_

## Agent 3 / C — Zero-conditioned cell large sieve

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: formulate and test an averaged zero-set version of the fixed-width cell theorem,

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J),
\]

as a degree-one precursor to the later \(\mathbf M\) zero-set large sieve. 

---

# 1. Setup

Use fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n},
\]

and partition the fixed \(x\)-interval into cells

\[
I_r,\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

The main cell sum is

\[
B_r^+(m)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For the dual branch,

\[
B_r^-(m)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}.
\]

The full cell vector is

\[
B_r(m)
=
B_r^+(m)
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m,\alpha)}B_r^-(m)
+
B_r^{\rm bg}(m)
+
B_r^E(m).
\]

The desired zero-conditioned averaged theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
}
\]

This is weaker than the pointwise theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\Rightarrow |B(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but it is a natural large-sieve formulation.

---

# 2. Zero-sampling kernel

Define

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

Then

\[
K_J(0)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)
\asymp
N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]

assuming \(w_J\) is nonnegative and adapted to \(J\).

For the main branch,

\[
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)|B^+(m_j)|_2^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n,n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\]

up to the mild \(m\)-dependence of AFE amplitudes.

Split this as

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)|B^+(m_j)|_2^2
=
K_J(0)\sum_n|z_n^+|^2
+
\mathcal O_{+}^{\rm zero}.
}
\]

The zero-set off-diagonal is

\[
\mathcal O_{+}^{\rm zero}
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
K_J(\log n-\log n').
\]

Similarly,

\[
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)|B^-(m_j)|_2^2
=
K_J(0)\sum_n|z_n^-|^2
+
\mathcal O_{-}^{\rm zero}.
\]

The main-dual cross term is

\[
2\Re
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)
e^{-i\Theta_Z(m_j,\alpha)}
\langle B^+(m_j),B^-(m_j)\rangle.
\]

At principal phase level this contains kernels of the form

\[
K_J(\log n+\log n')
\]

or gamma-shifted variants because

\[
B^+\sim e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
\overline{B^-}\sim e^{-im\log n'}.
\]

Thus the full zero-set large sieve requires kernel control at three families of frequencies:

\[
\boxed{
\log(n/n'),\qquad
-\log(n/n'),\qquad
\log(nn')
}
\]

plus folded gamma-phase perturbations.

---

# 3. Operator inequality needed

Let the coefficient vector for the main branch be indexed by pairs \((r,n)\) with \(x_n\in I_r\). The sampled quadratic form is governed by the matrix

\[
\mathcal K_{n,n'}
=
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\mathbf 1_{x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r\text{ for some }r}.
\]

The needed lower-frame inequality is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n,n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_n|z_n|^2.
}
\]

A sufficient operator estimate is

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\frac{K_J(\log n-\log n')}{K_J(0)}
\right)_{\substack{n,n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
-
I
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
1-Q^{-A}
}
\]

on each cell, and then summed over cells.

For the full main+dual cell vector, the lower-frame matrix is block-structured:

\[
\mathcal K_{\rm full}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal K_{++} & \mathcal K_{+-}\\
\mathcal K_{-+} & \mathcal K_{--}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

with

\[
\mathcal K_{++}:K_J(\log n-\log n'),
\]

\[
\mathcal K_{--}:K_J(-\log n+\log n'),
\]

\[
\mathcal K_{+-}:K_J(\log n+\log n')\text{ with gamma phase},
\]

and similarly for \(\mathcal K_{-+}\).

The full theorem requires

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal K_{\rm full}\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

on the actual AFE coefficient subspace, after including background/error perturbation bounds.

---

# 4. Argument-principle expression for \(K_J\)

Formally,

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

If \(Z_\alpha\) is analytically continued and the zeros in \(J\) are captured by a rectangle \(\mathcal R\), then

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\mathcal R}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]

modulo boundary smoothing and possible zeros/poles outside the intended strip.

This is the main possible analytic route.

Using an explicit-formula expansion for

\[
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s)
\]

would convert the kernel into prime-side sums.

For \(\xi=0\), the integral gives the zero count:

\[
K_J(0)\asymp N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

For \(\xi\ne0\), one needs cancellation:

\[
|K_J(\xi)|\ll K_J(0)
\]

or, more realistically, an operator-level large-sieve bound over the relevant frequency set.

---

# 5. Obstacles in the argument-principle route

## 5.1 Poles near the contour

The logarithmic derivative

\[
Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha
\]

has poles at zeros. A contour too close to zeros gives large contributions. A Cartan contour or zero-avoiding boundary is required.

Thus the zero-set large sieve depends on the same microscopic zero-control issues that appear in the \(|\mathbf z'|\) lane.

## 5.2 Nonanalytic absolute values

The target is

\[
|B(m_j)|_2^2.
\]

To use the argument principle, replace this by an analytic surrogate:

\[
B(s)\,B^\#(s),
\qquad
B^\#(s)=\overline{B(\overline{s})}.
\]

This doubles the frequency family and introduces mixed signs. It is manageable, but the resulting kernel includes both ratio and product frequencies.

## 5.3 No automatic diagonal dominance

The argument-principle formula gives a representation of \(K_J(\xi)\), but not automatically a diagonal main term. To prove a lower-frame inequality, one needs a pair-correlation-type statement for zeros of \(Z_\alpha\):

\[
K_J(\xi)\text{ is small for nonzero relevant }\xi
\]

in the operator sense.

This is a genuine zero-statistics theorem, not a formal consequence of the argument principle.

---

# 6. Comparison with the later \(\mathbf M\) large sieve

The cell large sieve is the degree-one version.

Cell frequencies:

\[
\omega_n=\log n.
\]

Cell kernel differences:

\[
\omega_n-\omega_{n'}=\log(n/n').
\]

For the cofactor vector,

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S},
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S.
\]

The \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve involves

\[
\Omega_S-\Omega_T
=
\log(N_S/N_T).
\]

This is the degree-\((R+1)\) subset-product lift of the degree-one problem.

Thus the cell large sieve is substantially narrower:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell large sieve: frequencies }\log(n/n'),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf M\text{ large sieve: frequencies }\log(N_S/N_T).
}
\]

A proof of the cell large sieve would not automatically prove the \(\mathbf M\) large sieve, but it would be a major prototype.

---

# 7. Does averaged zero-set cell mass imply pointwise cell mass?

Not by itself.

The averaged theorem

\[
\sum_{m_j\in J}
|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]

implies at least one zero in \(J\) has non-small cell mass, and that most zeros cannot all be extremely bad.

But the Wronskian route may require the specific admissible zero \(m_0\). Therefore an averaged theorem is insufficient unless the proof can choose a good zero, or unless it is strengthened to a local/windowed version around each admissible \(m_0\).

The needed local version is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\substack{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\\ |m_j-m_0|\le L}}
w\!\left(\frac{m_j-m_0}{L}\right)
|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-L,m_0+L])
}
\]

for windows small enough that a bad admissible zero cannot be isolated.

Even then, to get pointwise non-smallness at \(m_0\), one needs an exclusion of isolated bad zeros or a continuity/repulsion argument.

So the zero-set large sieve is a useful averaged input, but the pointwise cell theorem remains stronger.

---

# 8. Candidate theorem

## Zero-conditioned cell large sieve

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J=\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}.
\]

Let \(B(m)\) be the fixed-width multiblock cell vector for the full canonical \(Z_\alpha\)-AFE.

Assume:

1. \(Z_\alpha\) has controlled zero density in \(J\);
2. the zero-sampling kernel satisfies the block operator estimate

\[
\mathcal K_{\rm full}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
\]

on the packet-frequency cell coefficient space;

3. canonical background/error cell contributions are \(Q^{-C}\)-small or absorbed into the coefficient vector.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
}
\]

A pointwise corollary requires an additional local nonconcentration principle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{bad zeros with }|B(m_j)|_2<Q^{-A}
\text{ cannot occur isolated inside admissible packets.}
}
\]

---

# 9. No-go diagnosis

The following are insufficient:

## Continuous \(L^2\) in \(m\)

It does not control sampling at zeros.

## Diagonal coefficient mass

It does not control zero-set off-diagonals.

## Scalar zero condition

\[
\sum_r B_r=0
\]

does not imply cellwise lower bounds.

## Argument principle alone

It expresses \(K_J\), but controlling it requires bounds on \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\) and zero correlations.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-conditioned cell large sieve is a genuine actual-zeta zero-statistics theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The zero-conditioned cell large sieve is a useful averaged prototype, but it does not replace the pointwise cell theorem.}
}
\]

It is easier than the later \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve because it involves degree-one frequencies \(\log(n/n')\), not subset-product frequencies \(\log(N_S/N_T)\).

A successful theorem here would strongly support the cell route and may supply methods for \(\mathbf M\), but the exact pointwise theorem still needs actual-orbit cell nonrecurrence:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Thus this lane reduces to a degree-one zero-set spectral large sieve plus a local bad-zero exclusion principle.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:57:59)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 3 / C — Easy \(\alpha\)-tilted branch

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: analyze the easier regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q
\]

where the expectation is that one AFE branch dominates, preventing main/dual cell-vector cancellation once same-branch mass is known. 

---

# 1. Objective

We want to control

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-,
\]

where

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The desired nonalignment/dominance estimate is

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\left(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\right).
}
\]

In the tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q,
\]

the hope is that one branch has polynomially larger coefficient mass than the other, so cancellation is impossible.

---

# 2. Main/dual coefficient ratio

On packet-frequency support, write

\[
u=\log n,
\qquad
u^-=\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}.
\]

The main branch contains an \(\alpha\)-weight of the form

\[
e^{-\alpha u},
\]

while the folded dual branch contains the complementary weight

\[
e^{+\alpha u^-},
\]

up to AFE smoothing, gamma factors, and conductor-normalizing amplitudes.

In normalized packet coordinates,

\[
x^+=\lambda u,
\qquad
x^-=\lambda u^-.
\]

Since

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and packet-frequency blocks have

\[
u\asymp Q,\qquad u^-\asymp Q,
\]

we have

\[
x^+,x^-\asymp1.
\]

The cellwise main/dual coefficient ratio is therefore schematically

\[
\frac{|z_n^+|}{|z_n^-|}
\approx
\exp\{-\alpha u-\alpha u^-\}^{\phantom{1}}
\times
\frac{A_+(u)}{A_-(u^-)}
\times
\Gamma_{\rm ratio}(m_0,\alpha),
\]

depending on the exact normalization of \(Z_\alpha\). Equivalently, after absorbing smooth branch factors,

\[
\log\frac{|z^+|}{|z^-|}
=
-\alpha(u+u^-)
+
O(1)
+
\log\frac{A_+}{A_-}.
\]

Because

\[
u+u^-
=
\log n+\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}
=
\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi}
\asymp Q,
\]

the \(\alpha\)-tilt produces the factor

\[
\boxed{
\left|\log\frac{|z^+|}{|z^-|}\right|
\asymp
|\alpha|Q
}
\]

away from AFE transition regions.

Thus if

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C\log Q,
\]

one expects

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z^+|}{|z^-|}
\ge Q^{c}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
\ge Q^{c},
}
\]

depending on the sign convention for \(\alpha\).

This is the desired branch dominance mechanism.

---

# 3. Branch dominance theorem candidate

Assume cells are chosen away from saddle and AFE transition regions:

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12.
\]

Assume the AFE smoothing and gamma ratios satisfy

\[
Q^{-C_0}
\le
\left|
\frac{A_+(u)\Gamma_+(m,\alpha)}
     {A_-(u^-)\Gamma_-(m,\alpha)}
\right|
\le
Q^{C_0}
\]

on the chosen support.

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\]

with \(C_1\) sufficiently larger than \(C_0\), then one branch dominates coefficientwise:

\[
\boxed{
|z_n^+|
\ge
Q^{c}|z_{n'}^-|
}
\]

for corresponding folded cells, or the reverse.

More invariantly,

\[
\boxed{
D_+
=
\sum_r\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}|z_n^+|^2
\ge
Q^{c}D_-
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
D_-
\ge
Q^{c}D_+.
}
\]

Here

\[
D_\pm=\sum_r D_r^\pm
\]

are the branch diagonal masses.

---

# 4. From coefficient dominance to cell-vector dominance

Coefficient dominance alone does not immediately imply

\[
|B^+|_2\gg |B^-|_2
\]

because same-branch cell cancellation could reduce the dominant branch.

So combine branch dominance with the same-branch mass theorem:

\[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A stronger branchwise version is preferable:

\[
|B^+|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D_+,
\qquad
|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D_-.
\]

If

\[
D_+\ge Q^cD_-,
\]

then

\[
|B^+|_2
\ge
Q^{-A/2}D_+^{1/2},
\]

while

\[
|B^-|_2
\le
D_-^{1/2}
\le
Q^{-c/2}D_+^{1/2}.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
c/2>A/2+A',
\]

one obtains

\[
|B^-|_2\le Q^{-A'}|B^+|_2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
|B^+|_2-|B^-|_2
\ge
(1-Q^{-A'})|B^+|_2.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A''}(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2).
}
\]

This proves the main/dual nonalignment theorem in the tilted branch.

---

# 5. Easier tilted-branch theorem

A clean theorem statement is:

## Tilted branch dominance theorem

Let

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12
\]

and let the fixed-width packet-frequency support lie in the AFE plateau. Suppose

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_\alpha\log Q.
\]

Assume exact AFE branch ratios obey

\[
\left|
\log
\frac{|z_n^+|}{|z_{\tilde n}^-|}
+
\alpha Q_{\rm eff}
\right|
\le C_0\log Q,
\]

where

\[
Q_{\rm eff}\asymp Q
\]

and \(\tilde n\) denotes the folded-dual matching frequency.

Then, for \(C_\alpha\) sufficiently large,

\[
D_+\ge Q^{c}D_-
\quad\text{or}\quad
D_-\ge Q^{c}D_+.
\]

If, in addition, the dominant branch satisfies the same-branch cell lower bound

\[
|B^{\rm dom}|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D_{\rm dom},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Thus the full cell theorem holds in the tilted regime.

---

# 6. Obstructions and caveats

## 6.1 Same-branch cancellation can still kill the dominant branch

Branch dominance only helps after proving that the dominant branch does not self-cancel cellwise:

\[
|B^{\rm dom}|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D_{\rm dom}.
\]

So the tilted branch does **not** remove the need for the same-branch cell mass theorem.

It only removes the main/dual cancellation problem.

## 6.2 AFE transition regions may spoil dominance

If the support approaches the saddle or smoothing transition,

\[
A_+(u)
\]

or

\[
A_-(u^-)
\]

may be exponentially or polynomially distorted.

Therefore the theorem should require

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12
\]

with a margin from the transition.

## 6.3 The hard branch remains \(|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q\)

When

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll \log Q,
\]

the tilt factor is only

\[
e^{O(\log Q)}
\]

or smaller. For

\[
|\alpha|Q=O(1),
\]

there is no polynomial branch dominance.

In particular, the symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\]

remains the genuine main/dual nonalignment problem.

---

# 7. What this proves for the cell theorem

The full cell theorem can now be split as follows.

## Tilted regime

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q,
\]

then:

1. same-branch mass theorem gives

   \[
   |B^{\rm dom}|_2\ge Q^{-A};
   \]

2. \(\alpha\)-tilt gives branch dominance;

3. branch dominance gives

   \[
   |B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2\ge Q^{-A'}.
   \]

Thus the tilted regime reduces only to same-branch cell nonrecurrence.

## Symmetric regime

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q,
\]

especially

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

then branch dominance is unavailable.

One must prove a true branch nonalignment estimate:

\[
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
\]

This is a folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The tilted branch }|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\text{ is tractable by branch dominance.}
}
\]

Provided exact AFE branch ratios behave as expected away from transition regions, one can prove:

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

from same-branch mass alone.

However:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the hard uniform branch remains }|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
}
\]

In that branch, main and dual may have comparable size, and the theorem still requires folded main/dual cell-vector nonalignment.

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Tilted regime reduces cell theorem to same-branch cell mass;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetric regime remains a folded actual-orbit nonrecurrence problem.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:02:31)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 3 / C — Main/dual nonalignment in \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: focus only on the hard symmetric branch

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\]

and test whether one can prove

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\bigr).
\]

This is the main/dual cell-vector nonalignment subclaim in the fixed-width multiblock cell theorem. 

---

# 1. Common folded cell coordinate

Use ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

For the main branch,

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
x_{n'}^-=\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'},
\qquad
T=\frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

A shared cell \(I_r\) contains pairs satisfying

\[
x_n^+\in I_r,
\qquad
x_{n'}^-\in I_r.
\]

Thus

\[
\lambda\log n
\approx
\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'},
\]

so

\[
\log n+\log n'
\approx
\log T.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
nn'\approx T=\frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
}
\]

This complementary-product constraint is the key arithmetic structure in the hard branch.

---

# 2. Cell-vector expansion

The full cell vector is

\[
B_r=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^- + B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E.
\]

Ignore \(B^{\rm bg},B^E\) for the principal analysis.

We have

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_{n'}^-\in I_r}
z_{n'}^-e^{+im_0\log n'}.
\]

Then

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2^2
=
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
+
2\Re\left(e^{-i\Theta_Z}\langle B^+,B^-\rangle\right).
\]

The cross term is

\[
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-im_0\log n'}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
}
\]

Inside a shared folded cell,

\[
nn'\approx T,
\]

hence the phase is

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\approx
e^{-im_0\log T}
\cdot
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}.
\]

After multiplying by \(e^{-i\Theta_Z}\), near-Cauchy cancellation requires the residual phases and coefficients to align cellwise.

---

# 3. What near-Cauchy equality requires

Near-collapse means

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\left|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle\right|
\approx
|B^+|_2|B^-|_2
\]

and the phase of \(\langle B^+,B^-\rangle\) must be approximately

\[
\arg \langle B^+,B^-\rangle
\approx
\Theta_Z+\pi.
\]

By Cauchy–Schwarz, near equality occurs only if the two cell vectors are nearly collinear:

\[
B_r^+\approx \kappa B_r^-
\qquad
\text{for all active }r,
\]

for a single scalar \(\kappa\).

Thus the hard branch is equivalent to excluding the vector relation

\[
\boxed{
B^+(m_0)\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)
}
\]

over \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\) cells.

This is much stronger than the scalar zero condition

\[
\sum_r\left(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-\right)\approx0.
\]

The scalar zero says only that the **sum of coordinates** cancels. The dangerous relation says that the entire vectors cancel coordinatewise.

---

# 4. Does complementary-product rigidity help?

The complementary relation

\[
nn'\approx T
\]

does add arithmetic structure, but it does not by itself prove nonalignment.

For each main \(n\), the folded dual matching scale is

\[
n'\approx T/n.
\]

Since

\[
\log n\in[c_-Q,c_+Q],
\]

the dual variable satisfies

\[
\log n'\in[\log T-c_+Q,\log T-c_-Q].
\]

Away from the saddle, these are disjoint but complementary AFE regions.

The cross phase is

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
=
e^{-im_0\log T}
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}.
\]

If the cells are narrow,

\[
\log(nn'/T)=O(Q/R)
\]

in raw log scale, hence

\[
m_0\log(nn'/T)
\]

is generally enormous, not small. Thus residual phases can oscillate strongly inside a cell unless there is additional arithmetic synchronization.

This helps nonalignment heuristically: the cross term should not saturate Cauchy–Schwarz generically.

But it is not a proof. To prove it, one needs a bilinear fixed-\(m_0\) exponential-sum estimate for

\[
\sum_{n,n':\,nn'\approx T}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
\]

That is an actual prime-log bilinear nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 5. Hard symmetric branch \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\)

When

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

the main/dual coefficient magnitudes are comparable. The tilt factors

\[
e^{-\alpha u},
\qquad
e^{+\alpha u^-}
\]

do not create polynomial branch dominance.

Therefore one cannot use

\[
|B^+|_2\gg |B^-|_2
\]

or the reverse. The only viable route is a genuine angle estimate:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

In this branch, the theorem is not about magnitude dominance; it is about excluding near-collinearity of two actual cell vectors.

---

# 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, one can force collapse.

Let \(B_r^+\) and \(B_r^-\) be independently adjustable by choosing phases inside each cell. If each cell has enough coefficients and no dominant term, one can arrange

\[
B_r^+ = -e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\]

for every \(r\).

Then

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-=0,
\]

even while

\[
|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2
\]

is nonzero.

Thus main/dual nonalignment is false in the relaxed model.

The proof must use the actual one-parameter constraints

\[
e^{-im_0\log n},
\qquad
e^{+im_0\log n'},
\]

with the same \(m_0\), plus the folded relation \(nn'\approx T\).

---

# 7. Actual-orbit nonrecurrence formulation

The clean theorem needed is:

## Folded cell-vector nonalignment theorem

Let

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

and let \(B^\pm(m)\) be the fixed-width main and folded-dual cell vectors on cells \(I_r\), \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\). Then for every admissible \(m_0\) with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+(m_0),B^-(m_0)\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+(m_0)|_2|B^-(m_0)|_2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)+e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+(m_0)|_2+|B^-(m_0)|_2\bigr).
}
\]

Expanded as a bilinear exponential-sum theorem, this is:

\[
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
\]

This is the precise hard-branch theorem.

---

# 8. Is the theorem easier than full Wronskian incidence?

Yes, but still arithmetic.

This is a degree-one cell-vector theorem. It involves bilinear products of linear packet-frequency sums.

The later Wronskian incidence involves degree-\(R+1\) or degree-\(R+2\) subset-product frequencies. So the cell-vector nonalignment is substantially simpler.

However, it remains a fixed-\(m_0\), actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem. Standard averaged large-sieve estimates do not give it pointwise at a specified \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

So classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{easier than full incidence, harder than coefficient algebra.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Potential proof routes

## 9.1 Bilinear same-cell large sieve

Prove a pointwise bilinear estimate:

\[
\left|
\sum_{r,n,n'}
a_{n,n'}^{(r)}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
\]

Obstruction: this is pointwise in \(m_0\), not averaged.

## 9.2 Complementary-product spacing

Use that \(nn'\) varies substantially inside each cell and across cells, so the phase

\[
m_0\log(nn')
\]

should not remain constant.

Obstruction: one needs an effective lower bound against near-constant phase on actual support.

## 9.3 Folded explicit-formula obstruction

Translate near-collinearity into a prime-side or zero-side abnormality. If

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-,
\]

then main and dual packet-frequency projections cancel cellwise. This may imply a strong local functional-equation symmetry beyond the scalar AFE zero.

Obstruction: no concrete contradiction currently identified.

## 9.4 Tilt split

For

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

branch dominance handles nonalignment.

For

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

one must prove the bilinear nonalignment theorem above.

This split should be part of the final theorem architecture.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{In the hard branch }|\alpha|Q\ll1,\text{ main/dual nonalignment remains an actual-orbit theorem.}
}
\]

Complementary-product rigidity

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}
\]

gives the right arithmetic structure and may help, but it does not by itself prove nonalignment.

A theorem candidate is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\ |\alpha|Q\ll1
\Rightarrow
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
B^+(m_0)\not\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)
}
\]

cellwise.

This is the precise folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem needed to complete the cell-sum route in the symmetric branch.
## User (2026-04-27 07:10:42)

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:10:49)

_Thought for a few seconds_

## Agent 3 / C — Hard symmetric main/dual nonalignment

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: focus only on the hard symmetric branch

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

where branch dominance is unavailable and the cell theorem needs a genuine main/dual nonalignment estimate. 

---

# 1. Target

We need

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\bigr).
\]

Equivalently, we need to prevent near Cauchy–Schwarz saturation:

\[
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\approx
|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
\]

The hard branch is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

so the main/dual coefficient magnitudes can be comparable. The tilted-branch dominance argument does not apply.

---

# 2. Common folded cell coordinate

Use

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n,
\]

and

\[
x_{n'}^-=\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'},
\qquad
T=\frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

The same-cell condition is

\[
x_n^+\in I_r,
\qquad
x_{n'}^-\in I_r.
\]

Therefore

\[
\lambda\log n
\approx
\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'},
\]

hence

\[
\log(nn')\approx \log T,
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
nn'\approx T=\frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
}
\]

This is the complementary-product structure.

---

# 3. Cross-term expansion

The cell vectors are

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_{n'}^-\in I_r}
z_{n'}^-e^{+im_0\log n'}.
\]

The cross term is

\[
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r B_r^+\overline{B_r^-}.
\]

Since

\[
\overline{B_r^-}
=
\sum_{x_{n'}^-\in I_r}
\overline{z_{n'}^-}e^{-im_0\log n'},
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
}
\]

Set

\[
nn'=T e^\delta.
\]

Then

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
=
e^{-im_0\log T}
e^{-im_0\delta}.
\]

The same-cell relation gives

\[
|\lambda\delta|\lesssim R^{-1},
\]

so

\[
|\delta|\lesssim \frac{1}{\lambda R}\asymp \frac{Q}{R}.
\]

Although this looks “small” in log-scale compared with \(Q\), the phase variation is

\[
m_0\delta,
\]

which can be enormous because \(m_0\) is height-scale, not \(Q\)-scale.

Thus complementary-product localization does **not** make the cross phase constant. It creates a structured bilinear phase

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}
\]

over complementary \(n,n'\), and that phase should oscillate strongly unless the actual orbit is specially recurrent.

---

# 4. Cauchy saturation condition

Near-collapse of the full cell vector requires

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

Equivalently, there exists a scalar \(\kappa\) with

\[
B_r^+\approx \kappa B_r^-
\qquad
\forall r.
\]

This is stronger than scalar cancellation:

\[
\sum_r(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-)\approx0.
\]

The latter is just

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)\approx0.
\]

The former is a vector relation across

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

coordinates.

So the main/dual collapse event imposes roughly \(R\) complex constraints, not one.

This is why the cell theorem is plausibly much easier than full Wronskian incidence.

---

# 5. Can complementary-product rigidity prove nonalignment?

Not by itself.

The relation

\[
nn'\approx T
\]

identifies the cross-term pairs, but it does not force a sign or positivity. The cross term remains

\[
\sum_{r,n,n'} a_{n,n'}^{(r)} e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
\]

To prove nonalignment, one would need a bilinear estimate of the form

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

This is a pointwise fixed-\(m_0\) bilinear prime-log nonrecurrence theorem.

Complementary-product structure supplies the correct phase geometry, but it is not alone a proof.

---

# 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, make the phases in \(B^+\) and \(B^-\) adjustable independently cell by cell.

Then one can set

\[
B_r^+ = -e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\qquad
\forall r,
\]

provided each branch cell has enough internal phase freedom.

This gives

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-=0,
\]

while

\[
|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2
\]

remains nonzero.

Therefore the theorem is false in phase-relaxed models. Any proof must use the actual one-parameter constraints

\[
e^{-im_0\log n},
\qquad
e^{+im_0\log n'},
\]

and the complementary coupling

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

---

# 7. Hard-branch theorem candidate

The exact theorem needed in the symmetric branch is:

## Folded main/dual cell nonalignment theorem

Assume

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<1/2,
\]

and ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For every admissible \(m_0\) satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the folded cell vectors satisfy

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+(m_0),B^-(m_0)\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})
|B^+(m_0)|_2|B^-(m_0)|_2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)+e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+(m_0)|_2+|B^-(m_0)|_2\bigr).
}
\]

Expanded in bilinear form, this is

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

This is the named nonrecurrence theorem for the hard branch.

---

# 8. Possible proof routes

## 8.1 Bilinear phase dispersion

Use the residual phase

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}
\]

inside complementary cells. Since \(m_0\) is large, small variations in \(nn'/T\) may generate strong oscillation.

Need a bound showing the bilinear sum cannot saturate Cauchy–Schwarz.

Obstacle: the theorem is pointwise at \(m_0\), and no averaging over \(m\) is available.

## 8.2 Complementary-product Diophantine rigidity

If near-Cauchy saturation occurs, then the phases must align:

\[
m_0\log(nn'/T)
\approx \text{constant}
\]

for most contributing \((n,n')\) in each cell. This implies many ratios \(nn'/T\) lie near a phase lattice.

One could try to prove this is impossible for actual \(n,n'\) in broad packet-frequency cells.

Obstacle: \(m_0\) is also the parameter defining \(T\), so the condition is self-referential.

## 8.3 Main/dual AFE incompatibility

Cellwise cancellation says the main and dual projections cancel much more strongly than the scalar AFE zero requires. This might contradict the detailed shape of AFE weights across \(x\)-cells.

Obstacle: in \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\), branch magnitudes are deliberately similar, so no coefficient dominance is available.

## 8.4 Zero-set large-sieve route

Prove this nonalignment on average over \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros using a degree-one zero-set large sieve, then strengthen to pointwise.

Obstacle: averaged control does not immediately rule out a specific bad admissible zero.

---

# 9. Comparison to tilted branch

For

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

one branch should dominate by a polynomial factor. Then

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\]

is controlled by the dominant branch, assuming same-branch cell mass.

So the hard problem is only the symmetric branch:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q,
}
\]

especially

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
}
\]

This regime requires actual nonalignment, not dominance.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The hard symmetric main/dual nonalignment theorem is not proved, but it is now precisely formulated.}
}
\]

Complementary-product structure

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}
\]

is the right arithmetic feature. It may enable a bilinear nonrecurrence proof, but by itself it gives no sign, positivity, or automatic angle bound.

The remaining hard-branch input is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\ |\alpha|Q\ll1
\Rightarrow
B^+(m_0)\not\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)
\text{ cellwise}.
}
\]

This is a degree-one folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

## Agent 3 / C — Hard symmetric main/dual nonalignment

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: focus only on the hard branch

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\]

and sharpen the nonalignment theorem needed for

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\bigr).
\]

The prompt specifies this as the hard symmetric main/dual cell-vector problem inside the fixed-width multiblock cell theorem. 

---

# 1. Common folded cell coordinate

Let

\[
T=\frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

The plus branch uses

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

The folded dual branch uses

\[
x_{n'}^-=\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'}.
\]

Cells are common in \(x\)-space:

\[
x_n^+\in I_r,
\qquad
x_{n'}^-\in I_r.
\]

Therefore, in the same cell,

\[
\lambda\log n
\approx
\lambda\log\frac{T}{n'},
\]

hence

\[
\log(nn')\approx \log T,
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
nn'\approx T.
}
\]

This complementary-product relation is the one real structural feature available in the hard branch.

---

# 2. Cross term

The cell vectors are

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_{n'}^-\in I_r}
z_{n'}^-e^{+im_0\log n'}.
\]

Then

\[
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r B_r^+\overline{B_r^-}.
\]

Since

\[
\overline{B_r^-}
=
\sum_{x_{n'}^-\in I_r}
\overline{z_{n'}^-}e^{-im_0\log n'},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\langle B^+,B^-\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
}
\]

Write

\[
nn'=T e^\delta.
\]

Then

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
=
e^{-im_0\log T}
e^{-im_0\delta}.
\]

The same-cell condition gives

\[
|\lambda\delta|\lesssim R^{-1},
\]

so

\[
|\delta|\lesssim \frac{1}{\lambda R}\asymp \frac{Q}{R}.
\]

Although this is small relative to \(Q\), the actual phase variation is

\[
m_0\delta,
\]

which is enormous at zeta height. Therefore same-cell folding does **not** make the phase constant. It creates a structured bilinear phase

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}.
\]

---

# 3. Near-alignment condition

The dangerous event is

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\approx0.
\]

This implies

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

Equivalently, the cell vectors are nearly collinear:

\[
B_r^+\approx \kappa B_r^-
\qquad
\text{for all active cells }r,
\]

with one scalar

\[
\kappa\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}.
\]

By Cauchy–Schwarz, this is equivalent to near saturation:

\[
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\approx
|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
\]

So the desired hard-branch theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

This is the exact nonalignment estimate.

---

# 4. Complementary-product rigidity: useful but insufficient alone

The relation

\[
nn'\approx T
\]

constrains which pairs contribute to the cross term. But it does not produce positivity, a sign, or a fixed phase.

The cross term remains

\[
\sum_{r,n,n'}
a_{n,n'}^{(r)}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}.
\]

To prevent Cauchy saturation, one needs a bilinear pointwise estimate of the form

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

This is not a standard consequence of folding. It is an actual-orbit bilinear nonrecurrence statement.

---

# 5. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, choose phases independently inside each cell.

Then one can impose

\[
B_r^+
=
-e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\]

for every cell \(r\), provided each cell has enough internal phase freedom and no dominant coefficient.

Thus

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-=0
\]

while

\[
|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2
\]

remains nonzero.

So the theorem is false in phase-relaxed models. A proof must use the actual phase laws

\[
e^{-im_0\log n},
\qquad
e^{+im_0\log n'},
\]

and the coupled relation

\[
nn'\approx T.
\]

---

# 6. Hard-branch theorem candidate

The clean importable theorem is:

## Folded main/dual cell nonalignment theorem

Assume

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let \(B^\pm(m_0,\alpha)\) be the plus and folded-dual cell vectors. Then for every admissible \(m_0\) satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+(m_0,\alpha),B^-(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})
|B^+(m_0,\alpha)|_2
|B^-(m_0,\alpha)|_2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0,\alpha)+e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B^-(m_0,\alpha)|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\bigl(|B^+(m_0,\alpha)|_2+|B^-(m_0,\alpha)|_2\bigr).
}
\]

Expanded bilinearly, the theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{-im_0\log(nn')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

---

# 7. Potential proof routes

## 7.1 Bilinear phase dispersion

Try to prove that the residual phase

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nn'/T)}
\]

oscillates enough within and across folded cells to prevent Cauchy saturation.

This would require a pointwise bilinear estimate at \(m_0\).

## 7.2 Complementary-product Diophantine obstruction

Near-saturation implies

\[
m_0\log(nn'/T)
\]

is nearly constant on most contributing pairs in each cell. One could try to show this is impossible for broad fixed-width packet supports.

The issue is that \(T=m_0/(2\pi)\), so the phase condition is self-referential.

## 7.3 Main/dual AFE incompatibility

Cellwise cancellation would mean the functional-equation dual cancels the main branch in each packet-frequency cell, not only in total. This is much stronger than

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

A possible theorem would say scalar AFE cancellation cannot refine into \(R\)-many cellwise cancellations.

This is plausible, but it is exactly an actual main/dual nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 8. Relation to tilted branch

For

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

branch dominance should handle main/dual nonalignment after same-branch mass is known.

For

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

branch dominance vanishes. The theorem must be this bilinear nonalignment estimate.

Thus the cell theorem should split:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q:
\text{ dominance + same-branch mass}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll1:
\text{ folded bilinear nonalignment}
}
\]

with the intermediate region handled by whichever bound has margin.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hard symmetric main/dual nonalignment remains open.}
}
\]

It is now sharply reduced to a **degree-one folded bilinear actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem**:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\quad |\alpha|Q\ll1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
B^+(m_0)\not\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0)}B^-(m_0)
\text{ cellwise}.
\]

Complementary-product structure

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}
\]

is the key arithmetic feature, but it does not by itself yield a proof.
