## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:23:47)

_Thought for 4s_

## Agent 3 / C — Close the tilted branch cleanly

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: close the easier tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q
\]

by branch dominance, modulo the same-branch cell nonrecurrence input. 

---

# 1. Branch ratio on fixed-width plateau support

Work on fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
u=\log n,
\qquad
u^-=\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}.
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
u+u^-=\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi}=:Q_T.
\]

On ordinary scale, \(Q_T\asymp Q\). The main and folded-dual coefficient magnitudes have the schematic ratio

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
=
\mathcal A(m_0,\alpha,n)\,
e^{\alpha(u+u^-)}
=
\mathcal A(m_0,\alpha,n)\,e^{\alpha Q_T},
\]

where \(\mathcal A\) collects non-exponential factors from AFE smoothing, gamma normalization, log powers, and branch conventions.

On plateau support away from the saddle,

\[
Q^{-C_0}\le |\mathcal A(m_0,\alpha,n)|\le Q^{C_0}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q_T}.
}
\]

Depending on the sign of \(\alpha\), either the dual or the main branch dominates.

---

# 2. Sources of the \(Q^{O(1)}\) loss

The \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor consists of:

1. **AFE smoothing weights.**  
   On fixed plateau support,

   \[
   V_+(u)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}),
   \]

   and similarly for the folded branch if the support is kept away from transition. If a branch approaches the transition, this must be excluded by choosing

   \[
   c_+<c_1<\frac12.
   \]

2. **Gamma/Stirling factors.**  
   Gamma ratios over the ordinary packet-frequency range contribute powers of \(Q\), not exponentials in \(Q\), after completed normalization.

3. **Log-derivative / source-curvature powers.**  
   Factors such as \((\log n)^k\), \(u^{-3}\), or their folded analogues contribute \(Q^{O(1)}\).

4. **Cell normalization / basis conditioning.**  
   The fixed-width cell basis has at most

   \[
   \exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
   \]

   loss at

   \[
   R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
   \]

5. **Canonical background/error terms.**  
   \(B^{\rm bg}\) and \(B^E\) must be bounded at \(Q^{-C}\) relative to the dominant branch mass.

All non-tilt factors are polynomial in \(Q\). The only exponential-in-\(Q\) branch separator is

\[
e^{\alpha Q_T}.
\]

---

# 3. Tilted branch dominance

Assume

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_\alpha \log Q.
\]

Since \(Q_T\asymp Q\), there exists \(c_\alpha>0\) if \(C_\alpha\) is sufficiently large relative to the polynomial-loss constant \(C_0\), such that either

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}\ge Q^{c_\alpha}
\]

uniformly on corresponding folded cells, or

\[
\frac{|z^+|}{|z^-|}\ge Q^{c_\alpha}.
\]

Thus the diagonal branch masses satisfy either

\[
D^-\ge Q^{c_\alpha}D^+
\]

or

\[
D^+\ge Q^{c_\alpha}D^-.
\]

Let \(B^{\rm dom}\) denote the dominant branch and \(B^{\rm sub}\) the subordinate branch.

Assume the same-branch cell nonrecurrence theorem gives branchwise mass lower control:

\[
|B^{\rm dom}|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_s}D^{\rm dom}.
\]

Also use the trivial upper bound

\[
|B^{\rm sub}|_2^2\le D^{\rm sub}\cdot Q^{A_u}
\]

if normalization/operator effects require a polynomial factor. In the clean \(\ell^2\) cell vector normalization, one can take \(A_u=0\).

Then

\[
\frac{|B^{\rm sub}|_2}{|B^{\rm dom}|_2}
\le
Q^{(A_s+A_u-c_\alpha)/2}.
\]

Choosing \(C_\alpha\) so that

\[
c_\alpha>A_s+A_u+2A_*
\]

gives

\[
|B^{\rm sub}|_2\le Q^{-A_*}|B^{\rm dom}|_2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\begin{aligned}
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
&\ge |B^{\rm dom}|_2-|B^{\rm sub}|_2-|B^{\rm bg}+B^E|_2\\
&\ge (1-Q^{-A_*})|B^{\rm dom}|_2-|B^{\rm bg}+B^E|_2.
\end{aligned}
\]

If

\[
|B^{\rm bg}+B^E|_2\le Q^{-A_*}|B^{\rm dom}|_2,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\right).
}
\]

This closes main/dual nonalignment in the tilted regime.

---

# 4. Theorem: tilted branch closure

## Tilted Branch Cell Nonalignment Theorem

Assume:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and fixed-width plateau support

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12.
\]

Assume exact AFE branch coefficients satisfy

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q_T},
\qquad
Q_T\asymp Q,
\]

uniformly over matched folded cells.

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_\alpha\log Q
\]

with \(C_\alpha\) sufficiently large, then one branch dominates the other by \(Q^c\).

Assume the same-branch cell nonrecurrence theorem for the dominant branch:

\[
|B^{\rm dom}|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_s}D^{\rm dom}.
\]

Assume canonical background/error absorption:

\[
|B^{\rm bg}+B^E|_2\le Q^{-A_e}|B^{\rm dom}|_2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\left(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\right).
}
\]

Consequently, in the tilted regime, the full cell theorem reduces to same-branch cell nonrecurrence.

---

# 5. What remains outside the tilted branch

The above theorem does **not** cover

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

In particular, the symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\]

has no polynomial branch dominance. There the main and folded-dual magnitudes can be comparable, and one needs the hard nonalignment theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})|B^+|_2|B^-|_2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
B^+ \not\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-
\quad\text{cellwise}.
}
\]

That is the folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 6. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q:
\text{ closed modulo same-branch cell mass.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q:
\text{ not closed by dominance.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll1:
\text{ hard symmetric branch; requires folded bilinear nonalignment.}
}
\]

So the tilted branch can be removed from the list of independent main/dual problems. The remaining uniform cell theorem requires:

1. same-branch cell nonrecurrence; and  
2. hard-branch folded main/dual nonalignment for \(|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q\), especially \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\).
## User (2026-04-27 07:41:41)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:41:51)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 3 / C — Exterior coefficient mass for \(\mathbf M\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: verify or formulate the diagonal/exterior coefficient mass input for the cofactor vector

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S.
\]

This is the diagonal term needed for the proposed \(\mathbf M\) zero-set large sieve. 

---

# 1. Cofactor vector setup

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

Here \(\mathbf M\) is the Hodge-dual cofactor vector of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet block. Abstractly, if the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-rows are

\[
H_j(m)=C_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can}(m),
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

then \(\mathbf M\) is the vector of maximal minors of the \((R+1)\times(R+2)\) matrix

\[
\bigl(C_\ell(\mathcal D)H_j(m)\bigr)_
{0\le j\le R,\ 0\le \ell\le R+1}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\mathbf M
=
H_0\wedge H_1\wedge\cdots\wedge H_R
\]

in the exterior algebra of the column space.

The target coefficient mass is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the diagonal input for

\[
\sum_{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2.
\]

---

# 2. Packet-frequency model

For one main packet-frequency branch, write

\[
q''_{\rm can,+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Let the basis-normalized column operators be

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D),
\qquad 0\le \ell\le R+1,
\]

and the basis-normalized row operators be

\[
\phi_j(\mathcal D),
\qquad 0\le j\le R.
\]

At principal-symbol level,

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can,+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n\phi_j(x_n)C_\ell(x_n)e^{-im\log n},
\]

where

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

Define the column evaluation vector

\[
v_n
=
c_n
\begin{pmatrix}
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_R(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the cofactor expansion has coefficients

\[
\mathbf A_S
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S} c_n\right)
\mathbf a_S,
\qquad
|S|=R+1,
\]

where \(\mathbf a_S\) is the exterior coefficient determined by the basis-evaluation matrix on the chosen nodes.

More invariantly, let

\[
V
=
\bigl(v_n\bigr)_{n\in\mathcal B}
\]

be an \((R+1)\times M\) matrix. Then

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2
=
\det(VV^\ast)
\]

by Cauchy–Binet.

Thus the exterior mass theorem is equivalent to a Gram determinant lower bound.

---

# 3. Exterior mass theorem candidate

## Main-branch exterior mass theorem

Let \(\mathcal B\) be a fixed-width packet-frequency block

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<1/2,
\]

with normalized nodes

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\in[x_-,x_+].
\]

Assume:

1. the basis \(\phi_0,\ldots,\phi_R\) is discrete orthonormal or uniformly well-conditioned on \(\mathcal B\);

2. the coefficient weights satisfy

\[
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}|c_n|^2|\phi_j(x_n)|^2\asymp 1
\]

after amplitude normalization;

3. the weighted Gram matrix

\[
G_{jk}
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
|c_n|^2\phi_j(x_n)\overline{\phi_k(x_n)}
\]

has eigenvalues bounded below by

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2
=
\det G
\ge Q^{-C(R+1)}.
}
\]

At safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives a polynomial lower bound after basis/amplitude normalization if the determinant is normalized rowwise. More naturally, define the row-normalized Gram

\[
\widehat G_{jk}
=
\frac{G_{jk}}{(G_{jj}G_{kk})^{1/2}}.
\]

If

\[
\lambda_{\min}(\widehat G)\ge Q^{-C/R},
\]

then

\[
\det \widehat G\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus the theorem should be stated in **row-normalized exterior mass** form:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Does symbol rank imply exterior mass?

Not directly, but the same machinery helps.

The earlier \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank result says the \(Z_\alpha\)-row is not in the degree-\(\le R\) span of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet symbols.

For \(\mathbf M\), we do **not** need \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank. We need the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows themselves to have exterior volume.

That is a different rank condition:

\[
\boxed{
\phi_0(x),\ldots,\phi_R(x)
\quad\text{must remain linearly independent on the weighted packet block.}
}
\]

With a basis-normalized construction, this should be Green-feasible: choose \(\phi_j\) orthonormal on the packet nodes with respect to \(|c_n|^2\). Then

\[
G=I
\]

by construction in the model branch, and

\[
\det G=1.
\]

Therefore, in the basis-normalized model, exterior mass is not a deep arithmetic statement. It is a conditioning and coefficient-support statement.

The subtlety is canonical transfer: \(q''_{\rm can}\) includes main, dual, \(B_2\), and \(E_2\), not just one clean model branch.

---

# 5. Dual branch and mixed exterior mass

The full canonical object is

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The cofactor vector has contributions from:

1. pure main subsets;
2. pure dual subsets;
3. mixed main/dual subsets;
4. terms involving \(B_2\);
5. perturbative \(E_2\)-terms.

Schematically,

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_{+}
+
\mathbf M_{-}
+
\mathbf M_{\rm mix}
+
\mathbf M_{B_2}
+
\mathbf M_{E_2}.
\]

The exterior mass theorem can be proved in two different ways.

## Route A: one-branch dominance

If a single branch supplies a well-conditioned exterior block, then

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_{S,+}|^2\ge Q^{-C}
\]

or

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_{S,-}|^2\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is enough at the coefficient level. The full \(\mathbf M\)-coefficient mass then survives if mixed/dual/background/error do not cancel this branch coefficient system.

This is cleanest in tilted \(\alpha\)-regimes.

## Route B: combined Gram

Construct the weighted Gram matrix using all canonical packet frequencies:

\[
G_{\rm can}
=
\sum_{\omega\in\Omega_{\rm main}\cup\Omega_{\rm dual}}
|c_\omega|^2
\Phi(\omega)\Phi(\omega)^\ast
+
G_{B_2}
+
G_{\rm err}.
\]

If

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_{\rm can})\ge Q^{-C/R},
\]

then row-normalized exterior mass satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\sum_S|\widehat{\mathbf A}_{S,\rm can}|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the most canonical formulation.

---

# 6. Role of \(B_2\)

The background term

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
\]

is smooth and nonoscillatory compared with the packet-frequency AFE pieces.

In the cofactor matrix, \(B_2\)-derived rows or columns can contribute low-rank smooth components. They should **not** be used as the sole source of exterior mass, because \(B_2\)-only rows are diagnostics and not Gate 1 candidates.

For the exterior mass theorem, \(B_2\) should be handled as either:

1. a perturbative smooth row/column addition, if its normalized size is smaller than the packet-frequency exterior volume; or

2. an included canonical component in \(G_{\rm can}\), while requiring that the packet-frequency AFE part already supplies a \(Q^{-C}\) lower exterior volume.

The safe theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency }P_2+D_2\text{ exterior mass }\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\text{and}\quad
B_2,E_2\text{ perturbations }\le Q^{-C'}
\Rightarrow
\mathbf M_{\rm can}\text{ exterior mass }\ge Q^{-C''}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Error term \(E_2\)

For \(\mathbf M\), \(E_2\) enters through rows

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\phi_j(\mathcal D)E_2.
\]

Because \(\mathbf M\) is an exterior product of \(R+1\) rows, the perturbation estimate must control multilinear expansion:

\[
\|M_{\rm can}-M_{\rm model}\|
\le
(R+1)\|E_{\rm row}\|
\cdot
\|M_{\rm model}\|^{R}
+
\cdots.
\]

A sufficient condition is rowwise relative control:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j,\ell}
\left|
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\phi_j(\mathcal D)E_2
\right|
\le
Q^{-C_E}
\cdot
\text{row scale},
}
\]

with \(C_E\) large enough to absorb \(R\)-factors and exterior-condition-number losses.

At safe depth,

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

operator losses

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

are acceptable.

Thus the high-derivative AFE package previously used for the Wronskian should be enough, provided it is stated for all rows entering \(\mathbf M\).

---

# 8. Exterior coefficient mass result

The coefficient mass theorem should be stated as follows.

## Canonical exterior coefficient mass theorem

Let

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and let \(\mathcal B\) be a fixed-width ordinary packet-frequency support away from the saddle. Let \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\), \(\phi_j(\mathcal D)\) be basis-normalized row/column operators.

Assume:

1. packet-frequency main/dual coefficient support has nonzero weighted mass in at least \(R+1\) stable directions;

2. the row-normalized packet Gram satisfies

\[
\lambda_{\min}(\widehat G_{\rm packet})\ge Q^{-C/R};
\]

3. \(B_2\) is included canonically but does not serve as the sole source of exterior mass;

4. the \(E_2\)-row perturbation satisfies

\[
\|E_{\rm row}\|\le Q^{-C_E}
\]

relative to packet row scale.

Then the cofactor expansion

\[
\mathbf M_{\rm can}(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/mixed/background/error}
\]

has row-normalized diagonal coefficient mass

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This supplies the diagonal term

\[
K_J(0)\sum_S|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2
\]

in the \(\mathbf M\) zero-set large sieve.

---

# 9. Is this a hard arithmetic input?

No. Unlike the later zero-set sampling problem,

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\]

the exterior coefficient mass is mostly linear algebra plus canonical AFE control.

The hard arithmetic for \(\mathbf M\) is not diagonal mass. It is preventing zero-set off-diagonal cancellation:

\[
\sum_{S\ne T}
\langle\mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\]

from destroying the diagonal.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exterior mass is Green-feasible; zero-set large-sieve off-diagonal control is the hard part.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exterior coefficient mass for }\mathbf M\text{ is Green-feasible under basis normalization and canonical AFE transfer.}
}
\]

The theorem should be imported as a coefficient/conditioning lemma, not as a major arithmetic obstacle.

Remaining requirements:

1. exact construction of \(\mathbf A_S\) from the canonical main/dual packet model;
2. row-normalized Gram lower bound;
3. \(B_2\) included but not relied on as a sole source;
4. \(E_2\) controlled through the required Wronskian derivative order.

After this, the actual \(\mathbf M\)-problem is the zero-set large sieve for subset-product frequencies

\[
\Omega_S-\Omega_T=\log(N_S/N_T),
\]

not the diagonal exterior mass.

## Agent 3 / C — Exterior coefficient mass for \(\mathbf M\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: establish or formulate the diagonal coefficient-mass input

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for the cofactor vector

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+\cdots,
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S.
\]

This is the diagonal term needed before the zero-set large-sieve kernel \(K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\) becomes relevant. 

---

# 1. Cofactor-vector model

The Wronskian rows are

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\rm can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero, expansion along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

The vector \(\mathbf M\) is the Hodge dual / cofactor vector of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet block. If

\[
H_j(m)=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\rm can}(m),
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

and the column operators are

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D),
\qquad 0\le \ell\le R+1,
\]

then the relevant \((R+1)\times(R+2)\) matrix is

\[
\mathcal H_{j\ell}(m)
=
C_\ell(\mathcal D)H_j(m).
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
H_0(m)\wedge H_1(m)\wedge\cdots\wedge H_R(m),
\]

viewed in the exterior algebra of the \((R+2)\)-dimensional column space.

So \(\mathbf M\) is nonzero exactly when the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet block has exterior rank \(R+1\).

---

# 2. Packet-frequency expansion

On a main packet-frequency branch,

\[
q''_{{\rm can},+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

At principal-symbol level,

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{{\rm can},+}(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
c_n^+(m)\,
\Phi_j(x_n)\,
C_\ell(x_n)\,
e^{-im\log n},
\]

with

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

Define the row-basis evaluation vector

\[
u_n
=
c_n^+
\begin{pmatrix}
\Phi_0(x_n)\\
\Phi_1(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\Phi_R(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let \(U\) be the \((R+1)\times M\) matrix whose columns are \(u_n\). Then by Cauchy–Binet,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\det U_S|^2
=
\det(UU^\ast).
}
\]

This is the fundamental diagonal-mass identity.

The exterior coefficients \(\mathbf A_S\) are precisely these minors, multiplied by the column-basis determinant coming from the \(C_\ell(x_n)\)-side. In a basis-normalized construction, that column determinant is normalized to be \(Q^{O(1)}\), or exactly \(1\) on a Lagrange witness basis.

Therefore the diagonal coefficient mass reduces to a Gram determinant lower bound.

---

# 3. Basis-normalized exterior mass theorem

Choose \(\Phi_0,\dots,\Phi_R\) to be discrete orthonormal polynomials on the active packet-frequency support with respect to the weight

\[
d\mu(n)=|c_n^+|^2.
\]

Then the Gram matrix is

\[
G_{jk}
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B}
|c_n^+|^2
\Phi_j(x_n)\overline{\Phi_k(x_n)}.
\]

With exact discrete orthonormalization,

\[
G=I.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\det G=1,
\]

and hence

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_{S,+}|^2\asymp1
}
\]

in row-normalized coordinates.

If the basis is not exactly orthonormal but is stable, it is enough to require

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C/R},
\qquad
\lambda_{\max}(G)\le Q^{C/R}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\det G\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

So the correct diagonal theorem is not

\[
\det G\ge e^{-O(R^2)}
\]

in raw monomial coordinates, but rather

\[
\boxed{
\det \widehat G\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

in basis-normalized coordinates.

This is Green-feasible.

---

# 4. Exact theorem candidate

## Exterior Coefficient Mass Theorem

Let

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and let \(\mathcal B\) be a fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let \(q''_{{\rm model}}\) be the packet-frequency model for

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Assume:

1. The packet-frequency main/dual support contains at least \(R+1\) stable nodes in normalized coordinate \(x=\lambda\log n\) or folded \(x^-=\lambda\log(T/n)\).

2. The basis \(\Phi_0,\dots,\Phi_R\) is row-normalized so that the model Gram matrix satisfies

   \[
   \lambda_{\min}(\widehat G_{\rm model})\ge Q^{-C/R}.
   \]

3. Column operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) are basis-normalized with condition number

   \[
   \kappa_C\le Q^C.
   \]

4. The canonical error satisfies rowwise

   \[
   \max_{j,\ell}
   \left|
   C_\ell(\mathcal D)\Phi_j(\mathcal D)
   (q''_{\rm can}-q''_{\rm model})
   \right|
   \le Q^{-C_E}
   \]

   with \(C_E\) sufficiently large.

Then the cofactor expansion

\[
\mathbf M_{\rm can}(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{canonical lower-order terms}
\]

satisfies the row-normalized exterior coefficient mass bound

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the diagonal input for the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve.

---

# 5. Does \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank enter?

Not directly.

The earlier \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank theorem shows the \(Z_\alpha\)-row is not polynomially redundant with the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows. That is relevant for the full Wronskian.

But the cofactor mass of \(\mathbf M\) only needs exterior nondegeneracy of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet block itself.

So the relevant rank condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^0q''_{\rm can},\dots,\mathcal D^Rq''_{\rm can}
\text{ have stable exterior rank on packet-frequency support.}
}
\]

With basis-normalized row operators, this is almost built into the construction, provided the packet-frequency model has enough coefficient mass and enough stable nodes.

Thus \(Z_\alpha\)-rank is not a needed input for the diagonal \(\mathbf M\)-mass theorem.

---

# 6. Canonical components

The canonical source is

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

## \(P_2\)

The main packet-frequency branch supplies ordinary exponential phases

\[
e^{-im\log n}
\]

and coefficients \(c_n^+\). This branch alone can supply exterior mass if its weighted Gram is nondegenerate.

## \(D_2\)

The folded dual branch supplies phases

\[
e^{+im\log n}e^{i\Theta(m)}
\]

with folded coordinate

\[
x^-=\lambda\log(T/n).
\]

It can either:

1. supply its own exterior mass; or  
2. enlarge the combined packet-frequency Gram; or  
3. be handled as a perturbation if dominated by \(P_2\).

In the symmetric regime, \(P_2\) and \(D_2\) should both be included in the canonical model.

## \(B_2\)

The gamma/background term \(B_2\) is smooth and low-complexity. It must be included in the canonical rows, but it should not be used as the sole source of exterior mass.

The safe condition is:

\[
\boxed{
P_2+D_2\text{ packet-frequency block already gives exterior mass }Q^{-A};
}
\]

then \(B_2\) is allowed as a canonical perturbation or mixed contribution.

## \(E_2\)

The error \(E_2\) must be controlled through the row/column derivatives used in \(\mathbf M\).

Since the cofactor uses

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\mathcal D^j q''_{\rm can}
\]

with

\[
0\le j\le R,\qquad 0\le \ell\le R+1,
\]

the maximum derivative order is roughly

\[
2R+1.
\]

The required error package is

\[
\boxed{
\max_{k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^k E_2|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

after basis-operator losses.

---

# 7. Cofactor perturbation bound

Let

\[
\mathcal H_{\rm can}
=
\mathcal H_{\rm model}
+
\mathcal E
\]

be the \((R+1)\times(R+2)\) cofactor matrix.

The exterior product is multilinear:

\[
\mathbf M_{\rm can}
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^{R}
(H_j^{\rm model}+E_j).
\]

So

\[
\mathbf M_{\rm can}-\mathbf M_{\rm model}
=
\sum_{a=1}^{R+1}
\sum_{\#\text{error rows}=a}
\bigwedge E\wedge \bigwedge H^{\rm model}.
\]

A sufficient perturbation condition is

\[
\|\mathcal E\|_{\rm row}
\le
Q^{-C_E}
\lambda_{\min}(\mathcal H_{\rm model})
\]

with \(C_E\) large enough to absorb

\[
\binom{R+1}{a}
\]

and basis condition numbers.

Because

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

combinatorial factors are

\[
e^{O(R)}=Q^{o(1)}
\]

and basis factors are

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Thus if

\[
C_E
\]

is chosen sufficiently large,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M_{\rm model}|\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\rm can}|\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

at the coefficient-mass level.

---

# 8. Exterior mass is not the hard arithmetic step

The diagonal mass

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2
\]

is a coefficient-space quantity. With stable basis normalization, it is controlled by Gram determinants and AFE coefficient support.

The hard arithmetic for \(\mathbf M\) is not this diagonal term. It is the zero-set off-diagonal term:

\[
\sum_{S\ne T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T).
\]

That is where subset-product resonances and \(Z_\alpha\)-zero statistics enter.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exterior mass: Green-feasible.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zero-set off-diagonal control: hard.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final answer

The exterior coefficient mass theorem should be treated as a **canonical conditioning lemma**, not as a new deep arithmetic conjecture.

A concise black-box version is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Exterior Mass Lemma.}
}
\]

Under ordinary packet-frequency support, basis-normalized rows/columns, canonical high-derivative AFE control through \(2R+1\), and a packet Gram lower bound

\[
\lambda_{\min}(\widehat G_{\rm packet})\ge Q^{-C/R},
\]

the cofactor vector has diagonal coefficient mass

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\widehat{\mathbf A}_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This supplies the positive diagonal term in the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve. The next real obstacle is the zero-set spectral large sieve for

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\qquad
\Omega_S-\Omega_T=\log(N_S/N_T).
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Prime-block \(\mathbf M\) model and canonical transfer

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: determine whether the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve can first be proved for a **prime-supported model** and then transferred to the canonical cofactor vector \(\mathbf M_{\can}\). The prompt asks for either a viable prime-block-to-canonical transfer theorem or a no-go showing prime-only \(\mathbf M\) is insufficient. 

---

# 1. Prime-block model

Let

\[
\mathcal P_Q=\{p:c_-Q\le \log p\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Define a prime-supported model

\[
q''_{\prime}(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
P_{2,\prime}(m)
+
D_{2,\prime}(m),
\]

where

\[
P_{2,\prime}(m)
=
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q}c_p^+(m)e^{-im\log p},
\]

and the folded dual prime block is

\[
D_{2,\prime}(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_q(m)}
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q^-}c_p^-(m)e^{+im\log p}.
\]

The folded dual packet coordinate is

\[
x_p^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi p}.
\]

The cofactor vector \(\mathbf M_{\prime}\) is built from the same basis-normalized jet block as the canonical object:

\[
H_j^\prime(m)=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\prime}(m),
\qquad
0\le j\le R,
\]

and

\[
\mathcal H_{j\ell}^\prime(m)
=
C_\ell(\mathcal D)H_j^\prime(m),
\qquad
0\le \ell\le R+1.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M_{\prime}(m)
=
H_0^\prime(m)\wedge\cdots\wedge H_R^\prime(m).
\]

The prime-model target would be

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Why prime support is attractive

Prime support gives clean subset-product frequencies:

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{p\in S}p,
\qquad
|S|=R+1.
\]

By unique factorization,

\[
N_S=N_T
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
S=T
\]

for squarefree prime subsets. Therefore exact subset-product collisions disappear.

This is a major advantage for the zero-set large sieve because the diagonal

\[
K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2
\]

is not polluted by exact off-diagonal collisions.

So a prime model is a good **testbed** for the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve.

---

# 3. What is lost by using primes only

The canonical AFE packet is not prime-only. It includes all integers:

\[
P_2(m)
=
\sum_{n\in \mathcal B_Q}c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and similarly for the dual branch.

Thus

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

contains prime powers and composites. In log packet-frequency coordinates, many composites lie in the same support range

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q.
\]

The difference between the canonical packet and the prime block is

\[
q''_{\can}-q''_{\prime}
=
P_{2,\mathrm{comp}}
+
D_{2,\mathrm{comp}}
+
E_2,
\]

where

\[
P_{2,\mathrm{comp}}
=
\sum_{\substack{n\in\mathcal B_Q\\ n\notin\mathcal P_Q}}
c_n^+e^{-im\log n},
\]

and similarly for the dual.

This composite part is not obviously perturbative. In ordinary Dirichlet polynomial mass, primes alone do not generally dominate all integers. Depending on the AFE coefficients, the composite packet may contribute comparable or larger \(\ell^2\)-mass.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prime-only }\mathbf M\text{ is not automatically canonical.}
}
\]

A prime-model lower bound does not transfer unless the non-prime packet contribution is either perturbative or can be incorporated without destroying the large-sieve structure.

---

# 4. Transfer attempt

Let

\[
q''_{\model}=q''_{\prime},
\]

and write

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\prime}+r,
\]

where

\[
r=P_{2,\mathrm{comp}}+D_{2,\mathrm{comp}}+E_2.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^{R}
\left(H_j^\prime+H_j^r\right),
\]

with

\[
H_j^r=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)r.
\]

By multilinearity,

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M_{\prime}
+
\sum_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq\{0,\ldots,R\}}
\left(\bigwedge_{j\in A}H_j^r\right)
\wedge
\left(\bigwedge_{j\notin A}H_j^\prime\right).
\]

Thus a sufficient transfer condition is

\[
\|H^r\|_{\mathrm{row}}
\le
Q^{-C}
\|H^\prime\|_{\mathrm{row}}
\]

in a norm compatible with exterior products and condition numbers.

Then

\[
|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\prime}|
\le
Q^{-C'}|\mathbf M_{\prime}|
\]

and therefore

\[
|\mathbf M_{\prime}|\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\can}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

But this requires

\[
\boxed{
P_{2,\mathrm{comp}}+D_{2,\mathrm{comp}}
\text{ is perturbative relative to the prime packet.}
}
\]

That is not currently justified.

---

# 5. Why composite terms are probably not perturbative

The canonical AFE coefficients for \(q''_{\can}\) are weighted by log-derivative powers. Schematically, for many terms,

\[
c_n\sim \frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}(\log n)^k
\]

or related completed-phase weights, depending on the exact representation.

If coefficients involve \(\Lambda(n)\), prime powers appear, but not arbitrary composites. If coefficients involve more general divisor-type AFE coefficients, many composites may contribute.

Two cases:

## Case 1: von Mangoldt-type support

If the relevant \(q''_{\can}\) AFE coefficient is genuinely \(\Lambda(n)\)-supported, then only prime powers enter.

Prime powers \(p^a\) with \(a\ge2\) satisfy

\[
\log p = \frac{1}{a}\log n.
\]

Their total contribution may be smaller, especially for \(a\ge2\), but this needs proof.

In this case, prime-only may be a viable leading model, with prime powers perturbative.

## Case 2: divisor-type support

If the coefficients include divisor convolutions or broader AFE weights, composites are not perturbative. Then prime-only is a toy model and cannot transfer.

Therefore the viability of prime-block transfer depends critically on the exact canonical AFE coefficient support.

Current conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-only transfer is viable only if the canonical }q''_{\can}
\text{ packet is essentially }\Lambda\text{-supported.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Better alternative: squarefree integer model

If prime-only is too restrictive, a better compromise is a **squarefree-supported model** with unique factorization tracked explicitly.

Let \(\mathcal N_Q\) be squarefree integers in the packet support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q.
\]

Then exact collisions

\[
N_S=N_T
\]

can still occur if two different collections of squarefree integers multiply to the same integer. But by lifting to prime exponent vectors,

\[
n\mapsto \mathbf e(n)\in\{0,1\}^{\mathcal P},
\]

one can deduplicate subset-products by their total exponent vector.

The frequency becomes

\[
\Omega_S=\sum_{n\in S}\log n
=
\sum_p E_p(S)\log p.
\]

Exact collisions correspond exactly to equal exponent vectors

\[
E(S)=E(T).
\]

So instead of enforcing prime-only support, one can quotient by exact multiplicative collisions.

This gives a more canonical model while preserving a clean resonance structure.

Thus the better strategy may be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{use canonical integer support, but quotient exact subset-product collisions by prime-exponent vector.}
}
\]

That avoids throwing away potentially leading composite mass.

---

# 7. Prime-block-to-canonical transfer theorem candidate

A transfer theorem can be stated conditionally.

## Prime-Block Transfer Theorem

Let

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\prime}+r
\]

on the ordinary packet-frequency support. Assume:

1. Prime model cofactor lower bound:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

2. Rowwise residual control through all cofactor operators:

\[
\max_{0\le j\le R,\ 0\le \ell\le R+1}
\left|
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\Phi_j(\mathcal D)r(m_0)
\right|
\le
Q^{-A_r}
\cdot \mathcal S_{\prime},
\]

where \(\mathcal S_{\prime}\) is the prime-model row scale.

3. Cofactor condition number control:

\[
\kappa_{\wedge}(\mathcal H^\prime)\le Q^{A_\kappa}.
\]

4. \(A_r\) is large enough compared with \(A,A_\kappa\) and the \(R\)-dependent multilinear expansion loss.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This theorem is valid, but its key hypothesis is the residual control.

---

# 8. Current no-go

Without proving

\[
\|P_{2,\mathrm{comp}}+D_{2,\mathrm{comp}}+E_2\|
\ll
\|P_{2,\prime}+D_{2,\prime}\|,
\]

prime-only lower bounds are insufficient.

In particular, a lower bound for \(\mathbf M_{\prime}\) does not exclude cancellation in

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M_{\prime}
+
\mathbf M_{\mathrm{comp}}
+
\mathbf M_{\mathrm{mixed}}.
\]

Because \(\mathbf M\) is multilinear, mixed minors involving composite terms can be leading, not perturbative.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-only }\mathbf M\text{ is not a safe canonical target unless non-prime contributions are proved perturbative.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Recommendation

Use prime-only blocks for **resonance diagnostics** and **toy large-sieve development**, but do not make the main \(\mathbf M\)-theorem prime-only.

The canonical route should be:

1. Use full canonical packet-frequency support.
2. Represent subset products by prime-exponent vectors.
3. Quotient exact collisions.
4. Bound near-collisions in the exponent-vector model.
5. Prove exterior coefficient mass for the full support.
6. Prove zero-set large sieve on the quotient frequency family.
7. Transfer \(E_2\) by high-derivative canonical error control.

Prime-only is useful only if the exact AFE coefficient analysis shows composites are perturbative.

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-block }\mathbf M\text{ is useful as a clean model, but not canonically sufficient.}
}
\]

A prime-model lower bound transfers to \(\mathbf M_{\can}\) only under a strong residual theorem showing non-prime, tail, and mixed-minor contributions are perturbative.

Absent that theorem, the correct canonical \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve should use the full packet-frequency integer support, with exact subset-product collisions handled by quotienting via prime-exponent vectors.

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not rely on prime-only }\mathbf M\text{ as the main theorem.}
}
\]

Use it as a resonance-clean prototype, but formulate the canonical theorem on full AFE support.

## Agent 3 / C — Prime-block \(\mathbf M\) model and transfer to canonical \(\mathbf M\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: decide whether the first \(\mathbf M\)-large-sieve theorem should be proved on prime-supported packet blocks and then transferred to the full canonical cofactor vector. 

---

# 1. Prime-supported model

Define a prime packet block

\[
\mathcal P_Q=\{p:c_-Q\le \log p\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

A prime-supported model would be

\[
q''_{\prime}
=
P_{2,\prime}+D_{2,\prime}+B_2+E_{2,\rm trunc},
\]

where

\[
P_{2,\prime}(m)
=
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q}
c_p^+(m)e^{-im\log p},
\]

and

\[
D_{2,\prime}(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_q(m)}
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q^-}
c_p^-(m)e^{+im\log p}.
\]

The associated cofactor vector is

\[
\mathbf M_{\prime}(m)
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^{R}
\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\prime}(m),
\]

with the same basis-normalized row and column operators as the canonical object.

The prime-block target would be

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Why prime blocks are attractive

For prime subsets,

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{p\in S}p.
\]

If the subsets are squarefree and unordered, then unique factorization gives

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_S=\Omega_T \iff S=T.
}
\]

So prime blocks remove exact subset-product collisions.

That makes them the cleanest setting for testing:

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\]

in the \((Z_\alpha)\)-zero spectral large sieve.

Thus prime blocks are excellent for:

1. resonance diagnostics;
2. proving a prototype large sieve;
3. testing the subset-product machinery without exact collision clutter.

---

# 3. What is lost by restricting to primes

The canonical AFE packet is not automatically prime-supported. It is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)=\sum_{n}c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and analogously for \(D_2\).

If \(c_n^\pm\) are supported only on \(\Lambda(n)\)-type terms, then the non-prime part consists mainly of prime powers. That may be perturbative.

But if the canonical coefficients contain broader divisor-type or convolutional support, composite integers can carry comparable mass. Then the prime-only model is not canonical.

The residual is

\[
r_{\rm nonprime}
=
(P_2-P_{2,\prime})+(D_2-D_{2,\prime})+E_2.
\]

A prime-model lower bound transfers only if

\[
r_{\rm nonprime}
\]

is perturbative in the cofactor rows. That is currently not guaranteed.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-only }\mathbf M\text{ is safe only if non-prime canonical packet mass is perturbative.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Cofactor multilinearity makes transfer delicate

Write

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\prime}+r.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^{R}
\left(H_j^\prime+H_j^r\right).
\]

Expanding,

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M_{\prime}
+
\sum_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq\{0,\dots,R\}}
\left(\bigwedge_{j\in A}H_j^r\right)
\wedge
\left(\bigwedge_{j\notin A}H_j^\prime\right).
\]

Even if \(r\) is moderate in row norm, mixed minors can be leading if the prime-block cofactor is poorly conditioned.

A sufficient transfer condition is:

\[
\max_j\|H_j^r\|
\le
Q^{-C}
\,s_{\min}(H^\prime),
\]

where \(s_{\min}(H^\prime)\) denotes the relevant smallest exterior singular scale of the prime-model jet block.

Equivalently, in cofactor norm,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\prime}|
\le
\frac12 |\mathbf M_{\prime}|.
}
\]

This requires strong rowwise control through the same derivative depth used in \(\mathbf M\):

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^k r|
\le Q^{-C}.
\]

Without this, a prime-only theorem does not imply the canonical theorem.

---

# 5. Viable transfer theorem

A conditional transfer theorem is:

## Prime-block-to-canonical transfer theorem

Assume:

1. Prime cofactor lower bound:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

2. Rowwise residual control:

\[
\max_{0\le j\le R,\ 0\le \ell\le R+1}
\left|
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\Phi_j(\mathcal D)
(q''_{\can}-q''_{\prime})(m_0)
\right|
\le
Q^{-A_r}\mathcal S_{\prime},
\]

where \(\mathcal S_{\prime}\) is the prime-model row scale.

3. Cofactor condition control:

\[
\kappa_{\wedge}(H^\prime)\le Q^{A_\kappa}.
\]

4. \(A_r\) is larger than \(A+A_\kappa+O(1)\), absorbing multilinear \(R\)-losses.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is mathematically valid, but its residual hypothesis is strong and presently unproved.

---

# 6. Better canonical strategy

A safer route is not to discard composites. Instead:

1. Use the full canonical integer packet support.
2. Represent every integer \(n\) by its prime exponent vector

\[
\mathbf e(n)=(v_p(n))_p.
\]

3. For a subset \(S\),

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
\mathbf E(S)=\sum_{n\in S}\mathbf e(n).
\]

4. Exact subset-product collisions are precisely

\[
\mathbf E(S)=\mathbf E(T).
\]

5. Quotient exact collisions by \(\mathbf E(S)\).

Then the zero-set large sieve is run on the quotient frequency family.

This keeps the canonical mass while still handling exact resonances cleanly.

So the canonical theorem should be built on full AFE support with quotienting, not on prime-only support, unless non-prime perturbativity is proved.

---

# 7. Role of squarefree support

A useful compromise is squarefree support.

For squarefree \(n\), the exponent vectors are \(0/1\). But subset-products of squarefree integers can still collide:

\[
n_1n_2=n_3n_4
\]

through different groupings of prime factors.

So squarefree support does not remove exact collisions; it merely simplifies their combinatorics.

Prime support is collision-free.  
Squarefree support is more canonical but needs quotienting.  
Full integer support is canonical and also needs quotienting.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime support is clean but noncanonical; full support is canonical but collision-rich.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Recommendation

Use prime blocks only as a **prototype** for the zero-set large sieve and subset-product resonance analysis.

The main \(\mathbf M\) theorem should be stated canonically:

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
\]

built from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The resonance theorem should use prime-exponent-vector quotienting rather than prime-only support.

A valid canonical path is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{full packet support}
\rightarrow
\text{quotient exact subset-product collisions}
\rightarrow
\text{bound near-collision clusters}
\rightarrow
\text{zero-set spectral large sieve}
\rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\can}|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-block }\mathbf M\text{ is not sufficient as the main theorem.}
}
\]

It is useful for clean resonance diagnostics, but a prime-model lower bound transfers to the canonical cofactor only under a strong non-prime perturbation theorem.

The correct canonical formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{full AFE support with exact subset-product collisions quotiented by prime-exponent vectors.}
}
\]

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not make }\mathbf M_{\prime}\text{ the proof target unless non-prime perturbativity is first proved.}
}
\]

The proof target should remain \(\mathbf M_{\can}\), with resonance quotienting and canonical high-derivative transfer built in.

## Agent 3 / C — Prime-block theorem versus canonical \(\mathbf M_{\can}\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: decide whether the proof should use a prime-only \(\mathbf M\) theorem as a model, or whether the cofactor theorem must be canonical/full-support from the start. 

---

# 1. Prime-block model

Define a prime-supported packet model

\[
q''_{\prime}
=
B_2+P_{2,\prime}+D_{2,\prime}+E_{2,\rm trunc},
\]

where

\[
P_{2,\prime}(m)
=
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q}
c_p^+(m)e^{-im\log p},
\]

and

\[
D_{2,\prime}(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_q(m)}
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_Q^-}
c_p^-(m)e^{+im\log p}.
\]

The prime-supported cofactor vector is

\[
\mathbf M_{\prime}
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^R
\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\prime},
\]

using the same basis-normalized cofactor construction as

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}.
\]

The prime-block theorem would be

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Prime support is attractive because, for prime subsets,

\[
N_S=\prod_{p\in S}p
\]

has exact collision freeness:

\[
N_S=N_T
\iff
S=T.
\]

So the subset-product resonance structure is much cleaner.

---

# 2. Missing canonical terms

The canonical curvature is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The difference between the canonical object and the prime model is

\[
q''_{\can}-q''_{\prime}
=
(P_2-P_{2,\prime})
+
(D_2-D_{2,\prime})
+
(E_2-E_{2,\rm trunc}).
\]

Call this residual

\[
r_{\rm np}.
\]

Then

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\prime}+r_{\rm np}.
\]

Since \(\mathbf M\) is an \((R+1)\)-fold exterior product in the source rows,

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\bigwedge_{j=0}^R
\left(H_j^\prime+H_j^{\rm np}\right),
\]

where

\[
H_j^\prime=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\prime},
\qquad
H_j^{\rm np}=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)r_{\rm np}.
\]

Expanding,

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M_{\prime}
+
\sum_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq\{0,\dots,R\}}
\left(\bigwedge_{j\in A}H_j^{\rm np}\right)
\wedge
\left(\bigwedge_{j\notin A}H_j^\prime\right).
\]

So prime-block transfer requires every residual-containing mixed exterior term to be perturbative relative to \(\mathbf M_{\prime}\).

That is a strong condition.

---

# 3. Coefficient-support cases

Whether the prime model can transfer depends on the actual canonical AFE coefficient support.

## Case 1 — \(\Lambda(n)\)-supported coefficients

If the relevant packet coefficients are essentially von Mangoldt-supported,

\[
c_n\sim \Lambda(n)\cdot \text{smooth weight},
\]

then non-prime support consists mostly of prime powers

\[
n=p^a,\qquad a\ge2.
\]

Prime powers have

\[
\log p=\frac1a\log n,
\]

and their density and total mass may be lower.

In that case, a prime-only leading model may be viable if one proves

\[
\|P_{2,\rm pp}+D_{2,\rm pp}\|_{C^{2R+1}}
\le Q^{-C}
\|P_{2,\prime}+D_{2,\prime}\|_{C^{2R+1}}.
\]

But this requires a real estimate. It cannot be assumed.

## Case 2 — prime-power residual only, but not small

Even if only prime powers are omitted, their contribution may not be negligible after high derivatives. Derivatives multiply by powers of

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

so derivative order does not strongly suppress them. If their coefficient mass is polynomially comparable, mixed minors can be leading.

Then prime-only transfer fails unless prime powers are included in the leading model or controlled separately.

## Case 3 — divisor/convolution-supported coefficients

If the canonical AFE coefficients include divisor-like or convolutional support, composites may carry substantial mass.

Then

\[
P_2-P_{2,\prime}
\]

is not perturbative. Prime-only \(\mathbf M\) is only a toy model.

## Case 4 — full integer AFE support

If all integers in the packet support contribute meaningfully, the canonical theorem must use full support from the start.

Then exact subset-product collisions are abundant and must be quotient-handled by prime exponent vectors.

---

# 4. Conditional transfer theorem

The best valid transfer statement is conditional.

## Prime-block-to-canonical transfer theorem

Assume:

1. Prime cofactor lower bound:

\[
|\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

2. Residual row control through all cofactor operators:

\[
\max_{0\le j\le R}
\left\|
\Phi_j(\mathcal D)r_{\rm np}
\right\|
\le
Q^{-A_r}
\cdot
s_{\rm row}(\mathcal H^\prime),
\]

and similarly after all column operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\), up to derivative order

\[
2R+1.
\]

3. Exterior condition control:

\[
\kappa_\wedge(\mathcal H^\prime)\le Q^{A_\kappa}.
\]

4. \(A_r\) is large enough to absorb the multilinear expansion losses:

\[
A_r\gg A+A_\kappa+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)-\mathbf M_{\prime}(m_0)|
\le
\frac12Q^{-A},
\]

and hence

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This theorem is correct, but the crucial hypothesis is residual perturbativity of the non-prime packet.

---

# 5. Why prime-only should not be the main proof target

Without proving

\[
r_{\rm np}
=
(P_2-P_{2,\prime})+(D_2-D_{2,\prime})+(E_2-E_{2,\rm trunc})
\]

is perturbative through \(2R+1\) normalized derivatives, a prime-only theorem does not imply the canonical theorem.

Moreover, because \(\mathbf M\) is multilinear, even moderate residual rows can generate leading mixed minors:

\[
H_0^\prime\wedge\cdots\wedge H_{j-1}^\prime
\wedge H_j^{\rm np}
\wedge H_{j+1}^\prime\wedge\cdots\wedge H_R^\prime.
\]

So it is not enough to show prime mass is nonzero. One must show the omitted mass is lower order relative to the exterior geometry.

At present, that is not established.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-only }\mathbf M\text{ is a clean model, not a canonical proof target.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Better canonical route: full-support quotienting

The safer route is:

1. Use the full canonical AFE packet support.
2. Encode each integer \(n\) by its prime exponent vector:

\[
\mathbf e(n)=(v_p(n))_p.
\]

3. For a subset \(S\), define

\[
\mathbf E(S)=\sum_{n\in S}\mathbf e(n).
\]

4. Exact subset-product collisions are exactly

\[
N_S=N_T
\iff
\mathbf E(S)=\mathbf E(T).
\]

5. Quotient the exact collision classes:

\[
[S]_{\rm exact}=\{T:\mathbf E(T)=\mathbf E(S)\}.
\]

6. Prove near-collision estimates between quotient classes:

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le\eta.
\]

This keeps the canonical mass and handles collision structure honestly.

The quotient-support theorem should be the main \(\mathbf M\) formulation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full canonical support}
\to
\text{exponent-vector quotient}
\to
\text{near-collision bounds}
\to
\text{zero-set spectral large sieve}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Role of prime blocks

Prime blocks remain useful for two things.

## 7.1 Prototype resonance theorem

For prime support,

\[
N_S=N_T\iff S=T,
\]

so exact collisions vanish. This is the cleanest first setting for developing the kernel theory.

## 7.2 Numerical/stress diagnostic

Prime support can expose whether the zero-set spectral kernel has any chance without collision complications.

But a prime-block proof must be followed by a non-prime perturbativity theorem before it can be canonical.

---

# 8. Final recommendation

Do **not** make

\[
\mathbf M_{\prime}
\]

the main theorem unless the exact AFE coefficients show non-prime terms are perturbative.

Instead, formulate the main theorem as:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
}
\]

where \(\mathbf M_{\can}\) is built from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

For the averaged route, formulate the large sieve on the full-support quotient frequency family:

\[
\Omega_{[S]}=\log N_S,
\]

with exact collisions quotiented by

\[
\mathbf E(S).
\]

The prime-supported theorem may be retained as a **prototype** or **special case**, not the canonical endpoint.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-block }\mathbf M\text{ is insufficient as the main proof target.}
}
\]

A transfer theorem exists only under strong residual control:

\[
\|q''_{\can}-q''_{\prime}\|_{C^{2R+1}}\ll Q^{-A}
\]

relative to the prime cofactor row scale.

Since that is not currently established, the correct \(\mathbf M\)-route must use full canonical AFE support with exponent-vector quotienting of exact subset-product collisions.

Thus the next \(\mathbf M\)-work should prioritize:

\[
\boxed{
\text{full-support resonance quotienting + zero-set spectral large sieve.}
}
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Folded main/dual structure in the final angle

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: analyze whether folded main/dual arithmetic gives a nonalignment mechanism for

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]

in the final Wronskian angle theorem. The current shared background treats the cell theorem and \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence as parked inputs, leaving the final angle/incidence obstruction as the active target. 

---

# 1. Target

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the normalized Wronskian expands as

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

Assume the parked inputs:

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The remaining theorem is the angle bound

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
\not\perp
\mathbf M(m_0)
}
\]

with polynomial margin.

---

# 2. Main/dual decomposition

Write

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\mathbf z'_+
+
\mathbf z'_-
+
\mathbf z'_{B}
+
\mathbf z'_{E},
\]

where \(+\) is the main AFE branch, \(-\) is the folded dual branch, and \(B,E\) denote background/error contributions.

Similarly,

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_+
+
\mathbf M_-
+
\mathbf M_{\rm mix}
+
\mathbf M_{B}
+
\mathbf M_E.
\]

Then

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
+
\text{background/error}.
\]

The pure-main term has subset-product phases of the form

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nN_S)}.
\]

The pure-dual term has folded dual phases of the form

\[
e^{+im_0\log(nN_S)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}
\]

for an appropriate gamma-phase power \(k\).

The mixed terms have phases of the form

\[
e^{-im_0\log N_+}e^{+im_0\log N_-}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}
=
e^{-im_0\log(N_+/N_-)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

So the final pairing is a **folded subset-product exponential sum**, with pure-main, pure-dual, and mixed quotient phases.

---

# 3. Tilted regime: \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\)

In the tilted regime, the main and dual branch magnitudes differ by a polynomial factor. Schematically,

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q}.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C\log Q,
\]

one branch dominates after absorbing polynomial losses.

This suggests the following conditional theorem.

## Tilted final-angle theorem

Assume

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

and suppose the dominant branch also dominates the cofactor vector:

\[
|\mathbf z'_{\rm dom}|\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'|,
\]

\[
|\mathbf M_{\rm dom}|\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf M|.
\]

If the dominant-branch pairing satisfies

\[
|\langle \mathbf z'_{\rm dom},\mathbf M_{\rm dom}\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'_{\rm dom}||\mathbf M_{\rm dom}|,
\]

then the full angle theorem follows, because the subordinate branch and mixed/error terms are polynomially smaller.

However, the last displayed inequality is still an incidence statement inside the dominant branch. Branch dominance removes main/dual cancellation, but it does **not** automatically prove that

\[
\mathbf z'_{\rm dom}
\not\perp
\mathbf M_{\rm dom}.
\]

So in the tilted regime, main/dual structure simplifies the problem but does not close it.

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q
\text{ reduces final angle to a one-branch incidence theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Symmetric regime: \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\)

The hard case is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

Here main and dual magnitudes are comparable. Branch dominance is unavailable.

The final pairing contains terms such as

\[
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle,
\]

with folded phases satisfying complementary product relations.

At the cell-vector level, the key relation was

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

At the cofactor level, the analogous relation is

\[
nN_- \approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi} N_+
\]

or, more generally,

\[
\frac{N_+}{N_-}\approx \text{conductor-scale factor},
\]

depending on which branch contributes to \(\mathbf z'\) and which branch contributes to \(\mathbf M\).

The mixed phase is therefore

\[
e^{-im_0\log(N_+/N_-)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

A possible nonalignment theorem would need to show that these folded quotient phases cannot cancel the pure-branch contributions so as to make

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0.
\]

No sign or positivity is visible.

---

# 5. Search for a commutator or skew invariant

A plausible candidate would be a skew pairing such as

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm skew}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\right).
\]

If this had a fixed sign or a lower bound, it could prove nonalignment.

But after expanding the folded phases, one obtains sums of the form

\[
\sum_{n,S}
C_{n,S}^{+-}
e^{-im_0\log(n/N_S)}
e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}
-
\sum_{n,S}
C_{n,S}^{-+}
e^{+im_0\log(n/N_S)}
e^{ik'\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

The two sums are not conjugates with a positive sign; their coefficients depend on different AFE weights, basis functions, and exterior minors.

The gamma phase rotates terms but does not impose positivity.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No sign-definite skew/commutator invariant is visible.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Search for Hermitian positivity

Another possible route would be to express the final pairing as a Gram-type positive form:

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\stackrel{?}{=}
\langle U,U\rangle
+
\text{small error}.
\]

But \(\mathbf M\) is a cofactor/Hodge-dual vector of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet block, while \(\mathbf z'\) is the derivative row of \(Z_\alpha\).

The pairing is a determinant/oriented volume, not a norm square. It can have either sign and arbitrary phase.

Exterior algebra gives

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathbf z'\\
q''_{\rm can}\text{-jet rows}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

which is an oriented volume. Oriented volumes have no inherent positivity.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hodge-dual geometry gives a determinant, not a positive Gram form.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Relation to symbol-rank theorem

Earlier symbol-rank work showed that the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol is not polynomially generated by the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet symbols on packet-frequency blocks.

This proves a coefficient-level nondegeneracy:

\[
z_\alpha(x)
\notin
\operatorname{span}
\{q''_{\rm can}(x),\mathcal Dq''_{\rm can}(x),\dots,\mathcal D^Rq''_{\rm can}(x)\}
\]

in a model symbol sense.

But the final angle theorem is pointwise in \(m_0\), after actual phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

and subset-product cancellations have been applied.

Symbol rank prevents formal row redundancy. It does not prevent the actual exponential sums from producing

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0)\in V(m_0)
\]

approximately, where \(V(m_0)\) is the span of the \(q''_{\rm can}\)-jet rows at \(m_0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank does not by itself imply the pointwise angle bound.}
}
\]

It supplies coefficient-level transversality, but the actual theorem still needs orbit-level nonrecurrence.

---

# 8. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, the final angle theorem fails.

Let the phases in \(\mathbf z'\) and in the subset-product expansion of \(\mathbf M\) vary with enough freedom. Then one can impose:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but also

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

This is just orthogonality of two nonzero vectors in a high-dimensional complex space.

Therefore, as in the cell and \(\mathbf M\) branches, the proof must use the actual one-parameter orbit and exact zeta coefficients.

---

# 9. The named theorem needed

The final ordinary-route theorem should be named:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment Theorem.}
}
\]

A precise statement:

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Assume the canonical Wronskian is built from

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\rm can},
\quad 0\le j\le R,
\]

with

\[
q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

At every admissible zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

assuming

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A'}
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Regime split

## Tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q.
\]

Main/dual dominance may reduce the theorem to one-branch angle nonalignment. It does not eliminate the need for actual-orbit incidence, but it simplifies the branch structure.

## Intermediate regime

\[
1\lesssim |\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

Some branch imbalance exists but may not be polynomially decisive. One may get partial savings but probably not a full proof.

## Symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

This is the hard case. Folded main/dual terms are comparable. The final theorem is a folded subset-product actual-orbit nonrecurrence statement.

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No structural folded main/dual angle proof is currently visible.}
}
\]

Main/dual structure helps in tilted regimes by reducing the number of active branches. But in the hard symmetric regime, it reduces to an actual-orbit folded subset-product nonrecurrence theorem.

The final theorem should be parked as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment}
}
\]

unless another agent finds a genuine exterior-angle or common-small-value proof.

This is the third ordinary-route black-box input after:

1. Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence;
2. Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence;
3. Wronskian Angle Nonalignment.

## Agent 3 / C — Folded main/dual angle structure

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: determine whether main/dual arithmetic supplies a nonalignment mechanism for

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]

in the final Wronskian angle theorem. The current prompt treats the cell theorem and \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence as parked inputs, leaving the final angle/incidence obstruction as the active target. 

---

# 1. Target

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

we have

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

Assume the parked inputs:

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The remaining theorem is

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

The question here is whether folded main/dual structure can prove this angle lower bound.

---

# 2. Main/dual decomposition

Write

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\mathbf z'_+
+
\mathbf z'_-
+
\mathbf z'_B
+
\mathbf z'_E,
\]

where:

- \(\mathbf z'_+\) is the main AFE contribution;
- \(\mathbf z'_-\) is the folded dual contribution;
- \(\mathbf z'_B\) is the gamma/background contribution;
- \(\mathbf z'_E\) is the error/tail contribution.

Similarly decompose the cofactor vector:

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_+
+
\mathbf M_-
+
\mathbf M_{\rm mix}
+
\mathbf M_B
+
\mathbf M_E.
\]

Then

\[
\begin{aligned}
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
={}&
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle \\
&+
\langle \mathbf z'_+ + \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z'_B,\mathbf M\rangle
+
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M_B\rangle
+
\text{error terms}.
\end{aligned}
\]

At the phase level:

- pure-main terms have phases like

\[
e^{-im_0\log(nN_S)};
\]

- pure-dual terms have phases like

\[
e^{+im_0\log(nN_S)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)};
\]

- mixed terms have folded quotient phases like

\[
e^{-im_0\log(N_+/N_-)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

Thus the final pairing is a folded subset-product exponential sum, with no immediate positivity.

---

# 3. Tilted regime: \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\)

In the tilted regime, one branch has polynomially larger coefficient mass. Schematically,

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q}.
\]

So if

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C\log Q
\]

with \(C\) sufficiently large, one branch dominates.

This helps but does **not** close the final angle theorem.

It can reduce the final pairing to a dominant-branch problem:

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\langle \mathbf z'_{\rm dom},\mathbf M_{\rm dom}\rangle
+
\text{lower-order branch terms},
\]

provided the dominance also holds in the cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\). Then it is enough to prove

\[
|\langle \mathbf z'_{\rm dom},\mathbf M_{\rm dom}\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'_{\rm dom}||\mathbf M_{\rm dom}|.
\]

But this is still a one-branch incidence theorem. Branch dominance removes main/dual cancellation; it does not prove that the dominant \(\mathbf z'\)-row is nonorthogonal to the dominant cofactor vector.

So the tilted branch gives:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{final angle reduces to one-branch actual-orbit incidence.}
}
\]

It does not produce a structural proof.

---

# 4. Intermediate and symmetric regimes

## Intermediate regime

\[
1\lesssim |\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

There is some branch imbalance, but not enough to dominate all polynomial losses. The final pairing may receive comparable contributions from main, dual, and mixed terms.

This regime may admit savings, but not a clean dominance theorem.

## Hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

Here main and dual are genuinely comparable. This is the hard case.

The folded relation produces complementary subset-product phases. At the cell level this was

\[
nn'\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}.
\]

At the cofactor level the corresponding relation is of the form

\[
nN_-\approx \frac{m_0}{2\pi}N_+
\]

or, depending on which component contributes to \(\mathbf z'\) and which to \(\mathbf M\),

\[
\frac{N_+}{N_-}\approx \text{conductor-scale factor}.
\]

The mixed phase is therefore

\[
e^{-im_0\log(N_+/N_-)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

This is useful structure, but it does not have a sign or positivity.

The hard symmetric theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{folded subset-product phases cannot align so that }
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0.
}
\]

That is an actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 5. Search for a commutator or skew invariant

A natural candidate is a skew main/dual expression such as

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm skew}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\right).
\]

A useful theorem would show

\[
|\mathcal I_{\rm skew}|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

But after expansion, the two terms involve different folded subset-product coefficients and phases:

\[
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
\sim
\sum_{n,S}
C^{+-}_{n,S}
e^{-im_0\log(n/N_S)}e^{ik\Theta(m_0)},
\]

while

\[
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\sim
\sum_{n,S}
C^{-+}_{n,S}
e^{+im_0\log(n/N_S)}e^{ik'\Theta(m_0)}.
\]

They are not conjugate positive pieces. The coefficients come from different AFE weights, different exterior minors, and different branch conventions.

So I do **not** see a sign-definite skew invariant.

\[
\boxed{
\text{No usable main/dual commutator or skew invariant is visible.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Search for Hermitian positivity

Another possible route would be to rewrite

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]

as a norm square or Hermitian form.

But \(\mathbf M\) is the Hodge dual of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet row block. The pairing is an oriented determinant:

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathbf z' \\
q''_{\can}\text{-jet rows}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Determinants are signed/complex oriented volumes, not positive quadratic forms.

So exterior algebra gives the correct geometry but not positivity.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hodge-dual geometry identifies the angle; it does not lower-bound it.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Relation to \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank

Earlier packet-frequency symbol-rank results show that the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol is not polynomially generated by the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols. That is a coefficient-level transversality statement.

But the final angle theorem is pointwise after actual phases have been evaluated at \(m_0\). The bad event is

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\in V(m_0),
\]

where \(V(m_0)\) is the row span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block.

Symbol rank does not exclude a pointwise phase accident:

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
\approx
\sum_{j=0}^R a_j(m_0)\mathbf q_j(m_0).
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank does not imply the final angle theorem.}
}
\]

It prevents formal redundancy, not actual-orbit incidence.

---

# 8. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, the final angle theorem fails.

One can have:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but choose phases so that

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

This is just orthogonality of two nonzero complex vectors in a high-dimensional space.

Even retaining the main/dual folded structure, if the actual one-parameter orbit constraint is relaxed, there is enough freedom to tune the final determinant to zero.

Therefore, any proof must use the actual phase law

\[
e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

the folded dual law, and the exact canonical AFE coefficients.

---

# 9. The named theorem needed

The final ordinary input should be named:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence Theorem}.
}
\]

A precise statement is:

Assume ordinary scale, basis-normalized Wronskian construction, and canonical source

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

At every admissible zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

if

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A'}
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Folded main/dual structure does not currently prove the final angle theorem.}
}
\]

What it gives:

- In the tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

it can reduce the problem to a dominant-branch incidence theorem.

- In the symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

it identifies the relevant folded subset-product phase geometry.

What it does **not** give:

- sign;
- positivity;
- Hermitian coercivity;
- a usable commutator;
- a pointwise exterior-angle lower bound.

So Agent 3’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final angle/incidence remains an actual-orbit folded subset-product nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

Unless another agent finds a genuine structural mechanism, this should now be parked as the third ordinary-route black-box input.

## Agent 3 / C — Gate 2 row conversion and \(q_0\)-wall audit

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: audit the downstream Gate 2 / row-conversion layer, especially the unresolved \(q_0\)-wall. The current prompt places this after the ordinary Gate 1 stack has been reduced to named arithmetic inputs. 

---

# 1. What Gate 1 provides

Gate 1 gives source-curvature mass:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

Write

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

So Gate 1 gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|u(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This is a source-mass statement. It does **not** by itself give the final row lower bound, because the row architecture is source-divisible.

---

# 2. Gate 2 / row-conversion target

The current Gate 2 target is roughly:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|u(m)|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2
\right)\,dm
\ge
Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

Known structural rows have schematic leading form:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

where

\[
H=yq''_{\can}.
\]

At leading source order,

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Therefore, even if Gate 2 proves anisotropy-weighted source mass, the final row lower bound still needs a source-factor conversion:

\[
\boxed{
|H|\gtrsim Q^{-C}|u|^3
}
\]

or an alternative row/invariant that remains visible when \(H\) degenerates.

---

# 3. Why the \(q_0\)-wall is real

The source factor has leading behavior

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Thus if

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

then the known row pair

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

can collapse even when

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

is non-small and anisotropy is present.

This is not merely a technicality. Gate 1 only says \(u\) has \(L^2\)-mass. It does not forbid that mass from lying near points where

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

Indeed,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

this becomes

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

So the anisotropy factor can remain live exactly where the known source factor \(H\) loses \(q_0\). Therefore a sampling lemma of the form

\[
\text{Gate 1 or Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\text{ at a good row point}
\]

is false under the current assumptions.

---

# 4. What Gate 2 can and cannot solve

Gate 2 can plausibly show:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\ge
Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

This handles the anisotropy channel.

But the final row lower bound from the known rows requires more:

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|^2+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|^2
\sim
|H|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Since

\[
|H|^2\sim |q_0|^2|u|^6,
\]

one needs either:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on enough of the Gate 2 mass, or a replacement row/invariant whose leading term is not divisible by \(q_0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 does not by itself remove the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Required downstream split

The downstream proof must split into two regimes.

## Branch A — nondegenerate \(q_0\)

Assume there is a substantial sampling set or point \(m_\ast\in I_\rho\) where

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
(\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
|H(m_\ast)|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C_q}|u(m_\ast)|^3,
\]

and hence

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|^2+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|^2
\gtrsim
Q^{-C}
|u(m_\ast)|^6
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

This branch is conceptually straightforward once:

1. Gate 1 gives source mass;
2. Gate 2 gives anisotropy-weighted source mass;
3. a sampling lemma gives a point with \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}\).

But the sampling lemma cannot be assumed globally. It is a conditional branch.

---

## Branch B — \(q_0\)-wall

Assume instead that the relevant mass lies where

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Then the known \(H\)-driven rows may be too small.

At \(q_0\approx0\),

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u.
\]

So the geometry is not dead: source curvature remains visible in \(\Gamma_G\). What fails is the known row conversion through \(H\).

This branch needs one of the following.

### B1. Source-robust row

Find a row/invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) such that near \(q_0=0\),

\[
R_{\rm rob}
\sim
u^\beta \cdot \mathcal A
\]

with

\[
\beta>0,
\]

and \(\mathcal A\) not carrying a fatal \(q_0\)-factor.

A useful target would be:

\[
\boxed{
|R_{\rm rob}(m_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-C}|u(m_\ast)|^\beta
}
\]

on the \(q_0\)-wall branch.

No certified row of this type is currently available.

### B2. \(q_0\)-wall impossibility

Prove that Gate 2 mass cannot concentrate where

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

But current identities suggest this is false, because

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

is compatible with

\[
q_0=0,\qquad \Gamma_G=u.
\]

So this route is not promising unless additional global constraints on \(q_0\) are introduced.

### B3. Higher-order correction row

Prove that when

\[
q_0\approx0
\]

and \(u\) is non-small, the row algebra produces a different leading row at higher order.

This is possible but unproved. It requires explicit row search/algebra, not just Gate 1/Gate 2.

---

# 6. Gate 2 theorem checklist

## 6.1 Nondegenerate branch theorem

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{gathered}
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|,\\
\text{and enough of this mass lies where }|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
\end{gathered}
}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I_\rho:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditional/open}
}
\]

because the mass-location hypothesis is not guaranteed.

---

## 6.2 \(q_0\)-wall theorem

Needed theorem:

Either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass cannot concentrate on }|q_0|<Q^{-C_q},
}
\]

or:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is a source-robust row visible on }|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{open}
}
\]

and the first alternative is probably false under current identities.

---

## 6.3 Correction-cancellation control

Even in the nondegenerate branch, one must ensure lower-order/correction rows do not cancel the leading row terms.

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{leading row contribution dominates correction terms by }Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This requires:

1. finite-order row expansion;
2. derivative complexity bounds;
3. canonical source error control;
4. no cancellation between \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) and \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) channels.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditional/open but likely local-analytic once correct rows are fixed.}
}
\]

---

## 6.4 Source-robust fallback row

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q},\ |u|\ge Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\exists R_{\rm rob}: |R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not found}
}
\]

This is the main unresolved downstream algebraic issue.

---

# 7. Final downstream dependency map

Assuming ordinary Gate 1 is proved via Inputs 1–3, the downstream chain still needs:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

Gate 2 itself likely reduces to:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{anisotropy propagation}
+
\text{ODE/base-locus rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\int|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

But the final row conversion requires:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either }|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}\text{ on a good row point,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a source-robust row at the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

At present, this is still open.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 does not automatically close the downstream row conversion.}
}
\]

The \(q_0\)-wall is a real remaining obstruction.

The downstream status is:

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Gate 1 source mass | conditional on named arithmetic inputs |
| Gate 2 anisotropy/source propagation | plausible but still conditional |
| nondegenerate \(q_0\) row conversion | conditional |
| \(q_0\)-wall exclusion | open / likely false as stated |
| source-robust row at \(q_0\approx0\) | open |
| correction-cancellation control | open local-algebra task |

So the exact downstream split is:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{known row architecture may close,}
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{need new source-robust row or invariant.}
}
\]

This should be treated as a separate downstream theorem, not as something already supplied by Gate 1 or Gate 2.
