## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:30:25)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 3 / C — Gate 2 anisotropy propagation

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: formulate and attack Gate 2 after Gate 1, with focus on whether source mass forces anisotropy-weighted source mass. The current prompt places this downstream of the now-conditional ordinary Gate 1 architecture. 

---

# 1. Gate 1 input

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 provides

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|u(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

Gate 2 wants

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|u(m)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

So the missing implication is:

\[
\text{source mass}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{source mass away from anisotropy base-locus}.
\]

---

# 2. Anisotropy quantities

The known expression is

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

The second anisotropy channel satisfies the identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

up to the established convention for the local variable and normalized differentiation.

Thus the base-locus for Gate 2 is

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
}
\]

In terms of \(u\) and \(q_0\),

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
u\approx 6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

If additionally

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma_G''\approx 12q(q')^2.
\]

So Gate 2 fails only if the \(u\)-mass of Gate 1 concentrates near a constrained nonlinear ODE-like base-locus.

---

# 3. Gate 1 alone does not imply Gate 2

Purely measure-theoretically,

\[
\int |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

does not imply

\[
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

A countermodel is easy at the level of arbitrary functions:

take \(u\) nonzero and choose \(q_0\) so that

\[
u=6q_0-2q_0^3,
\]

and then choose higher derivatives so that

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

Thus Gate 2 needs structural rigidity of the actual \(q_\zeta\)-derived functions. It is not a formal consequence of Gate 1.

---

# 4. Base-locus rigidity formulation

The required theorem should be stated as an ODE/base-locus rigidity result.

## Gate 2 Base-Locus Rigidity Theorem

Assume ordinary or mildly singular scale, canonical derivative bounds

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q_\zeta|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0,
\]

with \(k_0\) at least \(6\), and denominator/separation assumptions already used in the local model.

If

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|u|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

Contrapositive:

If

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|u|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I_\rho|,
\]

then either

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

or \(q_\zeta\) lies within \(Q^{-C}\) of the base-locus solution set

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

on a thick subset, forcing a forbidden local ODE relation.

---

# 5. How to prove the rigidity theorem

A plausible proof has four parts.

## Step 1: Thick set from weighted smallness

Assume Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

but

\[
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then there is a thick subset \(E\subset I\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C}.
\]

This step uses Markov/Chebyshev plus derivative/Remez propagation to avoid mass hiding in extremely tiny sets.

## Step 2: Remez/Bernstein propagation

With derivative complexity

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q_\zeta|\le Q^{C_k},
\]

smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) on a thick set propagates to a controlled subinterval:

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C'}
\]

on \(I'\subset I\).

This requires \(q_\zeta\)-complexity bounds and a quantitative Remez inequality.

## Step 3: ODE base-locus rigidity

On \(I'\),

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0
\]

gives

\[
u\approx 6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Since

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

this is an approximate second-order ODE:

\[
q_0''\approx 6q_0-2q_0^3
\]

in the appropriate normalized coordinate.

The second condition

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

adds

\[
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\approx0.
\]

If \(\Gamma_G\approx0\) with enough derivative control, then \(\Gamma_G''\approx0\), so

\[
q(q')^2\approx0.
\]

Thus the base-locus forces either:

\[
q\approx0,
\]

or

\[
q'\approx0.
\]

Together with

\[
q''\approx 6q-2q^3,
\]

this may force \(q\) into a low-dimensional rigid family.

## Step 4: Exclude rigid family using source mass / packet geometry

The rigid family must be incompatible with Gate 1 source mass on an off-line packet, or with canonical zeta packet structure.

For example:

- if \(q\approx0\), then the ODE gives \(u=q''\approx0\), contradicting \(|u|\ge Q^{-C}\);
- if \(q'\approx0\), then \(q\) is locally nearly constant, and the ODE forces \(u\approx6q-2q^3\); additional phase/kernel constraints may exclude nonzero constant solutions.

This is the real Gate 2 rigidity step.

---

# 6. Potential obstruction

There may be nonzero approximate solutions to

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
q(q')^2=0
\]

with

\[
u=q''\ne0.
\]

If \(q'\approx0\) and \(q\approx c\), then

\[
u\approx 6c-2c^3.
\]

This is nonzero unless

\[
c\in\{0,\pm\sqrt3\}.
\]

So the base-locus may allow locally constant \(q\) with nonzero \(u\), at least formally. But if \(q\) is locally constant, then \(q''\approx0\), so consistency requires

\[
6c-2c^3\approx0.
\]

Thus \(c\in\{0,\pm\sqrt3\}\), and then \(u\approx0\). This contradicts the thick-set \(|u|\ge Q^{-C}\).

So the exact base-locus appears rigid enough, but the approximate quantitative proof must be supplied.

---

# 7. Needed derivative order

Gate 2 uses

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

and

\[
u=q'',
\]

we need at least fourth derivatives of \(q\) to control \(\Gamma_G''\). For propagation/Remez and correction control, it is safer to assume derivative bounds through order

\[
6
\]

or higher.

Thus the derivative package should include

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q_\zeta|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6.
}
\]

This is consistent with earlier Gate 2 notes.

---

# 8. Gate 2 theorem candidate

A clean theorem statement:

## Gate 2 Anisotropy Propagation Theorem

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Assume on \(I_\rho^\ast\):

1. canonical derivative complexity

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq_\zeta|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6;
\]

2. no singular denominator collapse, or singular branch has been handled separately;

3. quantitative Remez/Bernstein propagation for \(q_\zeta\)-generated functions;

4. base-locus rigidity:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,\quad\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\quad\text{on a thick set}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0
\quad\text{on a thick set}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\Rightarrow
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This is the Gate 2 theorem needed downstream.

---

# 9. Status

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Gate 1 source mass | conditional on ordinary/singular named inputs |
| derivative complexity through order \(6\) | plausible/canonical audit needed |
| Remez/Bernstein propagation | conditional but standard-type |
| base-locus rigidity \(\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0\Rightarrow u=0\) | plausible, needs quantitative proof |
| full Gate 2 theorem | open/conditional |

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is not automatic from Gate 1, but it has a plausible local rigidity route.}
}
\]

The exact remaining Gate 2 input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Anisotropy Base-Locus Rigidity: }
\Gamma_G\approx0,\quad\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\text{ on }u\text{-mass}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0.
}
\]

If this is proved with quantitative Remez/Bernstein propagation and derivative bounds, then Gate 1 implies Gate 2.

But this still does **not** solve the downstream \(q_0\)-wall. Even with Gate 2, the known row conversion remains obstructed when

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:34:16)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 3 / C — \(q_0\)-wall exclusion test

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: test whether Gate 2 mass can force a \(q_0\)-nondegenerate sampling point, or whether the \(q_0\)-wall is real and must be handled by a source-robust row. 

---

# 1. Desired sampling theorem

The hoped-for downstream theorem is:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\]

implies the existence of a point \(m_\ast\in I\) such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
(\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If true, the known rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

would be usable because

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

But this sampling theorem is **not** valid under the current assumptions.

---

# 2. Wall case analysis

Recall

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

If

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

unless there is a compensating \(6q_0-2q_0^3\) term, which is absent at the wall.

So on the \(q_0\)-wall,

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2
\approx |u|^4.
\]

Thus Gate 2 mass can remain large even when \(q_0\) is small.

Concretely, the local model

\[
q_0(m)=\varepsilon
\]

with

\[
|\varepsilon|\ll Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
u(m)=u_0,
\qquad |u_0|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

gives

\[
\Gamma_G=u_0-6\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3)
\approx u_0.
\]

Then

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2
\approx |u_0|^4,
\]

which can easily be polynomially non-small.

This shows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass does not force }|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Local countermodel with live Gate 2 mass

A clean local countermodel is:

\[
q_0(m)=\varepsilon+\frac12 u_0(m-m_\ast)^2
\]

near \(m_\ast\), with

\[
|\varepsilon|\ll Q^{-C},
\qquad
|u_0|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Then at \(m=m_\ast\),

\[
q_0(m_\ast)=\varepsilon\approx0,
\]

and

\[
u(m_\ast)=q_0''(m_\ast)\approx u_0.
\]

Hence

\[
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)
=
u_0-6\varepsilon+O(\varepsilon^3)
\approx u_0.
\]

For \(\Gamma_{G,2}\), using

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

we can arrange locally that \(q'(m_\ast)=0\) and \(\Gamma_G''(m_\ast)\) is controlled, so \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is not necessarily large, but this does not matter because \(\Gamma_G\) is already live.

Thus

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\]

is live while

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

This is precisely the \(q_0\)-wall.

---

# 4. Do canonical derivative / ODE constraints forbid the model?

The local model is not obviously forbidden by the canonical identities currently in use.

The Gate 2 base-locus rigidity concerns simultaneous smallness:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

But the \(q_0\)-wall model has

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u\not\approx0.
\]

So it is **not** near the anisotropy base-locus. Gate 2 sees it as good anisotropy mass.

The problem is downstream row conversion, because the row source factor

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\]

vanishes with \(q_0\).

Therefore canonical Gate 2 rigidity does not remove the wall. It proves mass is away from

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

not away from

\[
q_0=0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }q_0\text{-wall is independent of Gate 2 base-locus rigidity.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Nondegenerate sampling theorem is false as stated

The theorem

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast:\ |q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is false without an additional assumption.

A counterexample can concentrate all mass on a region where

\[
q_0\equiv0,
\qquad
u\not\equiv0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Then Gate 2 mass is

\[
\int_I |u|^4\,dm,
\]

which can be large, while

\[
|q_0|=0
\]

everywhere.

Of course, an exact canonical \(q_0\equiv0\) with \(u=q''_{\can}\not\equiv0\) may be impossible globally, but a local near-wall version is not excluded by the present local identities.

Thus the nondegenerate sampling theorem cannot be used as a downstream bridge unless a new global constraint on \(q_0\) is proved.

---

# 6. Required alternative: source-robust row

Since the \(q_0\)-wall is real, the downstream proof needs an alternative row or invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) such that

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The target should be something like:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\le Q^{-C},
\quad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\quad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\Rightarrow
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-C_R}.
}
\]

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u,
\]

so a plausible robust leading behavior would be

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^\beta
\]

or

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^\beta\Gamma_G^\gamma
\]

without a fatal \(q_0\)-factor.

The known rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

do not satisfy this because they carry

\[
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

---

# 7. Consequence for the proof architecture

The downstream split must be:

## Branch 1 — nondegenerate \(q_0\)

Assume

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then known rows may work:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This branch needs correction-cancellation control, but is conceptually straightforward.

## Branch 2 — \(q_0\)-wall

Assume

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}.
\]

Gate 2 mass may still be large because

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u.
\]

The known \(H\)-driven rows may collapse because

\[
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

This branch needs either:

1. a source-robust row/invariant; or  
2. a new theorem excluding canonical \(u\)-mass near \(q_0=0\).

The second option appears false under current local identities. So the realistic path is a source-robust row.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }q_0\text{-nondegenerate sampling theorem is false under current assumptions.}
}
\]

Gate 2 mass does **not** force a usable point with

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The \(q_0\)-wall is real:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u\not\approx0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\Gamma_G\approx u
\]

so anisotropy remains live while the known \(H\)-driven rows collapse.

Therefore the downstream proof requires a new input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\textbf{-Wall Theorem}.
}
\]

A precise statement is:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C},\quad
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\exists R_{\rm rob}: |R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Without such a row or invariant, Gate 1 + Gate 2 cannot be converted into the final row contradiction in the \(q_0\)-wall regime.

## Agent 3 / C — Raw / ambient row expansion at \(q_0=0\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: search outside the known projected tower for a source-robust row visible at the \(q_0\)-wall. The target is a row/invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) satisfying

\[
R_{\rm rob}\big|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The prompt states that the known projected rows have the structure

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

so they vanish at \(q_0=0\). 

---

# 1. Starting point

Known projected tower:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and generally

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

With

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288},
\]

we have

\[
H\big|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Therefore every row whose leading term factors through \(H\) fails at the wall:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

at leading order, even when

\[
u\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3\approx u.
\]

So the projected tower itself does not contain a source-robust wall row unless lower-order corrections survive.

---

# 2. What a wall-robust row must look like

At

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
u\ne0,
\]

a useful row must have leading behavior of one of the forms

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p,
\]

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

or

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p(q')^a
\]

with no factor

\[
q_0,\qquad H,\qquad q_0u^3.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G\big|_{q_0=0}=u,
\]

any term like

\[
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

would also survive as

\[
u^{p+1}.
\]

Thus the wall search should not look for more anisotropy factors. It should look for any row where the **source factor** is \(u^\beta\), not \(q_0u^\beta\).

---

# 3. Raw scattering rows before \(\mathfrak f\)-projection

The key question is whether the \(H\)-factor is intrinsic or introduced by the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

There are two possibilities.

## Case A — \(H\)-factor is projection-induced

Suppose a raw row has schematic form

\[
A_{\rm raw}
=
u^\beta \Gamma_G
+
q_0u^\gamma\Gamma_{G,k}
+
\cdots.
\]

Then after projection,

\[
A_{\rm raw}\mapsto A^{\mathfrak f}
\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

could erase the wall-live term.

If so, an unprojected or partially projected row may survive at \(q_0=0\):

\[
A_{\rm raw}\big|_{q_0=0}
\sim u^{\beta+1}\ne0.
\]

This would be the desired source-robust row.

## Case B — \(H\)-factor is intrinsic

If every raw scattering row already has a factor

\[
q_0
\]

or

\[
H,
\]

before projection, then the wall cannot be rescued by unprojecting. The row architecture is genuinely blind at \(q_0=0\).

Current information is insufficient to distinguish these cases without the explicit raw row formulas.

So the next concrete audit must inspect the raw, pre-\(\mathfrak f\)-projection expansions and ask:

\[
\boxed{
A_{\rm raw}\big|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}=0
\quad\text{or not?}
}
\]

---

# 4. Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

The same distinction applies to ambient Gram rows.

A projected row may vanish because projection enforces tangency, orthogonality, or gauge normalization that introduces \(y\) or \(q_0\). But an ambient row may include direct curvature terms.

Candidate ambient structures to inspect:

\[
\langle \partial^a K,\partial^b K\rangle_{\rm ambient},
\]

\[
\partial_m^j q''_{\can},
\]

\[
u^p,
\]

\[
u^p q',
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_G.
\]

The wall test is mechanical:

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0.
\]

If the ambient expression evaluates to a nonzero polynomial in \(u,q',q'',\ldots\), then it is a possible wall row.

If all ambient expressions reduce to terms divisible by

\[
q_0
\]

or by the projected factor

\[
H,
\]

then no ambient rescue exists.

---

# 5. Correction sectors

Even if the nominal leading rows are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+\text{corrections},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+\text{corrections},
\]

the corrections may become leading at the wall.

Write

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
H=0,
\]

we need to evaluate

\[
C_7\big|_{q_0=0,u\ne0},
\qquad
C_9\big|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}.
\]

If either correction contains a term

\[
u^p,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,
\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no \(q_0\)-factor, then the wall may be rescued by what was formerly “lower order” off-wall.

If every correction is also divisible by

\[
q_0,\quad H,\quad q_0u^3,
\]

then the known corrected rows do not rescue the wall.

I cannot certify either outcome without explicit correction expansions.

---

# 6. Candidate wall-row theorem, if a raw/correction term survives

If a wall-live row is found, the theorem should be stated as follows.

## Source-Robust Wall Row Theorem

Assume

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and canonical derivative/error bounds.

Suppose there exists a row \(R_{\rm rob}\) with expansion

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
c_{\rm rob}u^\beta
+
\mathcal R_{\rm rob}
\]

at \(q_0=0\), where

\[
c_{\rm rob}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
|\mathcal R_{\rm rob}|
\le
\frac12 |c_{\rm rob}||u|^\beta.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

on the \(q_0\)-wall branch.

This would close row conversion at the wall.

---

# 7. No-go if every raw/ambient/correction row is \(H\)-divisible

If the audit proves that all available rows satisfy

\[
R_{\rm available}
=
H\cdot \mathcal R
\]

or

\[
R_{\rm available}
=
q_0\cdot \mathcal R,
\]

then

\[
R_{\rm available}\big|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Since Gate 2 can remain live at \(q_0=0\) because

\[

\]

this gives a genuine downstream obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{known row architecture cannot convert Gate 2 mass at the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

Then the proof needs a new invariant outside the current row family.

---

# 8. Current verdict

I cannot honestly claim a source-robust row exists from the data currently available.

The state is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projected tower: no wall rescue;}
}

For each row \(R\), classify:

R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}
=

}

\Rightarrow
\exists R_{\rm rob}:\ |R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

At present, this theorem is open.

## Agent 3 / C — \(q_0\)-wall raw / ambient row expansion audit

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: search for a source-robust row outside the known projected \(H\)-divisible tower, by auditing raw scattering rows and ambient/unprojected Gram rows at

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}\ne0.
\]

The known projected tower has

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

so it vanishes on the \(q_0\)-wall. 

---

# 1. Wall test

For every candidate row \(R\), apply the evaluation functional

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm wall}(R)
:=
R\big|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}.
\]

Classify:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm wall}(R)\ne0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{wall-live candidate},
\]

\[
R\in(q_0)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{\(q_0\)-divisible, not wall-live},
\]

\[
R\in(H)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{\(H\)-divisible, not wall-live},
\]

\[
R\notin(q_0),(H),\quad \mathcal E_{\rm wall}(R)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{cancellation audit required}.
\]

The desired row must contain a monomial of one of the forms

\[
u^p,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no factor of \(q_0\), \(H\), or \(q_0u^3\).

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

we have at the wall

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

So any row with leading term

\[
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

is wall-live as

\[
u^{p+1}.
\]

---

# 2. Projected tower audit

Known projected rows have the schematic form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,k}+\text{corrections}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
H|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Therefore the leading projected tower contributes

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm wall}(H\Gamma_{G,k})=0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No projected-tower leading row rescues the \(q_0\)-wall.}
}
\]

A projected row can rescue the wall only if its correction sector has a wall-live term:

\[
C_{2k+1}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

That is Agent 4’s correction-row lane.

---

# 3. Raw scattering row possibilities

Let \(R_{\rm raw}\) be a raw row before \(\mathfrak f\)-projection. There are two possible structural cases.

## Case A — \(H\)-divisibility is projection-induced

If

\[
R_{\rm raw}
=
u^p\Gamma_G
+
q_0\cdot R_1
+
H\cdot R_2
+
\cdots,
\]

then

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}
=
u^{p+1}\ne0.
\]

In this case, the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection destroys a wall-live raw contribution, and the raw row is a source-robust candidate.

The theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
R_{\rm raw}
=
c\,u^p\Gamma_G
+
O(q_0\cdot \mathcal P)+O(E)
,\quad c\ne0
\Rightarrow
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}=c\,u^{p+1}.
}
\]

Then, under wall-branch Gate 2 mass,

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and \(\Gamma_G\approx u\), one obtains

\[
|R_{\rm raw}|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

provided corrections are smaller than the wall-leading term.

## Case B — \(H\)-divisibility is intrinsic

If every raw row has

\[
R_{\rm raw}=H\cdot \mathcal R
\]

or

\[
R_{\rm raw}=q_0\cdot \mathcal R,
\]

then

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

In this case, raw rows do not rescue the wall.

Current available information does not distinguish Case A from Case B. The required next calculation is the explicit raw row expansion before projection.

---

# 4. Ambient / unprojected Gram row possibilities

The same wall test applies to ambient Gram rows.

For an ambient candidate \(R_{\rm amb}\), inspect whether its leading expansion contains direct source curvature terms:

\[
R_{\rm amb}
=
c\,u^p
+
c'\,u^p\Gamma_G
+
c''\,u^p(q')^a
+
q_0\cdot R_1
+
H\cdot R_2
+
\cdots.
\]

If

\[
c\ne0
\quad\text{or}\quad
c'\ne0
\quad\text{or}\quad
c''\ne0
\]

and the corresponding term survives at \(q_0=0\), then \(R_{\rm amb}\) is source-robust.

If all ambient rows lie in

\[
(q_0)+(H),
\]

then ambient rows do not rescue the wall.

Again, without the explicit ambient Gram formulas, this remains an audit criterion rather than a proof.

---

# 5. Candidate source-robust theorem if a wall-live row exists

Suppose a raw or ambient row \(R_{\rm rob}\) has wall expansion

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
c_{\rm rob}u^\beta
+
q_0 R_q
+
H R_H
+
E_R,
\qquad c_{\rm rob}\ne0.
\]

At the wall,

\[
R_{\rm rob}=c_{\rm rob}u^\beta+E_R.
\]

Assume

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and an anisotropy upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-(A/2+C_\Gamma)}.
\]

If

\[
|E_R|+|q_0R_q|+|HR_H|
\le
\frac12|c_{\rm rob}||u|^\beta,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This would close the \(q_0\)-wall row-conversion branch.

---

# 6. No-go theorem if all rows are \(q_0/H\)-divisible

If the raw, ambient, and projected correction audit proves

\[
R\in(q_0)+(H)
\]

for every available row \(R\), then at the wall

\[
R|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Since Gate 2 mass can remain live at the wall because

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u,
\]

the known row architecture cannot convert Gate 2 mass to a final row lower bound.

The no-go statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\left[
\forall R\in\mathcal R_{\rm available},\ R\in(q_0)+(H)
\right]
\Rightarrow
\text{known rows cannot close the \(q_0\)-wall.}
}
\]

Then the proof requires a genuinely new invariant or row family.

---

# 7. Required explicit expansion audit

The next algebraic audit should produce a table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{row} & \text{leading expansion} & \mathcal E_{\rm wall}(R) & \text{classification}\\
\hline
R_1 & \cdots & \cdots & \text{wall-live / \(q_0\)-divisible / \(H\)-divisible}\\
R_2 & \cdots & \cdots & \cdots
\end{array}
\]

For each row, evaluate at

\[
q_0=0,\quad u\ne0,\quad \Gamma_G=u.
\]

The decisive question is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists R:\ R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0?
}
\]

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No certified source-robust row is currently available.}
}
\]

The known projected tower is wall-dead because it is \(H\)-divisible.

The raw/ambient/correction sectors remain the only possible rescue, but they require explicit term-by-term expansion.

So the current downstream input should be named:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Theorem}
}
\]

with target statement:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\le Q^{-C},
\quad
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\exists R_{\rm rob}:\ |R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This theorem is open until a raw, ambient, or correction row is shown to survive at

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0.
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:50:43)

## Agent 3 / C — Full Gate 2 theorem synthesis

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: synthesize the conditional Gate 2 proof from set extraction, thick-set propagation, derivative propagation, and interval rigidity. The current target is to prove, or isolate the precise missing sublemmas for,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

where \(u=q''_{\can}\). 

---

# 1. Contrapositive setup

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

We want to derive a contradiction using the base-locus identities

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

The exact interval rigidity already established is:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\text{ on an interval}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
u\equiv0.
\]

The missing issue is quantitative propagation from a bad set to an interval.

---

# 2. Set extraction

From Gate 1, choose a threshold

\[
\tau_u=Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Let

\[
E_u=\{m\in I: |u(m)|\ge \tau_u\}.
\]

For \(C_u\) sufficiently large relative to \(B\), Gate 1 implies

\[
\int_{E_u}|u|^2\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

unless the complement already carries enough \(u\)-mass with \(|u|<Q^{-C_u}\), which is impossible for \(C_u\gg B\).

Now define

\[
E=
\left\{
m\in E_u:
|\Gamma_G(m)|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|^2\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\right\}.
\]

If \(C_\Gamma\) is chosen sufficiently smaller than \(A-B\), then Gate 2 failure forces

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

Thus the extracted bad set satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
}
\]

This part is valid and should be treated as Green.

---

# 3. Missing black box 1: thick-set-to-interval propagation

The set \(E\) may be dust-like. Positive polynomial measure alone does not give an interval where both \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are uniformly small.

The required black box is:

## Thick-Set Propagation Lemma

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume finite analytic complexity on an enlarged interval \(I^\ast\):

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0.
\]

Assume there is a set \(E\subset I\) with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|
\]

and

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-C_1}.
}
\]

This is not currently proved. It is the first essential missing sublemma.

A weaker version that gives relative density on every subinterval of a certain scale would also suffice:

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|
\quad
\text{for all }J\text{ of scale }Q^{-C_J}|I|.
\]

But this density does not follow from measure alone; it requires a Remez/Bernstein/Cartan-type propagation theorem.

---

# 4. Missing black box 2: derivative propagation

Approximate interval rigidity needs either

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2},
\]

or direct control of

\[
\sup_J|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

However, thick-set propagation as stated only gives

\[
\Gamma_G,\ \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

small.

Using

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

we cannot infer \(q(q')^2\) is small unless we also know \(\Gamma_G''\) is small.

So we need a second black box.

## Derivative Propagation Lemma

If on an interval \(J\)

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

and the relevant functions have finite analytic complexity on \(J^\ast\), then on a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}.
}
\]

Alternatively, the lemma may directly assert:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}
}
\]

from

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1}.
\]

This derivative step is not automatic from real \(C^6\) bounds alone unless the interval scale and smallness exponents are strong enough. Complex Cauchy estimates would prove it if \(\Gamma_G\) is small in a complex tube, but real-axis smallness alone only gives derivative smallness under additional finite-complexity/Remez control.

So this is the second essential missing sublemma.

---

# 5. Approximate interval base-locus rigidity

Assume the two propagation lemmas have produced an interval \(J'\) such that

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

gives

\[
u=q''_{\can}=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1}).
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

gives

\[
2q(q')^2=O(Q^{-C_1}+Q^{-C_2}).
\]

Let

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C}.
\]

Then on \(J'\),

\[
q(q')^2=O(\varepsilon).
\]

Split into regions.

## Region 1: \(|q|\le \delta\)

Then

\[
u=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon)
\]

gives

\[
|u|\le 6\delta+O(\varepsilon).
\]

Choosing \(\delta=Q^{-C'}\) gives

\[
|u|\le Q^{-C''}.
\]

## Region 2: \(|q|>\delta\)

Then

\[
(q')^2=O(\varepsilon/\delta),
\]

so

\[
|q'|\le O((\varepsilon/\delta)^{1/2}).
\]

Thus \(q\) is nearly constant on a shrunken interval. Since

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon),
\]

near constancy forces

\[
6q-2q^3=O((\varepsilon/\delta)^{1/2}+\varepsilon)
\]

in a weak/averaged sense. Hence

\[
q
\]

is close to one of

\[
0,\quad \sqrt3,\quad -\sqrt3.
\]

But if \(q\approx\pm\sqrt3\), then

\[
6q-2q^3\approx0,
\]

so again

\[
u=q''\approx0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C_u'}
}
\]

on a further shrunken interval \(J''\subset J'\), provided the approximate rigidity estimates are quantitative enough.

This contradicts the retained condition

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

on a sufficiently thick portion of the original bad set, if the propagation lemmas preserve overlap with \(u\)-mass.

---

# 6. Full conditional Gate 2 theorem

The clean package is:

## Gate 2 Conditional Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Finite analytic complexity:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0,
\]

with \(k_0\ge6\).

3. Thick-set propagation:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\quad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C'}
\text{ on }E
\]

implies the existence of an interval \(J\) where

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C''}.
\]

4. Derivative propagation:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C''}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C'''}.
\]

5. Approximate interval rigidity:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C_u'}.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Current proof status

| Step | Status |
|---|---|
| Set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure | Green |
| Exact interval base-locus rigidity | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity with \(\Gamma_G''\)-smallness | Mostly Green / conditional |
| Thick-set-to-interval propagation | Open |
| Derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\) | Open |
| Full Gate 2 | Conditional on the two propagation lemmas |

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 reduces to two analytic propagation inputs.}
}
\]

The main missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}.
}
\]

The second missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Derivative Propagation for }\Gamma_G''\textbf{ or }q(q')^2.
}
\]

Once these are supplied, the interval base-locus rigidity gives Gate 2.

But Gate 2 still does **not** solve the downstream \(q_0\)-wall. The row-conversion layer remains split into:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\text{nondegenerate branch},
\]

and

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
\quad\text{source-robust row / wall branch}.
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Derivative propagation: \(\Gamma_G''\) and \(q(q')^2\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: close, or precisely isolate, the derivative-control gap in Gate 2. The current downstream bottleneck is that Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives small \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) on a bad set, but interval rigidity needs either small \(\Gamma_G''\) or small \(q(q')^2\). 

---

# 1. Starting point

Assume an interval \(J\) has already been produced where

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Recall

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

The interval-rigidity theorem needs either:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\), or directly:

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

The issue is that smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone does not automatically imply either of these.

---

# 2. Complex Cauchy route

If \(\Gamma_G\) is holomorphic on a complex tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(J)=\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,J)\le \rho\},
\]

and if we know the **complex-tube smallness**

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then Cauchy gives, on the central subinterval \(J'\),

\[
|\Gamma_G''(x)|
\le
2\rho^{-2}\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|
\le
2\rho^{-2}Q^{-A}.
\]

If

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
}
\]

So the complex route works if propagation gives smallness not merely on the real interval, but in a polynomial-width complex tube.

### Required theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}
+
\text{holomorphic complexity}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J')}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is stronger than ordinary real Remez. It is essentially a Cartan-type propagation theorem.

---

# 3. Real Bernstein route

Suppose instead we only have real-axis control:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

A Bernstein-type estimate would need a finite-complexity hypothesis of the form

\[
\sup_{J^\ast}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

If such an inequality holds, then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{C_D-A}.
}
\]

But this is not true for arbitrary \(C^6\) functions. A function can be tiny in value on an interval and have large second derivative through high-frequency oscillation unless its frequency/degree complexity is controlled.

The current derivative package

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

only gives an absolute upper bound

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{C},
\]

not a relative bound

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^C|\Gamma_G|.
\]

So real Bernstein works only if \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a low-complexity class such as:

- polynomial degree \(N=O(1)\);
- exponential type \(N=O(1)\);
- controlled zero count \(N=O(1)\);
- a Chebyshev system with polynomial condition number.

If the effective complexity is

\[
N\asymp R,
\]

the loss can be

\[
\exp(O(R))\quad\text{or}\quad\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

This may be polynomial in \(Q\) at safe depth, but only if the Remez constants are not \(\exp(O(R^2))\). If they are \(\exp(O(R^2))\), the loss is too large.

### Required theorem

A usable real theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

under an explicit low-complexity condition with loss \(Q^{O(1)}\).

Without such a condition, this step is false.

---

# 4. Direct derivation of \(q(q')^2\)-smallness

From

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

we have

\[
2q(q')^2
=
\Gamma_{G,2}+\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

If

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

is small but

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

is not controlled, then \(q(q')^2\) may be large and cancel against \(\Gamma_G''/6\).

Therefore smallness of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone does **not** imply smallness of \(q(q')^2\).

A local countermodel is easy at the level of functions: choose \(\Gamma_G\) with large second derivative, and set

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

so that

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

Thus the direct route fails unless there is an independent reason that \(q(q')^2\) and \(\Gamma_G''\) cannot cancel.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}\text{-smallness does not by itself control }q(q')^2.
}
\]

---

# 5. Counterexample to derivative propagation from real smallness alone

Let, on \(J=[-1,1]\),

\[
\Gamma_G(x)=\varepsilon\sin(Nx).
\]

Then

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le \varepsilon,
\]

but

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\asymp \varepsilon N^2.
\]

If \(N\) is as large as a power of \(Q\), derivative smallness is lost.

Even if \(N\asymp R\), this costs \(R^2\), which is acceptable. But if the effective local frequency is \(Q^C\), it is not.

Thus the derivative propagation theorem must explicitly bound the effective complexity/frequency of \(\Gamma_G\). The \(C^6\) derivative package alone provides an upper bound for \(N\), but not necessarily a polynomially mild one relative to the smallness exponent.

---

# 6. Sufficient derivative propagation theorem

A clean sufficient theorem is:

## Gate 2 Derivative Propagation Lemma

Let \(J\subset I\), and suppose \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a finite-complexity class \(\mathcal F_N\) on \(J^\ast\), with \(N\le C R\), satisfying the Bernstein inequality

\[
\sup_{J'}|\mathcal D^2 f|
\le
N^2 Q^{C_0}\sup_J|f|
\]

for all \(f\in\mathcal F_N\), where \(J'\subset J\) is a fixed shrunken interval.

If

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

At

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
N^2Q^{C_0}=Q^{C_0+o(1)}.
\]

So choosing \(A\) large gives \(A'>0\).

This is the most practical real-variable derivative propagation input.

---

# 7. Alternative sufficient theorem using complex tubes

A stronger but cleaner theorem is:

## Complex Gate 2 Propagation Lemma

Assume \(\Gamma_G\) is holomorphic in a tube \(\mathcal T_\rho(J)\) with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

If

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
}
\]

This is immediate by Cauchy.

The hard part is not Cauchy; it is obtaining tube smallness from the real bad set. That belongs to the Cartan/Remez propagation lane.

---

# 8. Full derivative package needed for Gate 2

For the Gate 2 proof, the propagation output should be stated as:

There exists an interval \(J'\subset I\) such that

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

Then interval rigidity gives

\[
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-A_3}.
\]

This contradicts retained \(u\)-mass if \(J''\) intersects the thick \(u\)-large set with sufficient density.

Thus derivative propagation must be bundled with thick-set propagation, not treated as automatic.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative propagation is not automatic from }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ smallness.}
}
\]

The identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

shows that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness can hide cancellation between \(q(q')^2\) and \(\Gamma_G''\).

Therefore Gate 2 needs one of the following named inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation Lemma}
}
\]

giving

\[
\sup|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

from propagated \(\Gamma_G\)-smallness plus finite complexity; or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Direct }q(q')^2\textbf{-Smallness Lemma}
}
\]

showing

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
q(q')^2\text{ small}.
\]

The second is false without additional anti-cancellation input. The first is the better route, provided the effective complexity of \(\Gamma_G\) is low enough to give only polynomial loss.

## Agent 3 / C — Derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: resolve the derivative-control gap in Gate 2. The issue is that approximate interval rigidity needs either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'},
\]

but the propagation stage initially gives only

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

The relevant identity is

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

This means \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness alone does **not** control either term separately unless \(\Gamma_G''\) is also controlled. 

---

# 1. Direct implication is false without derivative control

From

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

smallness of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) permits cancellation:

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

So

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ll1
\]

does not imply

\[
|q(q')^2|\ll1
\]

unless \(\Gamma_G''\) is already small, or unless there is an additional anti-cancellation theorem between \(q(q')^2\) and \(\Gamma_G''\).

A local countermodel is immediate: choose \(\Gamma_G\) with large second derivative and define \(q,q'\) locally so that

\[
2q(q')^2=\frac16\Gamma_G''+O(Q^{-A}).
\]

Then \(\Gamma_{G,2}=O(Q^{-A})\) while both \(q(q')^2\) and \(\Gamma_G''\) may be large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{-smallness does not itself imply interval rigidity.}
}
\]

Derivative propagation must be added as a separate sublemma.

---

# 2. Complex Cauchy route

A clean route is available if the Remez/Cartan propagation stage gives **complex-tube smallness**.

Assume \(\Gamma_G\) is holomorphic on a tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(J)
=
\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,J)\le \rho\},
\]

with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

If

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then Cauchy gives, on a shrunken real interval \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
2\rho^{-2}\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|
\le
Q^{-A+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

Thus, for \(A\) chosen large enough,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the simplest derivative-propagation theorem.

### Required input

The hard part is not Cauchy; it is obtaining

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}
\]

from smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) on a real thick set. That is a **Cartan/Remez propagation** input.

So the complex route gives the conditional theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real thick-set smallness}
\Rightarrow
\text{complex-tube smallness}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Real Bernstein route

If only real interval smallness is available,

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then a real Bernstein-type theorem is needed.

A sufficient statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|
}
\]

for a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\).

Then

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
Q^{C_D-A}
=
Q^{-A'}
\]

if \(A>C_D+A'\).

But this Bernstein inequality is **not true for arbitrary \(C^6\) functions**. It requires a finite-complexity hypothesis.

A usable complexity package would be one of:

\[
\Gamma_G\in \mathcal F_N
\]

with exponential type or polynomial/Chebyshev degree

\[
N\le Q^{O(1)}
\]

and preferably

\[
N=O(R)
\]

or

\[
N=Q^{o(1)}.
\]

Then one expects

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\lesssim
N^2|J|^{-2}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

If

\[
N=O(R),
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then

\[
N^2=Q^{o(1)},
\]

so the loss is harmless.

But if the effective complexity is as large as \(Q^C\), the loss is still polynomial and may be absorbable by choosing \(A\) large. If the Remez/Bernstein loss is instead \(\exp(O(R^2))\), then the loss becomes

\[
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{(\log\log Q)^2}\right)\right),
\]

which is super-polynomial in \(Q\), and may be fatal unless the extracted smallness is much stronger.

So the real route depends critically on proving a low-complexity bound with at most polynomial loss.

---

# 4. Direct \(q(q')^2\)-smallness route

Could one avoid \(\Gamma_G''\)-control and derive

\[
q(q')^2\approx0
\]

directly from

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0?
\]

No, not without an anti-cancellation input.

Since

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\frac1{12}\Gamma_G'',
\]

small \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) leaves \(q(q')^2\) controlled by \(\Gamma_G''\). Thus the direct route collapses back to derivative propagation.

A separate theorem could be formulated:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\approx0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\Rightarrow
q(q')^2\approx0
}
\]

but this is equivalent to saying that

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

cannot cancel

\[
\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

on the propagated interval. That is not currently justified.

So the preferred route remains:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\text{-smallness}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Counterexample to derivative propagation without complexity

Let

\[
\Gamma_G(x)=\varepsilon\sin(Nx)
\]

on an interval \(J\). Then

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le \varepsilon,
\]

but

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\asymp \varepsilon N^2.
\]

Taking \(N\gg Q^C\) makes the second derivative large even if the function is tiny.

Thus any derivative propagation theorem must explicitly bound effective frequency/complexity. A mere finite \(C^6\) upper bound gives only an absolute estimate; it does not give the relative estimate needed unless the smallness exponent dominates that absolute bound.

---

# 6. Sufficient theorem for Gate 2

The derivative component needed for Gate 2 can be stated as follows.

## Gate 2 Derivative Propagation Lemma

Let \(J\subset I\), and suppose \(\Gamma_G\) lies in a finite-complexity class \(\mathcal F_N\) on \(J^\ast\), with

\[
N\le Q^{C_N},
\]

and satisfies a Bernstein estimate

\[
\sup_{J'}|\mathcal D^2 f|
\le
Q^{C_D}\sup_J|f|
\]

for all \(f\in\mathcal F_N\), with \(J'\Subset J\).

Then

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A+C_D}.
}
\]

Choosing \(A\) large enough gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Together with

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

this yields

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''
=
O(Q^{-A'}).
\]

Then approximate interval rigidity applies.

---

# 7. Stronger complex version

A cleaner black-box version is:

## Complex Gate 2 Derivative Lemma

Assume there is a tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(J)
\]

with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}
\]

such that

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Then on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
}
\]

This is immediate by Cauchy and should be preferred if Agent 1/2 can obtain tube smallness via Cartan.

---

# 8. Required output from the propagation stage

For the full Gate 2 proof, the thick-set/Remez propagation stage should output not merely

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A},
\]

but the stronger package

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|
+
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Equivalently, it may output

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Without one of these, interval rigidity cannot be invoked.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative propagation is a separate necessary Gate 2 input.}
}
\]

Smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

on an interval is insufficient unless one also controls either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

The best formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation Lemma:}
\quad
\Gamma_G\text{-smallness plus finite complexity}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness}.
}
\]

The complex Cauchy version is cleanest if thick-set propagation gives tube smallness. The real Bernstein version is acceptable only if the effective complexity loss is polynomial in \(Q\).

## Agent 3 / C — Final conditional Gate 2 theorem

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: state the complete Gate 2 theorem conditionally on the two remaining propagation inputs, D1 and D2. The current downstream stop-condition round asks whether Gate 2 should now be treated as a conditional theorem depending on **Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation** and **Gate 2 Derivative Propagation**. 

---

# 1. Target

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Known identities:

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Exact interval rigidity is already established:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\quad\text{on an interval}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
u\equiv0.
\]

The problem is quantitative: Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives a polynomial-measure bad set, but not automatically an interval. Positive measure alone is insufficient.

---

# 2. Contrapositive proof

Assume Gate 1 holds but Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Choose thresholds

\[
\tau_u=Q^{-C_u},\qquad \tau_\Gamma=Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

By the already established set-extraction step, for suitable constants there exists

\[
E\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

and on \(E\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

This step is Green.

The missing bridge is converting this possibly dust-like set \(E\) into interval control.

---

# 3. D1 — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Use the following black-box input.

## D1. Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume finite analytic/real complexity on an enlarged interval \(I^\ast\), for example

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6,
\]

plus whichever Remez/Cartan/density hypothesis is required.

If

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

and

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

then there is an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

This input is currently open. It cannot be replaced by mere positive measure of \(E\); a dust-like set can evade interval control. D1 must include one of:

\[
\text{relative density, bounded components, zero-count control, Cartan control, or low effective Remez complexity.}
\]

---

# 4. D2 — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

Interval rigidity also needs control of either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

Smallness of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone does not provide this, because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation between \(2q(q')^2\) and \(\Gamma_G''/6\).

So use a second black-box input.

## D2. Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

If on an interval \(J\),

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and the same finite-complexity or holomorphic-tube hypotheses hold, then on a shrunken interval

\[
J'\Subset J
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

Equivalently, D2 may output

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

The cleanest sufficient version is the complex Cauchy form:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},\quad \rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_1+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

The real-variable form requires a Bernstein/Remez complexity bound such as

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

D2 is also currently open unless such a low-complexity or tube-smallness hypothesis is established.

---

# 5. Approximate interval rigidity

Assume D1 and D2 give an interval \(J'\) such that

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

gives

\[
u=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1}).
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

gives

\[
q(q')^2=O(Q^{-A_1}+Q^{-A_2}).
\]

Now split \(J'\) into the regions \(|q|\le\delta\) and \(|q|>\delta\).

If

\[
|q|\le\delta,
\]

then

\[
|u|\le 6\delta+O(Q^{-A_1}).
\]

If

\[
|q|>\delta,
\]

then

\[
|q'|^2\le O((Q^{-A_1}+Q^{-A_2})/\delta).
\]

Thus \(q\) is nearly constant on a shrunken subinterval. Combining near constancy with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1})
\]

forces \(q\) close to one of

\[
0,\quad \sqrt3,\quad -\sqrt3.
\]

For each of these,

\[
6q-2q^3\approx0,
\]

and therefore

\[
u=q''\approx0.
\]

Quantitatively, for suitable choices of \(\delta\) and the exponents,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-A_3}
}
\]

on a further shrunken interval \(J''\subset J'\).

This contradicts the retained bad-set condition \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) provided D1 preserves enough contact between the interval \(J''\) and the \(u\)-large set, or the propagation theorem is stated to carry the \(u\)-large condition forward.

---

# 6. Conditional Gate 2 theorem

The clean final statement is:

## Conditional Gate 2 Theorem

Assume:

1. **Gate 1 source mass**

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. **Finite complexity**

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6,
\]

or a holomorphic-tube analogue.

3. **D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation**

\[
\text{polynomial-measure smallness of }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval smallness}.
\]

4. **D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation**

\[
\Gamma_G\text{-smallness on an interval}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness}
\]

or directly

\[
q(q')^2\text{-smallness}.
\]

5. **Approximate interval rigidity**

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_G''\text{ small on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\text{ small}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 + D2 + interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Status of components

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure | Green |
| Exact interval rigidity | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity with \(\Gamma_G''\)-control | Conditional / mostly Green |
| D1: Density/Remez propagation | Open named input |
| D2: Derivative propagation | Open named input |
| Full Gate 2 | Conditional on D1 + D2 |

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now conditionally reduced to D1 and D2.}
}
\]

The strongest currently justified theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
+
\textbf{D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}
+
\text{interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This does not address the \(q_0\)-wall. Even after Gate 2, row conversion still needs the separate downstream input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\textbf{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:18:44)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 3 / C — D2: Derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: attack **D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation**. The issue is whether interval smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

can provide the extra control needed by approximate interval rigidity, namely smallness of either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

The latest downstream brief identifies D2 as one of the named inputs needed to complete Gate 2. 

---

# 1. Starting point

Assume D1 has produced an interval \(J\) such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

We know

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Approximate interval rigidity needs either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\).

---

# 2. Why \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness alone is insufficient

The identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation between the two terms. Thus

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\ll1
\]

does not imply either

\[
|q(q')^2|\ll1
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\ll1.
\]

A model obstruction is:

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

with both terms large. Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

while the rigidity input fails.

Therefore D2 cannot be derived from \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness alone.

---

# 3. Cauchy route

A clean D2 theorem follows if D1 can be strengthened from real interval smallness to complex-tube smallness.

Assume \(\Gamma_G\) is holomorphic in

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(J)=\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,J)\le \rho\},
\]

with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

and

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Then Cauchy gives, on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
C\rho^{-2}Q^{-A}
\le
Q^{-A+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

Thus, choosing \(A\) large enough,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Then

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}+\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''
\]

also satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

So the Cauchy version of D2 is straightforward once D1 provides tube smallness.

---

# 4. Bernstein route

If D1 provides only real interval smallness

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\]

then we need a Bernstein-type finite-complexity estimate:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
}
\]

This gives

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A+C_D},
\]

and hence derivative smallness if \(A>C_D+A'\).

But this estimate is not true for arbitrary \(C^6\) functions. The simple obstruction is

\[
\Gamma_G(x)=\varepsilon\sin(Nx),
\]

for which

\[
\sup|\Gamma_G|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
\sup|\Gamma_G''|\asymp \varepsilon N^2.
\]

So the Bernstein route requires an effective complexity bound on \(\Gamma_G\), for example:

\[
N\le Q^C
\]

with known \(C\), or better

\[
N=O(R).
\]

If the effective complexity is \(O(R)\), then

\[
N^2=Q^{o(1)}
\]

at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and the loss is harmless. If the only available complexity is much larger, the loss must be explicitly absorbed by the initial smallness exponent.

---

# 5. D2 theorem candidates

## D2-Cauchy

Assume D1 outputs complex-tube smallness:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

This is the strongest clean formulation.

## D2-Bernstein

Assume \(\Gamma_G\) belongs to a finite-complexity class satisfying

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

Then real interval smallness gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

after choosing the smallness exponent \(A\) large relative to \(C_D\).

This version is usable if D1 gives real interval smallness and an independent complexity/doubling bound.

---

# 6. Direct \(q(q')^2\)-smallness route

A direct theorem of the form

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
q(q')^2\text{ small}
\]

is false without extra anti-cancellation input, because

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}+\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''.
\]

So direct \(q(q')^2\)-control is equivalent to derivative propagation unless one can prove that

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

cannot cancel

\[
\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

on intervals. No such structural anti-cancellation is currently available.

---

# 7. Final D2 statement

The named downstream input should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}.
}
\]

A precise black-box form:

If D1 produces an interval \(J\) with

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A},
\]

and either:

1. complex-tube smallness for \(\Gamma_G\) on a tube of radius \(\rho\ge Q^{-C}\), or  
2. a real Bernstein/doubling inequality

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|,
\]

then on a shrunken interval \(J'\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|+\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is sufficient for the approximate interval rigidity step in Gate 2.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2 is not automatic, but it is cleanly isolated.}
}
\]

It is Green only if D1 provides complex-tube smallness or if \(\Gamma_G\) has a proven low-complexity Bernstein bound.

Otherwise D2 remains a named black-box input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}
}
\]

with Cauchy/Bernstein/doubling hypotheses made explicit.

## Agent 3 / C — Final conditional Gate 2 package

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: write the final conditional Gate 2 theorem using D1 and D2, marking set extraction and interval rigidity as Green and D1/D2 as named inputs. The latest prompt confirms that finite \(C^6\)-type bounds alone do not prove D1 and that D2 needs explicit Cauchy/Bernstein/doubling hypotheses. 

---

# 1. Target

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

The identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive proof skeleton

Assume Gate 1 holds and Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

but

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The established set extraction gives a bad set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

This is **Green**.

---

# 3. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Use D1 as a named input.

## D1 statement

If

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

together with the required low-complexity / relative-density / Cartan / doubling hypotheses, then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

D1 is **open/named**. Positive measure plus finite \(C^6\)-type bounds alone is insufficient because \(E\) may be dust-like; generic Remez with effective degree \(N\asymp R\) gives loss

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too expensive for a fixed-polynomial Gate 2 architecture.

---

# 4. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

Use D2 as a named input.

## D2 statement

If D1 gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

then, under either complex-tube smallness or a Bernstein/doubling estimate, there exists a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}
}
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A_2'}
}
\]

because

\[
q(q')^2=\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}+\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''.
\]

A clean sufficient Cauchy version is:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}
\]

implies

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A_1+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

A real Bernstein version is:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

D2 is **open/named** unless D1 supplies tube smallness or a proven Bernstein/doubling hypothesis.

---

# 5. Approximate interval rigidity

With D1 and D2, on \(J'\) we have

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A_2'}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

gives

\[
u=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1}),
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

gives

\[
q(q')^2=O(Q^{-A_1}+Q^{-A_2}).
\]

Split \(J'\) into:

\[
|q|\le \delta
\]

and

\[
|q|>\delta.
\]

On \(|q|\le\delta\),

\[
|u|\le 6\delta+O(Q^{-A_1}).
\]

On \(|q|>\delta\),

\[
|q'|^2\le O((Q^{-A_1}+Q^{-A_2})/\delta),
\]

so \(q\) is nearly constant on a further shrunken interval. Combining near constancy with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1})
\]

forces \(q\) near

\[
0,\quad \sqrt3,\quad -\sqrt3,
\]

and in all cases

\[
6q-2q^3\approx0,
\]

hence

\[
u=q''\approx0.
\]

Therefore on a shrunken interval \(J''\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-A_3}.
}
\]

This contradicts the retained bad-set property \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) if D1’s interval \(J\) is produced in a way that preserves contact with the \(u\)-large set, or if the propagation theorem carries that condition into the interval output.

---

# 6. Final conditional Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1 source mass:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Green set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure.

3. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.

4. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation.

5. Approximate interval rigidity.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 + D2 + interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Status table

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure | Green |
| Exact interval rigidity | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity with derivative control | Green/conditional |
| D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation | Named input, open |
| D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation | Named input, open |
| Gate 2 | Conditional on D1 + D2 |

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is conditionally reduced to D1 and D2.}
}
\]

The proof does not currently close from Gate 1 alone. The missing downstream analytic inputs are exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}.
}
\]

Even after Gate 2 is obtained, row conversion still requires either the nondegenerate branch D4 or the wall branch D3; Gate 2 itself does not resolve the \(q_0\)-wall.

## Agent 3 / C — Final handoff: Gate 2 D1/D2 theorem package

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: give the final conditional Gate 2 theorem using D1 and D2, with set extraction and interval rigidity marked Green, and D1/D2 marked as named open inputs. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 target

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 is the anisotropy-weighted source lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

The structural identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive framework

Assume Gate 1 holds but Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The goal is to force \(u\) to be small on the same region where Gate 1 says \(u\) has mass, giving a contradiction.

---

# 3. Green set-extraction step

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, one obtains a bad set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

such that on \(E\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

This step is Green: it is a measure extraction argument using the lower bound on \(\int |u|^2\) and the assumed upper bound on the weighted integral.

The problem is that \(E\) may be dust-like. Positive measure alone does not supply interval control.

---

# 4. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

D1 is the first named downstream input.

## D1 statement

Assume

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume in addition a propagation hypothesis such as one of:

\[
\text{relative density of }E,
\]

\[
\text{low effective Remez degree},
\]

\[
\text{Cartan/doubling control},
\]

\[
\text{bounded component or zero-count control}.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

D1 is not proved from current assumptions. Finite \(C^6\)-type derivative bounds alone do not rule out dust-like \(E\), and generic Remez loss with effective degree \(N\asymp R\) is too large for the fixed-polynomial architecture.

---

# 5. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

D2 is the second named downstream input.

Interval rigidity needs smallness of either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

But

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

permits cancellation, so small \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone does not imply small \(q(q')^2\).

## D2 statement

Assume D1 gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then, under one of the following additional hypotheses:

### Cauchy/tube version

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

which implies

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A_1+2C_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

### Bernstein/doubling version

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

D2 gives, on a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

Then

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}+\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''
\]

also gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A_2'}.
}
\]

D2 is not automatic; it is named/open unless D1 supplies tube smallness or one proves a suitable Bernstein/doubling bound.

---

# 6. Approximate interval rigidity

Once D1 and D2 hold, on \(J'\) we have

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

and either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A_2},
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A_2'}.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

we obtain

\[
u=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1}).
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

and D2, we obtain

\[
q(q')^2=O(Q^{-A_2'}).
\]

Split \(J'\) into

\[
|q|\le \delta
\]

and

\[
|q|>\delta.
\]

If \(|q|\le\delta\), then

\[
|u|\le 6\delta+O(Q^{-A_1}).
\]

If \(|q|>\delta\), then

\[
|q'|^2\le O(Q^{-A_2'}/\delta),
\]

so \(q\) is nearly constant on a smaller interval. Combining near constancy with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-A_1})
\]

forces \(q\) near

\[
0,\quad \sqrt3,\quad -\sqrt3.
\]

At these values,

\[
6q-2q^3\approx0,
\]

so

\[
u=q''\approx0.
\]

Thus on a shrunken interval or controlled subset,

\[
\boxed{
|u|\le Q^{-A_3}.
}
\]

This contradicts the retained \(u\)-large condition from the extracted bad set, provided D1/D2 preserve enough contact with that \(u\)-large set.

---

# 7. Final conditional Gate 2 theorem

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Conditional Theorem.}
}
\]

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Green set extraction from Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure.

3. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.

4. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation.

5. Approximate interval rigidity.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 + D2 + interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Status classification

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Gate 1 \(\Rightarrow\) bad-set extraction under Gate 2 failure | Green |
| Exact interval base-locus rigidity | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity given \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\) control | Green/conditional |
| D1: Density/Remez Propagation | named open input |
| D2: Derivative Propagation | named open input |
| Gate 2 | conditional on D1 + D2 |

---

# 9. Final verdict

Gate 2 is not proved from Gate 1 alone. It is now cleanly reduced to two analytic inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}.
}
\]

If D1 and D2 are supplied, the interval rigidity argument closes Gate 2. This still does not close row conversion at the \(q_0\)-wall, which remains a separate downstream input.

## Agent 3 / C — D3 finite wall-row residue audit plan

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: make D3 concrete by specifying the finite algebra needed to either find or rule out a source-robust row at the \(q_0\)-wall. The current handoff treats D3 as one of the final named downstream inputs unless this finite row audit produces a wall-live row. 

---

# 1. Wall-live criterion

The \(q_0\)-wall is

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}\ne0.
\]

Known projected rows have the form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Therefore all rows whose leading and correction terms lie in the ideal

\[
(q_0)
\]

or in the stronger ideal

\[
(H)
\]

are wall-dead.

The wall-live test for any row \(R\) is:

\[
\boxed{
R|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0.
}
\]

Acceptable wall-live leading monomials include:

\[
u^p,\qquad u^p\Gamma_G,\qquad u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad u^p(q')^a,
\]

provided they have no factor of \(q_0\) or \(H\). Since

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u,
\]

a term like

\[
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

is wall-live as

\[
u^{p+1}.
\]

---

# 2. Finite residue computations needed

The D3 audit is finite and algebraic. Compute residues modulo \(q_0\) for the relevant row families.

## 2.1 Raw scattering rows

For each raw row \(R_j^{\rm raw}\), compute

\[
\boxed{
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

Classification:

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0)\ne0
\Rightarrow
\text{wall-live raw row candidate}.
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\text{raw row is \(q_0\)-divisible}.
\]

If the raw row is wall-live but the projected row is wall-dead, then the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection is killing the wall-live component. That would suggest using a raw or partially projected row as the wall branch.

## 2.2 Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

For each ambient row \(R_j^{\rm amb}\), compute

\[
\boxed{
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

The key question is whether ambient geometry contains a direct source term, for example

\[
u^p,\qquad u^p\Gamma_G,\qquad u^p(q')^a.
\]

If yes, the wall may be rescuable before projection/gauge normalization.

## 2.3 Correction sectors

For projected rows

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}+C_{2k+1},
\]

compute

\[
\boxed{
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0)
}
\]

for at least

\[
k=3,4,5,6
\]

corresponding to

\[
A_7,\ A_9,\ A_{11},\ A_{13}.
\]

If any

\[
C_{2k+1}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then a correction term that was lower order off-wall becomes leading on-wall.

---

# 3. First rows to audit

Prioritize:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_9^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_{13}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

For each, produce:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}+C_{2k+1}.
\]

Then record:

\[
H\Gamma_{G,k}\bmod(q_0)=0,
\]

and compute:

\[
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0).
\]

Separately, audit the corresponding raw and ambient rows:

\[
R_{2k+1}^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
R_{2k+1}^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

This gives a finite table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
\text{row} & R^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0) & R^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0) & C\bmod(q_0) & \text{classification}\\
\hline
A_7 & ? & ? & ? & ?\\
A_9 & ? & ? & ? & ?\\
A_{11} & ? & ? & ? & ?\\
A_{13} & ? & ? & ? & ?
\end{array}
\]

---

# 4. Possible outcomes

## Outcome A — certified wall-live row

If some audited row satisfies

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then D3 becomes a concrete theorem.

A usable theorem would be:

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
c u^\beta
+
q_0R_1
+
E_R,
\qquad c\ne0.
\]

Then on the wall branch,

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q},
\]

and with Gate 2 pointwise mass

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

plus an anisotropy upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0R_1|+|E_R|\le \frac12 |c||u|^\beta,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This would close the \(q_0\)-wall row-conversion branch.

---

## Outcome B — projection kills a wall-live raw row

If

\[
R^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0)\ne0
\]

but

\[
A^{\mathfrak f}\bmod(q_0)=0,
\]

then the projection is responsible for the wall. The proof should consider replacing the projected row by:

1. raw row;
2. partially projected row;
3. ambient row;
4. a new gauge preserving the wall-live component.

This is promising but requires a canonical-transfer theorem for the raw/ambient row.

---

## Outcome C — all known rows are \(q_0\)-divisible

If

\[
R_j^{\rm raw},\ R_j^{\rm amb},\ C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all audited rows, then known rows cannot rescue the wall.

Then D3 must remain a named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

---

## Outcome D — cancellation only at vector level

If individual residues are nonzero but cancel in a scalar row, then retain the vector of residues:

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm wall}
=
(R_1\bmod q_0,\dots,R_m\bmod q_0).
\]

A vector lower bound may avoid scalar cancellation:

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm wall}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is analogous to using \((A_7,A_9)\) as a vector in the nondegenerate branch.

---

# 5. The theorem proved by a successful audit

If a wall-live residue is found, D3 can be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Wall Row Theorem.}
}
\]

Assume:

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

canonical derivative/error bounds, and a certified wall-live row expansion

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
c u^\beta
+
q_0R_1
+
\mathcal R,
\qquad c\ne0.
\]

If

\[
|q_0R_1+\mathcal R|
\le \frac12 |c||u|^\beta,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This would complete row conversion on the \(q_0\)-wall.

---

# 6. If no wall-live row is found

If the finite audit shows all available rows satisfy

\[
R\in(q_0)
\quad\text{or}\quad
R\in(H),
\]

then the wall remains unresolved.

The no-go statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Known projected/raw/ambient/correction rows are wall-dead.}
}
\]

Then the proof needs a genuinely new invariant or row family.

---

# 7. Final recommendation for D3

Do **not** run another conceptual \(q_0\)-wall discussion. The next useful work is a finite symbolic residue audit:

\[
\boxed{
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),\quad
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),\quad
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

Until that table exists, D3 should remain named as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

The wall-live criterion is simple and decisive:

\[
\boxed{
\exists R:\ R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
}
\]
