## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:19:32)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — turn wall escape into an integral row-conversion theorem

The wall-escape route can be strengthened. We do **not** need a source-robust row at \(q_0=0\) if the downstream contradiction accepts a row lower bound anywhere on \(I_\rho\), or a local row-energy lower bound. The wall can then be handled by escaping to a nearby non-wall point and applying D4 there. This attacks the \(q_0\)-wall problem identified in the downstream handoff. 

---

# 1. Starting assumptions

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

and define the Gate 2 density

\[
\mathcal G(m)
=
|u(m)|^2\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right).
\]

Assume Gate 2 has already produced

\[
\int_{I_\rho}\mathcal G(m)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Assume also polynomial upper bounds

\[
\|q_0\|_{C^3(I_\rho^\ast)}
+
\|u\|_{C^1(I_\rho^\ast)}
+
\|\mathcal G\|_{C^1(I_\rho^\ast)}
\le Q^{C}.
\]

These are the natural local-complexity hypotheses already needed for row conversion.

---

# 2. Pointwise sampling from Gate 2

From

\[
\int_{I_\rho}\mathcal G\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|,
\]

there exists

\[
m_0\in I_\rho
\]

such that

\[
\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

we are in the nondegenerate branch and D4 applies directly.

So only consider the wall branch:

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3\approx u.
\]

If \(\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}\) and \(|q_0(m_0)|\) is very small, then at least one of \(u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) is polynomially non-small. Under the natural polynomial upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Thus

\[
|q_0''(m_0)|=|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

This is precisely the wall-escape hypothesis.

---

# 3. Quantitative wall escape

Taylor expansion gives

\[
q_0(m_0+s)+q_0(m_0-s)
=
2q_0(m_0)+u(m_0)s^2+O\!\left(\|q_0'''\|_\infty s^3\right).
\]

Choose

\[
s=Q^{-C_s}
\]

so that

\[
\|q_0'''\|_\infty s\le \frac14 |u(m_0)|
\]

and

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le \frac18 |u(m_0)|s^2.
\]

Then at least one of \(m_0+s\), \(m_0-s\) satisfies

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge c|u(m_0)|s^2.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

With \(\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C\), choosing \(s\) smaller if necessary also gives

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

With \(\|\mathcal G'\|_\infty\le Q^C\), choosing \(s\) smaller again gives

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

So the wall sample produces a nearby non-wall sample with Gate 2 pointwise mass.

---

# 4. Apply D4 at the escaped point

At \(m_1\), we now have

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2\right)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

D4 gives, assuming correction control,

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Let

\[
R(m)=\left(A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m),A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)\right).
\]

If

\[
\|R'\|_{L^\infty(I_\rho^\ast)}\le Q^{C_R},
\]

then \(R\) remains polynomially non-small on a small interval around \(m_1\):

\[
|R(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C}
\]

for

\[
|m-m_1|\le Q^{-C-C_R-1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

So a nearby pointwise D4 lower bound gives a genuine local row-energy lower bound.

---

# 5. Updated theorem: wall escape row conversion

## Wall-Escape Row Conversion Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}\mathcal G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

2. Polynomial local bounds:

\[
\|q_0\|_{C^3}
+
\|u\|_{C^1}
+
\|\mathcal G\|_{C^1}
+
\|R\|_{C^1}
\le Q^C.
\]

3. D4 nondegenerate row conversion with correction control.

4. Nearby sampling is admissible; i.e. the downstream contradiction only needs row energy or a row sample somewhere in \(I_\rho\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
\left(
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2
\right)dm
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This handles both branches:

- if \(q_0\) is non-small at the Gate 2 sample, use D4 directly;
- if \(q_0\) is small, escape quadratically to a nearby non-wall point and then use D4.

---

# 6. Consequence: D3 may be unnecessary

This is the main update.

The previous D3 input was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

But if wall escape plus nearby sampling is valid, D3 can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling + D4 Correction Control}.
}
\]

That is much easier than finding a new row satisfying

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

So the downstream stack becomes:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1/D2 or source oscillation}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}
\]

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall Escape}
+
\text{D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

This removes the need for a new wall row **if** nearby sampling is permitted.

---

# 7. Remaining exact check

The only serious architectural condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the final row contradiction accept row mass somewhere in }I_\rho?
}
\]

If the contradiction is integral/energy-based, yes.

If the contradiction is pinned to the original \(Z_\alpha\)-zero or a fixed center \(m_0\), no.

Given the current Gate 2 formulation is already an integral statement over \(I_\rho\),

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2),
\]

the natural downstream row conversion should also be interval-energy based. Therefore nearby sampling appears admissible.

---

# 8. Revised priority

The previous priority was D3 wall-row search. This attack suggests shifting priority:

1. **First:** prove/confirm nearby sampling admissibility in the downstream contradiction.
2. **Second:** formalize wall-escape row conversion.
3. **Third:** close D4 correction control.
4. **Only if nearby sampling is not admissible:** resume source-robust row search.

Thus the \(q_0\)-wall may no longer be a major structural blocker. It becomes a local Taylor escape problem plus correction control.

## Continuing attack — make wall escape exponent-consistent

The wall-escape idea is viable, but it needs an exponent check. The escape step has competing requirements:

\[
q_0(m_1)\sim u(m_0)s^2
\]

must be **large enough** to enter the nondegenerate branch, while \(s\) must be **small enough** to preserve \(u\), preserve Gate 2 mass, and keep Taylor errors controlled.

The good news: these constraints are compatible if the nondegenerate threshold is chosen after the local derivative bounds. This gives a clean replacement for the old D3 wall-row input.

---

# 1. Wall branch data

Let

\[
\mathcal G(m)=|u(m)|^2(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2).
\]

Assume at a sampled wall point \(m_0\):

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-K_0},
\]

\[
\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-K_G},
\]

and polynomial upper bounds

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{K_\Gamma}.
\]

Then

\[
|u(m_0)|^2
\ge
Q^{-K_G}Q^{-2K_\Gamma},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-K_u},
\qquad
K_u=\frac12K_G+K_\Gamma.
}
\]

Since

\[
u=q_0'',
\]

we can use quadratic escape.

---

# 2. Exponent-compatible escape

Assume local derivative bounds

\[
\|q_0'''\|_\infty\le Q^{K_3},
\]

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{K_u'},
\]

\[
\|\mathcal G'\|_\infty\le Q^{K_G'}.
\]

Choose a step

\[
s=Q^{-L}.
\]

Taylor gives

\[
q_0(m_0+s)+q_0(m_0-s)
=
2q_0(m_0)+u(m_0)s^2+O(Q^{K_3}s^3).
\]

So one of \(m_0\pm s\) satisfies

\[
|q_0(m_1)|
\ge
cQ^{-K_u-2L}
-
Q^{-K_0}
-
CQ^{K_3-3L}.
\]

To ensure this is polynomially nonzero, require:

\[
K_0>K_u+2L+O(1),
\]

and

\[
K_3-3L<-K_u-2L-O(1),
\]

i.e.

\[
L>K_3+K_u+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_q},
\qquad
K_q=K_u+2L+O(1).
}
\]

Now preserve \(u\):

\[
|u(m_1)-u(m_0)|\le Q^{K_u'}s=Q^{K_u'-L}.
\]

Require

\[
L>K_u'+K_u+O(1),
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12Q^{-K_u}.
}
\]

Preserve Gate 2 mass:

\[
|\mathcal G(m_1)-\mathcal G(m_0)|\le Q^{K_G'}s.
\]

Require

\[
L>K_G'+K_G+O(1),
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G(m_1)\ge \frac12Q^{-K_G}.
}
\]

So choose

\[
\boxed{
L>
\max\{K_3+K_u,\ K_u'+K_u,\ K_G'+K_G\}+O(1).
}
\]

Then the escaped point \(m_1\) satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_q},
\quad
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_u-O(1)},
\quad
\mathcal G(m_1)\ge Q^{-K_G-O(1)}.
}
\]

This is exactly the nondegenerate D4 regime.

---

# 3. Threshold choice resolves the “thick wall” ambiguity

There is a subtle issue: what if

\[
|q_0(m_0)|
\]

is small, but not small enough relative to \(u(m_0)s^2\)?

Then we simply classify \(m_0\) as already nondegenerate.

Define the nondegenerate threshold by

\[
Q^{-K_q}=Q^{-K_u-2L-C}.
\]

Then:

- if \(|q_0(m_0)|\ge Q^{-K_q}\), D4 applies at \(m_0\);
- if \(|q_0(m_0)|<Q^{-K_q}\), the Taylor escape applies and produces \(m_1\) with \(|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_q}\).

Thus there is no ambiguous “medium wall” branch.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Choose the \(q_0\)-threshold to match the Taylor escape scale.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Interior and boundary handling

If both \(m_0+s\) and \(m_0-s\) lie in \(I_\rho\), use the symmetric second difference.

If \(m_0\) is near the boundary, use the one-sided identity

\[
q_0(m_0+2s)-2q_0(m_0+s)+q_0(m_0)
=
u(m_0)s^2+O(Q^{K_3}s^3).
\]

Then at least one of

\[
m_0,\quad m_0+s,\quad m_0+2s
\]

has

\[
|q_0|\ge cQ^{-K_u-2L},
\]

unless \(q_0(m_0)\) was already nondegenerate.

Thus wall escape works provided the interval has one-sided room

\[
2s\le \operatorname{dist}(m_0,\partial I_\rho)
\]

or the packet interval is enlarged to a slightly larger controlled interval \(I_\rho^\ast\).

This gives a mild boundary condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 pointwise mass must be sampled at distance }\ge Q^{-L}
\text{ from the boundary,}
}
\]

or one must allow one-sided/enlarged-interval sampling.

---

# 5. From escaped point to row-energy

Let

\[
R(m)=(A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m),A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)).
\]

D4 at \(m_1\) gives

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_R}.
\]

Assume

\[
\|R'\|_\infty\le Q^{K_R'}.
\]

Then on

\[
|m-m_1|\le r,
\qquad
r=Q^{-K_R-K_R'-C},
\]

we have

\[
|R(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-K_R}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-2K_R}r
=
Q^{-3K_R-K_R'-C}.
}
\]

So the row lower bound becomes an interval-energy lower bound.

This is stronger than merely finding a point.

---

# 6. Wall escape replaces D3 if downstream is energy-based

The downstream target after Gate 2 should be formulated as an interval row-energy statement:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
\left(
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|^2+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|^2
\right)dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{O(1)}
}
\]

or at least a polynomial lower bound on a local subinterval.

If that is the desired output, wall escape is admissible.

Then the old D3:

\[
\text{Source-Robust Row at }q_0=0
\]

is not needed.

Instead, use:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3'}:\text{ Wall-Escape Sampling}
}
\]

plus D4.

---

# 7. Revised downstream theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 + D4 + Wall Escape implies row energy

Assume:

1. Gate 2:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}\mathcal G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

2. Polynomial upper bounds for

\[
q_0''',\ u',\ \mathcal G',\ R'.
\]

3. D4 nondegenerate row conversion with correction control.

4. Interior or one-sided sampling admissibility at scale \(Q^{-L}\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
\left(
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2
\right)dm
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Proof:

- sample \(m_0\) with \(\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}\);
- if \(|q_0(m_0)|\) is non-small, apply D4;
- if \(|q_0(m_0)|\) is small, escape to \(m_1\);
- apply D4 at \(m_1\);
- use derivative bounds to thicken the pointwise row lower bound into row energy.

---

# 8. What remains open

This attack reduces D3 to local bookkeeping, but three checks remain:

## 8.1 Is row energy enough?

Need confirmation that the final contradiction uses an interval/local-energy lower bound, not exact row value at the original Gate 2 sample.

If yes, wall escape is valid.

## 8.2 Are derivative bounds polynomial?

Need bounds for:

\[
q_0''',\quad u',\quad \mathcal G',\quad R'.
\]

These should follow from the same canonical derivative package used elsewhere, but must be stated.

## 8.3 Is D4 correction control available at \(m_1\)?

D4 must be stable at nearby points and not tied to the original \(m_0\). This should hold if D4 is purely local and canonical.

---

# 9. Updated status

\[
\boxed{
\text{The \(q_0\)-wall is probably not a structural blocker if nearby sampling is allowed.}
}
\]

It becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling + D4 Correction Control}.
}
\]

So the downstream named inputs can be simplified:

- D1: source oscillation / density propagation for Gate 2;
- D2: derivative/interpolation propagation, likely folded into D1 if using component intervals;
- D4: nondegenerate row conversion plus correction control;
- D3 is replaced by a local wall-escape lemma, unless exact-point sampling is required.

The next best attack is therefore **not** row-residue search. It is to verify the downstream contradiction is interval-energy based.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:21:08)

I’ll now test the interval-energy admissibility condition. The key is whether a pointwise row lower bound can be converted into the exact downstream norm or contradiction functional without needing the original Gate 2 sample.

_Thought for 10s_

## Continuing attack — interval-energy admissibility for wall escape

The wall-escape route now depends on one architectural condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does downstream row conversion need the row at the original point, or only row mass somewhere in } I_\rho?
}
\]

If it only needs interval row energy, then the \(q_0\)-wall is essentially handled by wall escape plus D4. The current handoff already frames the downstream layer in integral/energy terms, so the natural answer is: **yes, nearby sampling should be admissible**, provided the row functional is measured on \(I_\rho\). 

---

# 1. Desired downstream output

The natural row-conversion target should be an interval lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
\left(
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)|^2
\right)\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{\beta}
}
\]

for some acceptable normalization exponent \(\beta\), often \(\beta=1\) if the row quantities are normalized as densities.

This is compatible with the upstream Gate 2 statement:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Both are interval-energy statements.

Thus a row lower bound at a nearby point \(m_1\in I_\rho\) is enough if it thickens to a small local interval.

---

# 2. Pointwise row lower bound thickens to row energy

Let

\[
R(m)=
\left(A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m),A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)\right).
\]

Assume at some point \(m_1\in I_\rho\),

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_R}.
\]

Assume a derivative bound

\[
\|R'\|_{L^\infty(I_\rho^\ast)}\le Q^{K_R'}.
\]

Then for

\[
r=\frac12Q^{-K_R-K_R'},
\]

we have

\[
|R(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-K_R}
\]

whenever

\[
|m-m_1|\le r
\]

and the interval stays inside \(I_\rho^\ast\).

Hence

\[
\int_{I_\rho^\ast}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
r\cdot Q^{-2K_R}
\ge
Q^{-3K_R-K_R'-O(1)}.
\]

If \(m_1\) is sufficiently interior to \(I_\rho\), this lower bound holds on \(I_\rho\) itself:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Thus pointwise row size anywhere in \(I_\rho\) gives interval row energy.

---

# 3. Boundary correction

If \(m_1\) is close to the boundary of \(I_\rho\), use a one-sided thickening.

If

\[
m_1\in I_\rho
\]

and at least one side has room \(r\), then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac{r}{2}Q^{-2K_R}
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If neither side has room, then

\[
|I_\rho|\lesssim r.
\]

In that case, since \(r=Q^{-O(1)}\), the interval is already polynomially small, and the row point lower bound itself may be enough for any sampling-based contradiction. If the proof demands an integral normalized by \(|I_\rho|\), one must check:

\[
Q^{-2K_R}\gtrsim Q^{-C}|I_\rho|
\]

or enlarge \(I_\rho\) to a controlled parent interval \(I_\rho^\ast\).

So the boundary issue is not fatal. It is a bookkeeping item:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either sample in the interior, use one-sided thickening, or work on an enlarged controlled interval.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Wall escape plus row energy

Now combine.

Gate 2 gives a point \(m_0\) with

\[
\mathcal G(m_0)
=
|u(m_0)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_0)
\ge Q^{-K_G}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\ge Q^{-K_q},
\]

D4 applies directly at \(m_0\).

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<Q^{-K_q},
\]

then under polynomial derivative bounds, wall escape gives \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_q'},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_u'},
\]

\[
\mathcal G(m_1)\ge Q^{-K_G'}.
\]

Then D4 applies at \(m_1\):

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-K_R}.
\]

Then row thickening gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + wall escape + D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row-energy lower bound.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Exact theorem package

## Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 pointwise sample:

\[
\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-K_G}.
\]

2. Local derivative bounds:

\[
\|q_0'''\|_\infty+
\|u'\|_\infty+
\|\mathcal G'\|_\infty+
\|R'\|_\infty
\le Q^{K_D}.
\]

3. D4 nondegenerate row conversion:

\[
|q_0(m)|\ge Q^{-K_q},
\quad
\mathcal G(m)\ge Q^{-K_G}
\Rightarrow
|R(m)|\ge Q^{-K_R}.
\]

4. Nearby sampling admissibility: a row lower bound at any \(m\in I_\rho^\ast\) within polynomial distance of \(I_\rho\) is acceptable for the downstream row-energy contradiction.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho^\ast}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-K}.
}
\]

If \(I_\rho^\ast=I_\rho\) or row energy transfers back to \(I_\rho\), this closes the downstream row-conversion step.

---

# 6. What this replaces

Previously D3 was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

That required finding

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The wall-escape route replaces this with a much simpler local theorem:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u\ne0
\Rightarrow
q_0\text{ becomes nonzero nearby.}
}
\]

Thus D3 can be downgraded from a structural row-algebra problem to a local sampling lemma, provided row energy is the downstream target.

---

# 7. Remaining possible obstruction

The only serious obstruction is if the final contradiction is **pointwise pinned** at the original point \(m_0\), for example if some later equation requires all quantities evaluated exactly at the same \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

But the downstream Gate 2 layer is already formulated as an integral over \(I_\rho\), not as a pointwise identity at \(m_0\). Therefore pointwise pinning would be unnatural here.

The clean architectural requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Downstream contradiction must use row energy on }I_\rho,\text{ not row value exactly at }m_0.
}
\]

If this is accepted, the \(q_0\)-wall is no longer a major blocker.

---

# 8. Revised downstream inputs

The downstream stack can be simplified:

## D1/D2 replacement

Prove Gate 2 via source oscillation / component control:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2
\Rightarrow
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
}
\]

## D4

Nondegenerate row conversion plus correction control:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C},\quad \mathcal G\ge Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
|R|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

## D3 becomes local sampling

Wall branch:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C},\quad \mathcal G\ge Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1:
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},\quad \mathcal G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Then D4 applies.

So the source-robust row search is only needed if nearby sampling is disallowed.

---

# 9. Next precise target

The next thing to formalize is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Nearby Sampling Admissibility Lemma}
}
\]

Statement:

If a downstream row vector \(R\) satisfies

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at some point

\[
m_1\in I_\rho^\ast
\]

with

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_1,I_\rho)\le Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
\|R'\|_{I_\rho^\ast}\le Q^C,
\]

then the required row-energy or row-sampling conclusion for \(I_\rho\) holds.

This is a local analytic lemma and should be provable.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall escape likely resolves the }q_0\text{-wall for interval-energy downstream architecture.}
}
\]

The \(q_0\)-wall remains a structural problem only if the final contradiction requires exact-point row conversion at the original sample. Otherwise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3} \Rightarrow \text{Wall Escape Sampling + D4}.
}
\]

The main remaining downstream blocker is therefore Gate 2 itself, especially the source oscillation / component-count route.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:22:56)

_Thought for 9s_

## Nearby Sampling Admissibility Lemma — attack and proof package

We want to justify replacing an exact-point row lower bound at the original Gate 2 sample \(m_0\) by a nearby row lower bound at \(m_1\). This is the key step that makes the \(q_0\)-wall escape useful: if row conversion is interval-energy based, then a row lower bound anywhere in the controlled packet interval should be sufficient. This directly targets the downstream row-conversion issue isolated in the current architecture. 

---

# 1. Basic point-to-energy lemma

Let

\[
R(m)=\left(A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m),A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)\right)
\]

or any finite row vector. Suppose

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-A_R}
\]

at some

\[
m_1\in I_\rho^\ast,
\]

and suppose

\[
\|R'\|_{L^\infty(I_\rho^\ast)}\le Q^{C_R}.
\]

Then for

\[
r=\frac12 Q^{-A_R-C_R},
\]

we have

\[
|R(m)|\ge \frac12 Q^{-A_R}
\]

whenever

\[
|m-m_1|\le r
\]

and the segment lies in \(I_\rho^\ast\).

Therefore, if

\[
[m_1-r,m_1+r]\subset I_\rho,
\]

then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
\int_{m_1-r}^{m_1+r}\frac14Q^{-2A_R}\,dm
\ge
\frac12 Q^{-2A_R}r.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-3A_R-C_R-O(1)}.
}
\]

So pointwise row size at an interior nearby point gives polynomial row energy.

---

# 2. One-sided boundary version

If \(m_1\) lies near the boundary of \(I_\rho\), the symmetric interval may not fit. Let

\[
d_1=\operatorname{dist}(m_1,\partial I_\rho).
\]

If

\[
d_1\ge r,
\]

the previous proof applies.

If

\[
0<d_1<r,
\]

then at least one one-sided interval of length \(d_1\) lies inside \(I_\rho\), giving

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac14Q^{-2A_R}d_1.
\]

Thus if

\[
d_1\ge Q^{-C_b},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-2A_R-C_b-O(1)}.
}
\]

So the only problematic case is when \(m_1\) is within a super-polynomially tiny boundary layer. With polynomial interior distance, nearby sampling is admissible.

---

# 3. Enlarged-interval transfer

Often the escape point \(m_1\) may lie in a controlled enlargement

\[
I_\rho^\ast\supset I_\rho
\]

rather than inside \(I_\rho\). Let

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_1,I_\rho)\le d_\ast.
\]

If

\[
d_\ast\le \frac r2,
\]

then the ball

\[
[m_1-r,m_1+r]
\]

intersects \(I_\rho\) in length at least \(r/2\), provided \(m_1\) is not outside both ends by more than \(r/2\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-3A_R-C_R-O(1)}.
}
\]

So it is enough for the escaped point to be within polynomially controlled distance of \(I_\rho\), at scale comparable to the row-stability radius.

---

# 4. Weighted row-energy version

If the downstream row norm uses a smooth weight \(w_\rho(m)\ge0\), assume

\[
w_\rho(m)\ge Q^{-C_w}
\]

on a neighborhood of \(m_1\) of radius \(r\). Then

\[
\int_{I_\rho^\ast}w_\rho(m)|R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-C_w}Q^{-2A_R}r
\]

and hence

\[
\boxed{
\int w_\rho |R|^2
\ge Q^{-3A_R-C_R-C_w-O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus weighted packet norms are compatible with nearby sampling as long as the escaped point is not in a region where the packet weight is exponentially small.

---

# 5. Full Nearby Sampling Admissibility Lemma

## Lemma

Let \(I_\rho\subset I_\rho^\ast\) be a controlled packet interval. Let \(R:I_\rho^\ast\to\mathbb C^d\) be \(C^1\). Assume:

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-A_R},
\]

\[
\|R'\|_{L^\infty(I_\rho^\ast)}\le Q^{C_R},
\]

and either:

1. \(m_1\in I_\rho\) with

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(m_1,\partial I_\rho)\ge Q^{-C_b};
   \]

2. or \(m_1\in I_\rho^\ast\) with

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(m_1,I_\rho)\le \frac12Q^{-A_R-C_R-O(1)};
   \]

3. or the row norm is taken over \(I_\rho^\ast\) itself.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some exponent

\[
A'=O(A_R+C_R+C_b+1).
\]

If a weight \(w_\rho\) is used and satisfies

\[
w_\rho\ge Q^{-C_w}
\]

near \(m_1\), then

\[
A'=O(A_R+C_R+C_b+C_w+1).
\]

---

# 6. Application to \(q_0\)-wall escape

Let

\[
\mathcal G(m)=|u(m)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m).
\]

Suppose Gate 2 gives a sample \(m_0\) with

\[
\mathcal G(m_0)\ge Q^{-A_G}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_q},
\]

D4 gives directly

\[
|R(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_R}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<Q^{-A_q},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_0)|=|q_0''(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_u},
\]

wall escape gives a nearby \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-A_q'},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-A_u'},
\]

and

\[
\mathcal G(m_1)\ge Q^{-A_G'}.
\]

Then D4 applies at \(m_1\):

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-A_R'}.
\]

By Nearby Sampling Admissibility,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|R(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

Thus the wall branch reduces to wall escape plus D4.

---

# 7. What must be checked in the proof architecture

The lemma is valid as a local analytic statement. The only architectural checks are:

## Check 1: downstream output is energy-based

The downstream contradiction must accept

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|R|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or row size at some admissible point in \(I_\rho\), not necessarily the original \(m_0\).

If exact-point evaluation at the original \(m_0\) is required, the lemma does not help.

## Check 2: packet weight is not zero near \(m_1\)

If rows are measured with a localization weight, require

\[
w_\rho(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is automatic if \(m_1\) lies in the interior of the packet window.

## Check 3: derivative bounds are polynomial

Need

\[
\|R'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Since \(R\) is built from finite normalized derivatives of canonical quantities, this should follow from the canonical derivative package, but it must be explicitly included.

## Check 4: wall escape remains inside the controlled interval

Need

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
m_1\in I_\rho^\ast
\]

with either interior distance or one-sided/enlarged interval control.

---

# 8. Consequence for D3

The original D3 was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

The nearby sampling lemma suggests replacing it with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling + Nearby Row-Energy Admissibility + D4}.
}
\]

This is a much more local and tractable package.

The source-robust row search is only necessary if the final contradiction insists on row conversion at the exact wall point.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Nearby Sampling Admissibility is true under standard polynomial derivative and localization hypotheses.}
}
\]

Therefore, for an interval-energy downstream architecture, the \(q_0\)-wall is not a fundamental structural blocker.

The downstream row-conversion layer can be reorganized as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall Escape}
+
\text{D4 Nondegenerate Row Conversion}
+
\text{Nearby Sampling}
\Rightarrow
\text{row-energy lower bound}.
}
\]

This replaces the need for a new wall-live row, unless exact-point row evaluation is required later.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:23:58)

I’ll now attack the Gate 2 source-oscillation route directly. The key is to replace generic Remez with a frequency-side zero-count theorem for \(u=q''_{\can}\).

_Thought for 25s_

## Continuing attack — prove Gate 2 from a Cartwright/Turán zero-count bound for \(u\)

I’ll attack the current best Gate 2 route:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

If this source-oscillation/component bound is proved, the earlier mass-bearing component argument gives Gate 2. The new task is therefore to prove the component bound from the AFE/bandlimited structure of \(u\). This is now more concrete than the earlier generic D1 Remez/Cartan input. 

---

# 1. Local normalized model

Use the local coordinate

\[
m=m_0+\lambda t,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

A main AFE packet term has phase

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-it\lambda\log n}.
\]

Set

\[
\xi_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

On ordinary support,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q,
\]

so

\[
|\xi_n|\lesssim1.
\]

Thus the packet model for

\[
u(t)=q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda t)
\]

has the schematic form

\[
u_{\rm model}(t)
=
B_2(t)
+
\sum_{\xi\in\Xi_+}a_\xi e^{-it\xi}
+
e^{i\Theta(t)}
\sum_{\xi\in\Xi_-}b_\xi e^{+it\xi}
+
\text{controlled tail}.
\]

After folding the dual phase into the local coordinate, the effective frequencies remain in a bounded or polynomially bounded interval. Therefore \(u\) should behave like an exponential polynomial / bandlimited function of type

\[
\boxed{B_{\rm eff}=Q^{O(1)},}
\]

and in the ordinary packet case plausibly

\[
B_{\rm eff}=O(1)\quad\text{or}\quad O(R).
\]

---

# 2. Component count via threshold zeros

Let

\[
U_\tau=\{t\in I: |u(t)|\ge \tau\},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Each connected component of \(U_\tau\) is bounded by zeros of

\[
g_\tau(t)=|u(t)|^2-\tau^2.
\]

So

\[
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)
\le
1+N_I(g_\tau),
\]

where \(N_I(g_\tau)\) is the number of real zeros of \(g_\tau\) in \(I\).

For a finite exponential model,

\[
u(t)=\sum_{\xi\in\Xi}a_\xi e^{-it\xi},
\]

we have

\[
|u(t)|^2
=
\sum_{\xi,\eta\in\Xi}
a_\xi\overline{a_\eta}e^{-it(\xi-\eta)}.
\]

Thus

\[
g_\tau(t)
\]

is itself an exponential polynomial with frequencies in

\[
[-2B_{\rm eff},2B_{\rm eff}].
\]

So the desired component bound follows from a zero-count theorem for exponential polynomials / functions of exponential type with polynomial height control.

---

# 3. Effective zero-count lemma

A suitable lemma is:

## Effective Cartwright zero-count lemma

Let \(g\) be real analytic on \(I\) and holomorphic in a complex neighborhood

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I)=\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I)\le \rho\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Assume \(g\) has exponential type

\[
B_{\rm eff}\le Q^{C_B}
\]

and height bound

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|g|\le Q^{C_H}.
\]

Assume \(g\) is not identically \(Q^{-A}\)-small on \(I\); more concretely, there exists \(t_\ast\in I\) with

\[
|g(t_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_g}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
N_I(g)\le Q^C(1+B_{\rm eff}|I|).
}
\]

This can be proved by Jensen/Cartan on a chain of disks covering \(I\). The zero count in each disk is bounded by

\[
O\!\left(\log\frac{\sup_{\text{larger disk}}|g|}{|g(t_\ast)|}\right),
\]

and the exponential-type bound controls growth along the chain. Since all height ratios are polynomial in \(Q\), the logarithmic factor is \(O(\log Q)\), hence polynomially harmless.

Applied to

\[
g_\tau=|u|^2-\tau^2,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge\tau\}\le Q^C.}
\]

---

# 4. Avoiding bad thresholds

There is a minor issue: for a pathological threshold \(\tau\), \(g_\tau\) may be nearly zero on a long interval. But that case is not bad.

If

\[
|u(t)|^2\approx \tau^2
\]

on a long interval, then \(U_\tau\) already has a long interval component or its complement does. Either way, the component-count / mass-bearing interval step becomes easier.

More formally, choose \(\tau\) by dyadic pigeonholing from Gate 1. Since

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

there exists a dyadic threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

such that

\[
U_\tau=\{|u|\ge\tau\}
\]

carries polynomial \(u\)-mass:

\[
\int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

If this \(\tau\) lies too close to a critical level where \(g_\tau\) is flat, shift \(\tau\) within the same dyadic annulus. The mass loss is only polynomial. If every nearby threshold is critical, then \(|u|\) is nearly constant on a large set, again giving a large component.

Thus threshold selection is manageable.

---

# 5. Gate 2 from component count

Assume the source oscillation bound:

\[
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le Q^{C_N}.
\]

Gate 1 gives a threshold \(\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}\) with

\[
\int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Hence

\[
|U_\tau|\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

Since \(U_\tau\) has at most \(Q^{C_N}\) components, one component \(J_0\subset U_\tau\) has

\[
|J_0|\ge Q^{-C''}|I|.
\]

On \(J_0\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

where

\[
F=(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then on \(J_0\),

\[
\int_{J_0}F^2
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Since

\[
|J_0|\ge Q^{-C''}|I|,
\]

we get

\[
\frac1{|J_0|}\int_{J_0}F^2
\le
Q^{-A+2C_\tau+C''}.
\]

For \(A\) large, \(F\) is small on most of \(J_0\).

Therefore the set

\[
E_0=\{t\in J_0:F(t)\le Q^{-C_F}\}
\]

has high relative measure in \(J_0\):

\[
|J_0\setminus E_0|\le Q^{-C}|J_0|.
\]

---

# 6. High relative measure gives gap-density

If

\[
|J_0\setminus E_0|\le \delta |J_0|,
\qquad \delta=Q^{-C},
\]

then after discarding endpoint gaps, there exists a central interval

\[
J\subset J_0,
\qquad |J|\ge \frac12|J_0|,
\]

such that the maximum gap of \(E_0\) in \(J\) is

\[
\operatorname{gap}_J(E_0)\le Q^{-C}|J|.
\]

Otherwise the complement would contain a gap of larger measure than allowed.

Thus \(E_0\) is polynomially gap-dense in \(J\).

---

# 7. Finite differences give derivative control

On the gap-dense interval \(J\), we have:

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_F}
\]

on a set with polynomial gap.

Using derivative bounds through order \(6\),

\[
\sup_{J^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

finite-difference interpolation yields on a shrunken interval \(J'\):

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|
+
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Then

\[
q(q')^2
=
\frac12\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\frac1{12}\Gamma_G''
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

Approximate interval rigidity then forces

\[
u\approx0
\]

on \(J''\subset J'\), contradicting

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}
\quad\text{on }J_0.
\]

Thus Gate 2 follows.

---

# 8. Updated theorem

## Gate 2 via Source Oscillation Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Effective source oscillation bound:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C
}
\]

for all relevant polynomial thresholds.

3. Polynomial derivative bounds through order \(6\).

4. Approximate interval rigidity.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

This replaces the vague D1/D2 propagation package with a concrete source oscillation theorem.

---

# 9. What remains to prove

The central remaining analytic theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
u(t)=q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda t)
\text{ is effectively bandlimited / finite type enough that}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u(t)|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is now the best near-term Gate 2 target.

It should be attacked by proving:

1. local AFE bandlimit for \(u\) in the normalized variable \(t\);
2. polynomial height bounds in a complex tube;
3. effective zero-count for \(g_\tau=|u|^2-\tau^2\);
4. stability under \(B_2\), folded dual, and \(E_2\).

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 can likely be reduced to a source oscillation/component-count theorem.}
}
\]

This is sharper and more concrete than the earlier D1/D2 Remez formulation. If the bandlimited zero-count lemma is proved canonically for \(u=q''_{\can}\), then Gate 2 should close.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:33:34)

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 3 / C — Full Gate 2 theorem from extraction + integral rigidity

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: combine the two-threshold extraction theorem and the integral rigidity lemma into a full Gate 2 theorem. The current target is to replace the older abstract D1/D2 package with the sharper chain

\[
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

---

# 1. Gate 1 and Gate 2

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Use

\[
g=\Gamma_G,\qquad h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with identities

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive assumption

Assume Gate 1 holds but Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then the failure condition is

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

We want to derive a contradiction for \(A\) sufficiently large.

---

# 3. Two-threshold extraction

Assume the two-threshold extraction theorem gives an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

and on \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

This is stronger than the older bad-set extraction: it gives genuine interval control, not only smallness on a measurable/dust-like set.

The extraction theorem uses:

1. a source threshold

   \[
   \tau=Q^{-T},
   \]

2. Gate 1 to find nontrivial \(|u|\)-mass above threshold,

3. Gate 2 failure to locate a point where \(F_{\rm aniso}\) is very small while \(|u|\) is non-small,

4. Lipschitz bounds on \(u\) and \(F_{\rm aniso}\) to grow this point into an interval \(J\).

For this Agent 3 synthesis, I treat that extraction theorem as the input from Agent 1.

---

# 4. Integral rigidity lemma

Assume the integral rigidity lemma states:

If on an interval \(J\),

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

then for a shrunken interval

\[
J'\Subset J
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Here \(\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}|J'|.
}
\]

This is the Agent 2 input.

The exponent \(2/5\) comes from balancing the small-\(|q|\) region against the integration-by-parts estimate on the region where \(|q|\) is bounded away from zero.

---

# 5. Contradiction with interval source lower bound

Since

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

throughout \(J\), the same holds on \(J'\subset J\). Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
}
\]

Combining with the integral rigidity upper bound gives

\[
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}|J'|.
\]

Cancel \(|J'|\):

\[
Q^{-2C_u}
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}.
\]

This is impossible if

\[
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
\]

Equivalently, choose

\[
\boxed{
A_1>\frac52(2C_u+C_R).
}
\]

Thus, for sufficiently strong extraction smallness \(A_1\), Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure cannot coexist.

Therefore Gate 2 holds.

---

# 6. Conditional Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem

Assume the following.

### Gate 1

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

### Two-threshold extraction

If Gate 2 fails, then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

on \(J\).

### Integral rigidity

For every interval \(J\) satisfying

\[
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

there is \(J'\Subset J\) such that

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then, if

\[
A_1>\frac52(2C_u+C_R),
\]

Gate 2 follows:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. What this replaces

This route replaces the older package

\[
\text{D1 Density/Remez}
+
\text{D2 Derivative Propagation}
\]

with the sharper pair

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold interval extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}.
}
\]

The benefit is that one no longer needs to prove pointwise smallness of \(\Gamma_G''\) by Remez/Bernstein. The integral rigidity lemma handles the \(g''\) term by integration by parts inside

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

---

# 8. Remaining hypotheses to make rigorous

The combined Gate 2 theorem is strong, but it still depends on two nontrivial pieces.

## 8.1 Two-threshold extraction

Needed output:

\[
\exists J:\quad |u|\ge Q^{-C_u},\quad |g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}\quad\text{on }J.
\]

This requires:

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_u'}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
F_{\rm aniso}'\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1},
\]

and a point extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure producing simultaneous

\[
|u|\ge 2Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
F_{\rm aniso}\le Q^{-A_0}.
\]

The key inequality is that the interval grown by Lipschitz propagation remains polynomially long.

## 8.2 Integral rigidity

Needed proof:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

This requires controlling integration-by-parts boundary/cutoff terms and polynomial upper bounds on

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ g,\ g',\ g''.
\]

The proof structure is plausible and sharper than earlier Remez, but the cutoff estimates must be checked carefully.

---

# 9. Status

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Gate 1 source lower bound | conditional from upstream architecture |
| Two-threshold extraction | plausible, needs Lipschitz/exponent bookkeeping |
| Integral rigidity lemma | promising proof candidate |
| Gate 2 from extraction + rigidity | formally closed |
| Old D1/D2 | replaced if extraction + rigidity are proved |

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 reduces to two-threshold extraction plus integral rigidity.}
}
\]

The formal implication is clean:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is a substantial improvement over the earlier D1/D2 formulation because it avoids generic Remez losses and avoids separately proving pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\)-smallness.

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem package

I am executing **Agent 3 / C**: synthesize the two-threshold extraction and integral rigidity routes into a complete conditional Gate 2 theorem. The current downstream plan is to replace the older abstract D1/D2 package with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 1. Target theorem

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

and define

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g''.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

The goal is to prove Gate 2 by contradiction.

---

# 2. Contrapositive setup

Assume Gate 1 holds:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

but Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then the failure condition is

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 3. Input G2-A: two-threshold extraction

Assume the two-threshold extraction theorem gives an interval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

This is the replacement for the earlier dust-like bad set / Remez step. It requires polynomial Lipschitz bounds of the form

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^{C_u'}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|g'|_\infty+|h'|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

The extraction route is:

1. Use Gate 1 to find a polynomial threshold \(\tau=Q^{-C_u}\) with nontrivial \(|u|\)-mass above \(2\tau\).
2. Use Gate 2 failure to locate a point \(m_\ast\) where

   \[
   |u(m_\ast)|\ge2\tau,
   \qquad
   F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)\le Q^{-A_0}.
   \]

3. Use Lipschitz bounds to grow \(m_\ast\) into an interval \(J\) where

   \[
   |u|\ge\tau,
   \qquad
   F_{\rm aniso}\le Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

This produces genuine interval control rather than set-level control.

---

# 4. Input G2-B: integral rigidity

Assume the integral rigidity lemma:

If on \(J\),

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

then for a shrunken interval

\[
J'\Subset J
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Apply this with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Contradiction

From the extraction interval,

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Therefore also on

\[
J'\subset J,
\]

we have

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

Combining the lower and upper bounds gives

\[
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}|J'|.
\]

Cancel \(|J'|\):

\[
Q^{-2C_u}
\le
Q^{-2A_1/5+C_R}.
\]

This is impossible if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A_1>\frac52(2C_u+C_R).
}
\]

Thus Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure cannot coexist once the extraction smallness exponent \(A_1\) is sufficiently large.

Therefore Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Final conditional Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 from two-threshold extraction and integral rigidity

Assume:

### Gate 1

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

### G2-A: two-threshold extraction

If Gate 2 fails, then there exists \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}\quad\text{on }J.
\]

### G2-B: integral rigidity

If

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

If

\[
A_1>\frac52(2C_u+C_R),
\]

then Gate 2 follows:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. What this replaces

This package replaces the previous abstract downstream pair:

\[
\text{D1: Density/Remez Propagation}
\]

and

\[
\text{D2: Derivative Propagation}.
\]

The new Gate 2 package is sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A: two-threshold extraction}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B: integral rigidity}.
}
\]

The improvement is that G2-B avoids separately proving pointwise smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

by integrating the \(g''\)-term in

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by parts inside the rigidity lemma.

---

# 8. Remaining proof obligations

## 8.1 G2-A obligations

Need to prove the interval extraction with exact exponent bookkeeping:

\[
\text{Gate 1}+\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\exists J:
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\quad
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Required analytic bounds:

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^{C_u'}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|g'|_\infty+|h'|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Boundary cases must be handled by one-sided intervals or by trimming \(I\).

## 8.2 G2-B obligations

Need to complete the cutoff/integration-by-parts proof:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Required controls:

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

on the cutoff support.

Need to check:

- cutoff derivative losses;
- boundary terms;
- sign conventions in \(h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\);
- small-\(|q|\) versus large-\(|q|\) decomposition;
- optimization \(\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}\).

---

# 9. Current status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is no longer best viewed as D1 + D2.}
}
\]

It is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is materially stronger and more local than the previous Remez/derivative-propagation formulation.

The downstream priority should therefore be:

1. formalize G2-B integral rigidity completely;
2. formalize G2-A two-threshold extraction with exponent bookkeeping;
3. then combine them as above.

## Agent 3 / C — Canonical Gate 2 theorem with all hypotheses exposed

I am executing **Agent 3 / C**: write the final Gate 2 theorem package with every hypothesis explicit, using the updated downstream route

\[
\text{G2-A: two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{G2-B: integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

This reflects the latest downstream simplification in the coordinator brief. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 target

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 supplies

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
}
\]

where

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g''.
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive setup

Assume Gate 1 holds and Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

but

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then failure is

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 3. G2-A: two-threshold extraction

Assume polynomial Lipschitz bounds on \(I\):

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^{C_u'}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|g'|_\infty+|h'|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

G2-A gives an interval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

The extracted exponents have the schematic form

\[
\boxed{
C_1=\frac B2+O(1),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_J=
\max\left(\frac B2+C_u',\ \frac{A-B}{2}+C_F\right)
+O(1).
}
\]

The exact constants depend on the threshold choices and one-sided boundary handling, but the dependence is polynomial.

---

# 4. G2-B: integral rigidity

Assume the integral rigidity lemma:

If on an interval \(J\),

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

then for a shrunken interval

\[
J'\Subset J
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Apply this with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R-2A_1/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Here \(C_R\) includes cutoff losses, polynomial bounds for

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q''',\ q^{(4)},
\]

and normalized derivative conventions.

---

# 5. Contradiction

Since

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\]

on \(J\), we also have on \(J'\subset J\):

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
}
\]

Combining the lower and upper estimates gives

\[
Q^{-2C_1}|J'|
\le
Q^{C_R-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

Cancel \(|J'|\):

\[
Q^{-2C_1}\le Q^{C_R-2A_1/5}.
\]

This is impossible if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_1.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A_1>\frac52(2C_1+C_R).
}
\]

Substituting the schematic extraction exponent

\[
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1),
\]

a sufficient condition on the Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) is

\[
\boxed{
A
>
B
+
5(2C_1+C_R)
+
O(C_F)
+
O(1).
}
\]

Using

\[
C_1=\frac B2+O(1),
\]

one convenient sufficient form is

\[
\boxed{
A>6B+5C_R+O(C_F)+O(1).
}
\]

The precise numerical coefficient is not important; the point is that a sufficiently large polynomial exponent in the Gate 2 contradiction hypothesis forces a contradiction.

---

# 6. Final Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 from two-threshold extraction and integral rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |q''_{\can}|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Canonical Lipschitz bounds:

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^{C_u'}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|_\infty+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. G2-B integral rigidity:

\[
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then, choosing \(A\) sufficiently large relative to \(B,C_F,C_R\), Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |q''_{\can}|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. What remains to verify

This theorem reduces Gate 2 to two local analytic checks.

## 7.1 G2-A Lipschitz/canonical derivative bounds

Need canonical bounds for

\[
u',
\quad
\Gamma_G',
\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}'.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

one needs enough derivatives of \(q\). In particular:

- \(u'\) needs \(q^{(3)}\);
- \(g'\) needs \(q^{(3)}\);
- \(h'\) needs up to \(g^{(3)}\), hence up to \(q^{(5)}\).

So \(k_0=5\) may suffice for extraction, while \(k_0=6\) remains safer for integral rigidity and error control.

## 7.2 G2-B cutoff proof

Need to finish the real-variable proof of

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

The proof must check:

- cutoff construction;
- integration by parts in

  \[
  h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'';
  \]

- boundary terms;
- transition region

  \[
  |q|\sim \delta;
  \]

- the optimization

  \[
  \delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
  \]

---

# 8. Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now reduced to local calculus, not global Remez.}
}
\]

The old D1/D2 labels can be replaced downstream by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A: two-threshold extraction}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B: integral rigidity}.
}
\]

G2-A is essentially bookkeeping under Lipschitz bounds. G2-B is the main remaining technical lemma.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:54:39)

I’ll focus on the integral rigidity lemma now, because it is the highest-leverage remaining downstream piece. The key issue is whether the \(g''\) term in \(h\) can be integrated by parts without losing more than the claimed \(\varepsilon^{2/5}\).

_Thought for 22s_

## Continuing attack — rigorous skeleton for the Gate 2 integral rigidity lemma

I’ll now attack **G2-B**, the integral rigidity lemma:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|.
\]

The target exponent from the previous plan was \(c=2/5\). After checking the integration-by-parts bookkeeping, the proof still looks viable, though I would state the first version with a flexible positive exponent \(c>0\), then optimize once all cutoff constants are fixed.

Recall:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

The lemma is local real-variable calculus. It does not use RH-specific arithmetic once the identities and polynomial derivative bounds are available. 

---

# 1. Setup and cutoffs

Let

\[
J'\Subset J,
\]

and choose a smooth cutoff

\[
\phi\in C_c^\infty(J),
\qquad
0\le \phi\le1,
\qquad
\phi\equiv1\text{ on }J',
\]

with polynomial cutoff bounds

\[
|\phi^{(r)}|\le Q^C|J|^{-r}.
\]

Assume polynomial local bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

on \(\operatorname{supp}\phi\).

Let \(\delta\in(0,1)\) be chosen later.

Choose an even cutoff \(\chi_\delta(q)\) such that

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad (|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(r)}(q)|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Choose a smooth sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) such that

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)\quad (|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le\delta),
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta^{(r)}(q)|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Then

\[
s_\delta(q)q=|q|
\quad\text{on } |q|\ge2\delta.
\]

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate away from \(q=0\)

Start with

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Multiply by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q)
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=|q|,
\]

so the main positive term is

\[
2\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

The left side is bounded by

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\varepsilon |J|\,Q^C,
\]

because \(|h|\le\varepsilon\).

For the \(g''\)-term, integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g\left(\phi s_\delta(q)\right)''.
\]

Since \(|g|\le\varepsilon\),

\[
\left|\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
\varepsilon\int \left|(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta(q)
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The terms with \(\phi'',\phi',q''\) are bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon \delta^{-1}|J|
\]

or better.

The term

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\]

is supported where

\[
\delta\le |q|\le2\delta,
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta''(q)|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

On this transition region,

\[
(q')^2
\le
\delta^{-1}|q|(q')^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\varepsilon\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}\phi\delta^{-2}(q')^2
\le
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

This term is not automatically absorbable unless

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\ll1.
\]

This is exactly why the exponent bookkeeping matters. We impose

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\le \frac12
\]

which will hold for the later choice \(\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}\), since

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

After absorption, we get

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

Since \(|q|\ge2\delta\) on this region,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

This gives a slightly worse \(\delta^{-4}\) than the optimistic \(\delta^{-3}\). The earlier \(\delta^{-3}\) can be recovered with a sharper cutoff choice or weighted estimate, but \(\delta^{-4}\) is already enough for a positive exponent.

---

# 3. Potential estimate away from \(q=0\)

We want to control

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g
\]

and

\[
u=q'',
\]

we have

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Multiply by

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon|J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int (\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'
=
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

Thus

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''\right|
\le
T_1+T_2+T_3,
\]

where

\[
T_1=
\left|\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|,
\]

\[
T_2=
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2\right|,
\]

\[
T_3=
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2\right|.
\]

The terms \(T_2,T_3\) are bounded by the kinetic estimate.

On the support of \(\chi_\delta\),

\[
|q|\ge2\delta,
\]

except in the transition where \(|q|\sim\delta\). Also \(F,F'\) are polynomially bounded, and in the transition

\[
|F(q)|=O(\delta).
\]

So

\[
T_2+T_3
\le
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
\]

For \(T_1\), use Cauchy–Schwarz and choose \(\phi=\psi^2\). Then

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi.
\]

Hence

\[
T_1
\le
\left(\int Q^C\phi \chi_\delta F(q)^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Let

\[
X=\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2.
\]

Then

\[
T_1\le
Q^C X^{1/2}
\left(\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
X
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|
+
Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|)^{1/2}.
\]

Absorbing the last term by \(ab\le \frac12a^2+\frac12b^2\), we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

Thus on

\[
J'\cap \{|q|\ge3\delta\}
\]

where \(\phi=1,\chi_\delta=1\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

Since \(J'\) is a fixed polynomial fraction of \(J\), replace \(|J|\) by \(Q^C|J'|\):

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g
\]

and \(|g|\le\varepsilon\),

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Combine large and small regions

On the large-\(|q|\) region,

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

so

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J'|+Q^C\varepsilon^2|J'|.
\]

On the small-\(|q|\) region,

\[
\int |u|^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-4}+\varepsilon^2
\right)|J'|.
}
\]

Optimize by balancing

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^6=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/6}.
\]

This gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

So the fully safe cutoff proof gives exponent

\[
\boxed{c=\frac13}
\]

rather than the previously claimed \(2/5\), unless one sharpens the transition kinetic estimate from \(\delta^{-4}\) to \(\delta^{-3}\).

This is still more than enough for Gate 2.

---

# 6. Improved exponent if transition is sharpened

If one can improve the kinetic bound to

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

then the combined estimate becomes

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3})|J'|.
\]

Balancing gives

\[
\delta^5=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5},
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
2/5\text{ is plausible with sharper cutoff bookkeeping;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
1/3\text{ is the robust exponent from the conservative proof.}
}
\]

Either exponent is sufficient.

---

# 7. Gate 2 contradiction with exponent \(1/3\)

From two-threshold extraction,

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1},
\]

this is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^{C_R-A_1/3}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction follows if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_1}{3}-C_R>2C_1.
}
\]

This is only slightly stronger than the previous condition with \(2/5\). We can simply require \(A_1\) larger.

Thus Gate 2 remains closeable.

---

# 8. Final integral rigidity lemma, conservative version

## Lemma

Assume on \(J\)

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume polynomial bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

on a cutoff neighborhood of \(J'\Subset J\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|q''|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

With sharper transition bookkeeping, the exponent can improve to \(2/5\), but \(1/3\) is enough.

---

# 9. Updated Gate 2 theorem

Use G2-A to produce

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\qquad
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

on \(J\).

Use conservative G2-B:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C Q^{-A_1/3}|J'|.
\]

Contradict

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|
\]

if

\[
\boxed{
A_1>3(2C_1+C).
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + conservative integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Verdict

The integral rigidity route survives detailed cutoff stress-testing.

The exact exponent may be

\[
\frac13
\]

rather than

\[
\frac25
\]

unless the kinetic transition estimate is sharpened, but either is sufficient.

So the downstream Gate 2 layer is now much more concrete:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{G2-B integral rigidity with exponent }c>0
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The remaining work is mostly canonical derivative bookkeeping and verifying the row-conversion D4 normal form.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:56:28)

I’ll attack the two-threshold extraction step itself. The main check is whether the point with non-small \(u\) and small anisotropy can be thickened into a polynomial interval without hidden dependence on \(|I|\) or on the nonsmooth square root \(F_{\rm aniso}\).

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — formal two-threshold extraction proof

I’ll now pin down **G2-A: two-threshold extraction**, because the integral rigidity lemma is now in usable shape with at least a conservative positive exponent. The target is:

\[
\text{Gate 1}+\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\exists J\subset I:
|u|\ge Q^{-C},\quad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\text{ on }J.
\]

This is the extraction step needed before applying the integral rigidity lemma from the previous attack. The latest downstream handoff identifies precisely this two-threshold extraction plus integral rigidity package as the current strongest Gate 2 route. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
F=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume polynomial pointwise and Lipschitz bounds:

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_0},
\]

\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_{L^\infty(I)}+\|h'\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Avoid differentiating \(F=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}\) directly; use \(g,h\) separately.

---

# 2. Source threshold

Choose

\[
\tau^2=\frac12 Q^{-B}.
\]

Then

\[
\tau=2^{-1/2}Q^{-B/2}.
\]

On the complement

\[
\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

we have

\[
\int_{\{|u|<\tau\}}|u|^2\,dm
\le
\tau^2|I|
=
\frac12Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{\{|u|\ge\tau\}}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac12Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
U=\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_U |u|^2\,dm\ge \frac12Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 3. Find a point with non-small \(u\) and small anisotropy

By Gate 2 failure,

\[
\int_U |u|^2F^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by the lower bound on \(\int_U|u|^2\):

\[
\frac{\int_U |u|^2F^2\,dm}
{\int_U |u|^2\,dm}
\le
2Q^{-A+B}.
\]

Hence there exists

\[
m_\ast\in U
\]

such that

\[
F(m_\ast)^2\le 2Q^{-A+B}.
\]

Thus

\[
F(m_\ast)\le C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

Since

\[
F=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2},
\]

we get

\[
|g(m_\ast)|+|h(m_\ast)|
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

Also

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge \tau
\asymp Q^{-B/2}.
\]

So the pointwise extraction is:

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge cQ^{-B/2},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|g(m_\ast)|+|h(m_\ast)|
\le C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Thicken the point into an interval

Define the radius

\[
r
=
c_0|I|
\min
\left(
Q^{-B/2-C_u},
\,
Q^{-(A-B)/2-C_F}
\right),
\]

where \(c_0>0\) is a small absolute constant.

Let

\[
J=[m_\ast-r,m_\ast+r]\cap I,
\]

using a one-sided interval if \(m_\ast\) is near the boundary.

For \(m\in J\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
\|u'\|_\infty r
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}r
\le
\frac12 |u(m_\ast)|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|u(m)|\ge cQ^{-B/2}
\quad (m\in J).
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
|g(m)-g(m_\ast)|
+
|h(m)-h(m_\ast)|
\le
(Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1})r
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|g(m)|+|h(m)|
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}
\quad (m\in J).
}
\]

The interval length satisfies

\[
|J|
\ge
Q^{-C_J}|I|
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_J=
\max\left(
\frac B2+C_u,
\frac{A-B}{2}+C_F
\right)
+O(1),
}
\]

unless \(J\) is one-sided at the boundary, in which case the same polynomial lower bound holds with a harmless factor \(1/2\).

---

# 5. Extracted exponents

The extraction yields

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_1=\frac B2+O(1).
}
\]

It also yields

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(1).
}
\]

If the Lipschitz thickening requires room for \(C_F\), write the effective exponent as

\[
\boxed{
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1).
}
\]

The interval length is

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_J=
\max\left(
\frac B2+C_u,
\frac{A-B}{2}+C_F
\right)+O(1).
}
\]

The dependence of \(C_J\) on \(A\) is acceptable for the integral rigidity argument as long as cutoff derivative losses in G2-B are tracked through \(C_R\). If \(C_R\) depends on \(C_J\), include it in the final exponent condition.

---

# 6. Combine with conservative integral rigidity

From the previous integral rigidity attack, a robust version is:

If on \(J\),

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon,
\]

then on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

The exponent \(1/3\) is conservative. A sharper cutoff argument may give \(2/5\), but \(1/3\) is enough.

Here

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

So

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-A_1/3}|J'|.
\]

But extraction gives

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J',
\]

so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^{-2C_1}
>
Q^{C_R-A_1/3},
\]

i.e.

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_1}{3}-C_R>2C_1.
}
\]

Using

\[
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1),
\]

and

\[
C_1=\frac B2+O(1),
\]

it is enough to choose

\[
\boxed{
A>8B+6C_R+O(C_F)+O(1).
}
\]

Again, exact constants are unimportant; the point is that Gate 2 follows once the contradiction exponent \(A\) is chosen sufficiently large relative to the local complexity constants.

---

# 7. Formal G2-A theorem

## Two-Threshold Extraction Theorem

Assume:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-B/2-O(1)}\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|
\le Q^{-(A-B)/2+O(C_F)+O(1)}
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Boundary cases are handled by using one-sided intervals.

---

# 8. Final Gate 2 implication

Assume additionally the integral rigidity lemma:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^c|J'|
\]

for some fixed

\[
c>0
\]

currently certified with \(c=1/3\).

Then Gate 2 holds if

\[
cA_1-C_R>2C_1.
\]

Equivalently, for sufficiently large \(A\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{Lipschitz extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Remaining technical checks

The remaining items are local and finite:

1. Prove canonical Lipschitz bounds:

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty,\quad \|g'\|_\infty,\quad \|h'\|_\infty
   \le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
   \]

2. Complete the G2-B integral rigidity proof with cutoff bookkeeping. Conservative exponent \(1/3\) already appears safe.

3. Ensure \(J'\Subset J\) has length comparable to \(J\) up to polynomial factors, so cutoff losses stay in \(Q^{C_R}\).

4. Confirm all derivative conventions match the normalized coordinate.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction is essentially proved under polynomial Lipschitz bounds.}
}
\]

The Gate 2 proof now depends primarily on the real-variable integral rigidity lemma and canonical derivative bookkeeping, not on generic Remez/Cartan propagation.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:58:40)

I’ll continue by stress-testing the integral rigidity proof at the one place it can fail: the large-\(|q|\) potential estimate. The concern is whether integration by parts actually controls \(F(q)^2\) without assuming monotonicity or sign.

_Thought for 24s_

## Continuing attack — stress-test and repair the integral rigidity proof

I’ll stress-test the large-\(|q|\) part of the integral rigidity lemma. The concern is legitimate: the identity

\[
q''=F(q)+g,\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3
\]

does not have a globally favorable sign after integration by parts, because

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2
\]

changes sign. But the proof does **not** need positivity of \(F'\). It only needs the kinetic estimate from \(h\)-smallness:

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g'',
\]

which controls \((q')^2\) away from \(q=0\). With that, the sign-changing term is bounded in absolute value. The rigidity lemma survives, with the conservative exponent \(1/3\). This is the key local lemma in the current downstream route. 

---

# 1. Target lemma

Assume on \(J\)

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Let

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

We want, for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^c |J'|
}
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\). The conservative proof gives

\[
\boxed{c=\frac13.}
\]

---

# 2. Kinetic control away from \(q=0\)

Let \(\delta>0\). Choose a smooth sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) with

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)
\quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0
\quad (|q|\le\delta),
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q),
\]

where \(\phi\) is supported in \(J\), equals \(1\) on \(J'\), and satisfies polynomial derivative bounds.

Then

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=|q|,
\]

so the main term is positive:

\[
2\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

The left side is

\[
O(\varepsilon |J|Q^C).
\]

For the \(g''\)-term, integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Since \(|g|\le\varepsilon\), all terms in

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''
\]

are bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon \delta^{-O(1)}|J|
\]

except the transition term

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2.
\]

This term is supported on \(\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\), and

\[
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

Since on that support

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-1}|q|(q')^2,
\]

we get

\[
\varepsilon\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}
\phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}
\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

If

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\ll1,
\]

this term is absorbed into the left side. With the later choice \(\delta=\varepsilon^{1/6}\),

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{1/2}\ll1.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

Dividing by \(|q|\ge2\delta\) gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi (q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

This \(\delta^{-4}\) is the robust bound. A sharper cutoff could maybe recover \(\delta^{-3}\), but \(\delta^{-4}\) is enough.

---

# 3. Large-\(|q|\) potential estimate without sign

Now choose \(\chi_\delta(q)\) with

\[
\chi_\delta=0\quad(|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta=1\quad(|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

We want to bound

\[
X:=\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
X
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is

\[
O(Q^C\varepsilon |J|).
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'
=
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

The last two terms are bounded in absolute value by the kinetic estimate. No sign of \(F'\) is needed:

\[
\left|
\int\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2
\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
\]

Similarly, on the transition \(2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|=O(\delta),
\qquad
|\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1},
\]

so

\[
\left|
\int\phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2
\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
\]

The remaining boundary cutoff term is

\[
T_1=
\left|
\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'
\right|.
\]

Choose

\[
\phi=\psi^2
\]

so that

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi.
\]

Then Cauchy–Schwarz gives

\[
T_1
\le
Q^C
\left(\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
T_1
\le
Q^C X^{1/2}
\left(\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|\right)^{1/2}.
\]

So

\[
X
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|
+
Q^C X^{1/2}
(\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|)^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb the last term using

\[
ab\le \frac12a^2+\frac12b^2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
X
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

Therefore, on \(J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}\),

\[
\boxed{
\int F(q)^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J'|.
}
\]

The sign change of \(F'\) causes no problem because the estimate uses absolute values plus kinetic control.

---

# 4. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g
\]

and

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

we have

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Combine and optimize

On the large-\(|q|\) region,

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

so

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J'|
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2|J'|.
\]

Together with the small-\(|q|\) estimate,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C
\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-4}+\varepsilon^2
\right)|J'|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/6}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{1/3},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-4}
=
\varepsilon\varepsilon^{-4/6}
=
\varepsilon^{1/3}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

This proves the conservative integral rigidity lemma.

---

# 6. Final lemma

## Gate 2 Integral Rigidity Lemma

Assume on \(J\),

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon,
\]

with

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q'',q''',q^{(4)}\) on a cutoff neighborhood of \(J'\Subset J\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|q''|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

The exponent \(1/3\) is safe. The previously hoped-for \(2/5\) requires sharpening the kinetic estimate from \(\delta^{-4}\) to \(\delta^{-3}\), but this is unnecessary for Gate 2.

---

# 7. Consequence for Gate 2

If two-threshold extraction gives on \(J\):

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1},
\]

then the integral rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R-A_1/3}|J'|.
\]

But

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\]

on \(J'\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_1}{3}-C_R>2C_1.
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This completes the main local analytic Gate 2 attack, modulo canonical derivative/cutoff bookkeeping.
