## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:01:00)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — canonical derivative bookkeeping for G2-A/G2-B

The integral rigidity lemma is now locally viable:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\Longrightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
\]

The next possible failure point is derivative bookkeeping: do the required Lipschitz and cutoff bounds follow from a reasonable canonical derivative package? I’ll attack that now.

---

# 1. Normalized derivative convention

Let \(\mathcal D\) denote the normalized local derivative used throughout the local model. For this audit, write ordinary derivatives in the local coordinate as primes. The needed conversion is:

\[
q^{(k)}=\mathcal D^k q
\]

after fixing the normalized coordinate. If \(m\)-derivatives are used instead, each derivative introduces the appropriate power of \(\lambda\); the estimates below should be read in the normalized coordinate.

The required local bounds are polynomial:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|q^{(k)}|\le Q^{C_k}
}
\]

for enough \(k\).

The question is how large \(k\) must be.

---

# 2. Required objects

We use

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Gate 2 extraction needs Lipschitz bounds for

\[
u,\quad g,\quad h.
\]

Integral rigidity needs pointwise polynomial bounds for

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q''',\ q^{(4)}
\]

on the cutoff support.

So calculate explicitly.

---

# 3. Derivatives needed for \(u\)

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

we have

\[
u'=q'''.
\]

Thus G2-A needs

\[
\boxed{
\sup |q'''|\le Q^C.
}
\]

So \(k_0\ge3\) suffices for \(u'\).

---

# 4. Derivatives needed for \(g\)

Recall

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g'=q'''-6q'+6q^2q'.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
|g'|
\le |q'''|+6|q'|+6|q|^2|q'|.
}
\]

Thus \(g'\) needs

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q'''.
\]

No \(q^{(4)}\) is needed for the extraction Lipschitz bound on \(g\).

For integral rigidity, however, the proof uses \(g''\) structurally and integrates it by parts. Compute:

\[
g''=q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

So pointwise polynomial control of \(g''\) needs

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q^{(4)}.
\]

The integral-rigidity proof does not need \(\|g''\|_\infty\) directly if it uses \(h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\) and integrates \(g''\) by parts onto \(g\), but it does need \(q,q',q'',q''',q^{(4)}\) to control cutoff expressions and polynomial terms.

---

# 5. Derivatives needed for \(h\)

Now

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Using the formula for \(g''\),

\[
h
=
2q(q')^2
-\frac16q^{(4)}
+q''
-2q(q')^2
-q^2q''.
\]

The \(2q(q')^2\) terms cancel, giving the useful simplification:

\[
\boxed{
h=q''-q^2q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
}
\]

This is important: \(h\) itself is simpler than its definition suggests.

Then

\[
h'
=
(1-q^2)q'''-2q(q')q''-\frac16q^{(5)}.
\]

Thus G2-A Lipschitz extraction for \(h\) needs

\[
\boxed{
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q''',\ q^{(5)}.
}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
k_0=5
}
\]

is enough for G2-A extraction.

For safety, and because the row/canonical layers often already need one additional derivative, use:

\[
\boxed{
k_0=6
}
\]

as the standard Gate 2 derivative package.

---

# 6. Important simplification of \(h\)

The identity

\[
h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\]

also helps canonical bookkeeping. It means \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) has a fourth-derivative component but no explicit \(q(q')^2\) term after simplification. The \(q(q')^2\) term reappears only when using the structural identity for rigidity:

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Thus there are two useful forms:

## Lipschitz / derivative bookkeeping form

\[
\boxed{
h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
}
\]

## Rigidity / integration-by-parts form

\[
\boxed{
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
}
\]

The first minimizes derivative bookkeeping.  
The second exposes the kinetic term.

---

# 7. Canonical derivative package

A sufficient canonical local package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|q^{(k)}|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le6.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\|g'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

If scaling by \(|I|^{-1}\) is used, rewrite these as

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

The \(|I|^{-1}\) factor is harmless if \(I\) is the normalized local interval. If \(I\) has physical length, then the scaling must be explicitly inserted through \(\lambda\).

---

# 8. Does this follow from \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\)?

We need \(q^{(k)}\) up to \(k=6\), hence \(q''_{\can}\) derivatives up to order \(4\), because

\[
q^{(6)}=(q'')^{(4)}.
\]

Thus the canonical source-side requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^r q''_{\can}|\le Q^C,
\qquad
0\le r\le4.
}
\]

This is much lighter than the \(2R+1\) derivative package needed for the Wronskian/cofactor stages. Therefore, if the earlier canonical transfer has derivatives through \(2R+1\), Gate 2 derivative bookkeeping is automatically covered.

For the canonical decomposition:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we need

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{r\le4}|\mathcal D^r B_2|\le Q^C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{r\le4}|\mathcal D^r P_2|\le Q^C,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{r\le4}|\mathcal D^r D_2|\le Q^C,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{r\le4}|\mathcal D^r E_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
\quad\text{or at least}\quad
\le Q^C.
}
\]

For lower-bound transfer, \(E_2\) should be small; for mere Lipschitz/cutoff bounds, polynomial boundedness suffices.

---

# 9. Cutoff derivative bookkeeping for integral rigidity

The integral rigidity proof uses cutoffs:

\[
\phi(m),
\qquad
s_\delta(q),
\qquad
\chi_\delta(q).
\]

The worst terms involve:

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
\]

and

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q))'.
\]

These require polynomial bounds on:

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q'',\quad F(q),\quad F'(q).
\]

Since

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\) suffice for those terms.

The kinetic estimate uses no derivatives higher than \(q''\) after integrating \(g''\) by parts, because

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
\]

contains only \(q'\) and \(q''\).

The \(q^{(4)}\) appears inside \(h\), but \(h\) is assumed small on the interval from G2-A; the proof does not differentiate \(h\).

Therefore, for the integral rigidity proof itself, it is enough to assume:

\[
\boxed{
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C
}
\]

plus the identity involving \(g''\). The stronger bounds through \(q^{(4)}\) are needed to guarantee \(h\) and \(h'\) are well behaved during extraction.

So:

- G2-A extraction requires \(q^{(5)}\);
- G2-B rigidity proof needs only low derivatives once \(g,h\) are small;
- canonical safety package \(k_0=6\) covers both.

---

# 10. Updated theorem: derivative bookkeeping

## Lemma

Assume

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|q^{(k)}|\le Q^C,
\qquad
0\le k\le6.
\]

Then:

1. \(u=q''\) satisfies

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

2. \(g=q''-6q+2q^3\) satisfies

   \[
   \|g'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

3. \(h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\) satisfies

   \[
   h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
   \]

   and therefore

   \[
   \|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

4. All cutoff terms in the integral rigidity proof are bounded by polynomial powers of \(Q\).

Thus the analytic complexity assumptions needed for G2-A and G2-B follow from the \(C^6\)-type canonical derivative package.

---

# 11. Consequence

The Gate 2 route is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical derivative package through }q^{(6)}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{G2-A Lipschitz extraction is valid}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{G2-B integral rigidity applies}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

So the remaining Gate 2 proof burden is not derivative bookkeeping; it is the rigorous cutoff proof of the integral rigidity lemma and canonical transfer of derivative bounds.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:03:03)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — normalized proof of the Gate 2 integral rigidity lemma

I’ll now formalize the integral rigidity lemma in a normalized interval, because this is where hidden scale losses can enter. The goal is to make the proof robust enough that the only remaining tasks are canonical derivative transfer and row-correction bookkeeping. The downstream target is still:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction}+\text{G2-B integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

The latest handoff identifies this as the strongest current Gate 2 route. 

---

# 1. Normalized statement

Rescale the interval so that

\[
J=(-2,2),
\qquad
J'=(-1,1).
\]

All derivatives below are in the normalized coordinate. Assume

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Assume polynomial local bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le M,
\qquad
M\le Q^C.
\]

Then the conservative integral rigidity lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}.
}
\]

The earlier hoped-for exponent \(2/5\) is still possible with sharper transition bookkeeping, but \(1/3\) is enough for the Gate 2 contradiction.

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate

Choose \(s_\delta(q)\) such that

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)\quad (|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le\delta),
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Let \(\phi\in C_c^\infty((-2,2))\), \(\phi\equiv1\) on \((-3/2,3/2)\), and \(0\le\phi\le1\), with fixed derivative bounds.

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by \(\phi s_\delta(q)\) and integrate:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=|q|.
\]

The left side is bounded by

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le C\varepsilon.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The first, second, and fourth terms are bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}.
\]

The third term is

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2,
\]

supported where

\[
\delta\le |q|\le2\delta.
\]

There

\[
|s_\delta''(q)|\le C\delta^{-2},
\]

and

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-1}|q|(q')^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}\phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

If

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\le c_0
\]

for sufficiently small \(c_0\), this term is absorbed into the positive kinetic term. Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
}
\]

Since \(|q|\ge2\delta\) on this region,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
}
\]

This is the robust kinetic estimate.

---

# 3. Potential estimate

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad(|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad(|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Set

\[
X=\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
X
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'
=
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

The last term is bounded by the kinetic estimate:

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
\]

For the transition term, on \(2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta,
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)q'\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
\]

For the cutoff boundary term,

\[
T=
\left|\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|.
\]

Choose \(\phi=\psi^2\), so that

\[
|\phi'|^2\le C\phi.
\]

Then

\[
T
\le
C
\left(\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
T
\le
Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-4})^{1/2}.
\]

Combining,

\[
X
\le
Q^C\varepsilon
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}
+
Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-4})^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb the mixed term:

\[
ab\le \frac12a^2+\frac12b^2.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
}
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge3\delta\}\cap J'}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

and

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

we get

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\le3\delta\}\cap J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

---

# 5. Combine

On the large-\(|q|\) region,

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge3\delta\}\cap J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2.
\]

Adding the small-\(|q|\) region:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C
\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-4}+\varepsilon^2
\right).
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/6}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{1/3},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-4}
=
\varepsilon^{1/3}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}.
}
\]

Rescaling back to an interval of length \(|J'|\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Gate 2 consequence

G2-A gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Apply the integral rigidity lemma with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R-A_1/3}|J'|.
\]

But since \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}\) on \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
\boxed{
A_1>3(2C_1+C_R).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. What is now actually open

The integral rigidity lemma is now essentially proved in normalized form, with conservative exponent \(1/3\).

The remaining checks are:

1. **Canonical derivative bounds**  
   Need \(q,q',q''\) polynomially bounded on the cutoff support. G2-A also needs \(u',g',h'\), which requires derivatives up to \(q^{(5)}\). The standard \(C^6\)-type local package is sufficient.

2. **Normalized coordinate consistency**  
   All derivatives must be in the same normalized coordinate. If physical \(m\)-derivatives are used, insert the relevant powers of \(\lambda\).

3. **Cutoff interval margin**  
   Need \(J'\Subset J\) with polynomially controlled margin. G2-A gives \(|J|\ge Q^{-C}|I|\), so this is fine.

4. **Exact sign convention in \(h\)**  
   The proof uses

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
   \]

   If the convention differs by harmless nonzero constants/signs, the proof still works with modified constants. If the identity has extra lower-order terms, they must be included in the \(Q^C\varepsilon\)-type error or explicitly controlled.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 integral rigidity lemma is viable and essentially closed as a local real-variable estimate.}
}
\]

With G2-A two-threshold extraction and the conservative \(1/3\) exponent, Gate 2 follows under polynomial local derivative bounds.
## User (2026-04-27 11:09:28)

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:09:41)

_Thought for 11s_

## Continuing attack — stress-test G2-A two-threshold extraction

The integral rigidity lemma now looks locally solid with exponent \(1/3\). The next weak point is **G2-A**: extracting an actual interval \(J\) on which both

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

hold. I will stress-test whether the extraction really follows from Gate 1, Gate 2 failure, and Lipschitz bounds. This is directly within the latest downstream package. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
F=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume Lipschitz bounds

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

We avoid differentiating \(F\) directly; use \(g,h\).

---

# 2. Correct source-threshold extraction

The earlier shortcut

\[
\tau^2=\frac12 Q^{-B}
\]

only works if \(\|u\|_\infty\) is controlled in a compatible way. More robustly, use dyadic pigeonholing.

Assume

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0}.
\]

Decompose levels

\[
E_j=\{2^{-j-1}Q^{C_0}<|u|\le 2^{-j}Q^{C_0}\}.
\]

Since

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

there exists a level with

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

such that

\[
\int_{\{|u|\ge 2\tau\}} |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C_M\). We do not need \(\tau=Q^{-B/2}\) exactly; we only need a polynomial threshold and polynomial mass.

Thus define

\[
U=\{|u|\ge 2\tau\},
\]

with

\[
\int_U |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|.
\]

---

# 3. Find a point with small anisotropy

Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\int_U |u|^2F^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore the \(|u|^2\)-weighted average of \(F^2\) over \(U\) satisfies

\[
\frac{\int_U |u|^2F^2}{\int_U |u|^2}
\le
Q^{-A+C_M}.
\]

So there exists

\[
m_\ast\in U
\]

such that

\[
F(m_\ast)^2\le Q^{-A+C_M},
\]

hence

\[
F(m_\ast)\le Q^{-(A-C_M)/2}.
\]

Also,

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge 2\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge 2Q^{-C_\tau},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|g(m_\ast)|+|h(m_\ast)|\le Q^{-A_0},
\qquad
A_0=\frac{A-C_M}{2}-O(1).
}
\]

This point extraction is valid.

---

# 4. Thicken to an interval

Let

\[
r_u=c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\]

so that for \(|m-m_\ast|\le r_u\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}r_u
\le c\tau.
\]

Choosing \(c\) small,

\[
|u(m)|\ge \tau.
\]

For \(g,h\), let

\[
r_F=c\,Q^{-A_0-C_F}|I|.
\]

For \(|m-m_\ast|\le r_F\),

\[
|g(m)-g(m_\ast)|+|h(m)-h(m_\ast)|
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}r_F
\le cQ^{-A_0}.
\]

Thus

\[
|g(m)|+|h(m)|\le Q^{-A_0+O(1)}.
\]

Take

\[
r=\min(r_u,r_F).
\]

Then there is a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

with

\[
m_\ast\in J,
\qquad
|J|\ge r,
\]

such that on \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\qquad
C_1=C_\tau+O(1),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
A_1=A_0-O(1).
}
\]

The length is

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_J=
\max(C_\tau+C_u,\ A_0+C_F)+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 5. A subtle issue: \(C_J\) depends on \(A_0\)

The interval length shrinks as \(A_0\) grows because we demand very small \(g,h\) throughout \(J\):

\[
r_F\sim Q^{-A_0-C_F}|I|.
\]

This matters because the integral rigidity cutoff loss \(C_R\) may depend on the shrinkage margin:

\[
C_R=C_R(C_J).
\]

If \(C_R\) grows linearly in \(C_J\), then increasing \(A\) increases \(A_1\) but also increases \(C_R\). We need to check the contradiction inequality remains feasible.

The Gate 2 contradiction requires, using exponent \(1/3\),

\[
\frac{A_1}{3}-C_R(C_J)>2C_1.
\]

If

\[
C_R(C_J)=C_R^0+\kappa C_J,
\]

and

\[
C_J\approx A_0+C_F,
\qquad
A_1\approx A_0,
\]

then the inequality becomes

\[
\frac{A_0}{3}-\kappa A_0 > O(1).
\]

Thus we need

\[
\boxed{
\kappa<\frac13.
}
\]

If the cutoff loss grows too fast with interval shrinkage, the extraction-plus-rigidity proof fails.

So the next critical check is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{How does the integral-rigidity loss }C_R\text{ depend on }|J|^{-1}?
}
\]

---

# 6. Repair: choose moderate anisotropy smallness

We do **not** need \(A_0\) arbitrarily large. We only need enough smallness to beat the rigidity loss.

Instead of using the absolute smallest point guaranteed by weighted averaging, choose a target anisotropy threshold

\[
F\le Q^{-S}
\]

with \(S\) fixed large but not scaling with the contradiction exponent beyond what is needed.

Gate 2 failure ensures the set

\[
U\cap\{F>Q^{-S}\}
\]

has small weighted mass if

\[
A\gg C_M+2S.
\]

So there exists a point with

\[
F(m_\ast)\le Q^{-S}
\]

as long as the Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) is chosen large relative to \(S\).

Then the interval length from anisotropy thickening is

\[
r_F\sim Q^{-S-C_F}|I|,
\]

so

\[
C_J\sim S+C_F,
\]

and the integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^{C_R(S)}Q^{-S/3}|J'|.
\]

Now choose \(S\) so that

\[
\frac S3-C_R(S)>2C_1.
\]

If \(C_R(S)\) grows mildly or is independent of \(S\), this works.

This avoids sending \(A_0\to\infty\) and thereby shrinking \(J\) too much.

Thus G2-A should be formulated with a **chosen target smallness** \(S\), not necessarily the maximal smallness supplied by averaging.

---

# 7. Corrected G2-A theorem

## Two-Threshold Extraction with Target Smallness

Fix a target exponent \(S\). Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure with exponent \(A\) satisfying

\[
A\ge C_M+2S+O(1).
\]

Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J(S)}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S}\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Here

\[
C_J(S)=\max(C_\tau+C_u,\ S+C_F)+O(1).
\]

This is more stable than tying \(S\) directly to \(A\).

---

# 8. Gate 2 closure condition

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R(S)}Q^{-S/3}|J'|.
\]

Extraction gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
\boxed{
\frac S3-C_R(S)>2C_1.
}
\]

Therefore the full Gate 2 proof requires selecting \(S\) such that:

1. Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) is large enough to produce \(F\le Q^{-S}\);
2. the interval rigidity cutoff loss satisfies

   \[
   C_R(S)<S/3-2C_1.
   \]

This is now the exact exponent condition.

---

# 9. Estimate \(C_R(S)\)

From the normalized integral rigidity proof, if \(J\) is rescaled to unit size, cutoff derivatives are \(O(1)\) in normalized coordinates. The \(Q^C\) loss comes from bounds on \(q,q',q''\), not directly from \(|J|^{-1}\), provided all derivatives are normalized to \(J\).

But if canonical derivative bounds are given in the ambient coordinate, rescaling \(J\) introduces powers of \(|J|^{-1}\). Since

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J(S)}|I|,
\]

this contributes polynomial losses proportional to \(C_J(S)\).

The key is that only finitely many derivatives are used, so

\[
C_R(S)=C_R^0+\kappa C_J(S)
\]

for some fixed finite \(\kappa\). The proof closes if the finite derivative order gives

\[
\kappa<\frac13
\]

for the conservative exponent. If not, one needs either:

- the sharper \(2/5\) rigidity exponent;
- normalized derivative bounds already adapted to \(J\);
- or choose the cutoff margin differently to reduce \(C_R(S)\).

This is the current most technical exponent issue.

---

# 10. Proposed solution: use normalized derivative package on all polynomial subintervals

If the canonical derivative package gives scale-invariant bounds on any polynomial subinterval \(J\), i.e.

\[
\sup_J |J|^k |q^{(k)}|\le Q^C,
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

then \(C_R\) is independent of \(S\) up to \(O(1)\). Then choose \(S\) large and Gate 2 closes.

So the required canonical derivative package should be stated in scale-invariant form:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J\subset I,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I|}
|J|^k|\partial^k q|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is natural for bandlimited/AFE functions.

Under this package,

\[
C_R(S)=O(1),
\]

and the two-threshold + integral rigidity proof closes.

---

# 11. Verdict

G2-A is valid, but the proof must be formulated with a **target smallness exponent \(S\)** and a **scale-invariant derivative package**.

The corrected Gate 2 closure is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Choose }S\text{ such that }S/3>C_R+2C_1.
}
\]

Then choose Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) large enough to extract \(F\le Q^{-S}\).

With scale-invariant polynomial derivative bounds, the proof works.

Thus the remaining Gate 2 technical task is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove scale-invariant canonical derivative bounds on polynomial subintervals.}
}
\]

If those are available, Gate 2 is essentially closed by G2-A + G2-B.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:11:22)

_Thought for 12s_

## Continuing attack — scale-invariant derivative package for Gate 2

The previous Gate 2 attack exposed a technical requirement:

\[
\sup_{J\subset I,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I|}
|J|^k|\partial^k q|
\le Q^C,
\qquad 0\le k\le6.
\]

If this scale-invariant derivative package is available on every polynomial subinterval \(J\), then the two-threshold extraction plus integral rigidity proof closes Gate 2 with a fixed positive exponent. I’ll now attack whether this package follows from the canonical local model.

---

# 1. What we actually need

For G2-A and G2-B, the needed quantities are:

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Useful alternate form:

\[
h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The extraction step needs Lipschitz bounds:

\[
|u'|,\quad |g'|,\quad |h'|.
\]

The rigidity step needs polynomial bounds for:

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q''',\ q^{(4)}
\]

on cutoff supports.

Since

\[
h'=(1-q^2)q'''-2qq'q''-\frac16q^{(5)},
\]

the extraction step needs up to

\[
q^{(5)}.
\]

For safety, use:

\[
\boxed{
\sup |q^{(k)}|\le Q^C,\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

But for the cutoff proof on a small subinterval \(J\), the relevant form is scale-invariant:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |J|^k|q^{(k)}|\le Q^C,\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

---

# 2. Why scale-invariant bounds are plausible

On ordinary scale, write

\[
m=m_0+\lambda t,\qquad \lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

The canonical source has packet-frequency structure

\[
q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda t)
=
B_2(t)+P_2(t)+D_2(t)+E_2(t),
\]

where the oscillatory phases are of the form

\[
e^{-it\lambda\log n},
\]

with

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim 1
\]

on ordinary support.

Thus in the normalized coordinate \(t\), the oscillatory part of \(u=q''_{\can}\) is effectively bandlimited at bounded frequency, or at worst polynomial frequency if tails/transition buffers are retained.

For a bandlimited function \(f\) of type \(B\), Bernstein gives

\[
\|f^{(k)}\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\le
B^k\|f\|_{L^\infty(J^\ast)}
\]

for \(J\Subset J^\ast\), or more globally

\[
\|f^{(k)}\|_\infty\le B^k\|f\|_\infty.
\]

If

\[
B\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
|J|^k\|f^{(k)}\|_\infty
\le
(Q^C|J|)^k\|f\|_\infty.
\]

For polynomial subintervals \(|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}\), this remains polynomial.

So for the oscillatory source \(u=q''\), scale-invariant bounds are plausible.

---

# 3. The issue: bounds for \(q\), not just \(u=q''\)

The rigidity lemma needs \(q\) and \(q'\), not only \(q''\). Since \(q''=u\), integrating twice gives

\[
q(t)=q(t_0)+q'(t_0)(t-t_0)+\int_{t_0}^t(t-s)u(s)\,ds.
\]

So even if \(u\) is bandlimited and controlled, \(q\) may contain affine components:

\[
q_{\rm aff}(t)=a+bt.
\]

These are low-frequency, not dangerous for derivative growth, but their size must be polynomially bounded.

Thus the derivative package splits into:

## Source part

For \(k\ge2\),

\[
q^{(k)}=u^{(k-2)}.
\]

So bounds for \(q^{(k)}\), \(k\ge2\), follow from source bounds for \(u\).

## Affine part

For \(q\) and \(q'\), need independent local bounds:

\[
|q|\le Q^C,\qquad |q'|\le Q^C.
\]

These are not consequences of Gate 1. They must come from the canonical local coordinate normalization / admissibility assumptions.

This is important:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 derivative package requires polynomial bounds on }q\text{ and }q'.
}
\]

But this is a mild local boundedness/admissibility condition, not a deep arithmetic input.

---

# 4. Canonical derivative theorem candidate

## Canonical Local Complexity Lemma

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\]

and a polynomial-size local interval \(I^\ast\) in normalized coordinates.

Assume the canonical source decomposition

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

satisfies, for \(0\le r\le4\),

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial^r B_2|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial^r P_2|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial^r D_2|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial^r E_2|\le Q^C.
\]

Assume also local coordinate admissibility:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}(|q|+|q'|)\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|q^{(k)}|\le Q^C,\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

Moreover, on every polynomial subinterval \(J\subset I^\ast\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |J|^k|q^{(k)}|\le Q^{C'},\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

The last statement follows because \(|J|\le |I^\ast|\le Q^C\), and \(|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}\) in the Gate 2 extraction.

---

# 5. Check source derivatives

For \(k\ge2\),

\[
q^{(k)}=(q'')^{(k-2)}=u^{(k-2)}.
\]

So to bound \(q^{(6)}\), need

\[
u^{(4)}.
\]

Thus the source derivative requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{0\le r\le4}|\partial^r q''_{\can}|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is lighter than the Wronskian derivative budget, which previously required derivatives up to roughly \(2R+1\). Therefore, if canonical transfer has already been established for the Wronskian/cofactor layers, Gate 2’s derivative needs are covered.

---

# 6. Component-specific canonical checks

## \(B_2\)

The finalized background is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

For \(t\ge50\), the asymptotic model is

\[
B_2(t)\sim -\frac{1}{2t^2}+\cdots.
\]

Its normalized derivatives through finite order are polynomially bounded, indeed decaying at height. So \(B_2\) is safe.

## \(P_2,D_2\)

Each local derivative in normalized coordinate brings factors

\[
(\lambda\log n)^r,
\]

and on ordinary support

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim Q^C,
\]

usually \(O(1)\). Thus finite derivatives of \(P_2,D_2\) are bounded by polynomial multiples of the coefficient mass.

So it is enough to assume a local AFE coefficient-size bound:

\[
\sum |c_n| \le Q^C
\]

or a sharper \(L^2\)-to-\(L^\infty\) bound on the packet model.

## \(E_2\)

For Gate 2 Lipschitz/cutoff bounds, only polynomial boundedness is required:

\[
\sup_{r\le4}|\partial^rE_2|\le Q^C.
\]

For canonical lower-bound transfer, smallness may be needed elsewhere, but not for this local derivative package.

---

# 7. Does scale-invariant control survive shrinking \(J\)?

In G2-A, the extracted interval length is

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|.
\]

Cutoff functions on \(J\) have derivatives

\[
|\phi^{(r)}|\lesssim |J|^{-r}\le Q^{rC_J}|I|^{-r}.
\]

These losses enter the integral rigidity constant \(C_R\). Since \(r\le2\) in the main integration by parts and finite powers in cutoff construction, the loss is polynomial:

\[
Q^{O(C_J)}.
\]

The earlier exponent issue was that if \(C_J\) grows with the anisotropy smallness target \(S\), then \(C_R\) may grow with \(S\).

But the two-threshold extraction can fix the target \(S=A_1\) at a finite large value. Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) is chosen only large enough to produce that \(S\). Thus \(C_J\) is fixed polynomial, and \(C_R\) is finite.

So the proof closes after selecting \(S\) satisfying

\[
\frac{S}{3}>2C_1+C_R(S).
\]

No contradiction arises unless \(C_R(S)\) grows faster than \(S/3\). With finite-order cutoffs, \(C_R(S)\) is linear in \(S\) with a small coefficient determined by the number of interval derivatives. If that coefficient is too large, one should decouple interval length from \(S\) by extracting smallness at a point then using only the needed finite radius.

But as a practical theorem, state:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Choose extraction target }S\text{ and cutoff scale so that }S/3>C_R(S)+2C_1.
}
\]

This is an exponent bookkeeping condition, not a conceptual blocker.

---

# 8. Updated Gate 2 local theorem

## Gate 2 Local Analytic Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Gate 2 failure with sufficiently large exponent \(A\).

3. Canonical local complexity:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}(|q|+|q'|)\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\sup_{0\le r\le4}|\partial^r q''_{\can}|\le Q^C.
\]

4. Two-threshold extraction produces \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\]

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S}.
\]

5. Integral rigidity:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le Q^{-S}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^{C_R(S)}Q^{-S/3}|J'|.
\]

If

\[
S/3>C_R(S)+2C_1,
\]

then Gate 2 holds.

---

# 9. Remaining verification list

The Gate 2 route is now reduced to finite local checks:

1. **Local admissibility:**

   \[
   |q|+|q'|\le Q^C.
   \]

2. **Canonical source derivative bounds:**

   \[
   \partial^r q''_{\can},\quad 0\le r\le4.
   \]

3. **G2-A exponent bookkeeping.**

4. **G2-B integral rigidity cutoff proof.**

All are local analytic/canonical tasks.

This is a major simplification from the prior abstract D1/D2 formulation.

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scale-invariant derivative control is plausible and likely follows from canonical local complexity.}
}
\]

The only nontrivial extra assumptions are polynomial bounds for \(q,q'\), which should be included as local admissibility conditions.

Thus, Gate 2 now appears conditionally closeable by local analysis:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical local complexity}
+
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The next most valuable attack is D4 matrix row conversion and correction control.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:12:37)

_Thought for 11s_

## Continuing attack — D4 matrix row conversion and correction control

I’ll now attack the next local downstream piece: **D4 matrix row conversion**. Gate 2 now looks locally closeable via two-threshold extraction plus integral rigidity; the remaining row-conversion task is to prove that, away from the \(q_0\)-wall, the rows \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) really expose Gate 2 anisotropy. The current normal form is

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

where

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The goal is to make this a finite local theorem. 

---

# 1. D4 target

Assume a non-wall sample point \(m_\ast\) with

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and Gate 2 pointwise mass

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2|\Gamma(m_\ast)|^2
=
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

D4 must prove

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the bridge from Gate 2 anisotropy to an actual downstream row lower bound.

---

# 2. Leading row model

The row expansions are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

with

\[
H=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H.
\]

Substitute \(H\) into the row vector:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7H\Gamma_G\\
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
+
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal R_7\\
\mathcal R_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The leading vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
c_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
q_0u^3L_{\rm lead}\Gamma,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Thus, if

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_9|\ge Q^{-C_c},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

This is the first finite local check.

---

# 3. Incorporating same-order corrections into \(L\)

Some correction terms may have the same algebraic shape as the leading matrix. Write

\[
\mathcal R_H=q_0u^3\rho_H+\widehat{\mathcal R}_H,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_7
=
q_0u^3(a_{77}\Gamma_G+a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2})
+
\widehat{\mathcal R}_7,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_9
=
q_0u^3(a_{97}\Gamma_G+a_{99}\Gamma_{G,2})
+
\widehat{\mathcal R}_9.
\]

Then the row vector becomes

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\widehat{\mathbf R},
\]

where

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\frac{c_7}{288}+c_7\rho_H+a_{77} & a_{79}\\
a_{97} & -\frac{c_9}{288}+c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\widehat{\mathbf R}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\widehat{\mathcal R}_H\Gamma_G+\widehat{\mathcal R}_7\\
c_9\widehat{\mathcal R}_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\widehat{\mathcal R}_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So D4 reduces to two finite checks:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\widehat{\mathbf R}|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

If both hold, D4 is proved.

---

# 4. Row lower bound from Gate 2 mass

Assume

\[
|\widehat{\mathbf R}|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
|q_0||u|^3|L\Gamma|-|\widehat{\mathbf R}|
\]

and

\[
|L\Gamma|\ge \sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Using

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12Q^{-C_q-C_L}|u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

Gate 2 pointwise mass gives

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

This implies

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

But the row lower bound contains

\[
|u|^3|\Gamma|
=
|u|^2\cdot |u||\Gamma|.
\]

So we still need a pointwise lower bound for \(|u|\), or an upper bound for \(|\Gamma|\) to extract one.

There are two valid versions.

---

# 5. Version A: with explicit source lower bound

Assume

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Then

\[
|u|^3|\Gamma|
=
|u|^2(|u||\Gamma|)
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-2C_u-A_2/2-O(1)}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest D4 form.

---

# 6. Version B: with anisotropy upper bound

If no explicit lower bound on \(|u|\) is supplied, assume

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then from

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

we get

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A_2/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Set

\[
C_u=A_2/2+C_\Gamma.
\]

Then Version A applies and gives

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\]

with

\[
C=C_q+C_L+2(A_2/2+C_\Gamma)+A_2/2+O(1).
\]

That is,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-\frac32A_2-2C_\Gamma-O(1)}.
}
\]

This is also acceptable.

---

# 7. D4 theorem

## Matrix Row Conversion Theorem

Assume at \(m_\ast\):

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Assume the row vector admits the normal form

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\widehat{\mathbf R},
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\widehat{\mathbf R}|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is D4 in final local form.

---

# 8. What must be computed

The finite verification list is:

\[
c_7,\quad c_9,
\]

\[
\rho_H,
\]

\[
a_{77},a_{79},a_{97},a_{99},
\]

\[
\widehat{\mathcal R}_H,\quad
\widehat{\mathcal R}_7,\quad
\widehat{\mathcal R}_9.
\]

Then check:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}
\begin{pmatrix}
-\frac{c_7}{288}+c_7\rho_H+a_{77} & a_{79}\\
a_{97} & -\frac{c_9}{288}+c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix}
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\widehat{\mathcal R}_H\Gamma_G+\widehat{\mathcal R}_7\\
c_9\widehat{\mathcal R}_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\widehat{\mathcal R}_9
\end{pmatrix}
\right|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

This is concrete and finite.

---

# 9. Correction sources

The remainders \(\widehat{\mathbf R}\) must absorb all lower-order or non-leading contributions:

1. \(E_2\) and canonical source-tail error;
2. truncation errors in row expansions;
3. projection/gauge corrections;
4. row normalization errors;
5. lower-order terms in \(u,\Gamma,q_0\);
6. error in

   \[
   H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
   \]

The half-leading condition is local. It does not require arithmetic. It requires explicit row expansions and polynomial separation of the leading term.

---

# 10. Relation to wall escape

Wall escape produces a non-wall point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Thus Version A of D4 applies at \(m_1\).

Then row mobility converts

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

into interval row energy.

Therefore the \(q_0\)-wall is handled by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall Escape}
+
\text{D4}
+
\text{Row Mobility}.
}
\]

A source-robust row at \(q_0=0\) is no longer required unless exact-point conversion is demanded.

---

# 11. Verdict

D4 is now a finite local algebra theorem.

The theorem is not yet “proved” until the row expansions are computed, but there is no conceptual obstruction left in the nondegenerate branch.

The remaining D4 work is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }L\text{ and prove }\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C};
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove }\widehat{\mathbf R}\text{ is half-leading}.
}
\]

This is row-expansion and correction bookkeeping, not a new global arithmetic input.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:14:03)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — D4 correction control via weighted row algebra

I’ll keep attacking **D4**, because after the Gate 2 simplification the downstream proof now depends heavily on the finite row-conversion theorem:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

The remaining question is not conceptual; it is algebraic: when can we guarantee

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12 |q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_{\min}(L)\,|\Gamma|?
\]

This is the “half-leading” correction-control condition in the latest downstream package. 

---

# 1. D4 leading scale

At a non-wall sample point, we assume

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

The leading row scale is

\[
\boxed{
S_{\rm lead}
=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_{\min}(L)\,|\Gamma|.
}
\]

If

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

then

\[
S_{\rm lead}
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L}|u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

Using the explicit \(u\)-lower-bound version,

\[
|u|^3|\Gamma|
=
|u|^2(|u||\Gamma|)
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
S_{\rm lead}\ge Q^{-C_q-C_L-2C_u-A_2/2}.
}
\]

So any correction term bounded by

\[
Q^{-K}
\]

with

\[
K>C_q+C_L+2C_u+A_2/2+O(1)
\]

is harmless.

This gives one clean way to certify corrections: **absolute smallness**.

---

# 2. Correction classes

Write

\[
\mathbf R
=
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm higher}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm lower}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm tail}.
\]

Each class needs a different treatment.

---

## 2.1 Same-shape corrections

These are terms of the form

\[
q_0u^3M\Gamma.
\]

They should not be treated as error. They should be absorbed into \(L\):

\[
L=L_{\rm lead}+M.
\]

The required check is

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead}+M)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

A sufficient condition is

\[
\|M\|\le \frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead}).
\]

But this is stronger than necessary. The real finite check is simply:

\[
\det(L_{\rm lead}+M)\not\approx0,
\]

and

\[
\|L_{\rm lead}+M\|\le Q^C.
\]

For a \(2\times2\) matrix,

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)
\ge
\frac{|\det L|}{\|L\|}.
\]

So a practical certificate is:

\[
\boxed{
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C},\qquad \|L\|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is likely the best D4 matrix test.

---

## 2.2 Higher-order multiplicative corrections

These are terms like

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma\cdot \Delta,
\]

where \(\Delta\) is a small analytic parameter, tail error, projection error, truncation error, or higher-order normal-form remainder.

If

\[
|\Delta|\le Q^{-K_\Delta},
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm higher}|
\le
Q^{-K_\Delta}|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

This is half-leading if

\[
Q^{-K_\Delta}
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L).
\]

Since

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
K_\Delta>C_L+O(1).
}
\]

These terms are easy if the normal-form expansion has a genuinely small parameter.

---

## 2.3 Lower-degree dangerous corrections

The dangerous terms are those not carrying the full factor

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma.
\]

Examples:

\[
u^4,\quad q_0u^2\Gamma,\quad q_0u^3,\quad u^3\Gamma,\quad q_0u^2\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

These are dangerous because, when \(q_0\), \(u\), or \(\Gamma\) is small, they may dominate or cancel the leading row.

Such terms must be ruled out structurally.

The finite D4 audit should prove:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
\in
(q_0u^3\Gamma_G,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2})
+
\text{small tail ideal}.
}
\]

Equivalently, modulo small canonical errors,

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
\text{ is divisible by }q_0u^3
\text{ and linear in }\Gamma
\text{ at leading order.}
}
\]

If any lower-degree term survives, D4 is false as currently stated; it would need a larger row vector or a different leading matrix.

---

## 2.4 Canonical tail and \(E_2\) corrections

Canonical errors should be controlled absolutely:

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm tail}|\le Q^{-K_E}.
\]

As above, this is harmless if

\[
K_E>C_q+C_L+2C_u+A_2/2+O(1).
\]

This is more stringent than merely polynomial boundedness. For D4, tail errors must be small relative to the row lower scale, not merely bounded.

Thus D4 needs a stronger canonical row-transfer condition than Gate 2’s derivative bookkeeping.

---

# 3. Weighted valuation audit

Define a leading monomial weight

\[
w(q_0)=1,\qquad w(u)=3,\qquad w(\Gamma)=1,
\]

so the leading row has symbolic weight

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma.
\]

But ordinary degree is not enough, because \(q_0,u,\Gamma\) may all be small polynomially.

Use **relative divisibility**, not just degree.

For every correction monomial \(M_{\rm corr}\), compute the ratio

\[
\mathcal R_M
=
\frac{|M_{\rm corr}|}
{|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|}.
\]

D4 requires

\[
\boxed{
\sum_M |\mathcal R_M|
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L).
}
\]

Under bounds

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma^-},
\]

and upper bounds

\[
|q_0|,|u|,|\Gamma|\le Q^C,
\]

each monomial ratio can be estimated explicitly.

For example:

### Term \(q_0u^4\Gamma\)

\[
\frac{|q_0u^4\Gamma|}
{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
=|u|\le Q^C.
\]

This is **not** small unless \(u\) is known small. It must be absorbed into \(L\) only if it is actually same-shape after rewriting, or ruled out.

### Term \(q_0u^3\Gamma^2\)

\[
\frac{|q_0u^3\Gamma^2|}
{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
=|\Gamma|,
\]

not small unless \(\Gamma\) is small. Since Gate 2 only gives \(\Gamma\) may be large, this is dangerous.

### Term \(q_0^2u^3\Gamma\)

\[
\frac{|q_0^2u^3\Gamma|}
{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
=|q_0|.
\]

Not small unless \(q_0\) is bounded by a small constant, not merely polynomial.

Therefore the D4 expansion must be genuinely linear at the relevant leading order, not just “higher degree.”

---

# 4. Correct finite D4 verification target

The right algebraic statement is not “higher-order corrections are harmless.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_{\rm small},
}
\]

where every non-linear or non-divisible term is included in

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm small}
\]

and is quantitatively small because of an actual expansion parameter, tail estimate, projection estimate, or canonical truncation estimate.

Thus the finite row audit must classify each term into one of three buckets:

| Bucket | Treatment |
|---|---|
| exactly \(q_0u^3\) times linear \(\Gamma\) | absorb into \(L\) |
| absolutely \(Q^{-K}\)-small | absorb into \(\mathbf R_{\rm small}\) |
| anything else | dangerous; D4 normal form fails |

This is the cleanest D4 audit protocol.

---

# 5. Matrix nondegeneracy check

Once all same-shape terms are absorbed, compute

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{77}&\ell_{79}\\
\ell_{97}&\ell_{99}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Need

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

For \(2\times2\), sufficient:

\[
\boxed{
|\ell_{77}\ell_{99}-\ell_{79}\ell_{97}|\ge Q^{-C},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\ell_{ij}|\le Q^C.
}
\]

If \(L\) is diagonal to leading order,

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix},
\]

then a simple sufficient condition is

\[
|c_7c_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
\left\|
L-L_{\rm lead}
\right\|
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead}).
\]

But again, this half-leading matrix perturbation is only sufficient, not necessary.

---

# 6. D4 theorem after audit

The final D4 theorem should be:

## D4 Matrix Row Conversion Theorem

Assume at \(m_\ast\):

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Assume the finite row expansion satisfies:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R_{\rm small},
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm small}|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This theorem is already proved once the finite expansion assumptions are verified.

---

# 7. What remains genuinely open in D4

The open part is not the inequality; it is the row expansion audit:

1. Compute all terms in \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) to the needed order.
2. Verify every non-small term is exactly of the form

   \[
   q_0u^3\cdot \text{linear combination of }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
   \]

3. Compute \(L\).
4. Prove \(\det L\) is polynomially nonzero.
5. Prove all remaining terms are absolutely small relative to the leading row scale.

If any non-small term lies outside the leading ideal

\[
(q_0u^3\Gamma_G,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

then D4 must be reformulated.

---

# 8. Updated verdict

D4 is a finite algebra/correction problem with a sharp audit criterion.

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 closes iff the finite row expansion has no dangerous non-leading terms.}
}
\]

The next concrete task is not conceptual. It is to compute the row expansion and classify each term:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-shape},\quad
\text{absolutely small},\quad
\text{dangerous}.
}
\]

If the dangerous bucket is empty and \(L\) is nonsingular, D4 is closed.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:15:36)

_Thought for 10s_

## Continuing attack — D4 as a finite ideal/normal-form certificate

I’ll keep attacking **D4**, because after Gate 2 and wall escape, the remaining downstream obstruction is finite row algebra:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

The previous pass classified corrections into “same-shape,” “absolutely small,” and “dangerous.” The next useful move is to turn that into a **finite ideal-certificate test**. This gives an executable algebraic protocol: either D4 closes, or we get an explicit obstruction term. 

---

# 1. Define the D4 leading ideal

Let the local variables be

\[
q_0,\quad u,\quad \Gamma_1=\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

plus auxiliary bounded variables such as

\[
q_0',\ u',\ q_0'',\ldots
\]

The D4 leading ideal is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{\rm lead}
=
(q_0u^3\Gamma_1,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_2).
}
\]

The row vector

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})^T
\]

must satisfy, up to small canonical errors,

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\in \mathcal I_{\rm lead}^2
}
\]

componentwise, in the stronger sense that its projection onto

\[
q_0u^3(\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2)
\]

has a nonsingular \(2\times2\) coefficient matrix.

Concretely:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_1\\
\Gamma_2
\end{pmatrix}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm small}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Quotient test for dangerous terms

Define the quotient module

\[
\mathcal Q
=
\mathcal M/\mathcal I_{\rm lead}\mathcal M,
\]

where \(\mathcal M\) is the module of row-vector polynomial/differential expressions.

Compute

\[
\boxed{
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}.
}
\]

If

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}\ne0
\]

with a non-small term, then D4 in its current form fails: there is a row contribution not divisible by

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma.
\]

Such a term could still be useful, but it is not covered by the current D4 theorem. It must either:

1. be added to the leading row model;
2. be shown absolutely small;
3. produce an independent row lower bound;
4. or be a genuine obstruction to the current downstream architecture.

So the first finite algebra test is:

\[
\boxed{
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}
=
\text{small}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Extract the leading matrix \(L\)

Assuming the quotient obstruction vanishes, compute the coefficient matrix \(L\) by reducing

\[
\frac{1}{q_0u^3}\mathbf A_{\rm row}
\]

modulo terms not linear in \(\Gamma\).

More explicitly, write

\[
\frac{1}{q_0u^3}\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
L
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_1\\
\Gamma_2
\end{pmatrix}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm rel}.
\]

Then \(L\) is the Jacobian of the row vector with respect to \(\Gamma\) at the leading level:

\[
\boxed{
L_{ij}
=
\left[
\frac{\partial}{\partial \Gamma_j}
\left(
\frac{A_i}{q_0u^3}
\right)
\right]_{\rm lead}.
}
\]

For the expected leading rows,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_1+\cdots,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_2+\cdots,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Same-shape corrections perturb \(L\). The finite check is:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

For \(2\times2\), it is enough to verify

\[
\boxed{
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C},\qquad \|L\|\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 4. Relative remainder test

After extracting \(L\), the relative remainder is

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rel}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
-
q_0u^3L\Gamma.
\]

D4 needs

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf R_{\rm rel}|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

This can be checked term-by-term.

For every monomial/differential term \(T\) in \(\mathbf R_{\rm rel}\), compute the ratio

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_T
=
\frac{|T|}
{|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|}.
}
\]

Then require

\[
\boxed{
\sum_T \mathcal E_T
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L).
}
\]

This is the actual finite correction-control problem.

---

# 5. Three possible outcomes of the finite audit

## Outcome A — D4 closes

If:

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}=0\quad\text{up to small errors},
\]

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm rel}|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|,
\]

then D4 is proved:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\quad
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Together with wall escape and row mobility, this closes the downstream row-conversion layer.

---

## Outcome B — extra useful leading term appears

If

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}\ne0
\]

but the surviving term is nonzero on the Gate 2 admissible set, then this may **help**, not hurt.

For example, if a term like

\[
u^4
\]

or

\[
u^3\Gamma_1
\]

survives, it can provide a row lower bound independent of \(q_0\). That would partially solve the wall branch too.

Then revise the leading model:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm extra}
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R.
}
\]

The lower-bound theorem becomes a row-pencil nonvanishing problem:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm extra}+q_0u^3L\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the Gate 2 admissible set.

---

## Outcome C — dangerous cancellation term appears

If a surviving quotient term can cancel the leading row on the Gate 2 admissible set, then D4 is not closed. One must use a larger row vector:

\[
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)
\]

and prove a higher-dimensional row-pencil nonvanishing theorem.

This leads to the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil problem:

\[
\mathbf R_N(q_0,Y)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{K}q_0^r\mathbf C_r(Y)+\mathbf E_K,
\]

and the target

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm G2}}|\mathbf R_N(q_0,Y)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 6. D4 certificate theorem

A clean finite certificate is:

## D4 Ideal-Normal-Form Certificate

Let

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

Suppose the row vector admits the decomposition

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R
\]

on the Gate 2 admissible set, with:

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then for all points satisfying

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is a complete D4 theorem.

The certificate data are finite:

\[
\boxed{
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q},
\quad
L,
\quad
\det L,
\quad
\mathbf R.
}
\]

---

# 7. Concrete audit table

The symbolic audit should produce:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{row term} & \text{normal form} & \text{classification} & \text{action}\\
\hline
c_7H\Gamma_G & q_0u^3L_{11}\Gamma_G & same-shape & absorb into L\\
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2} & q_0u^3L_{22}\Gamma_{G,2} & same-shape & absorb into L\\
\mathcal R_H\Gamma & ? & same/small/dangerous & classify\\
\mathcal R_7 & ? & same/small/dangerous & classify\\
\mathcal R_9 & ? & same/small/dangerous & classify\\
E_2\text{-terms} & ? & small or dangerous & bound\\
projection terms & ? & same/small/dangerous & classify
\end{array}
\]

The audit is finite and local. No global number theory is involved.

---

# 8. Updated downstream state

With the recent progress:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{G2-B integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

Then:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{wall escape}
+
\text{row mobility}
+
\text{D4 ideal-normal-form certificate}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

So the remaining downstream proof has been reduced to:

1. canonical derivative/Lipschitz bounds;
2. cutoff proof of integral rigidity;
3. finite D4 row-normal-form audit.

The largest remaining finite item is D4.

# 9. Next attack target

The next attack should be one of:

1. **Compute \(L\) exactly** from the row formulas and verify

   \[
   \det L\neq0.
   \]

2. **Prove quotient vanishing**

   \[
   [\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{\mathcal Q}=0
   \]

   up to small errors.

3. **Classify correction terms**

   into same-shape / small / dangerous.

Without actual row formulas, this is the sharpest possible D4 reduction.

## Continuing attack — D4 can be reduced to a leading-symbol rank test

I’ll continue the D4 attack. Without the explicit row formulas, the best possible next move is to reduce the row-conversion problem to a **finite leading-symbol rank test** that is invariant under row recombination.

The current D4 target is

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\mathbf R|\le \frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

The issue is whether the actual row expansion has dangerous terms outside the ideal

\[
(q_0u^3\Gamma_G,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

I’ll attack that by defining a finite graded quotient where the D4 leading term is the first nonzero symbol. This turns D4 into a concrete rank computation. The latest downstream architecture already points to this finite row/correction-control task as the main row-conversion residue. 

---

# 1. Define the D4 leading filtration

Introduce a bookkeeping parameter \(\epsilon\) and assign the D4 leading scale

\[
q_0\sim \epsilon,
\qquad
u\sim \epsilon,
\qquad
\Gamma_G\sim\epsilon,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim\epsilon.
\]

Then the D4 leading row scale

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma
\]

has formal weight

\[
1+3+1=5.
\]

Define the weight

\[
\operatorname{wt}(q_0)=1,\qquad
\operatorname{wt}(u)=1,\qquad
\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_G)=1,\qquad
\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_{G,2})=1.
\]

Auxiliary bounded variables, such as normalized coefficients and harmless functions of \(q_0,q_0'\), have weight \(0\), unless they vanish at the relevant base locus.

The leading D4 module is

\[
\mathcal L_5
=
q_0u^3\cdot \operatorname{span}\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

Rows \(A_7,A_9\) should have first nonzero projection in this weight-5 module.

Thus D4 reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gr}_5(\mathbf A_{\rm row})
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\qquad
\operatorname{rank} L=2.
}
\]

All terms of weight \(>5\) are perturbative if the expansion parameter is genuinely small or if they are absolutely controlled by canonical error bounds. Terms of weight \(<5\) are dangerous unless they themselves give a lower bound.

---

# 2. Dangerous terms are exactly lower-weight quotient classes

Define the quotient

\[
\mathcal Q_{<5}
=
\mathcal M/\mathcal M_{\ge5},
\]

where \(\mathcal M_{\ge5}\) is the submodule of row expressions of weight at least \(5\).

Then compute

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}.
\]

There are three possibilities.

## Case 1: lower-weight quotient vanishes

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}=0.
\]

Then no dangerous lower-weight terms exist. Proceed to the weight-5 rank test.

## Case 2: lower-weight quotient is nonzero and wall-live

Example:

\[
u^4,\qquad u^3\Gamma_G,\qquad u^2\Gamma_G^2.
\]

Then D4 is actually easier: this lower-weight row can provide a row lower bound before the \(q_0u^3\Gamma\) term is needed, provided it cannot cancel in the row vector. The D4 theorem should be enlarged to include it.

## Case 3: lower-weight quotient is nonzero but cancellable

Then the two-row system \((A_7,A_9)\) is insufficient. One must add rows

\[
A_{11},A_{13},\ldots
\]

and prove a larger row-pencil nonvanishing theorem.

So the first finite computation is:

\[
\boxed{
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}=0
\quad\text{or identify the surviving lower-weight symbol.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Weight-5 rank test

Assume no dangerous lower-weight terms. Then compute

\[
\operatorname{gr}_5(\mathbf A_{\rm row})
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma.
\]

Expected leading structure:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\cdots,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\cdots,
\]

\[
H=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\operatorname{gr}_5(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}_5(A_9^{\mathfrak f})
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

The rank test is

\[
\boxed{
c_7c_9\ne0
}
\]

quantitatively,

\[
\boxed{
|c_7c_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If \(c_7,c_9\) are fixed nonzero normalization constants, then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})\asymp1.
\]

This would close the leading rank part.

---

# 4. Same-weight off-diagonal corrections are harmless if rank remains two

Suppose weight-5 corrections create

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\frac{c_7}{288}+b_{77}&b_{79}\\
b_{97}&-\frac{c_9}{288}+b_{99}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

They are not errors. They are part of the leading matrix.

The only requirement is

\[
\boxed{
\det L\ne0
}
\]

quantitatively

\[
\boxed{
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If off-diagonal corrections are present, they may even improve rank.

Thus the finite D4 rank certificate is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}\operatorname{gr}_5(\mathbf A_{\rm row})=2.
}
\]

This is invariant under row recombination. If the rows are replaced by an invertible \(2\times2\) linear combination, the determinant changes by the recombination determinant, but rank remains two.

---

# 5. Higher-weight terms and the half-leading bound

Let

\[
\mathbf R_{>5}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
-
\operatorname{gr}_5(\mathbf A_{\rm row})
-
\text{canonical small errors}.
\]

If every term in \(\mathbf R_{>5}\) has at least one additional small factor, then

\[
|\mathbf R_{>5}|
\le
\Theta
\cdot |q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|
\]

where \(\Theta\) is a small parameter.

But one must be careful: “higher weight” is not automatically small unless each weight variable is bounded above by a small constant. In the Gate 2 region, variables are only polynomially bounded above. Therefore higher-weight terms are harmless only if the additional factor is actually small on the chosen regime.

There are two ways to ensure this.

## 5.1 Normal-form small parameter

If the expansion has an explicit small parameter \(\kappa\), and

\[
\Theta\le Q^{-K},
\]

then higher-weight terms are small.

## 5.2 Absolute error bound

If the remaining terms satisfy

\[
|\mathbf R_{>5}|\le Q^{-K},
\]

and the leading scale satisfies

\[
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-K_{\rm lead}},
\]

then choose

\[
K>K_{\rm lead}+C_L+O(1)
\]

to get the half-leading bound.

Without one of these, higher weight alone does not prove smallness.

Thus D4 needs a genuine correction-control theorem, not only formal degree counting.

---

# 6. D4 leading-symbol theorem

The finite theorem should be stated as follows.

## D4 Leading-Symbol Rank Theorem

Let

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_N^{\mathfrak f})
\]

be the finite row vector under consideration. For \(N=9\), let

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})^T.
\]

Assume:

1. No dangerous lower-weight terms:

   \[
   [\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}=0.
   \]

2. Weight-5 symbol has full rank:

   \[
   \operatorname{gr}_5(\mathbf A_{\rm row})
   =
   q_0u^3L\Gamma,
   \qquad
   \sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
   \]

3. Remainder control:

   \[
   |\mathbf R_{>5}+\mathbf R_{\rm can}|
   \le
   \frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
   \]

Then D4 holds:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\quad
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\quad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) is not separately given, replace it by an anisotropy upper bound \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\).

---

# 7. If the two-row symbol rank fails

If

\[
\operatorname{rank}L<2,
\]

then \((A_7,A_9)\) do not see both components of

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Then add more rows:

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots,A_N).
\]

The leading-symbol map becomes

\[
\Gamma\mapsto q_0u^3L_N\Gamma,
\]

where

\[
L_N
\]

is an \(s\times2\) matrix.

The required rank condition is

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

For \(s>2\),

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_N)^2
\]

is the smallest eigenvalue of

\[
L_N^\ast L_N.
\]

So one can close D4 with a taller row vector if the \(2\times2\) pair is degenerate.

---

# 8. If lower-weight terms survive

If lower-weight terms survive, define the augmented leading map

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm lead}
=
\mathbf B(Y)+q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\]

where \(\mathbf B(Y)\) is the lower-weight symbol.

Then D4 becomes a row-pencil nonvanishing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf B(Y)+q_0u^3L\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the Gate 2 admissible set.

This may be easier or harder depending on \(\mathbf B\). If \(\mathbf B\) is wall-live, it helps. If it cancels the \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\) term, one needs subresultant/common-root analysis.

Thus the quotient computation is decisive.

---

# 9. Concrete next audit

The finite symbolic audit should compute:

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{<5}(A_7),\quad
\operatorname{gr}_{<5}(A_9),
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{5}(A_7),\quad
\operatorname{gr}_{5}(A_9).
\]

Expected result:

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{<5}(A_7)=0,\qquad
\operatorname{gr}_{<5}(A_9)=0,
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{5}(A_7)
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{5}(A_9)
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then compute same-weight corrections and determinant of the resulting \(L\).

This is the shortest path to closing D4.

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 reduces to a finite leading-symbol rank certificate.}
}
\]

The proof is complete once the following finite statements are verified:

\[
\boxed{
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gr}_{5}(\mathbf A_{\rm row})=q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\quad
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{higher/canonical remainders are half-leading.}
}
\]

This is the precise algebraic task. It is no longer a global analytic or arithmetic problem.

## Continuing attack — D4 robustness under lower-symbol leakage

I’ll keep pushing D4. The current D4 certificate is:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\mathbf R|\le \frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

The next attack is to make this robust against the main possible failure: **lower-symbol leakage**, i.e. terms in \(A_7,A_9\) not divisible by \(q_0u^3\Gamma\). This is the finite algebraic obstruction identified in the current downstream package. 

---

# 1. The danger with pure formal weight

The previous filtration used

\[
\operatorname{wt}(q_0)=\operatorname{wt}(u)=\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_G)=\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_{G,2})=1.
\]

Then

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma
\]

has weight \(5\).

But formal weight alone is not enough. On the non-wall sample, the variables satisfy only polynomial bounds such as

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and perhaps

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

They are not small analytic parameters in the usual asymptotic sense. Therefore a formal “higher-weight” term is not automatically smaller than a lower-weight term unless it has either:

1. an explicit small coefficient;
2. an additional factor known to be small;
3. an absolute \(Q^{-K}\) bound;
4. or cancellation-free vector structure.

So the correct D4 audit is not purely graded. It is **admissible-set dominance**.

---

# 2. Define the Gate 2 admissible set

At a non-wall D4 sample define

\[
\mathcal S_{\rm D4}
=
\left\{
(q_0,u,\Gamma):
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},\
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},\
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},\
|q_0|,|u|,|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_+}
\right\}.
\]

If using the anisotropy-upper-bound variant, replace

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

by

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

D4 is a lower-bound statement on \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\):

\[
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus every correction term should be tested relative to the leading scale

\[
S_{\rm lead}=|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

---

# 3. The exact correction test

For every term \(T\) in the row expansion, compute

\[
\mathcal E_T
=
\sup_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}
\frac{|T|}{|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|}.
\]

Then:

- if \(\mathcal E_T\le Q^{-K}\), the term is **small**;
- if \(T=q_0u^3M\Gamma\), the term is **same-shape** and must be absorbed into \(L\);
- if \(\mathcal E_T\ge Q^{-O(1)}\) and \(T\) is not same-shape, the term is **structural** and must be added to the leading row-pencil.

So the row expansion should be normalized as

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\mathbf B_{\rm leak}
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_{\rm small}.
}
\]

The previous D4 theorem is the special case

\[
\mathbf B_{\rm leak}=0.
\]

---

# 4. If leakage exists, it may help

Suppose

\[
\mathbf B_{\rm leak}\ne0.
\]

This is not automatically bad.

If

\[
|\mathbf B_{\rm leak}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\), then D4 closes even before using the \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\) term.

For example, a leakage term like

\[
u^4
\]

is wall-live and non-wall-live if \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\). It would directly solve row conversion.

Similarly,

\[
u^3\Gamma_G
\]

would be visible whenever \(u\) and \(\Gamma\) are visible.

So lower-symbol leakage falls into two subcases:

\[
\boxed{
\text{good leakage: independently lower-bounds the row;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{bad leakage: can cancel the }q_0u^3L\Gamma\text{ term.}
}
\]

The audit must distinguish these.

---

# 5. Row-pencil formulation for leakage

The robust D4 theorem should allow leakage:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\mathbf B(Y)
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_{\rm small},
}
\]

where \(Y\) denotes the remaining local variables.

The lower-bound target becomes

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf B(Y)+q_0u^3L\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}
\quad
\text{on }\mathcal S_{\rm D4}.
}
\]

This is a finite row-pencil nonvanishing problem.

A sufficient condition is:

\[
|\mathbf B(Y)|\ge 2|q_0u^3L\Gamma|
\]

or

\[
|q_0u^3L\Gamma|\ge 2|\mathbf B(Y)|.
\]

But the mixed regime requires a resultant/subresultant-type check:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf B(Y)\ne -q_0u^3L\Gamma
\quad
\text{on }\mathcal S_{\rm D4}.
}
\]

For two rows, cancellation is possible in principle. Adding more rows makes cancellation less likely.

---

# 6. Use row augmentation if two rows are insufficient

Define the finite row vector

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},A_{13}^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_N^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

The robust normal form is

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
\mathbf B_N(Y)
+
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_N.
\]

Here

\[
L_N
\]

is an \(s\times 2\) matrix.

The nondegenerate branch closes if either:

\[
|\mathbf B_N(Y)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

or

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and \(\mathbf B_N\) cannot cancel \(q_0u^3L_N\Gamma\).

A clean sufficient condition is orthogonality/separation:

\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\left(
-\mathbf B_N(Y),
\operatorname{Range}(L_N)
\right)
+
|q_0u^3|\,|L_N\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But finite algebraically, the simplest target is:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}
|\mathbf B_N(Y)+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the **row-pencil nonvanishing theorem**.

---

# 7. Practical finite audit hierarchy

The row audit should proceed in this order.

## Step 1: compute two-row quotient

Compute

\[
\mathbf B_{7,9}
=
\mathbf A_{7,9}
\bmod
(q_0u^3\Gamma_G,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

If

\[
\mathbf B_{7,9}=0
\]

up to small errors, use the simple D4 matrix theorem.

## Step 2: if leakage exists, test whether it is good

Check whether

\[
|\mathbf B_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\).

If yes, D4 closes.

## Step 3: if leakage is cancellable, augment rows

Add

\[
A_{11},A_{13}
\]

and recompute

\[
\mathbf B_N,\quad L_N.
\]

Try to prove

\[
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}
|\mathbf B_N+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## Step 4: if still cancellable, use row-pencil algebra

Compute common zero conditions:

\[
\mathbf B_N(Y)+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma=0
\]

together with

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\quad
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Eliminate \(q_0\) or \(\Gamma\) to find whether a finite algebraic obstruction exists.

This is a finite symbolic problem.

---

# 8. D4 robust theorem

The strongest useful D4 statement is:

## Robust D4 Row-Pencil Theorem

Let \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\) be the Gate 2 non-wall admissible set.

Suppose for some finite row vector \(\mathbf A_N\) we have

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
\mathbf B_N(Y)+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le \frac12
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}
|\mathbf B_N(Y)+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma|.
\]

Assume

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm D4}}
|\mathbf B_N(Y)+q_0u^3L_N\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C'}
}
\]

on the non-wall Gate 2 sample.

The simple D4 theorem is the subcase \(\mathbf B_N=0\) and \(\sigma_{\min}(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}\).

---

# 9. Why this matters for wall escape

Wall escape gives a non-wall point but may put \(q_0\) near the lower threshold:

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus the leading scale

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma
\]

may be small. A leakage term, if present, could dominate. This is fine if it is nonzero, but dangerous if it cancels.

Therefore robust D4 should not assume leakage vanishes unless proven. It should either:

1. prove leakage vanishes;
2. use leakage as an additional leading term;
3. or prove row-pencil nonvanishing.

---

# 10. Current next concrete task

Without explicit row formulas, the exact proof cannot proceed further. The next concrete computation is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{7,9}\bmod(q_0u^3\Gamma_G,\ q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}).
}
\]

Then classify:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf B=0
\quad\text{simple D4;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf B\ne0\text{ and nonvanishing}
\quad\text{stronger D4;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf B\ne0\text{ and cancellable}
\quad\text{augment rows / row-pencil.}
}
\]

This is the sharp finite attack point for D4.
