_Thought for 13s_

## Continuing attack — D4 via dyadic/tropical row-pencil certification

I’ll continue the D4 attack by making the row-pencil test quantitative. The previous step said: compute the row expansion, classify leakage, and prove nonvanishing on the Gate 2 admissible set. The next sharper tool is a **dyadic valuation / tropical certificate**: split the admissible set into polynomially many size regimes for \((q_0,u,\Gamma)\), identify the leading row terms in each regime, and prove no leading cancellation. This turns D4 into a finite, checkable lower-bound problem. 

---

# 1. D4 admissible set

At a non-wall sample point, D4 assumes

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and polynomial upper bounds

\[
|q_0|,\ |u|,\ |\Gamma|\le Q^{C_+}.
\]

The row vector is

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_N^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

The robust row-pencil form is

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
\mathbf B_N(Y)
+
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_N.
\]

The task is to prove

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the admissible set.

---

# 2. Dyadic decomposition of the admissible set

Decompose into dyadic valuation boxes:

\[
|q_0|\asymp Q^{-a},
\qquad
|u|\asymp Q^{-b},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\asymp Q^{-c},
\]

where

\[
0\le a,b,c\le C_+
\]

after allowing signs/complex phases separately, and the Gate 2 constraint gives

\[
2b+2c\le A_2+O(1).
\]

The non-wall condition is

\[
a\le C_q.
\]

There are only polynomially many boxes in exponent space after discretizing \(a,b,c\) at unit or \(O(1)\) precision.

On each box, every monomial term in the row expansion has a predictable \(Q\)-valuation.

For a term

\[
T=q_0^{\alpha}u^{\beta}\Gamma_1^{\gamma_1}\Gamma_2^{\gamma_2}Z,
\]

where \(Z\) is bounded polynomially above and below, the valuation is

\[
v(T)=
\alpha a+\beta b+\gamma c+O(1),
\]

with

\[
\gamma=\gamma_1+\gamma_2
\]

if only \(|\Gamma|\) is tracked. If direction matters, decompose \(\Gamma\) projectively.

The leading D4 term

\[
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma
\]

has valuation

\[
v_{\rm lead}=a+3b+c+O(1).
\]

---

# 3. Tropical leading-row criterion

For each dyadic box, compute the minimal valuation among all row terms:

\[
v_{\min}=\min_T v(T).
\]

Then split.

## Case A: unique leading term

If the minimal valuation belongs to a single row-vector term \(\mathbf T_\ast\), and

\[
|\mathbf T_\ast|\ge Q^{-v_{\min}-O(1)}
\]

with coefficient nonzero, then all higher-valuation terms are smaller by a polynomial factor if the valuation gap is at least \(O(1)\). Hence

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-v_{\min}-O(1)}.
\]

D4 closes on that box.

## Case B: leading subspace is \(q_0u^3L_N\Gamma\)

If the minimal terms are exactly

\[
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma,
\]

then D4 closes if

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
|q_0u^3L_N\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-a-3b-c-C}.
\]

Using

\[
a\le C_q,
\qquad
2b+2c\le A_2,
\]

and either \(b\le C_u\) or \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\) to control the remaining factor, this is polynomially non-small.

## Case C: multiple leading terms can cancel

If the minimal valuation contains several terms, define the leading row pencil on that box:

\[
\mathbf P_{\rm box}(\theta)
=
\sum_{T:v(T)=v_{\min}} \mathbf T(\theta),
\]

where \(\theta\) denotes phase/projective variables.

Then the box is closed if

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\theta\in\Theta_{\rm box}}
|\mathbf P_{\rm box}(\theta)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If this infimum is zero, then the current row set is insufficient on that box unless the next valuation layer rescues it.

This is a finite algebraic test.

---

# 4. Projective reduction for \(\Gamma\)

Write

\[
\Gamma=|\Gamma|\omega,
\qquad
|\omega|=1.
\]

Then

\[
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma
=
q_0u^3|\Gamma|L_N\omega.
\]

The leading row-pencil cancellation condition becomes a projective equation in

\[
\omega\in S^1_{\mathbb C}
\]

or the real/complex projective line depending on the row field.

For the simple D4 case with no leakage,

\[
\mathbf P_{\rm box}(\omega)=L_N\omega.
\]

Then

\[
\inf_{|\omega|=1}|L_N\omega|
=
\sigma_{\min}(L_N).
\]

So projective reduction recovers the matrix singular-value condition.

If leakage appears, the leading pencil may be

\[
\mathbf P_{\rm box}(\omega,\zeta)
=
\mathbf B_{\rm lead}(\zeta)+\lambda L_N\omega,
\]

where \(\zeta\) are other bounded variables and \(\lambda\) records the relative dyadic size of \(q_0u^3|\Gamma|\). The finite test is whether this vector vanishes on the compact projective domain.

---

# 5. Quantitative algebraic nonvanishing

Suppose the leading pencil

\[
\mathbf P(\theta)
\]

has coefficients bounded by \(Q^{O(1)}\), degree \(d=O(1)\), and no zero on a compact semialgebraic domain \(\Theta\). Then an effective Łojasiewicz/Nullstellensatz bound gives

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\theta\in\Theta}|\mathbf P(\theta)|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

provided the coefficients have polynomial height and the separation from the algebraic zero set is polynomial.

A finite certificate can be written as a sum-of-squares / Positivstellensatz identity:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf P(\theta)|^2
=
Q^{-C}
+
\sum_j s_j(\theta)r_j(\theta)
}
\]

on the constraint set, where the \(r_j\) encode the projective-domain constraints. In practice, for low-dimensional \(2\times2\) or \(s\times2\) row pencils, one can usually avoid full Positivstellensatz and compute determinants/minors.

For a tall matrix \(L_N\), the certificate is

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(L_N^\ast L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

For leakage pencils, compute resultants or Gröbner eliminants for the system

\[
\mathbf P(\theta)=0
\]

plus admissibility constraints.

---

# 6. Finite D4 tropical certificate theorem

## Theorem

Assume the row vector has a finite expansion

\[
\mathbf A_N=\sum_T \mathbf T
\]

with polynomial-height coefficients and canonical remainders bounded absolutely by \(Q^{-K}\).

Assume a dyadic decomposition of the D4 admissible set into boxes

\[
\mathcal B_\nu
\]

such that on each box:

1. the leading valuation \(v_{\min,\nu}\) is identified;
2. the leading pencil

   \[
   \mathbf P_\nu
   =
   \sum_{T:v(T)=v_{\min,\nu}}\mathbf T
   \]

   satisfies

   \[
   \inf_{\mathcal B_\nu}|\mathbf P_\nu|\ge Q^{-C};
   \]

3. all non-leading terms have valuation at least

   \[
   v_{\min,\nu}+C_{\rm gap}
   \]

   or are absolutely \(Q^{-K}\)-small.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C'}
}
\]

on the whole D4 admissible set.

This is the robust D4 certificate.

---

# 7. How this helps the simple D4 normal form

If the audit shows

\[
[\mathbf A_{\rm row}]_{<5}=0,
\]

and the weight-5 symbol is

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\]

then the dyadic leading pencil is always

\[
\mathbf P=L\omega.
\]

The certificate reduces to

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

So the simple D4 theorem is a special case of the tropical certificate.

If lower-weight leakage exists, the dyadic method tells whether it is good, bad, or cancellable.

---

# 8. Explicit row audit protocol

For each row \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\), compute its finite expansion in the variables

\[
q_0,\ u,\ \Gamma_1,\ \Gamma_2,\ \text{auxiliary bounded variables}.
\]

Then build a table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{term} & \text{valuation }v(a,b,c) & \text{row vector coefficient} & \text{classification}\\
\hline
q_0u^3\Gamma_1 & a+3b+c & \mathbf v_1 & same-shape\\
q_0u^3\Gamma_2 & a+3b+c & \mathbf v_2 & same-shape\\
u^4 & 4b & \mathbf v_3 & leakage\\
q_0^2u^3\Gamma & 2a+3b+c & \mathbf v_4 & higher/nonlinear\\
E_2\text{ tail} & K_E & \mathbf v_E & small?
\end{array}
\]

For each dyadic region, select the lowest valuation rows and test nonvanishing.

This is mechanical and finite.

---

# 9. Likely outcomes

## If the expected row formula is exact

Rows \(A_7,A_9\) have no lower leakage and

\[
L=
-\frac1{288}\operatorname{diag}(c_7,c_9)
\]

up to small perturbation. Then D4 closes quickly.

## If leakage is wall-live

Then D3 is also helped, because wall-live leakage can produce rows at \(q_0=0\).

## If leakage cancels leading terms

Need row augmentation:

\[
A_{11},A_{13},\ldots
\]

and row-pencil nonvanishing.

Thus the tropical audit will not just verify D4; it will also decide whether wall escape is necessary or whether the wall has a direct row.

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 can be reduced to a finite dyadic/tropical row-pencil certificate.}
}
\]

The essential finite tasks are:

1. expand rows;
2. compute valuations of every term on the D4 admissible set;
3. identify leading pencils by dyadic region;
4. certify nonvanishing of each leading pencil;
5. bound remainders.

This is the most robust formulation because it handles leakage, cancellation, row augmentation, and the simple expected normal form in one framework.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:29:58)

_Thought for 9s_

## Continuing attack — make the D4 tropical certificate executable

I’ll keep attacking D4, but now in a more operational way. The previous step gave the right robust framework:

\[
\mathbf A_N=\sum_T \mathbf T,
\]

split the D4 admissible set into dyadic valuation boxes, identify the leading row-pencil on each box, and prove that leading pencil is nonvanishing. The missing piece is an executable certificate: what exactly do we compute, and what exact algebraic condition proves D4? This is the finite row-conversion problem left by the downstream package. 

---

# 1. D4 admissible variables and constraints

Let

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2)
=
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

At a D4 sample, assume

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and polynomial upper bounds

\[
|q_0|,\ |u|,\ |\Gamma|,\ |Y|\le Q^{C_+},
\]

where \(Y\) denotes all auxiliary bounded local variables appearing in the row formulas.

For the version with an explicit source lower bound, also assume

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Otherwise assume

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

so that Gate 2 mass implies a lower bound for \(|u|\).

The target is

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

for a finite row vector

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},\ldots,A_N).
\]

---

# 2. Normalize by the Gate 2 scale

A useful normalization is to divide row expressions by the minimal expected D4 scale.

Let

\[
S=q_0u^3|\Gamma|.
\]

In the simple D4 model,

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R.
\]

So

\[
\frac{\mathbf A_{\rm row}}{S}
=
L\omega+\frac{\mathbf R}{S},
\qquad
\omega=\frac{\Gamma}{|\Gamma|}.
\]

The simple D4 theorem is equivalent to

\[
|L\omega|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

uniformly in \(|\omega|=1\), plus

\[
|\mathbf R|/S\le \frac12Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus the finite audit should always ask:

\[
\boxed{
\text{What is }\mathbf A_N/S\text{ on each dyadic box?}
}
\]

Terms with valuation lower than \(S\) become large in this normalization; they must either help or be included in a row-pencil.

---

# 3. Dyadic box coordinates

Use dyadic exponents

\[
|q_0|\asymp Q^{-a},
\qquad
|u|\asymp Q^{-b},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\asymp Q^{-c}.
\]

The admissible constraints are

\[
a\le C_q,
\]

\[
2b+2c\le A_2+O(1),
\]

and upper bounds

\[
a,b,c\ge -C_+.
\]

For the explicit source-lower-bound branch,

\[
b\le C_u.
\]

For the anisotropy-upper-bound branch,

\[
c\ge -C_\Gamma.
\]

The expected leading scale has valuation

\[
v_S=a+3b+c.
\]

For each row term \(T\), compute its valuation \(v_T(a,b,c)\). Then compare

\[
v_T-v_S.
\]

Three cases:

\[
v_T=v_S+O(1)
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{same-scale row-pencil term};
\]

\[
v_T>v_S+C
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{small correction};
\]

\[
v_T<v_S-C
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{dominant leakage term}.
\]

Dominant leakage is not a problem if it is nonzero as a row vector. It is a problem only if it can cancel with other terms of the same valuation.

---

# 4. Leading pencil on a dyadic box

For each box \(\mathcal B\), define

\[
v_{\min}(\mathcal B)=\min_T v_T.
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}
=
\sum_{T:\,v_T=v_{\min}+O(1)} T
\]

be the leading pencil on that box, after factoring out \(Q^{-v_{\min}}\).

The D4 certificate on \(\mathcal B\) is:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\mathcal B}
|\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If true, all higher-valuation terms are lower order after choosing the dyadic gap large enough or absorbing polynomial losses.

If false, inspect the common zero set

\[
\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}=0.
\]

If the common zero set is empty under the admissibility constraints, use an effective algebraic separation theorem. If nonempty, add the next valuation layer or add more rows.

---

# 5. Simple D4 as the principal box certificate

If no leakage terms exist below \(v_S\), then

\[
v_{\min}=v_S
\]

and

\[
\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma.
\]

After factoring \(q_0u^3|\Gamma|\), the pencil is

\[
P(\omega)=L\omega,
\qquad
|\omega|=1.
\]

The certificate is

\[
\inf_{|\omega|=1}|L\omega|
=
\sigma_{\min}(L)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the simple expected D4 proof is just:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no lower leakage}
+
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}
+
\text{small higher remainders}.
}
\]

---

# 6. If lower leakage appears

Suppose a leakage term appears, for example

\[
\mathbf B(Y,u,\Gamma)
\]

with valuation

\[
v_B<v_S.
\]

Then on that dyadic box, \(\mathbf B\) dominates

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma.
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf B|\ge Q^{-C}Q^{-v_B}
\]

uniformly, D4 is easier than expected.

The only danger is if \(\mathbf B\) has its own zeros or cancels with other same-valuation leakage terms.

Thus leakage should be treated as follows:

## Good leakage

If

\[
\inf_{\mathcal B}|\mathbf B_{\rm lead}|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then row conversion closes on that box independently of \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\).

## Cancellable leakage

If

\[
\mathbf B_{\rm lead}=0
\]

has solutions inside the box, include the next layer:

\[
\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}
=
\mathbf B_{\rm lead}
+
\mathbf B_{\rm next}
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma
\]

up to the first nonvanishing layer.

This becomes a finite row-pencil nonvanishing problem.

---

# 7. Effective finite algebra certificate

For a leading pencil

\[
\mathbf P(\theta)
\]

on a compact semialgebraic domain \(\Theta\), we need

\[
\inf_{\Theta}|\mathbf P(\theta)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

A practical certificate can be one of the following.

## 7.1 Singular-value certificate

If

\[
\mathbf P(\theta)=M\omega
\]

with \(|\omega|=1\), prove

\[
\sigma_{\min}(M)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## 7.2 Minor certificate for tall row matrices

If

\[
M
\]

is \(s\times2\), prove at least one \(2\times2\) minor satisfies

\[
|\det M_{i,j}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(M)\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

given polynomial upper bounds.

## 7.3 Resultant certificate

If

\[
\mathbf P(\theta)
\]

is nonlinear, compute the algebraic system

\[
P_1(\theta)=\cdots=P_s(\theta)=0
\]

plus admissibility constraints. If no solution exists, use a quantitative Nullstellensatz / resultant lower bound.

For a finite symbolic audit, it is enough to produce a certificate of the form

\[
1=\sum_j U_j(\theta)P_j(\theta)+\sum_k V_k(\theta)R_k(\theta),
\]

where \(R_k\) encode constraints, with polynomial-height coefficients. This gives a polynomial lower bound after controlling heights.

## 7.4 Sum-of-squares certificate

For real variables, prove

\[
|\mathbf P(\theta)|^2-Q^{-C}
=
\sum_\ell S_\ell(\theta)^2
+
\sum_k \lambda_k(\theta)R_k(\theta)
\]

on the domain. This is strongest but may be overkill.

---

# 8. Concrete finite audit protocol

For each candidate row set

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,\ldots,A_N),
\]

do:

### Step 1: Expand

Write all terms as monomials in

\[
q_0,\ u,\ \Gamma_1,\ \Gamma_2,\ Y
\]

plus canonical error terms.

### Step 2: Assign valuations

For each monomial \(T\), compute

\[
v_T(a,b,c)
\]

on dyadic exponents.

### Step 3: Partition exponent space

Partition the admissible exponent polytope into regions where the same set of monomials is leading.

This is a tropical subdivision.

### Step 4: Leading-pencil test

On each region, write the leading pencil

\[
\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}.
\]

Certify

\[
\inf|\mathbf P_{\mathcal B}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

### Step 5: Remainder bound

Show all non-leading and canonical error terms are at least polynomially smaller than the certified leading lower bound.

If every region passes, D4 is proved.

---

# 9. Why this is robust under row augmentation

If two rows are insufficient, add more rows. The leading-pencil test only improves with more rows because

\[
|\mathbf A_N|^2
=
|\mathbf A_{N-2}|^2+|A_N|^2.
\]

A new row cannot make the vector norm smaller. It can only help nonvanishing. Therefore, if \(A_7,A_9\) have a cancellation region, adding \(A_{11},A_{13}\) is a natural fix.

The finite certificate should allow row augmentation until the leading pencil is nonvanishing.

---

# 10. Current sharp D4 theorem

## D4 Tropical Row-Pencil Theorem

Let \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\) be the D4 admissible set. Suppose a finite row vector \(\mathbf A_N\) has a finite expansion with polynomial-height coefficients and small canonical errors. Suppose the dyadic/tropical subdivision of \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\) has, on every cell, a leading pencil \(\mathbf P_\nu\) satisfying

\[
\inf_{\mathcal S_\nu}|\mathbf P_\nu|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Suppose all non-leading terms and canonical errors are bounded by at most half of this leading lower bound on each cell.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C'}
}
\]

on all of \(\mathcal S_{\rm D4}\).

This theorem subsumes:

- simple matrix D4;
- leakage-positive D4;
- augmented-row D4;
- row-pencil D4.

---

# 11. Next exact algebraic task

The proof cannot advance further without row formulas. The exact next computation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Expand }A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}
\text{ into monomials in }q_0,u,\Gamma,Y.
}
\]

Then run the tropical audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{leading valuations}
\Rightarrow
\text{leading pencils}
\Rightarrow
\text{nonvanishing certificates}.
}
\]

This is now a finite symbolic problem, not a conceptual or analytic problem.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:31:29)

_Thought for 8s_

## Continuing attack — squeeze D4 without row formulas: universal tests from row covariance

Since the explicit row formulas are still unavailable, the only way to advance D4 is to extract **formula-independent consequences** that any successful row package must satisfy. The current D4 problem is finite algebraic:

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},\ldots,A_N)
\]

must be non-small on the D4 admissible set. The last attack reduced this to a dyadic/tropical row-pencil certificate. I’ll now push one level further: formulate **universal covariance tests** that can certify or falsify the expected normal form before full symbolic expansion. This is still within the current downstream plan: Gate 2 is locally handled by extraction + integral rigidity, while D4 is now the row-expansion/correction-control bottleneck. 

---

# 1. Expected covariance of the rows

The D4 expected normal form is

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

Thus, under the simultaneous scaling

\[
\Gamma\mapsto s\Gamma,
\]

with \(q_0,u\) fixed, the leading row should scale linearly:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\mapsto s\mathbf A_{\rm row}.
\]

Under

\[
u\mapsto r u,
\]

with \(q_0,\Gamma\) fixed, the leading row scales cubically:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\mapsto r^3\mathbf A_{\rm row}.
\]

Under

\[
q_0\mapsto t q_0,
\]

with \(u,\Gamma\) fixed, it scales linearly:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\mapsto t\mathbf A_{\rm row}.
\]

So a necessary leading-symbol test is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
\text{ must be tri-homogeneous of degree }(1,3,1)
\text{ in }(q_0,u,\Gamma)
}
\]

at the first nonzero D4 order.

This gives a formula-independent audit:

- Any leading term with different degree is leakage.
- Any same-degree term is part of \(L\).
- Any term with higher degree needs an actual smallness parameter or absolute error bound.

---

# 2. Use directional derivatives to extract \(L\)

Even without full expansion, \(L\) can be defined intrinsically by differentiating the row vector with respect to \(\Gamma\) at the D4 leading scale.

Let

\[
\Gamma=s\omega,
\qquad |\omega|=1.
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal L(q_0,u)
=
\lim_{s\to0}
\frac{1}{q_0u^3s}
\mathbf A_{\rm row}(q_0,u,s\omega),
\]

if the limit exists linearly in \(\omega\). Then

\[
\mathcal L(q_0,u)\omega=L\omega.
\]

So the leading-matrix test can be performed by the limit

\[
\boxed{
L\omega
=
\operatorname*{lead}_{s\to0}
\frac{\mathbf A_{\rm row}(q_0,u,s\omega)}
{q_0u^3s}.
}
\]

The D4 matrix theorem requires:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{|\omega|=1}|L\omega|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is often easier than expanding every row term. It tests the row response to infinitesimal anisotropy \(\Gamma\).

---

# 3. Leakage test by anisotropy-zero restriction

Set

\[
\Gamma=0.
\]

If the expected D4 normal form is correct, then

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}(q_0,u,0)
\]

should be small:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\big|_{\Gamma=0}
=
\mathbf R_{\rm small}.
}
\]

So the first leakage test is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\big|_{\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0}
\stackrel{?}{=}0
\quad\text{up to canonical small errors}.
}
\]

If this restriction is nonzero and polynomially large, that is not necessarily bad; it means the row sees something even when Gate 2 anisotropy vanishes. But then D4 should be reformulated with an additional leading term:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\mathbf B(q_0,u,Y)
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R.
\]

If \(\mathbf B\) can vanish or cancel, row-pencil analysis is needed.

Thus the zero-anisotropy restriction is the fastest way to detect lower-symbol leakage.

---

# 4. Wall restriction test

Set

\[
q_0=0.
\]

The expected D4 leading term vanishes:

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{q_0=0}
}
\]

detects wall-live leakage.

If

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0,\Gamma\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then the wall is actually easier than expected; we have a source-robust row.

If

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

for all known rows, then wall escape remains necessary.

So D4 and D3 can share the same audit:

\[
\boxed{
q_0=0\text{ quotient}
}
\]

detects source-robust wall rows;

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma=0\text{ quotient}
}
\]

detects anisotropy-independent leakage;

\[
\boxed{
(q_0,\Gamma)\text{ quotient}
}
\]

detects mixed leakage.

---

# 5. \(u=0\) restriction test

Set

\[
u=0.
\]

Expected leading D4 term vanishes because of \(u^3\):

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma=0.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{u=0}
}
\]

should be small or vanish. If a nonzero row term survives at \(u=0\), it is leakage.

This may help: if a row survives at \(u=0\), it is not an obstruction to lower bounds unless it can cancel elsewhere. It gives an additional leading branch. But it means the simple \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\) normal form is incomplete.

Thus the three quick quotient tests are:

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u=0,\qquad \Gamma=0.
\]

If all three restrictions vanish, then the row vector is divisible by

\[
q_0,\quad u,\quad \Gamma
\]

separately. But D4 needs divisibility by \(q_0u^3\Gamma\), so we also need multiplicity in \(u\).

---

# 6. \(u\)-multiplicity test

To confirm the \(u^3\) factor, compute the first nonzero \(u\)-jet at \(u=0\):

\[
\partial_u^j \mathbf A_{\rm row}\big|_{u=0},
\qquad j=0,1,2,3.
\]

Expected:

\[
\partial_u^j\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{u=0}=0
\quad(j=0,1,2),
\]

and

\[
\partial_u^3\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{u=0}
=
6q_0L\Gamma
\]

up to constants.

So the \(u^3\)-factor certificate is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{ord}_{u=0}\mathbf A_{\rm row}=3
\quad\text{in the }q_0\Gamma\text{ channel}.
}
\]

This is a finite derivative test and is easier than full expansion.

---

# 7. Complete local covariance certificate

A concise D4 normal-form certificate can be:

## D4 Covariance Certificate

For the row vector \(\mathbf A_{\rm row}\), verify:

1. Wall divisibility:

   \[
   \mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{q_0=0}=0
   \quad\text{or classify wall-live terms}.
   \]

2. Source cubic divisibility:

   \[
   \partial_u^j\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{u=0}=0,
   \qquad j=0,1,2.
   \]

3. Anisotropy divisibility:

   \[
   \mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{\Gamma=0}=0
   \quad\text{or classify leakage}.
   \]

4. Leading anisotropy response:

   \[
   L\omega
   =
   \operatorname*{lead}_{s\to0}
   \frac{\mathbf A_{\rm row}(q_0,u,s\omega)}
   {q_0u^3s},
   \]

   with

   \[
   \sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
   \]

5. Remainder control:

   all higher-order/canonical terms are half-leading on the D4 admissible set.

If 1–5 hold, D4 is proved.

---

# 8. Why this certificate is useful

The full row expansion may be large. But these covariance tests are much smaller:

- \(q_0=0\) tests the wall branch.
- \(\Gamma=0\) tests anisotropy-independent leakage.
- \(u=0\) and \(u\)-jets test source order.
- Directional anisotropy derivative extracts \(L\).

This is the fastest finite algebra path.

Instead of expanding every term, we can first test whether the expected structure is true at the level of restrictions and first jets.

Only if these tests fail do we need full row-pencil/tropical analysis.

---

# 9. D4 proof under covariance certificate

Assume the covariance certificate holds. Then

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
\mathbf R
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

At a D4 admissible point,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the covariance certificate implies D4.

---

# 10. Next exact test sequence

Without explicit row formulas, the most efficient next symbolic computation is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{q_0=0}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{\Gamma=0}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\partial_u^0,\partial_u^1,\partial_u^2,\partial_u^3
\mathbf A_{\rm row}|_{u=0}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\partial}{\partial \Gamma}
\left(
\frac{\mathbf A_{\rm row}}{q_0u^3}
\right)_{\rm lead}
}
\]

If these match the expected pattern, D4 is reduced to small remainders.

If not, the failure tells exactly which row-pencil branch to use.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 can be attacked by a much smaller covariance/jet certificate before full expansion.}
}
\]

This gives a practical algebraic protocol:

1. quotient tests: \(q_0=0,u=0,\Gamma=0\);
2. source multiplicity test: \(u\)-jets up to order 3;
3. anisotropy response test: compute \(L\);
4. singular-value test: \(\sigma_{\min}(L)\);
5. remainder half-leading bound.

This is the shortest path to closing D4 once row formulas are available.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:32:16)

## Continuing attack — D4 covariance certificate plus wall-escape compatibility

The D4 covariance certificate now gives a compact symbolic route:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

But we need to make sure it is compatible with **wall escape**, where \(q_0\) exits the wall at a controlled but possibly very small level:

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

The risk is that even if D4 is true algebraically, the leading row

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma
\]

may be too small after escape unless the exit level, source size, and Gate 2 signal are exponent-compatible.

This attack checks those exponents and gives the final wall-escape + D4 theorem in a usable form.

---

# 1. Wall-escape output

Wall escape supplies a point \(m_1\) such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2,
\]

and, because

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

with \(\varepsilon\ll \tau\),

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|
=
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}
\ge c\tau.
\]

So the Gate 2 pointwise signal at \(m_1\) satisfies

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

If

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus D4 applies at \(m_1\) with

\[
A_2=4C_\tau+O(1),
\]

\[
C_u=C_\tau+O(1),
\]

\[
C_q=C_\varepsilon.
\]

---

# 2. D4 leading row size at the escape point

D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|
\ge
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

At the wall-exit point,

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)},
\]

and

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1)}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_A=C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

This is polynomially non-small as long as \(C_\varepsilon,C_\tau,C_L\) are finite constants.

Thus wall escape is exponent-compatible with D4.

---

# 3. Wall-exit radius and exponent compatibility

Wall escape used the first-exit radius

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

we get

\[
\rho\asymp Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

To preserve \(u\), assume

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

In normalized coordinates, preservation requires

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\ll \tau,
\]

i.e.

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\ll Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\frac{C_\varepsilon-C_\tau}{2}
>
C_{u'}+C_\tau,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
}
\]

This is the same condition from the wall-escape theorem. Under it,

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2.
\]

Also, to ensure

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

we need

\[
6|q_0(m_1)|+2|q_0(m_1)|^3\ll |u(m_1)|,
\]

which follows from

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

i.e.

\[
C_\varepsilon>C_\tau+O(1).
\]

This is weaker than the previous escape condition.

Thus the only real exponent requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 4. Row mobility after escape

Let

\[
R(m)=\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m).
\]

Suppose

\[
\|R'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_R}|I|^{-1}.
\]

At \(m_1\),

\[
|R(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Then on an interval of radius

\[
r\asymp Q^{-C_A-C_R}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|R(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I |R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-2C_A}Q^{-C_A-C_R}|I|
=
Q^{-3C_A-C_R}|I|.
\]

So wall escape plus D4 plus row mobility gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C_{\rm row}}|I|
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm row}=3(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)+C_R+O(1).
}
\]

This is a clean row-energy lower bound.

---

# 5. Full wall-escape + D4 theorem

## Theorem

Assume on \(I\):

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A_G}|I|.
\]

2. Wall split parameters:

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

3. If non-wall mass exists, D4 applies directly. If wall mass dominates, then after removing \(|u|<\tau\), there exists a live wall point with

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\ge\tau.
\]

4. Local derivative bound:

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

5. Exponent condition:

\[
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

6. D4 covariance certificate:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R|\le \frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

7. Row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'|\le Q^{C_R}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Thus the \(q_0\)-wall is handled without a source-robust wall row.

---

# 6. Remaining subtlety: existence of a live wall point

If Gate 2 mass is concentrated in the wall strip, we remove the low-source set

\[
\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

We need to ensure the remaining live wall set is nonempty or carries mass.

Let

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Assume an anisotropy upper bound

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

On \(|u|<\tau\),

\[
G\le \tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

So

\[
\int_{\{|u|<\tau\}}G
\le
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|.
\]

If Gate 2 gives

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A_G}|I|,
\]

then choosing

\[
2C_\tau-2C_\Gamma>A_G+O(1)
\]

makes the low-source contribution negligible.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_\tau>\frac{A_G}{2}+C_\Gamma+O(1).
}
\]

This condition must be compatible with the escape condition requiring \(C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_{u'}\). It is compatible: choose \(C_\tau\) first, then \(C_\varepsilon\) much larger.

Thus live wall points exist if wall mass dominates.

---

# 7. Non-wall branch

If non-wall mass is nontrivial, there exists \(m_\ast\) with

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

by pointwise sampling, assuming \(G\) has polynomial upper bound or simply by average.

At such a point, D4 applies directly with

\[
C_q=C_\varepsilon.
\]

If \(|u|\) is not explicitly lower-bounded, use

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\) to get

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then D4 gives a row lower bound. Row mobility gives row energy.

Thus both branches close under the same D4 + mobility theorem.

---

# 8. Updated downstream row theorem

The downstream row-conversion layer can now be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{anisotropy/source upper bounds}
+
\text{wall escape}
+
\text{D4 covariance certificate}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row-energy lower bound}.
}
\]

This replaces the old D3 source-robust row theorem.

The fallback \(q_0\)-adic wall-row audit is only needed if:

1. row conversion must occur exactly at a preassigned point; or
2. wall escape cannot stay inside the admissible packet interval; or
3. D4 fails at the escaped non-wall point.

---

# 9. Final exponent summary

Choose:

\[
C_\tau>\frac{A_G}{2}+C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Then choose:

\[
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then wall exit gives:

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

and D4 gives:

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1)}.
\]

Row mobility gives:

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2
\ge
Q^{-3(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)-C_R-O(1)}|I|.
\]

All exponents are finite polynomial constants. Thus the wall branch is exponent-consistent.

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }q_0\text{-wall is no longer a primary structural blocker under existential/energy row sampling.}
}
\]

The remaining downstream proof tasks are now:

1. finalize Gate 2 integral rigidity and two-threshold extraction;
2. prove canonical derivative/upper bounds;
3. verify D4 covariance certificate and correction control;
4. confirm row-energy, not exact-point row value, is the required downstream output.

If 4 is true, wall escape closes the wall branch.

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem with target-smallness \(S\)

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: assemble the final Gate 2 theorem package using Agent 1’s local complexity / extraction assumptions and Agent 2’s integral rigidity lemma. The key is to avoid exponent mistakes by choosing a fixed target-smallness exponent \(S\), rather than tying the interval size directly to the full Gate 2 contradiction exponent \(A\). 

---

# 1. Objects and identities

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Define

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive setup

Assume Gate 1 holds but Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 3. Target-smallness extraction

Fix a target exponent

\[
S>0.
\]

Do **not** set \(S=(A-B)/2\) automatically. Instead, choose \(S\) large enough for the later integral-rigidity contradiction, then choose the Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) large enough to extract that target.

Assume polynomial Lipschitz bounds

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

From Gate 1, choose a polynomial source threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

so that the set

\[
U=\{|u|\ge 2\tau\}
\]

carries polynomial \(u\)-mass:

\[
\boxed{
\int_U |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|.
}
\]

A simple safe choice has

\[
C_\tau=B/2+O(1),
\qquad
C_M=B+O(1),
\]

assuming polynomial \(L^\infty\) control of \(u\). Dyadic thresholding can be used if one wants a more flexible version.

Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\int_U |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore the weighted average of \(F_{\rm aniso}^2\) on \(U\) is at most

\[
Q^{-A+C_M}.
\]

If

\[
A\ge C_M+2S+O(1),
\]

then there exists \(m_\ast\in U\) with

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)\le Q^{-S-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge 2Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

and

\[
|g(m_\ast)|+|h(m_\ast)|\le Q^{-S}.
\]

Now thicken \(m_\ast\) using the Lipschitz bounds. Let

\[
r_u\asymp Q^{-C_\tau-C_u}|I|,
\]

\[
r_F\asymp Q^{-S-C_F}|I|.
\]

On an interval \(J\subset I\) centered at \(m_\ast\), or one-sided near the boundary, with

\[
|J|\asymp \min(r_u,r_F),
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S+O(1)}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

Absorb the harmless \(O(1)\) loss into \(S\). Then write

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
\qquad
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

The extracted exponents are

\[
\boxed{
C_1=C_\tau+O(1),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J(S)}|I|,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
C_J(S)=\max(C_\tau+C_u,\ S+C_F)+O(1).
}
\]

This is the correct target-smallness extraction statement.

---

# 4. G2-B integral rigidity

Assume the safe integral rigidity lemma:

If on an interval \(J\),

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon,
\]

then on a shrunken interval

\[
J'\Subset J
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R(S)}\varepsilon^{c}|J'|.
}
\]

The current safe exponent is

\[
\boxed{
c=\frac13.
}
\]

The sharper optional target is

\[
c=\frac25,
\]

but \(2/5\) should not be used unless the transition kinetic estimate is fully closed.

Here

\[
C_R(S)
\]

contains cutoff losses, derivative bounds, and the loss coming from the size of \(J\). If the derivative package is scale-invariant on polynomial subintervals, then \(C_R(S)\) can be treated as \(O(1)\) or at least as a controlled polynomial-loss constant.

Apply the lemma with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-S}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R(S)-cS}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Contradiction

From extraction,

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

hence on \(J'\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
}
\]

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R(S)-cS}|J'|.
\]

These are incompatible if

\[
Q^{-2C_1}>Q^{C_R(S)-cS},
\]

i.e.

\[
\boxed{
cS-C_R(S)>2C_1.
}
\]

This is the exact Gate 2 closure condition.

With the safe exponent

\[
c=\frac13,
\]

the condition is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{S}{3}-C_R(S)>2C_1.
}
\]

With the optional sharper exponent

\[
c=\frac25,
\]

it becomes

\[
\boxed{
\frac{2S}{5}-C_R(S)>2C_1.
}
\]

Thus, for any \(S\) satisfying this condition, choose \(A\) large enough so that

\[
A\ge C_M+2S+O(1).
\]

Then Gate 2 failure is impossible.

---

# 6. Final Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 from target-smallness extraction and integral rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Canonical local Lipschitz bounds:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. Target-smallness extraction as above.

4. Integral rigidity with exponent \(c>0\):

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R(S)}\varepsilon^c|J'|.
\]

5. There exists a target \(S\) satisfying

\[
\boxed{
cS-C_R(S)>2C_1.
}
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for \(A\) chosen sufficiently large relative to \(S\), \(B\), and the local complexity constants.

---

# 7. Safe version

Using the safe integral rigidity exponent

\[
c=\frac13,
\]

the concrete condition is

\[
\boxed{
S>3(C_R(S)+2C_1).
}
\]

If scale-invariant local complexity makes

\[
C_R(S)=O(1),
\]

then simply choose \(S\) large. Then choose

\[
A\ge C_M+2S+O(1).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + local complexity + G2-B with }c=1/3
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Sharper optional version

If Agent 2 closes the sharper kinetic transition estimate giving

\[
c=\frac25,
\]

then the condition improves to

\[
\boxed{
S>\frac52(C_R(S)+2C_1).
}
\]

This is useful but not structurally necessary.

The downstream proof should record

\[
\boxed{
c=1/3\text{ safe; }c=2/5\text{ optional}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Dependency on \(C_R(S)\)

The only possible exponent trap is if \(C_R(S)\) grows too quickly with \(S\), because the extracted interval length is

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J(S)}|I|,
\]

where

\[
C_J(S)=\max(C_\tau+C_u,\ S+C_F)+O(1).
\]

If the integral rigidity proof is performed in normalized coordinates on \(J\), and the canonical derivative package is scale-invariant, then

\[
C_R(S)=O(1)
\]

or at worst controlled independently of \(S\).

If derivative bounds are only ambient, then cutoff losses may make

\[
C_R(S)=C_R^0+\kappa S.
\]

The safe \(c=1/3\) closes only if

\[
\boxed{
\kappa<\frac13.
}
\]

The sharper \(c=2/5\) closes if

\[
\boxed{
\kappa<\frac25.
}
\]

Therefore Agent 1’s local complexity theorem should be stated in **scale-invariant form** on polynomial subintervals to prevent this problem:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J\subset I^\ast,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I^\ast|}
\sup_J |J|^k |\partial^k q|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Under this form, \(C_R(S)\) is harmless.

---

# 10. Final classification

The old downstream inputs

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez},
\qquad
D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}
\]

are replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A: target-smallness two-threshold extraction}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B: integral rigidity with }c=1/3\text{ safe}.
}
\]

So the Gate 2 theorem is now local and exponent-controlled:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{ordinary local complexity}
+
\text{G2-A}
+
\text{G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The remaining Gate 2 work is:

1. prove/record the scale-invariant local derivative package;
2. finalize the G2-B cutoff proof;
3. set the target \(S\) satisfying \(cS-C_R(S)>2C_1\).

Continue your attack

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:17:24)

_Thought for 8s_

## Continuing attack — eliminate the \(C_R(S)\) exponent trap in Gate 2

The current Gate 2 theorem depends on the condition

\[
cS-C_R(S)>2C_1,
\]

where \(S\) is the target smallness exponent in

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and \(C_R(S)\) is the loss in the integral rigidity lemma

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^{C_R(S)}Q^{-cS}|J'|.
\]

The only remaining danger is that \(C_R(S)\) grows linearly with \(S\) because the extracted interval \(J\) gets shorter as \(S\) increases. I’ll attack that directly. The goal is to show that, under a **scale-invariant derivative package**, \(C_R(S)\) is independent of \(S\) up to harmless constants. This would make Gate 2 genuinely local and closeable with the safe exponent \(c=1/3\). This is exactly the exponent issue isolated in the latest downstream prompt. 

---

# 1. Source of the possible \(S\)-dependence

Two-threshold extraction gives

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J(S)}|I|,
\]

with

\[
C_J(S)=\max(C_\tau+C_u,\ S+C_F)+O(1).
\]

So if \(S\) is large, \(J\) may be short:

\[
|J|\asymp Q^{-S-O(1)}|I|.
\]

In the integral rigidity proof, cutoffs on \(J\) have derivatives like

\[
|\phi'|\sim |J|^{-1},
\qquad
|\phi''|\sim |J|^{-2}.
\]

If these derivatives are measured in the original \(I\)-coordinate without rescaling, they create losses

\[
Q^{O(C_J(S))},
\]

possibly

\[
Q^{O(S)}.
\]

Then the rigidity estimate becomes

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R^0+\kappa S}Q^{-S/3}|J'|.
\]

This closes only if

\[
\kappa<\frac13.
\]

We need to avoid relying on such an accident.

---

# 2. Rescale the integral rigidity proof to \(J\)

Let

\[
m=m_J+Lx,
\qquad
L=|J|,
\]

where

\[
x\in(-2,2),
\qquad
J'=m_J+L(-1,1).
\]

Define rescaled functions

\[
\widetilde q(x)=q(m_J+Lx),
\]

\[
\widetilde u(x)=L^2u(m_J+Lx)
\]

if \(u=q''\) in the original coordinate.

But this scaling changes the algebraic identities unless all quantities are already defined in the normalized local coordinate. Therefore we must be precise.

There are two options.

---

# 3. Option A: work entirely in the intrinsic normalized coordinate

If \(q,u,g,h\) are already defined using the intrinsic local normalized derivative \(\mathcal D\), and \(J\) is measured in that same coordinate, then rescaling \(J\) is only a proof device. The identities remain

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

where primes are intrinsic normalized derivatives.

After rescaling \(J\to(-2,2)\), the identities become

\[
\widetilde g
=
L^{-2}\widetilde q''-6\widetilde q+2\widetilde q^3
\]

unless we also rescale \(g,h,u\). That is inconvenient.

So the cleanest statement is not to physically rescale the identities. Instead, require **scale-invariant derivative bounds** on \(J\) and keep the original normalized coordinate.

The cutoff derivatives produce \(L^{-1},L^{-2}\), but every appearance of such a derivative is paired with a scale-invariant bound such as

\[
L|q'|\le Q^C,
\qquad
L^2|q''|\le Q^C.
\]

Thus the \(L^{-r}\) losses cancel.

---

# 4. Required scale-invariant package

For every polynomial interval

\[
J\subset I^\ast,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C}|I^\ast|,
\]

require

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |J|^k |\partial^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le 6.
}
\]

This implies:

\[
|q'|\le Q^C L^{-1},
\]

\[
|q''|\le Q^C L^{-2},
\]

\[
|q'''|\le Q^C L^{-3},
\]

and so on.

But the identities contain fixed coefficients:

\[
q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

So if \(L\ll1\), then \(q''\) may be much larger than \(q\). That is fine; the integral rigidity proof estimates actual \(u=q''\), and the cutoff terms scale consistently.

The integral rigidity lemma should then be stated with the correct scale:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}\int_{J'} 1\,dm,
}
\]

provided the identities hold in the same coordinate and the scale-invariant package is available.

---

# 5. Check the kinetic estimate with scale \(L\)

Let \(L=|J|\). Choose \(\phi\) supported in \(J\), equal to \(1\) on \(J'\), with

\[
|\phi'|\le C L^{-1},
\qquad
|\phi''|\le C L^{-2}.
\]

In the kinetic estimate, after integration by parts, we encounter

\[
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

Estimate each term.

### Term 1

\[
\int |g||\phi''s_\delta|
\le
\varepsilon L^{-2}|J|
=
\varepsilon L^{-1}.
\]

This looks dangerous compared with the desired right side \(Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|\). Since \(|J|=L\), the desired bound is

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}L.
\]

So we need

\[
\varepsilon L^{-1}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}L,
\]

i.e.

\[
L^{-2}\le Q^C\delta^{-3}.
\]

If \(L=Q^{-S}\), this can fail unless \(\delta\) is very small or \(Q^C\) absorbs \(L^{-2}\).

This reveals a genuine issue: scale-invariant derivative bounds alone do not remove cutoff derivative losses from terms involving \(\phi''\). The cutoff itself creates an \(L^{-2}\) cost independent of \(q\).

---

# 6. Repair: choose \(J'\) with soft cutoff at a fixed relative scale and include \(L^{-2}\)

The integral rigidity lemma on a short interval must include a scale factor:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon^{1/3}
+
\varepsilon L^{-p}
\right)|J'|.
\]

But if \(L\) depends on \(S\), this reintroduces exponent dependence.

Alternative: avoid cutoff derivatives by using an interval \(J'\) whose boundary is chosen so boundary terms are small, rather than using an arbitrary smooth cutoff.

This is a standard one-dimensional trick.

---

# 7. Boundary-selection version

Instead of a fixed cutoff, integrate on a subinterval

\[
K=(a,b)\subset J
\]

with endpoints chosen from a good set. Since \(|g|\le\varepsilon\) and \(|h|\le\varepsilon\) throughout \(J\), we can choose \(a,b\) such that boundary quantities involving \(q',F(q),g'\) are not too large on average.

But integration by parts of \(g''\) produces boundary terms:

\[
\int_K s_\delta(q)g''
=
[s_\delta(q)g']_a^b
-
\int_K s_\delta'(q)q'g'.
\]

This uses \(g'\), which may not be small. Integrating twice with compact cutoff avoided \(g'\) boundary terms but introduced \(L^{-2}\).

Boundary selection can control \(g'\) if we have an \(L^2\) or \(L^1\) bound for \(g'\), but not from \(|g|\le\varepsilon\) alone.

So cutoff derivatives may be unavoidable unless D1 gives a longer interval independent of \(S\), or unless the extraction is modified.

---

# 8. Better repair: extract moderate \(S\), not arbitrarily large

We do not need to send \(S\to\infty\). We need only one \(S\) satisfying the closure inequality.

If \(L\sim Q^{-S-C_F}\), then cutoff loss \(L^{-2}\) contributes roughly \(Q^{2S}\).

With the conservative integral rigidity exponent \(1/3\), this would be fatal:

\[
Q^{2S}\varepsilon^{1/3}=Q^{2S}Q^{-S/3}=Q^{5S/3}.
\]

So the naive cutoff proof cannot tolerate \(L\sim Q^{-S}\).

This means the earlier thickening method that shrinks \(J\) according to \(F\)-smallness is too expensive for the cutoff proof.

We need a different extraction method: produce an interval \(J\) of length independent of \(S\), or at least with length loss coefficient \(<1/(2\cdot3)\), not \(1\).

---

# 9. Use integral rigidity directly from pointwise smallness plus Lipschitz? No.

The two-threshold extraction grew the small-anisotropy point by Lipschitz:

\[
r_F\sim Q^{-S-C_F}|I|.
\]

This necessarily shrinks with \(S\). If the rigidity proof requires cutoff derivatives on this same interval, the exponent fails.

Thus we need either:

1. a cutoff-free integral rigidity proof whose constants do not depend badly on \(|J|\);
2. a stronger extraction that gives small anisotropy on a longer interval;
3. a version of integral rigidity that works on very short intervals after rescaling with appropriately rescaled identities.

Option 3 is likely the right one: the identities must be expressed in the local coordinate adapted to \(J\), not the original one.

---

# 10. Rescaled identities on \(J\)

Let

\[
m=m_J+Lx.
\]

Define

\[
Q_J(x)=q(m_J+Lx).
\]

Then

\[
Q_J''(x)=L^2q''(m_J+Lx)=L^2u.
\]

The identity

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

becomes

\[
L^2g
=
Q_J''-L^2(6Q_J-2Q_J^3).
\]

So define rescaled quantities:

\[
u_J=Q_J''=L^2u,
\]

\[
g_J=L^2g,
\]

\[
F_J(Q)=L^2(6Q-2Q^3).
\]

Then

\[
g_J=u_J-F_J(Q).
\]

Similarly, \(h\) rescales more delicately. Since

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

in \(x\)-coordinates:

\[
q'=L^{-1}Q_J',
\]

\[
g''=L^{-2}g_J''/L^2? 
\]

Carefully:

\[
g(m)=L^{-2}g_J(x).
\]

Then

\[
\frac{d^2}{dm^2}g(m)
=
L^{-4}g_J''(x).
\]

So

\[
h
=
2Q_J(L^{-1}Q_J')^2
-\frac16L^{-4}g_J''.
\]

Multiply by \(L^4\):

\[
L^4h
=
2L^2Q_J(Q_J')^2-\frac16g_J''.
\]

Define

\[
h_J=L^4h.
\]

Then

\[
h_J=2L^2Q_J(Q_J')^2-\frac16g_J''.
\]

Now the kinetic positive term has coefficient \(L^2\), which weakens control of \((Q_J')^2\) by \(L^{-2}\). This is exactly the scale issue in another form.

Thus, on very short intervals, \(h\)-smallness gives weak kinetic control unless \(h\) is small enough by \(L^{-4}\).

But from extraction, \(h\le Q^{-S}\), and \(L\sim Q^{-S}\), so

\[
h_J=L^4h\sim Q^{-5S},
\]

very small. The coefficient \(L^2\) in front of kinetic is \(Q^{-2S}\), so the effective kinetic smallness is \(Q^{-3S}\), maybe enough. Need compute.

---

# 11. Rescaled rigidity estimate

In \(x\)-coordinates, the smallness is:

\[
|g_J|\le L^2\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|h_J|\le L^4\varepsilon.
\]

The identity is:

\[
g_J=u_J-L^2F(Q),
\]

\[
h_J=2L^2Q(Q')^2-\frac16g_J''.
\]

The target is

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
=
L^{-3}\int |u_J|^2\,dx
\]

because \(u=L^{-2}u_J\), \(dm=Ldx\).

If rescaled rigidity gives

\[
\int |u_J|^2
\le
Q^C (L^2\varepsilon)^{\alpha} L^{\beta},
\]

we need translate back.

This becomes messy, but it suggests the rigidity lemma must be stated in scale-aware form, not naive fixed-coordinate form.

---

# 12. Current conclusion: target-smallness extraction and rigidity must be scale-coupled

The previous Gate 2 package was too optimistic if \(J\) shrinks like \(Q^{-S}\) and the rigidity proof uses cutoffs in the original coordinate.

The correct theorem should couple:

\[
\varepsilon=\sup_J(|g|+|h|)
\]

and

\[
L=|J|.
\]

A scale-aware rigidity lemma should look like:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C \mathcal R(\varepsilon,L)|J'|.
}
\]

Then Gate 2 closes if

\[
\mathcal R(Q^{-S},Q^{-C_J(S)})\ll Q^{-2C_1}.
\]

The earlier simple form

\[
\mathcal R=\varepsilon^{1/3}
\]

is valid only when \(L\) is \(O(1)\) in the coordinate of the identities, or when derivative/cutoff losses are scale-invariant in a stronger way than currently shown.

---

# 13. Revised attack target

The next exact target is:

## Scale-Aware Integral Rigidity Lemma

Let \(J\) have length \(L\). Assume on \(J\):

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon.
\]

Prove an estimate

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C
\left[
\delta^2
+
\varepsilon\delta^{-4}L^{-p}
+
\text{scale terms}
\right]
|J'|
}
\]

with the optimal \(p\) determined by integration by parts.

Then combine with the extraction relation

\[
L\sim \min(Q^{-C_u},Q^{-S-C_F})|I|.
\]

This will give the true exponent condition.

If \(p\) is too large, the two-threshold method fails and we need a different extraction producing longer intervals.

---

# 14. Possible rescue: use averaged smallness instead of sup smallness

Instead of extracting a very short interval where \(g,h\) are uniformly tiny, use a larger interval where the weighted average

\[
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)
\]

is tiny. The integral rigidity proof might be adaptable to \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\), avoiding small interval cutoffs.

This may be better:

Gate 2 failure already gives integral smallness on all of \(I\). We may not need pointwise smallness.

A direct Gate 2 rigidity theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\Rightarrow
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

proved by contradiction using \(L^2\)-small weighted \(g,h\), not pointwise extraction.

But that is a larger real-variable problem.

---

# 15. Verdict of this attack

The integral rigidity lemma is locally valid on a fixed normalized interval, but when combined with two-threshold extraction, interval length dependence becomes a serious exponent issue.

Therefore the correct next attack is one of:

1. **prove a scale-aware integral rigidity lemma** and check exponents;
2. **derive a longer interval extraction** that does not shrink like \(Q^{-S}\);
3. **prove an averaged integral rigidity theorem** directly from Gate 2 failure, avoiding pointwise interval extraction.

This is a real issue, not bookkeeping.

The most promising next move is the scale-aware rigidity lemma, because it is closest to the existing proof.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:18:39)

I’ll focus on repairing the scale issue in Gate 2. The previous two-threshold interval proof creates a short interval whose cutoff losses may overwhelm the \(\varepsilon^{1/3}\) gain, so the next attack is to avoid shrinking by the anisotropy target.

_Thought for 35s_

## Continuing attack — replace pointwise extraction by source-interval \(L^2\) rigidity

The previous Gate 2 route had a scale problem:

\[
\text{small anisotropy target }Q^{-S}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{short interval }|J|\sim Q^{-S},
\]

and then cutoff derivatives in the integral-rigidity proof can lose powers of \(|J|^{-1}\), potentially overwhelming the \(\varepsilon^{1/3}\) gain.

There is a cleaner repair:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not thicken the anisotropy-small point.}
}
\]

Instead:

1. Use Gate 1 and \(|u'|\) to get a **source-large interval** \(J\) whose length depends only on the source threshold, not on anisotropy smallness.
2. Use Gate 2 failure to get **\(L^2\)-smallness** of \(g,h\) on that whole interval.
3. Prove an **\(L^2\)-input integral rigidity lemma**, not a pointwise-input lemma.

This avoids generic Remez and avoids interval length shrinking with the anisotropy exponent. It is now the strongest Gate 2 route I see.

---

# 1. Source-large interval from Gate 1

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume the local source upper bound

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_0}
\]

and Lipschitz bound

\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

There exists \(m_\ast\in I\) with

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

By Lipschitz control, on an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

centered at \(m_\ast\), or one-sided near the boundary, with

\[
|J|\ge c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
=
Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau\ge Q^{-B/2-O(1)}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

This interval length is independent of the target anisotropy smallness exponent \(A\).

That is the key repair.

---

# 2. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on \(J\)

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
g=\Gamma_G,\qquad h=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Since on \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau,
\]

we get

\[
\tau^2\int_J F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_J (g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\). Since

\[
|J|\ge \tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we get

\[
\frac1{|J|}
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}\tau^{-3}Q^{C_u+O(1)}.
\]

With

\[
\tau=Q^{-B/2-O(1)},
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

So Gate 2 failure gives normalized \(L^2\)-smallness:

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
}
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

This is a much better extraction output than a dust-like set or a tiny pointwise interval.

---

# 3. Needed replacement lemma: \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

The previous integral rigidity lemma assumed

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon.
\]

We now need the \(L^2\) version:

## \(L^2\) Gate 2 Integral Rigidity Lemma

Assume on an interval \(J\),

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume polynomial local bounds on \(q,q',q''\) and the required cutoff margins.

Then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|
}
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\).

I expect the safe exponent to degrade but remain positive. Even \(c=1/4\) or \(c=1/6\) would be enough, because \(\varepsilon\) can be made polynomially small by taking the Gate 2 contradiction exponent \(A\) large.

---

# 4. Check \(L^2\)-kinetic estimate

Normalize \(J=(-2,2)\), \(J'=(-1,1)\).

Assume

\[
\|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le\varepsilon.
\]

Start from

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Multiply by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q)
\]

as before.

The \(h\)-term is now bounded by Cauchy–Schwarz:

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi s_\delta(q)\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Then

\[
\left|\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
\|g\|_2\|(\phi s_\delta(q))''\|_2.
\]

We have

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The first, second, and fourth terms are bounded in \(L^2\) by

\[
Q^C\delta^{-1}.
\]

The third term is the dangerous one:

\[
\|\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2.
\]

On the transition set \(\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta\),

\[
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

So

\[
\|\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2
\le
C\delta^{-2}\|(q')^2\|_{L^2(\delta\le|q|\le2\delta)}.
\]

Using polynomial \(L^\infty\) bounds on \(q'\), this is

\[
\le Q^C\delta^{-2}.
\]

This gives

\[
\left|\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}.
\]

Thus the positive kinetic term satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}.
}
\]

Dividing by \(|q|\ge2\delta\) gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
}
\]

This is actually comparable to the sharp pointwise version.

The price is that we used \(L^\infty\) bounds on \(q'\), which are polynomial and acceptable.

---

# 5. \(L^2\)-potential estimate

As before, set

\[
X=\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Use

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Then

\[
X
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is now

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g\right|
\le
\|g\|_2 X^{1/2}
\le
\varepsilon X^{1/2}.
\]

This can be absorbed as

\[
\varepsilon X^{1/2}\le \frac14X+C\varepsilon^2.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

The \(F'\) and transition terms are bounded by the kinetic estimate:

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The cutoff term is

\[
T=\left|\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|.
\]

Using \(\phi=\psi^2\) again,

\[
T
\le
Q^C X^{1/2}
\left(\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}
\le
Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-3})^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb:

\[
T\le \frac14X+Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

So on \(|q|\ge3\delta\),

\[
\int F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

---

# 6. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
\int_{|q|\le3\delta}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\delta^2+\int |g|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

---

# 7. Combine and optimize

Large-\(|q|\):

\[
\int |u|^2
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Small-\(|q|\):

\[
\int |u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Balance

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^5=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This recovers the sharper \(2/5\) exponent in the \(L^2\)-input version.

This is a major improvement.

---

# 8. Gate 2 contradiction using \(L^2\)-input rigidity

From the source interval extraction,

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\]

on \(J\), with

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-B/2-O(1)}.
\]

So on \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

The \(L^2\)-input rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Recall

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

So contradiction follows if

\[
-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+C
<
-B.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A>
\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+O(C).
}
\]

The exact coefficient is not important. It is finite and polynomial.

Therefore Gate 2 closes under the \(L^2\)-input rigidity theorem.

---

# 9. Major simplification

This route eliminates the earlier scale issue completely:

- We extract a source-large interval using only \(u\), whose length depends on the source threshold, not anisotropy smallness.
- Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on that interval.
- \(L^2\)-integral rigidity handles the rest.

So we no longer need:

\[
\text{pointwise anisotropy smallness on a tiny interval},
\]

or

\[
\text{Remez/Cartan propagation},
\]

or

\[
\text{D2 pointwise derivative propagation}.
\]

The new Gate 2 proof is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{source interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Current theorem

## \(L^2\) Gate 2 Integral Rigidity Lemma

If

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This uses:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\), and standard cutoffs.

## Gate 2 Theorem

Gate 1 plus canonical local bounds imply Gate 2, by contradiction, using the source interval and the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma.

---

# 11. Verdict

This is the strongest Gate 2 attack so far.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 appears locally provable from Gate 1 using }L^2\text{-integral rigidity.}
}
\]

The old G2-A/G2-B pointwise route is superseded by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-integral rigidity}.
}
\]

The remaining work is to formalize the \(L^2\) cutoff estimates and canonical derivative bounds.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:20:36)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — stress-test the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma

The \(L^2\)-input version is the best Gate 2 route so far:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

I’ll now stress-test the proof carefully. The point where it could fail is the kinetic estimate: when we integrate

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

against a sign cutoff, the term

\[
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''
\]

contains \((q')^2\) inside the cutoff derivative. In the \(L^\infty\)-small proof this required absorption. In the \(L^2\)-small proof, we can instead use polynomial \(L^\infty\) bounds for \(q'\) and \(q''\). That gives a robust kinetic estimate and preserves the \(2/5\) exponent. This is the key local estimate needed for the Gate 2 simplification described in the latest handoff. 

---

# 1. Normalized lemma

Work on

\[
J=(-2,2),\qquad J'=(-1,1).
\]

Assume

\[
\|g\|_{2}+\|h\|_{2}\le \varepsilon,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Assume polynomial local bounds

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le M,
\qquad
M\le Q^C.
\]

Claim:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
}
\]

This is the improved \(L^2\)-input rigidity estimate.

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate

Choose \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(J)\), \(\phi=1\) on a slightly smaller interval containing \(J'\), and \(0\le\phi\le1\).

Choose a smooth sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) with

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)\quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
|s_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by \(\phi s_\delta(q)\):

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=|q|.
\]

So the positive term dominates

\[
2\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term is controlled by Cauchy–Schwarz:

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi s_\delta(q)\|_2
\le Q^C\varepsilon.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Compute

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

Each term is controlled in \(L^2\):

\[
\|\phi''s_\delta\|_2\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'\|_2
\le Q^C\delta^{-1},
\]

\[
\|\phi s_\delta'(q)q''\|_2
\le Q^C\delta^{-1},
\]

and

\[
\|\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2
\le Q^C\delta^{-2}.
\]

The last estimate uses

\[
\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore

\[
\left|\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
\|g\|_2\,\|(\phi s_\delta(q))''\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}.
}
\]

Since \(|q|\ge2\delta\) in that region,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
}
\]

This is the key improvement over the conservative pointwise proof.

---

# 3. Potential estimate

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad (|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Set

\[
X=\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
X
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term satisfies

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g\right|
\le
\|g\|_2X^{1/2}
\le
\varepsilon X^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb later using

\[
\varepsilon X^{1/2}\le \frac14X+C\varepsilon^2.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'
=
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)
+
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

The \(F'\)-term is bounded by kinetic control:

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The transition term is supported on

\[
2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta.
\]

There

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\qquad
|\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Hence

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)q'\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The cutoff term

\[
T=\left|\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|
\]

is handled by taking \(\phi=\psi^2\), so

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi.
\]

Then

\[
T
\le
Q^C
\left(\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

So

\[
T\le
Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-3})^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb:

\[
T\le \frac14X+Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

Combining all terms gives

\[
X
\le
\frac12X+Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(|q|\) region

On \(|q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

we get

\[
|u|^2\le 2F(q)^2+2g^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\delta^2+\|g\|_2^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

---

# 5. Combine and optimize

On the large-\(|q|\) region,

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2,
\]

so

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

On the small region,

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Optimize:

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^5=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
}
\]

This proves the sharper exponent \(2/5\) in the \(L^2\)-input version.

---

# 6. Residual version

If the identities have residuals

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

with

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le \varepsilon,
\]

then absorb them into the definitions:

\[
\tilde g=g-r_g,
\qquad
\tilde h=h-r_h,
\]

or track them as additional \(L^2\)-small terms. The same estimates survive with a larger \(Q^C\) constant, because every occurrence of \(g,h\) is controlled in \(L^2\).

Thus the lemma is stable under \(L^2\)-small structural residuals.

---

# 7. Gate 2 consequence

From Gate 1 and source interval extraction, obtain \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

where

\[
\tau\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A/2+O(B+C_u)}.
\]

The \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

But \(|u|\ge\tau\) on \(J'\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
\tau^2|J'|
\ge Q^{-2C_\tau}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<Q^{-2C_\tau}.
\]

This is achieved by taking the Gate 2 contradiction exponent \(A\) sufficiently large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + source interval extraction + }L^2\text{-integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. What is needed for source interval extraction

This improved proof does **not** require pointwise smallness of \(g,h\) on \(J\). It only needs \(L^2\)-smallness on a source-large interval.

Source extraction requires:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|;
   \]

2. a point or interval where \(|u|\) is non-small, using \(|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}\);

3. Gate 2 failure to imply

   \[
   \int_J(g^2+h^2)\le \varepsilon^2|J|
   \]

   because \(|u|\ge\tau\) on \(J\).

This is all much simpler than the old two-threshold pointwise anisotropy extraction.

---

# 9. Final status of Gate 2

The Gate 2 proof now rests on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-large interval extraction}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity with exponent }2/5.
}
\]

This removes the old D1/D2 Remez/derivative-propagation issues and also improves the exponent.

The remaining checks are:

1. polynomial derivative bounds for \(u\) to get a source-large interval;
2. polynomial bounds for \(q,q',q''\) in the rigidity lemma;
3. canonical residuals are \(L^2\)-small or exactly absent.

This is a much stronger and cleaner Gate 2 route.
