## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:21:35)

I’ll now stress-test the source-large interval extraction. The hidden issue is whether the interval where \(|u|\) is uniformly large can also be chosen so that \(g,h\) are \(L^2\)-small.

_Thought for 18s_

## Continuing attack — repair source-interval extraction for \(L^2\)-rigidity

The \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma is now the best Gate 2 mechanism:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

But the extraction step needs a careful repair. It is not enough to find **some** interval where \(|u|\) is large. We need an interval \(J\) where:

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\le \varepsilon^2.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives global weighted smallness:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

so we must select a source-large interval that also has small anisotropy average. This is the next extraction problem. It is still local and tractable. The downstream package currently depends on exactly this kind of extraction plus the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},\qquad g=\Gamma_G,\qquad h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
F^2=g^2+h^2.
\]

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume the local source Lipschitz bound

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

We want to produce an interval \(J\subset I\) with:

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
\int_J F^2\le Q^{-S}|J|.
\]

---

# 2. Choose a source threshold with mass

Pick a threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-T}
\]

by dyadic pigeonholing so that

\[
U_{\rm hi}:=\{|u|\ge 2\tau\}
\]

carries polynomial \(u\)-mass:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{U_{\rm hi}} |u|^2\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|.
}
\]

This can be done with \(T=O(B+C_0)\) if

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0}.
\]

Since on \(U_{\rm hi}\),

\[
|u|^2\ge4\tau^2,
\]

we also get a measure lower bound

\[
|U_{\rm hi}|\ge Q^{-C_M}\|u\|_\infty^{-2}|I|
\]

if needed, but the weighted mass lower bound is the more useful statement.

---

# 3. Local source intervals around high-source points

For any \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\), define

\[
r_u=c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\]

with \(c>0\) small. Then for

\[
|x-m|\le r_u,
\]

we have

\[
|u(x)-u(m)|
\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}r_u
\le c\tau.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|u(x)|\ge \tau
}
\]

on the local interval

\[
J_m=[m-r_u,m+r_u]\cap I.
\]

So each high-source point generates a source-large interval of length at least polynomial, except for boundary truncation.

The remaining question is: can we choose one such \(J_m\) with small \(F\)-average?

---

# 4. Weighted averaging selects a good source interval

Use a covering/averaging argument.

Let \(r=r_u\). Consider the local averages

\[
\mathcal A(m)=\int_{J_m} F^2(x)\,dx.
\]

Integrate \(\mathcal A(m)\) over \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\) with weight \(|u(m)|^2\):

\[
\int_{U_{\rm hi}} |u(m)|^2\mathcal A(m)\,dm
=
\int_I F^2(x)
\left(
\int_{U_{\rm hi}\cap[x-r,x+r]} |u(m)|^2\,dm
\right)dx.
\]

The inner integral is bounded by

\[
\int_{|m-x|\le r}|u(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

By Lipschitz and local upper bounds, this is at most polynomially comparable to \(r\) times a local source upper bound. But this expression is not immediately controlled by the global weighted Gate 2 quantity

\[
\int |u(x)|^2F^2(x)\,dx
\]

because the weight is \(|u(m)|^2\), not \(|u(x)|^2\).

However, if \(x\in J_m\), then \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\) implies

\[
|u(x)|\ge \tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
F^2(x)
\le \tau^{-2}|u(x)|^2F^2(x)
\]

on every \(x\in J_m\).

Thus for each \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\),

\[
\int_{J_m}F^2
\le
\tau^{-2}\int_{J_m}|u|^2F^2.
\]

Now average over \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\):

If every \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\) had

\[
\int_{J_m}F^2 > \eta |J_m|,
\]

then since \(|J_m|\asymp r\) except near boundary, we would obtain

\[
\int_{J_m}|u|^2F^2
>
\tau^2\eta r
\]

for every such \(m\). A Vitali-disjoint subcollection of the \(J_m\)'s covering a fixed fraction of \(U_{\rm hi}\) then forces a global lower bound on

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2,
\]

contradicting Gate 2 failure if \(\eta\) is too large.

So there exists at least one source interval \(J\) with

\[
\boxed{
\int_JF^2\le \eta |J|
}
\]

where

\[
\eta
\]

is polynomially small once \(A\) is large.

Let us make this quantitative.

---

# 5. Quantitative Vitali selection

Choose a maximal disjoint family

\[
\{J_{m_j}\}_{j=1}^N
\]

with centers \(m_j\in U_{\rm hi}\). Then the expanded intervals \(3J_{m_j}\) cover \(U_{\rm hi}\).

Since each \(J_{m_j}\) is source-large:

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J_{m_j}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J_{m_j}}F^2
\le
\tau^{-2}\int_{J_{m_j}}|u|^2F^2.
\]

Suppose, for contradiction, that all selected intervals satisfy

\[
\int_{J_{m_j}}F^2>\eta |J_{m_j}|.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{J_{m_j}}|u|^2F^2
>
\tau^2\eta |J_{m_j}|.
\]

Summing over disjoint intervals:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2
\ge
\tau^2\eta\sum_j |J_{m_j}|.
\]

We need a lower bound on

\[
\sum_j |J_{m_j}|.
\]

Because \(3J_{m_j}\) cover \(U_{\rm hi}\),

\[
|U_{\rm hi}|
\le
\sum_j |3J_{m_j}|
\le
3\sum_j |J_{m_j}|.
\]

Thus

\[
\sum_j|J_{m_j}|\ge \frac13|U_{\rm hi}|.
\]

If \(U_{\rm hi}\) has measure lower bound

\[
|U_{\rm hi}|\ge Q^{-C_U}|I|,
\]

then

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2
\ge
\frac13\tau^2\eta Q^{-C_U}|I|.
\]

But Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
\eta>3Q^{-A}\tau^{-2}Q^{C_U},
\]

a contradiction follows. Hence some selected interval satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_JF^2
\le
3Q^{-A}\tau^{-2}Q^{C_U}.
}
\]

Since \(\tau=Q^{-T}\), this is

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_JF^2
\le
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{-A/2+T+C_U/2+O(1)}|J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

This is exactly the \(L^2\)-input needed for integral rigidity.

---

# 6. Lower bound for \(|U_{\rm hi}|\)

We used

\[
|U_{\rm hi}|\ge Q^{-C_U}|I|.
\]

This follows from

\[
\int_{U_{\rm hi}}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|
\]

and

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
\int_{U_{\rm hi}}|u|^2
\le
Q^{2C_0}|U_{\rm hi}|,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
|U_{\rm hi}|\ge Q^{-C_M-2C_0}|I|.
}
\]

Thus

\[
C_U=C_M+2C_0.
\]

---

# 7. Final extraction theorem

## Source-Large \(L^2\)-Anisotropy Interval Extraction

Assume:

\[
\int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2F^2\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0},
\]

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-T-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-T-O(1)}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)
\le
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
}
\]

Here \(T\) is a dyadic source threshold exponent selected so that \(U_{\rm hi}\) carries polynomial source mass.

This is the precise extraction needed for \(L^2\)-integral rigidity.

---

# 8. Combine with \(L^2\)-integral rigidity

Let

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-A/2+T+C_U/2+O(1)}.
\]

The \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Extraction gives

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-T-O(1)}
\]

on \(J'\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-2T-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<Q^{-2T-O(1)}.
\]

Substitute \(\varepsilon\):

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-A/5+\frac{2T}{5}+\frac{C_U}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Need

\[
-A/5+\frac{2T}{5}+\frac{C_U}{5}+C
<
-2T.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A>12T+C_U+O(C).
}
\]

Since \(T\) is polynomially bounded in terms of Gate 1/source upper exponents, this is achievable by choosing the Gate 2 contradiction exponent \(A\) large.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + source extraction + }L^2\text{-integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 9. This fixes the scale problem

This extraction avoids demanding pointwise anisotropy smallness on an interval. The interval length depends only on the source threshold and \(u'\), not on anisotropy smallness.

Anisotropy smallness enters only as an \(L^2\)-average on \(J\), which the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma can use directly.

Therefore the earlier \(C_R(S)\) scale trap is gone.

The route is now stable:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
\Rightarrow
\text{source-large intervals}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{one source-large interval has }L^2\text{-small anisotropy}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
L^2\text{-integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
u\text{ small on a subinterval}
}
\]

contradiction.

---

# 10. Remaining assumptions

The Gate 2 proof now needs only:

1. \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0}\);
2. \(\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}\);
3. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity with exponent \(2/5\);
4. polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\) for the rigidity lemma.

No Remez, no component count, no pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\) propagation.

This is a major simplification.

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem using source intervals and \(L^2\)-rigidity

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: replace the older pointwise target-smallness Gate 2 package with the newer route

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{source-large interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This supersedes the earlier D1/D2 formulation based on pointwise Remez/derivative propagation. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Set

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

We prove Gate 2 by contradiction.

---

# 2. Assume Gate 2 failure

Assume

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume the local source bounds

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_0},
\]

\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

---

# 3. Source-large interval extraction

Choose a dyadic threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-T}
\]

so that

\[
U_{\rm hi}:=\{|u|\ge 2\tau\}
\]

carries polynomial source mass:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{U_{\rm hi}}|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C_M}|I|.
}
\]

Such a threshold exists by dyadic pigeonholing from Gate 1 and the upper bound \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0}\). In the simplest coarse bookkeeping, one may take \(T=O(B+C_0)\).

Since

\[
\int_{U_{\rm hi}}|u|^2\,dm\le Q^{2C_0}|U_{\rm hi}|,
\]

we also get

\[
\boxed{
|U_{\rm hi}|\ge Q^{-C_U}|I|,
\qquad
C_U=C_M+2C_0.
}
\]

For every \(m\in U_{\rm hi}\), define a source interval

\[
J_m=[m-r,m+r]\cap I,
\]

where

\[
r=c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|.
\]

By the Lipschitz bound on \(u\), if \(c>0\) is sufficiently small, then on \(J_m\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau.
}
\]

Thus each high-source point generates a polynomial-length source-large interval.

---

# 4. Select a source interval with small average anisotropy

Choose a maximal disjoint subcollection

\[
\{J_{m_j}\}_{j=1}^N
\]

with centers \(m_j\in U_{\rm hi}\). The enlarged intervals \(3J_{m_j}\) cover \(U_{\rm hi}\), hence

\[
\sum_j |J_{m_j}|\ge c|U_{\rm hi}|
\ge Q^{-C_U-O(1)}|I|.
\]

On each \(J_{m_j}\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau,
\]

so

\[
\int_{J_{m_j}} F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}
\int_{J_{m_j}} |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm.
\]

Suppose every selected interval had

\[
\frac1{|J_{m_j}|}\int_{J_{m_j}}F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
>
\eta.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{J_{m_j}} |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
>
\tau^2\eta |J_{m_j}|.
\]

Summing over disjoint \(J_{m_j}\),

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
>
\tau^2\eta\sum_j |J_{m_j}|
\ge
Q^{-2T}\eta Q^{-C_U-O(1)}|I|.
\]

But Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore some selected source interval \(J\) satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J (g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
}
\]

Also, on this same \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-T}.
}
\]

And the interval length satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-T-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
}
\]

This is the desired source-large interval extraction.

---

# 5. Define the \(L^2\)-smallness parameter

Set

\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-A/2+T+C_U/2+O(1)}.
\]

The harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor can be absorbed into the final exponent.

---

# 6. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Use the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

## Lemma

Assume on \(J\)

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

with

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and local polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\). Then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

The exponent \(2/5\) comes from the multiplier \(q\chi_\delta(q)\) against \(h\), the kinetic estimate

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

and the optimization

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

This avoids the older pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\)-propagation problem entirely.

---

# 7. Contradiction

Since

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-T}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

we also have on \(J'\subset J\)

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-2T}|J'|.
}
\]

But \(L^2\)-rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Substitute

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-A/2+T+C_U/2+O(1)}.
\]

Then

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-A/5+\frac{2T}{5}+\frac{C_U}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

So the upper bound is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-A/5+\frac{2T}{5}+\frac{C_U}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
\]

Contradiction with

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-2T}|J'|
\]

if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{2T}{5}+\frac{C_U}{5}+O(1)<-2T.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A>12T+C_U+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

Thus, choosing the Gate 2 contradiction exponent \(A\) sufficiently large relative to the source threshold and local-complexity constants, Gate 2 failure is impossible.

---

# 8. Final Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 from source interval extraction and \(L^2\)-rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Source bounds:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_0},
\qquad
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. Local polynomial rigidity bounds on \(q,q',q''\).

4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for all sufficiently large polynomial exponents \(A\), for instance any

\[
\boxed{
A>12T+C_U+5C_R+O(1)
}
\]

with \(T,C_U\) chosen as above.

---

# 9. What this replaces

This theorem replaces the old active pair

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez Propagation},
\]

\[
D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}.
\]

It also improves on the intermediate pointwise target-smallness package. The active Gate 2 package is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-large interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

No Remez, no Cartan, and no pointwise control of \(\Gamma_G''\) is required.

---

# 10. Remaining proof obligations

The Gate 2 proof is now local and finite, but still needs these checks:

1. **Source bounds**

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty,\quad \|u'\|_\infty
   \]

   from canonical ordinary local complexity.

2. **Primitive bounds**

   Polynomial control of

   \[
   q,\quad q',\quad q''
   \]

   for the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma.

3. **Rigidity cutoff proof**

   Finalize the \(q\chi_\delta(q)\)-multiplier proof and verify residual terms if the identities are approximate.

4. **Coordinate normalization**

   All derivatives and interval lengths must use the same local coordinate.

---

# 11. Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now reduced to a concrete }L^2\text{ real-variable lemma plus canonical local bounds.}
}
\]

The previous broad D1/D2 inputs should be demoted to historical/fallback status.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:33:36)

_Thought for 17s_

## Continuing attack — remove primitive-bound dependence from Gate 2 where possible

The current Gate 2 proof needs the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

The proof assumed polynomial bounds on

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q''.
\]

The next possible failure point is whether \(q,q'\) are genuinely available from canonical local complexity, or whether Gate 2 needs separate primitive/basepoint assumptions. I’ll attack that dependence.

---

# 1. Can \(q\) be bounded from \(u\) and \(g\)?

Recall

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

so

\[
F(q):=6q-2q^3=u-g.
\]

If we know

\[
|u|\le Q^{C_u}
\]

pointwise and

\[
|g|\le Q^{C_g}
\]

pointwise, then

\[
|F(q)|\le Q^C.
\]

Since

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

large \(|q|\) gives

\[
|F(q)|\asymp |q|^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|q|\le Q^C.
}
\]

But in the improved Gate 2 route we only get

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

not pointwise \(g\)-small. So the direct pointwise bound for \(q\) is not immediate.

However, the integral rigidity proof does not really need \(q\) bounded by an externally supplied constant everywhere. It uses \(q\) through cutoffs \(s_\delta(q),\chi_\delta(q)\), and the dangerous region is large \(|q|\). On that region, \(F(q)^2\) itself controls \(q\). So one can replace a global \(|q|\le Q^C\) assumption by a combination of:

\[
|u|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|g\|_2\le \varepsilon,
\]

and the potential estimate.

This suggests \(q\)-boundedness is not a fundamental separate input.

---

# 2. Avoiding global \(q\)-bounds in the kinetic estimate

The kinetic estimate multiplies

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q).
\]

The main term is

\[
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2.
\]

Because \(s_\delta(q)q\ge0\), this term is positive:

\[
2\int \phi |q|(q')^2
\quad \text{on } |q|\ge 2\delta.
\]

No upper bound on \(q\) is needed here.

The \(h\)-term satisfies

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi s_\delta(q)\|_2.
\]

Since

\[
|s_\delta|\le1,
\]

no upper bound on \(q\) is needed.

The \(g''\)-term after integration by parts is

\[
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expanding,

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The first term needs no \(q\)-bound.

The second and third need control of \(q'\).

The fourth needs \(q''=u\), which is already source-controlled.

So the real primitive issue is \(q'\), not \(q\).

---

# 3. Can \(q'\) be bounded from \(h\)-smallness?

The identity

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

controls \(q(q')^2\), not \(q'\), and degenerates near

\[
q=0.
\]

Near \(q=0\), however, the cutoff transition method avoids dividing by \(q\); the \(q'\)-dependence appears in cutoff derivatives. In the \(L^2\)-input proof, we bounded

\[
\|\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2
\]

using

\[
\|q'\|_\infty.
\]

This is the main remaining primitive dependence.

Can we avoid \(\|q'\|_\infty\)? Maybe partially.

On the transition region

\[
\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta,
\]

we used

\[
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

Then

\[
\int |g|\,|s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\]

appears. Instead of bounding \((q')^2\) by \(\|q'\|_\infty^2\), try to absorb it into the positive kinetic term:

\[
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
\delta^{-1}\int_{\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

But the coefficient is

\[
|g|\,\delta^{-2}.
\]

With \(g\in L^2\), not \(L^\infty\), we cannot simply absorb pointwise. Use Cauchy–Schwarz:

\[
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}|g|\delta^{-2}(q')^2
\le
\delta^{-2}\|g\|_2
\|(q')^2\|_{L^2(\delta\le |q|\le2\delta)}.
\]

This requires \(q'\in L^4\), not just the kinetic \(L^2\) quantity. One can interpolate \(L^4\) from \(L^2\) plus \(H^1\), but that introduces \(q''=u\), which is controlled. This might remove the need for \(\|q'\|_\infty\).

---

# 4. Alternative \(L^4\) transition control

Let

\[
K_\delta=\{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\}.
\]

We need to bound

\[
\|(q')^2\|_{L^2(K_\delta)}
=
\|q'\|_{L^4(K_\delta)}^2.
\]

In one dimension,

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4(K_\delta)}^2
\le
\|q'\|_{L^2(K_\delta)}
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(K_\delta)}.
\]

But this still uses \(L^\infty\).

Use Gagliardo–Nirenberg:

\[
\|q'\|_{L^4}^2
\lesssim
\|q'\|_{L^2}^{3/2}\|q''\|_{L^2}^{1/2}
+
\|q'\|_{L^2}^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=u,
\]

and on the source interval \(u\) is bounded above polynomially, \(\|u\|_2\le Q^C\), this yields

\[
\|(q')^2\|_2
\lesssim
\|q'\|_2^{3/2}Q^{C/2}
+
\|q'\|_2^2.
\]

On \(K_\delta\),

\[
\|q'\|_2^2
\le
\delta^{-1}\int_{K_\delta}|q|(q')^2.
\]

Let

\[
Y=\int_{|q|\ge\delta}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

Then

\[
\|q'\|_{L^2(K_\delta)}\le \delta^{-1/2}Y^{1/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|(q')^2\|_{L^2(K_\delta)}
\lesssim
Q^C \delta^{-3/4}Y^{3/4}
+
\delta^{-1}Y.
\]

The transition contribution is bounded by

\[
\delta^{-2}\|g\|_2\|(q')^2\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon
\left(
\delta^{-11/4}Y^{3/4}
+
\delta^{-3}Y
\right).
\]

The second term

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}Y
\]

is absorbable if

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\ll Q^{-C}.
\]

The first term can be absorbed by Young’s inequality:

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-11/4}Y^{3/4}
\le
\frac12Y
+
Q^C\varepsilon^4\delta^{-11}.
\]

This introduces a term

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^4\delta^{-11}.
\]

That may be worse than the previous estimate depending on optimization, but still gives a positive exponent.

---

# 5. Rigidity exponent without \(q'\_\infty\)

Using the \(L^4\)-transition estimate, the kinetic bound becomes roughly

\[
Y\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon
+
\varepsilon\delta^{-1}
+
\varepsilon^4\delta^{-11}
\right)
\]

up to powers.

After dividing by \(\delta\) to estimate \(\int(q')^2\), we may get

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon\delta^{-1}
+
\varepsilon^4\delta^{-12}
\right).
\]

Potential estimate then yields something like

\[
\int F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon\delta^{-1}
+
\varepsilon^4\delta^{-12}
+
\varepsilon^2
\right).
\]

Together with the small-\(q\) estimate \(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2\), choose \(\delta=\varepsilon^\alpha\).

Terms:

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2\alpha},
\]

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-1}=\varepsilon^{1-\alpha},
\]

\[
\varepsilon^4\delta^{-12}=\varepsilon^{4-12\alpha}.
\]

Balance by choosing \(\alpha\) so all exponents positive. Need

\[
\alpha<1,
\qquad
\alpha<\frac13.
\]

Pick

\[
\alpha=\frac14.
\]

Then exponents are:

\[
2\alpha=\frac12,
\]

\[
1-\alpha=\frac34,
\]

\[
4-12\alpha=1.
\]

So one obtains at least

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|
}
\]

formally, which is even better. But the estimates were rough and may hide extra powers.

The key point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{It may be possible to remove the }q'\_\infty\text{ assumption entirely using }H^1\text{ interpolation.}
}
\]

But this proof is more delicate.

---

# 6. Practical conclusion

There are two versions of the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma.

## Version A: simple proof with \(q'\_\infty\)

Assume

\[
\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This is clean and should be used first.

## Version B: primitive-light proof

Assume instead

\[
\|q''\|_{L^2}+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

and use interpolation to control the transition term. Then a positive exponent \(c>0\) should still follow, possibly with a different \(c\).

This would reduce dependence on explicit \(q'\) bounds, but it is not needed if Agent 1 can provide \(q'\) polynomially bounded.

---

# 7. Attack on \(q\)-bound

The proof also used \(|F(q)|\le Q^C\) in the potential estimate. If \(q\) is unbounded, \(F\) can be large. But the estimate for

\[
X=\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
\]

does not require an a priori \(F\)-bound except in terms involving \(F'\) and transition \(F(q)\). The \(F'\)-term has

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2.
\]

If \(q\) is large, \(F'\) is large. But on the large-\(q\) region, \(F(q)^2\sim q^6\), and \(F'\sim q^2\). One might control \(F'\) by \(1+|F|^{2/3}\), then absorb via \(X\). This suggests \(q\)-boundedness may also be removable.

But the clean route is again to keep a polynomial \(q\)-bound. It is likely available from local admissibility/basepoint normalization.

---

# 8. Recommended final form

For the current proof, state the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma with assumptions:

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is sufficient and natural.

Then add a remark:

\[
\boxed{
q'\text{ and possibly }q\text{ bounds may be weakenable by 1D interpolation/absorption, but this is not needed.}
}
\]

This prevents overcomplicating the proof.

---

# 9. Gate 2 local complexity reduced

The new minimal Gate 2 local package is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

for source interval extraction, and

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

for \(L^2\)-integral rigidity.

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

this is essentially:

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty+\|q'''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is significantly lighter than the previous \(q^{(6)}\) package.

If canonical zero-separated transfer can supply this, Gate 2 is locally proved.

---

# 10. Current verdict

The \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity proof is robust with a simple \(q,q',q''\) polynomial bound. The dependence on primitive bounds is real but mild.

So Gate 2 now reduces to:

1. source interval extraction using \(u,u'\);
2. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity using \(q,q',q''\);
3. canonical local complexity supplying those polynomial bounds.

No Remez, no pointwise derivative propagation, no source component-count theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:35:08)

## Continuing attack — primitive bounds for \(q,q'\) from a source-large interval

The \(L^2\)-Gate 2 route now needs only a relatively light local package:

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

with

\[
u=q''.
\]

The remaining primitive issue is:

\[
u=q''\text{ may be controlled, but }q,q'\text{ are primitives.}
\]

I will attack whether the Gate 2 argument can derive the needed primitive bounds locally, or whether they must remain as an explicit admissibility/basepoint assumption.

---

# 1. What the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma actually needs

The proof uses

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

The clean \(L^2\)-rigidity proof assumed

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

on the source interval \(J\).

Since

\[
q''=u,
\]

the real primitive burden is

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 2. \(q\)-bound from \(u-g=F(q)\), locally in \(L^2\)

On the source interval \(J\), Gate 2 failure plus extraction gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

and source extraction gives

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Also canonical source complexity gives

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Since

\[
F(q)=u-g,
\]

we get

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^C |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Because

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

large \(q\) satisfies

\[
|F(q)|\gtrsim |q|^3.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_J |q|^6\,dm
\le Q^C |J|.
\]

So we get an \(L^6\)-bound:

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C |J|^{1/6}.
}
\]

This is not yet an \(L^\infty\)-bound, but in one dimension it can be upgraded if we control \(q'\).

So \(q\)-control reduces to \(q'\)-control.

---

# 3. \(q'\)-control from \(h\)-smallness away from \(q=0\)

The identity

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

controls \(q(q')^2\), but degenerates near \(q=0\).

Using the same multiplier argument as in the rigidity lemma, one obtains

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|
\]

under the \(L^2\)-input version, assuming only polynomial control of \(q'\) in the transition term. But that is circular if we are trying to prove \(q'\)-control.

Use the interpolation variant instead. It yields a weaker but still useful estimate without \(q'_\infty\):

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon\delta^{-1}
+
\varepsilon^4\delta^{-12}
+
1
\right)|J|.
\]

The final \(+1\) is too weak for rigidity, but enough to show \(q'\) is polynomially \(L^2\)-bounded on the large-\(|q|\) region:

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^2(|q|\ge2\delta)}\le Q^C |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Near \(q=0\), the function value is small, and large \(q'\) would move \(q\) out of the small region quickly. In one dimension, a coarea-type argument gives

\[
\int_{|q|\le 2\delta}(q')^2
\]

is controlled by the number of crossings and the kinetic energy outside, but this again needs oscillation control.

So this route is possible but not clean.

---

# 4. Cleaner route: basepoint primitive normalization

The cleanest theorem is to retain a local primitive/basepoint condition:

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C
}
\]

at one point \(m_b\in J^\ast\), plus

\[
\|u\|_\infty=\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Then for every \(m\in J^\ast\),

\[
q'(m)=q'(m_b)+\int_{m_b}^m u(s)\,ds,
\]

so

\[
|q'(m)|\le Q^C+|J^\ast|Q^C\le Q^C.
\]

Similarly,

\[
q(m)=q(m_b)+q'(m_b)(m-m_b)+\int_{m_b}^m(m-s)u(s)\,ds,
\]

so

\[
|q(m)|\le Q^C+Q^C|J^\ast|+Q^C|J^\ast|^2\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C,\quad
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C
\Rightarrow
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the simplest way to close the primitive gap.

---

# 5. Is the basepoint condition natural?

Yes. \(q\) is not arbitrary; it is part of the canonical local coordinate / shape data. If the local model is admissible, one normally already excludes

\[
|q|+|q'|
\]

being super-polynomial at the basepoint. Otherwise the local expansion itself is ill-conditioned.

So the Gate 2 local complexity theorem should include:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Primitive admissibility: }
\exists m_b\in I^\ast:
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with source derivative bounds, this implies all primitive bounds needed for Gate 2.

---

# 6. Can primitive admissibility be derived from the completed meromorphic formula?

Likely yes, but it is a separate audit.

If \(q\) is a logarithmic-derivative or normalized curvature expression built from \(\Xi\), then ordinary zero-separatedness gives meromorphic bounds:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho,\mathcal Z_\Xi)\ge \lambda Q^{-C}
\]

should imply

\[
|q|+|q'|+\cdots \le Q^C
\]

by standard log-derivative estimates.

But that requires knowing the exact formula for \(q\) and its pole set.

So there are two possible formulations.

## Strong canonical version

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated tube}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{I^\ast}|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|\le Q^C.
}
\]

## Modular version

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated source bounds}
+
\text{primitive admissibility}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2 local complexity}.
}
\]

The modular version is safer until the exact meromorphic formula is audited.

---

# 7. Updated Gate 2 local complexity theorem

## Lemma: Gate 2 Local Complexity from Source and Primitive Bounds

Assume on \(I^\ast\):

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
u=q''.
\]

Assume primitive admissibility at some basepoint \(m_b\in I^\ast\):

\[
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty+\|q'''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

Consequently, all local bounds required for:

1. source-large interval extraction;
2. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity;
3. wall escape;

are available.

If additionally row derivatives are polynomially bounded, row mobility is also available.

---

# 8. Gate 2 now depends on a very small local package

The full Gate 2 proof needs:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Source bounds:

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

3. Primitive admissibility:

   \[
   |q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C.
   \]

4. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity.

Then Gate 2 follows.

This is significantly lighter than the earlier local \(C^6\) package.

---

# 9. What remains to attack

The remaining analytic audits are now precise:

## Audit A — source bounds

Prove from the canonical completed object:

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_\infty+\|(q''_{\can})'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

This is a finite log-derivative / AFE / zero-separated estimate.

## Audit B — primitive admissibility

Either prove:

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

directly from the completed meromorphic formula, or assume basepoint normalization.

## Audit C — residual identity

Verify the identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

hold exactly or with \(L^2\)-small residuals.

If residuals are present:

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le Q^{-A}|J|^{1/2},
\]

the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof survives.

---

# 10. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 does not need a broad }C^6\text{ package if primitive admissibility is available.}
}
\]

A minimal local package is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This makes the Gate 2 proof substantially cleaner.

If the completed meromorphic formula proves the primitive bound directly, even the basepoint assumption can be removed.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:36:04)

I’ll simplify Gate 2 further. The dyadic/Vitali source-selection machinery is unnecessary: Gate 1 alone gives a point where \(u\) is large, and the \(u'\)-bound thickens that point into the needed source-large interval.

_Thought for 15s_

## Continuing attack — remove dyadic/Vitali extraction from Gate 2

The Gate 2 route can be simplified further. We do **not** need dyadic thresholding, a Vitali subcover, or an \(L^\infty\)-bound for \(u\). Gate 1 alone gives a point where \(|u|\) is large. The \(u'\)-bound thickens that point into a source-large interval. Gate 2 failure then gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on that same interval.

This produces a cleaner Gate 2 theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}+\|u'\|_\infty\text{ bound}+L^2\text{-integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This improves the latest downstream route, which still used dyadic/Vitali source interval extraction. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume only the source Lipschitz bound

\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

No \(\|u\|_\infty\) is needed for this extraction.

---

# 2. Gate 1 gives a large source point

From

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B},
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
}
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

---

# 3. Thicken the source point

Let

\[
r=c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\]

with \(c>0\) sufficiently small.

For \(|m-m_\ast|\le r\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}r
\le
c\tau.
\]

Choosing \(c\) small enough gives

\[
|u(m)|\ge \tau
\]

on the one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

of length

\[
|J|\ge c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau= \frac12 Q^{-B/2}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
}
\]

This is a source-large interval obtained directly from Gate 1.

---

# 4. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on \(J\)

On \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
\tau^2\int_J F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Hence

\[
\int_J F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\). Since

\[
|J|\ge c\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we obtain

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
C Q^{-A}\tau^{-3}Q^{C_u}.
\]

Since

\[
\tau\asymp Q^{-B/2},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

This is exactly the input needed for \(L^2\)-integral rigidity.

---

# 5. Apply \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Use the repaired rigidity lemma:

If

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Here

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and the proof uses local polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\).

Substitute the extracted \(\varepsilon\):

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
\]

---

# 6. Contradiction with source largeness

On \(J'\subset J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau\asymp Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
}
\]

For contradiction, require

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}
<
-B.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\frac A5
>
\frac{13B}{10}
+
\frac{C_u}{5}
+
C_R
+
O(1).
\]

Thus it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

With \(A\) chosen this large, Gate 2 failure contradicts Gate 1.

Therefore Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Clean Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem: Gate 2 from source Lipschitz and \(L^2\)-rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Source Lipschitz bound:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. Local primitive/source bounds sufficient for \(L^2\)-integral rigidity:

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

on the extracted interval.

4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 follows for sufficiently large \(A\):

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. What this removes

This argument removes the need for:

\[
\text{dyadic source thresholding},
\]

\[
\text{Vitali source interval selection},
\]

\[
\|u\|_\infty\text{ for measure extraction},
\]

\[
\text{pointwise anisotropy smallness},
\]

\[
\text{Remez/Cartan propagation},
\]

\[
\text{pointwise }\Gamma_G''\text{ propagation}.
\]

The only extraction requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 gives a large }u\text{ point, and }u'\text{ thickens it.}
}
\]

This is considerably cleaner.

---

# 9. Updated downstream Gate 2 package

The active Gate 2 package should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\|u'\|_\infty\text{ bound}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The older source interval extraction via dyadic/Vitali is no longer needed except as a fallback if one wants a more robust threshold selection.

---

# 10. Remaining proof obligations

The remaining Gate 2 obligations are now minimal:

1. Prove

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
   \]

   from canonical local complexity.

2. Prove primitive bounds

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
   \]

   on the extracted source interval.

3. Finalize the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma.

Once these are in place, Gate 2 is locally proved from Gate 1.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:37:22)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — repair the \(L^2\)-rigidity multiplier and confirm the \(2/5\) exponent

The current Gate 2 route is now very clean:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\|u'\|_\infty\text{ control}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

The remaining technical core is the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma. The last version used a sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\). A sharper and cleaner multiplier is

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\,\chi_\delta(q),
\]

because it reduces the worst transition derivative loss. This is the multiplier mentioned in the latest coordinator update. 

---

# 1. \(L^2\)-rigidity target

Work on normalized intervals

\[
J=(-2,2),\qquad J'=(-1,1).
\]

Assume

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Assume polynomial local bounds

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Goal:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Use the multiplier \(a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)\)

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad(|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad(|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Define

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q).
\]

Then on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
a_\delta(q)=q.
\]

The derivatives are better than for the sign cutoff:

\[
a_\delta'(q)=\chi_\delta(q)+q\chi_\delta'(q)=O(1),
\]

because on the transition \(|q|\sim \delta\),

\[
q\chi_\delta'(q)=O(1).
\]

Similarly,

\[
a_\delta''(q)=2\chi_\delta'(q)+q\chi_\delta''(q)=O(\delta^{-1}).
\]

This is the key gain: the second derivative costs \(\delta^{-1}\), not \(\delta^{-2}\).

---

# 3. Kinetic estimate

Choose \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(J)\), \(0\le\phi\le1\), \(\phi=1\) on a slightly larger interval containing \(J'\), with fixed normalized derivative bounds.

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi a_\delta(q)
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi a_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi a_\delta(q)q(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi a_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
a_\delta(q)q=q^2\ge \delta^2.
\]

Hence the positive term controls

\[
2\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi q^2(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term satisfies

\[
\left|\int \phi a_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi a_\delta(q)\|_2.
\]

Since \(|a_\delta(q)|\le |q|\le Q^C\),

\[
\left|\int \phi a_\delta(q)h\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi a_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi a_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''a_\delta(q)
+
2\phi'a_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi a_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi a_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

Using

\[
|a_\delta|\le Q^C,\qquad |a_\delta'|\le Q^C,\qquad |a_\delta''|\le Q^C\delta^{-1},
\]

and the polynomial bounds on \(q',q''\), we get

\[
\|(\phi a_\delta(q))''\|_2
\le Q^C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\left|\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi q^2(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}.
}
\]

Since \(q^2\ge\delta^2\) on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
}
\]

This is the desired kinetic estimate. No absorption argument is needed.

---

# 4. Potential estimate

Let \(\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy

\[
\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad(|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad(|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

with

\[
|\widetilde\chi_\delta^{(r)}|\le C_r\delta^{-r}.
\]

Set

\[
X=\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

we get

\[
X
=
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is

\[
\left|\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)g\right|
\le
\|g\|_2X^{1/2}
\le
\varepsilon X^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb later.

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q))'
=
\phi'\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)
+
\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)
+
\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

The \(F'\)-term is bounded by kinetic control:

\[
\left|\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The transition term is supported on

\[
2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta.
\]

There,

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\qquad
|\widetilde\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Hence

\[
\left|\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta'(q)q'F(q)q'\right|
\le
Q^C\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The cutoff boundary term is

\[
T=\left|\int \phi'\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|.
\]

Take \(\phi=\psi^2\), so

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi.
\]

Then

\[
T
\le
Q^C
\left(\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
T\le Q^C X^{1/2}(\varepsilon\delta^{-3})^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb:

\[
T\le \frac14X+Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The \(g\)-term also absorbs:

\[
\varepsilon X^{1/2}\le \frac14X+C\varepsilon^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
X\le \frac12X+Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap |q|\ge3\delta}F(q)^2
\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

---

# 5. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'\cap |q|\le3\delta}|u|^2
\le Q^C\delta^2+\|g\|_2^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

---

# 6. Combine and optimize

On the large-\(|q|\) region,

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2g^2,
\]

so

\[
\int_{J'\cap |q|\ge3\delta}|u|^2
\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

On the small region,

\[
\int_{J'\cap |q|\le3\delta}|u|^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
\]

Optimize by

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon\delta^{-3},
\]

so

\[
\delta^5=\varepsilon,
\qquad
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/5},
\qquad
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
}
\]

This proves the \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity lemma with the sharp exponent \(2/5\) under the clean local polynomial bound

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

---

# 7. Residual-stable version

If the identities have residuals:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

with

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le \varepsilon,
\]

then the same proof holds after replacing

\[
g,h
\]

by their exact-identity parts and absorbing \(r_g,r_h\) into the \(L^2\)-small quantities. The constants change only by \(Q^C\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
L^2\text{-integral rigidity is stable under }L^2\text{-small residuals.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Consequence for Gate 2

The full Gate 2 proof now uses:

1. Gate 1 gives a large source point:

   \[
   |u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
   \]

2. \(\|u'\|_\infty\) thickens it to a source interval \(J\) with

   \[
   |u|\ge \tau\asymp Q^{-B/2}
   \]

   and

   \[
   |J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u}|I|.
   \]

3. Gate 2 failure gives

   \[
   \|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
   \le
   \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
   \]

   with

   \[
   \varepsilon
   =
   Q^{-A/2+3B/4+C_u/2+O(1)}.
   \]

4. Rigidity gives

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
   \]

5. But \(|u|\ge \tau\) on \(J'\), so

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
   \]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<Q^{-B}.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+O(C).
\]

Thus Gate 2 is locally proved under the current assumptions.

---

# 9. Current minimal Gate 2 package

The Gate 2 proof now needs:

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
}
\]

for source interval extraction;

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

for \(L^2\)-integral rigidity;

and the exact or residual-stable identities for \(g,h\).

This is significantly lighter than the earlier \(C^6\), Remez, or pointwise-derivative packages.

---

# 10. Updated verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now essentially a local real-variable theorem.}
}
\]

The active proof is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{source Lipschitz}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The next remaining downstream task is not Gate 2; it is D4 principal-symbol rank and correction control.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:58:26)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem from one large source point

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: state the final Gate 2 theorem using the simplified route

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This replaces the older dyadic/Vitali and pointwise target-smallness routes. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Gate 1 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive assumption

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Set

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(g^2+h^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume the source Lipschitz bound

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Gate 1 gives one large source point

From Gate 1,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
}
\]

Define

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

---

# 4. Source thickening

Let

\[
r=c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\]

with \(c>0\) sufficiently small.

For

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le r,
\]

the Lipschitz bound gives

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}r
\le c\tau.
\]

Choosing \(c\) small enough,

\[
|u(m)|\ge \tau
\]

on a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
}
\]

So on \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
}
\]

Boundary points are handled by taking the available one-sided interval.

---

# 5. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on \(J\)

Since \(|u|\ge \tau\) on \(J\),

\[
\tau^2\int_J F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_J (g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\). Since

\[
|J|\ge c\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we obtain

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}\tau^{-3}Q^{C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Because

\[
\tau\asymp Q^{-B/2},
\]

this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

The harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor is absorbed into \(C_R\) below.

---

# 6. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Assume the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

If

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

The lemma uses

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and polynomial local bounds on

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q''.
\]

Its current proof uses the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

against \(h\), yielding

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

then the potential estimate and optimization

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

---

# 7. Contradiction

On \(J'\subset J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau\asymp Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
}
\]

The rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Substitute

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Then

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Thus the rigidity upper bound is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}|J'|.
\]

This contradicts

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|
\]

provided

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}
<
-B-O(1).
\]

Equivalently, it is enough that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

For such \(A\), Gate 2 failure is impossible.

---

# 8. Final Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Source Lipschitz bound:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. Local primitive bounds for the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma:

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

on the extracted source interval.

4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for every \(A\) satisfying

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 9. What this replaces

The mainline Gate 2 proof no longer needs:

- dyadic/Vitali source-band extraction;
- pointwise target-smallness extraction;
- Remez/Cartan propagation;
- pointwise derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\).

The active Gate 2 package is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

The older D1/D2 labels should be treated as fallback/historical.

---

# 10. Remaining hypotheses to audit

The proof is now reduced to three local items:

1. **Source Lipschitz from ordinary local complexity**

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
   \]

2. **Primitive bounds**

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

   These can come either from completed-meromorphic formulas or from primitive/basepoint admissibility plus \(u=q''\).

3. **Residual-stable \(L^2\)-rigidity**

   If the identities for \(g,h\) have residuals

   \[
   r_g,\quad r_h,
   \]

   need

   \[
   \|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le Q^{-K}|J|^{1/2}
   \]

   so they are absorbed into \(\varepsilon\).

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is locally proved modulo source Lipschitz, primitive bounds, and }L^2\text{-rigidity.}
}
\]

The active downstream obstacle is no longer Gate 2 propagation. It is now mainly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 row-span principal rank + residual control.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:00:33)

## Continuing attack — remove a hidden issue in source thickening: complex-valued \(u\)

The latest Gate 2 proof uses:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

to find \(m_\ast\) with

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2},
\]

then uses

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}
\]

to thicken this point into an interval \(J\) on which

\[
|u|\ge \tau.
\]

This is straightforward if \(u\) is real-valued. If \(u\) is complex-valued, we need to check the same argument works for \(|u|\). It does, because \(|u|\) is Lipschitz with constant at most \(|u'|\). This removes a small but real technical gap.

---

# 1. Complex source thickening lemma

Let

\[
u:I\to\mathbb C
\]

be \(C^1\), and assume

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le M|I|^{-1}.
\]

If

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge U_0,
\]

then for

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le r:=\frac{U_0}{2M}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)|
\ge
|u(m_\ast)|-|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\ge
U_0-M|I|^{-1}r
=
\frac12U_0.
\]

Thus the same source interval extraction holds for complex-valued \(u\).

With

\[
U_0=Q^{-B/2},
\qquad
M=Q^{C_u},
\]

we get an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
|u|\ge \frac12Q^{-B/2}
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

So no real-valuedness assumption is needed for source thickening.

---

# 2. Gate 2 failure still yields \(L^2\)-small anisotropy

On \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\]

with

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Gate 2 failure says

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

If \(g,h\) are complex-valued, replace

\[
g^2+h^2
\]

by

\[
|g|^2+|h|^2.
\]

The Gate 2 density should be understood as

\[
|u|^2(|g|^2+|h|^2).
\]

Then

\[
\tau^2\int_J(|g|^2+|h|^2)
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\ge c\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|\):

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(|g|^2+|h|^2)
\le
Q^{-A}\tau^{-3}Q^{C_u+O(1)}.
\]

As before,

\[
\tau\asymp Q^{-B/2}
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(|g|^2+|h|^2)
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus the \(L^2\)-smallness parameter remains

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Complex-valued issue in \(L^2\)-rigidity

The \(L^2\)-rigidity proof used signs and positivity, especially:

\[
2\int \phi a_\delta(q)q(q')^2
\]

being positive. This assumes \(q\) is real-valued.

So the source extraction works complex-valued, but the rigidity lemma requires either:

1. \(q\) is real-valued in the relevant local variable; or  
2. one applies the argument to a real scalar component / real gauge of \(q\); or  
3. one proves a complex analogue using \(\overline q\), e.g. a multiplier involving \(\overline q\chi_\delta(|q|)\).

This is important.

The current formula

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

also looks algebraic over reals. If \(q\) is complex, \(q(q')^2\) has no sign.

The positivity of the kinetic term is a core part of the proof. Therefore the Gate 2 integral rigidity lemma must explicitly assume the local variables are real, or be reformulated for complex \(q\).

---

# 4. Is \(q\) real in the actual local model?

Based on the downstream formulas, \(q_0\), \(u=q''_{\can}\), \(\Gamma_G\), and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) have been treated as real scalar quantities in the row geometry:

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

The wall branch uses

\[
q_0''=u
\]

and convexity/concavity, which only makes sense over real \(q_0\).

Thus the downstream Gate 2 layer is implicitly in a real normal form. The proof should explicitly state:

\[
\boxed{
q,\ u,\ g,\ h\text{ are real-valued in the Gate 2 normalized coordinate.}
}
\]

or at least:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the relevant scalar channel is real-valued after canonical gauge normalization.}
}
\]

This is not optional. Without real-valuedness, the integral rigidity proof and wall escape both fail.

---

# 5. Complex fallback if needed

If \(q\) is genuinely complex, one might try a complex rigidity identity using

\[
\overline q
\]

as multiplier:

\[
h\cdot \overline q\chi_\delta(|q|)
\]

would produce something like

\[
2|q|^2(q')^2,
\]

not

\[
2|q|^2|q'|^2.
\]

That is still not positive.

To get positivity, the structural identity would need to involve

\[
q|q'|^2
\]

or a Hermitian quantity, not

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

So the current rigidity method is specifically real.

Therefore the proof architecture must include a real-gauge lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma:}
\quad
q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},u
\text{ are real-valued on }I.
}
\]

If this cannot be justified, the \(L^2\)-rigidity route must be redesigned.

---

# 6. Gate 2 theorem with real-normal-form hypothesis

The cleaned-up theorem is:

## Gate 2 Local Real Theorem

Assume:

1. \(q,u,g,h\) are real-valued on \(I\).

2. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

3. Source Lipschitz:

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
   \]

4. Local primitive bounds:

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

5. Identities:

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
   \]

6. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity.

Then Gate 2 follows:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\]

for sufficiently large \(A\).

The exponent condition remains:

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 7. Impact on wall escape

Wall escape also relies on real-valuedness:

\[
q_0''=u,\quad |u|\ge\tau
\]

implies local convexity/concavity only if \(q_0,u\) are real. If \(q_0\) is complex, \(q_0''\ne0\) still implies \(q_0\) moves quadratically in the complex plane, and one can escape the disk \(|q_0|<\varepsilon\) using a complex Taylor argument, but not by real first-exit convexity.

Actually, a complex wall escape is still possible:

If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le \eta,
\qquad
|q_0''(m_0)|\ge\tau,
\]

then

\[
q_0(m_0+s)+q_0(m_0-s)-2q_0(m_0)
=
q_0''(m_0)s^2+O(M_3s^3).
\]

Hence at least one of \(q_0(m_0\pm s)\) has modulus

\[
\gtrsim \tau s^2-\eta-O(M_3s^3).
\]

So wall escape does **not** require real-valuedness if formulated via symmetric second differences.

But the integral rigidity lemma still does.

---

# 8. Current new requirement

Add to the downstream checklist:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Verify Gate 2 real normal form.}
}
\]

Specifically:

- Are \(q,u,g,h\) real scalar functions on the interval?
- If they arise from a complex object, what gauge or real part produces these identities?
- Are the identities exact in that real scalar gauge?

This is now the highest conceptual check for the local Gate 2 proof.

---

# 9. If real normal form is confirmed

Then Gate 2 is locally very close:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
u'\text{ bound}
+
q,q',q''\text{ bounds}
+
L^2\text{-rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

No Remez, no D1/D2, no pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\).

---

# 10. Verdict

The source-thickening Gate 2 proof is valid for complex-valued \(u\) at the extraction stage, but the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma and wall convexity intuition require a **real scalar normal form**.

So the next attack target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma}.
}
\]

If this is part of the existing row/local geometry, Gate 2 remains on track. If not, the integral rigidity proof must be replaced by a Hermitian/complex analogue.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:02:58)

## Continuing attack — Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma

The previous attack exposed a necessary condition for the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity proof:

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

must be a **real scalar identity**, because the kinetic term

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

is sign-coercive only after multiplying by a real cutoff such as \(q\chi_\delta(q)\). If \(q\) were genuinely complex, that kinetic positivity would disappear.

So the next target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma.}
}
\]

If this lemma is true, the current Gate 2 proof remains viable. If false, the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity proof must be replaced by a Hermitian complex analogue. This is the main conceptual check left in the local Gate 2 package. 

---

# 1. Required statement

The local Gate 2 variables must satisfy:

\[
q:I\to\mathbb R,
\qquad
u=q''\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\in\mathbb R.
\]

Then the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

gives the positive kinetic term

\[
2\int \phi a_\delta(q)q(q')^2
=
2\int \phi q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2
\ge0.
\]

This is the key coercive input behind the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma.

---

# 2. Why this is plausible in the canonical zeta setting

The proof should not use raw \(\zeta(1/2+it)\). It should use the real completed critical-line object, e.g. a Hardy/xi-normalized scalar.

For the completed xi-function, one has the critical-line reality property:

\[
\Xi(t):=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)\in\mathbb R
\quad(t\in\mathbb R),
\]

after the standard real normalization. On a zero-separated interval, \(\Xi(t)\neq0\), so its sign is locally constant and

\[
\log |\Xi(t)|
\]

is a real smooth function. Any differential polynomial built from this real scalar is real.

Therefore, if

\[
q
\]

is defined from the real canonical critical-line scalar, or from the real local jet/Gram normal form derived from it, then

\[
q,q',q'',g,h
\]

are real-valued.

This is consistent with the rest of the downstream layer, which already uses:

\[
q_0''=u
\]

and wall escape via convexity/first-exit behavior. Those arguments implicitly assume a real scalar \(q_0\).

---

# 3. Canonical versus proxy warning

The real normal form is true only for the **canonical combined object**.

It is not necessarily true for:

\[
P_2
\]

alone, or for a one-sided AFE branch. A raw main branch has complex phases

\[
e^{-it\log n},
\]

so it is complex-valued. The real object arises only after adding the folded dual/gamma-conjugate structure and using the completed critical-line normalization.

Thus the proof must use:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
}
\]

as a real canonical quantity, not a one-branch proxy. The \(B_2\) term is real; the main/dual pair must be arranged as a real critical-line combination; and \(E_2\) must be included in the same real canonical normalization, not treated as a complex residual unless split into real and imaginary parts.

This gives the guardrail:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 rigidity applies to }q''_{\can}\text{, not to }P_2\text{ or }D_2\text{ alone.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Formal Real Normal Form Lemma

A clean lemma is:

## Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma

Assume the local Gate 2 variable \(q\) is generated from a real critical-line canonical scalar \(\mathcal Z(t)\), where

\[
\mathcal Z(t)\in\mathbb R
\]

on the real interval \(I\), and \(\mathcal Z\) is zero-free on the complex tube used for local estimates. Assume \(q\) is a real differential expression in \(\mathcal Z\), \(\log|\mathcal Z|\), or the corresponding real jet/Gram normal form. Then on \(I\),

\[
q,q',q'',q''',\ldots\in\mathbb R.
\]

Consequently,

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

are real scalar functions, and the \(L^2\)-integral rigidity multiplier proof is valid.

---

# 5. What must be audited

The real-normal-form audit has four finite checks.

## 5.1 Critical-line real scalar

Verify that the scalar used for \(q\) is the real completed/Hardy-normalized object, not raw \(\zeta\). The local object must satisfy:

\[
\overline{\mathcal Z(t)}=\mathcal Z(t)
\quad(t\in\mathbb R).
\]

## 5.2 Zero-separated logarithmic regularity

On the relevant interval/tube, ensure there is no zero or pole crossing:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C}.
\]

This makes the real branch of \(\log|\mathcal Z|\) smooth and prevents singular sign changes.

## 5.3 Real canonical decomposition

Verify

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

is real on the real line. In particular, the dual term must be the correct folded conjugate, not an independent complex branch.

## 5.4 Exact real identities

Verify the identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

hold in this same real gauge. If extra lower-order terms appear, they must be incorporated into residuals:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

with

\[
\|r_g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{-K}|J|^{1/2}.
\]

The \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma is residual-stable under such errors.

---

# 6. If \(q\) is complex: no-go for the current proof

If \(q\) is complex-valued, the current multiplier proof fails.

Indeed,

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

is not meaningful as a real sign/size cutoff unless \(q\) is real. If one tries a Hermitian multiplier such as

\[
\overline q\chi_\delta(|q|),
\]

then

\[
2q(q')^2\cdot \overline q
=
2|q|^2(q')^2,
\]

which is still not positive, because \((q')^2\) is complex. It is not

\[
2|q|^2|q'|^2.
\]

So the complex version does not give a coercive kinetic term.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The present }L^2\text{-rigidity proof requires a real scalar normal form.}
}
\]

A genuinely complex proof would need a different identity containing a Hermitian kinetic term, e.g.

\[
q|q'|^2
\]

or a vector-valued real/imaginary system with a positive energy. That is a different theorem.

---

# 7. Complex wall escape is easier than complex rigidity

Wall escape itself can survive complex values by using symmetric second differences:

\[
q(m+s)+q(m-s)-2q(m)
=
q''(m)s^2+O(s^3).
\]

If

\[
|q''(m)|\ge\tau,
\]

then at least one of \(q(m\pm s)\) must move a distance \(\gtrsim \tau s^2\) in the complex plane, unless \(q(m)\) is already large. So wall escape can be complexified.

But Gate 2 rigidity cannot, at least not with the present multiplier.

Therefore the real-normal-form audit is primarily needed for Gate 2, not for wall escape.

---

# 8. Impact on Gate 2 theorem

The final Gate 2 theorem should include:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Real critical-line normal form for }q,u,g,h.
}
\]

Then the active proof is:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\|u'\|_\infty
\Rightarrow
\text{source-large interval}
\]

\[
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

\[
L^2\text{-real integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|
\]

contradicting

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-B/2}
\quad\text{on }J'.
\]

So Gate 2 is locally proved, conditional on real normal form and local complexity.

---

# 9. Updated downstream checklist

Gate 2 now requires:

1. **Real Normal Form**

   \[
   q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
   \]

2. **Source Lipschitz**

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
   \]

3. **Primitive/local bounds**

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

4. **Exact or residual-stable identities**

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
   \]

5. **\(L^2\)-rigidity lemma**

   \[
   \|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le\varepsilon
   \Rightarrow
   \int|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
   \]

No Remez, no pointwise target-smallness, no pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\).

---

# 10. Verdict

The next proof obligation is not another analytic inequality. It is a structural audit:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Verify Gate 2 Real Normal Form.}
}
\]

If \(q,u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are indeed real canonical scalar functions on the real interval, then the current Gate 2 route is coherent and closeable.

If not, the entire \(L^2\)-integral rigidity proof must be replaced by a Hermitian complex analogue.

_Thought for 9s_

## Continuing attack — prove Real Normal Form from completed critical-line symmetry

The current Gate 2 proof depends on a real scalar normal form. The analytic inequality

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g''
\]

is coercive only if \(q\) is real on the interval. If \(q\) is complex, the multiplier proof loses positivity. So the immediate target is:

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R\quad\text{on the Gate 2 interval}.
}
\]

This is plausible if \(q\) is built from the completed critical-line real scalar, not from a one-sided AFE branch. The latest downstream architecture already warns that Gate 2 must use the canonical object \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\), not a proxy. 

---

# 1. Correct real scalar source

Use the completed xi-function

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s).
\]

On the critical line define

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

By the functional equation and conjugation symmetry,

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R
\quad(t\in\mathbb R).
}
\]

Equivalently, one may use the Hardy-normalized function

\[
Z(t)=e^{i\theta(t)}\zeta\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]

which is also real on the real line.

Therefore any real differential expression in

\[
\Xi(t),\quad \log|\Xi(t)|,\quad Z(t),
\]

and their real \(t\)-derivatives is real-valued away from zeros.

This gives the basic route:

\[
\boxed{
q\text{ must be defined from a real completed critical-line scalar.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Zero-separated interval gives real smoothness

Assume the ordinary zero-separated tube condition:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Then on the real interval \(I\), \(\Xi(t)\neq0\), and since \(\Xi(t)\) is real, its sign is constant on each connected component of \(I\). Hence

\[
\log|\Xi(t)|
\]

is real and smooth on \(I\).

Thus if \(q\) is defined by a real local formula such as

\[
q=\mathcal P\bigl(\partial_t^j\log|\Xi(t)|:0\le j\le k\bigr)
\]

with real coefficients and no singular denominators involving \(q,u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), then

\[
\boxed{
q(t)\in\mathbb R,\qquad q^{(j)}(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
u=q''\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\in\mathbb R.
\]

This proves the Real Normal Form Lemma under a concrete construction hypothesis.

---

# 3. Canonical AFE must be paired, not one-sided

The real normal form is **not** valid for a single AFE branch. A main packet

\[
P_2(t)=\sum_n c_n e^{-it\log n}
\]

is generally complex-valued. The real object emerges only after the completed real-line normalization pairs main and dual branches with the correct gamma phase.

So the correct canonical statement is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
}
\]

is real on the real interval because it is the finite/local representation of a real completed critical-line scalar derivative.

The row/Gate 2 proof must not use:

\[
P_2\quad\text{alone},
\]

\[
D_2\quad\text{alone},
\]

or a prime-only / \(B_2\)-only proxy as the Gate 2 source.

Those may be useful diagnostics, but not for the real rigidity theorem.

---

# 4. Sufficient Real Normal Form Lemma

A usable theorem:

## Gate 2 Real Normal Form Lemma

Let \(I\) be an ordinary zero-separated interval. Suppose \(q\) is constructed from a real completed critical-line scalar \(\mathcal Z(t)\), with

\[
\mathcal Z(t)\in\mathbb R\quad(t\in I),
\]

by a real differential expression with real coefficients, and suppose all denominators in the expression are bounded away from zero by \(Q^{-C}\) on \(I\). Then

\[
q,q',q'',q''',\ldots \in \mathbb R
\]

on \(I\). In particular, with

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Therefore the \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity lemma applies.

---

# 5. Denominator audit

The lemma requires denominator safety. The Gate 2 normal form must not divide by quantities that can vanish in the regimes we are studying.

Forbidden denominator types:

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Why: Gate 2 specifically studies small or wall regimes where these quantities may be small. Any such denominator would invalidate the local polynomial bounds and real smoothness.

Allowed denominators:

- completed scalar \(\mathcal Z(t)\), if zero-separated;
- Gram/normalization factors already proved \(Q^{-C}\)-bounded below;
- fixed nonzero constants;
- gauge denominators with explicit chart conditions and finite chart cover.

Thus the audit condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{all Gate 2 variables are real differential-polynomial functions in the zero-separated completed scalar, with only safe denominators.}
}
\]

---

# 6. What if \(q\) is chart-dependent?

If \(q\) comes from a projective/local coordinate chart, then real normal form must be checked chartwise.

For each chart \(\mathcal U_\alpha\), verify:

\[
q_\alpha\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
g_\alpha=q_\alpha''-6q_\alpha+2q_\alpha^3,
\]

\[
h_\alpha=2q_\alpha(q_\alpha')^2-\frac16g_\alpha'',
\]

and denominator lower bounds

\[
|\Delta_\alpha|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If the interval crosses chart boundaries, either:

1. refine \(I\) into subintervals inside charts; or  
2. use a partition of unity and prove the rigidity lemma chartwise.

Since the Gate 2 proof needs only one source-large interval \(J\), it is enough to choose \(J\) inside a good chart. If the source-large interval crosses a chart boundary, shrink to a subinterval; polynomial losses are acceptable if the chart cover is finite and denominators have polynomial separation.

---

# 7. Residual-stable version

If the identities are not exact but have residuals:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

then the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof survives if

\[
\boxed{
\|r_g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{-K}|J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

In that case, redefine

\[
\tilde g=g-r_g,
\qquad
\tilde h=h-r_h,
\]

apply rigidity to \((\tilde g,\tilde h)\), and absorb the residuals into the \(\varepsilon\)-budget.

So exactness is not strictly required, but the residuals must be real or at least have real components controlled in the scalar channel used by the multiplier proof.

---

# 8. Complex no-go remains

If \(q\) is genuinely complex and no real scalar gauge is available, the current integral rigidity proof fails.

Trying to multiply by

\[
\overline q\chi_\delta(|q|)
\]

does not yield positivity, because

\[
q(q')^2\overline q
=
|q|^2(q')^2,
\]

which is not

\[
|q|^2|q'|^2.
\]

Thus the kinetic estimate collapses.

So the dichotomy is sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real scalar normal form} \Rightarrow \text{Gate 2 rigidity works;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{genuinely complex }q \Rightarrow \text{need new Hermitian identity.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Integration with Gate 2 theorem

Under Real Normal Form, the current Gate 2 proof is:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Large source point:

   \[
   |u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
   \]

3. Source thickening using

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
   \]

4. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small real \(g,h\) on the source interval.

5. Real \(L^2\)-rigidity gives

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
   \]

6. Contradiction with \(|u|\ge Q^{-B/2}\) on \(J'\).

Thus Gate 2 is locally proved.

---

# 10. Final audit checklist

To close this branch, verify the following:

\[
\boxed{\text{A. }\mathcal Z(t)\in\mathbb R\text{ on }I.}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{B. }q\text{ is a real differential expression in }\mathcal Z\text{ or }\log|\mathcal Z|.}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{C. zero-separatedness gives all denominators }\ge Q^{-C}.}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{D. }q''_{\can}=q''\text{ agrees with the canonical }B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{E. }g,h\text{ identities hold exactly or with }L^2\text{-small residuals.}
}
\]

If A–E hold, the Real Normal Form Lemma is proved.

---

# Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 now hinges on verifying that the local variables are in a real completed critical-line gauge.}
}
\]

This is a structural/canonical audit, not a new analytic inequality. If confirmed, the \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 proof is coherent and closeable.
