_Thought for 49s_

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem from source thickening and \(L^2\)-rigidity

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: formulate the final Gate 2 theorem using the current active route

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This supersedes the older pointwise target-smallness/Remez formulation. The latest local-complexity audit also shows the minimal analytic transfer needed for Gate 2 is essentially \(u,u'\), with \(q,q'\) recoverable locally or handled by primitive admissibility. 

---

# 1. Objects

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Gate 1 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Gate 2 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 2. Assumptions for the local Gate 2 theorem

Assume the following local analytic package on \(I\):

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

For the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma, assume either direct primitive bounds

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
}
\]

or use the minimal package from the current audit:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

plus local primitive recovery from \(u=q''\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g=u-F(q)\). The latter is currently the sharper Gate 2 formulation; the stronger primitive package remains the safer paper statement. 

Assume the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|
}
\]

for every \(J'\Subset J\). The active proof uses the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

against

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

giving the kinetic estimate

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

and optimizing at

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

---

# 3. Contrapositive proof

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

By Gate 1, there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12 Q^{-B/2}.
\]

By the source Lipschitz bound, there is a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

---

# 4. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on \(J\)

On \(J\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\tau^2\int_J (g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Since

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
\tau^2\asymp Q^{-B},
\]

we get

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon=
Q^{-A/2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Apply \(L^2\)-input rigidity

The rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Substitute \(\varepsilon\):

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-A/5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
}
\]

But on \(J'\subset J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau\asymp Q^{-B/2},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
}
\]

These bounds are incompatible if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)<-B.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

Hence, for \(A\) sufficiently large relative to the local complexity constants, Gate 2 failure is impossible.

---

# 6. Final theorem

## Gate 2 from source thickening and \(L^2\)-rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Source thickening:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. Local bounds sufficient for \(L^2\)-rigidity, either as primitive bounds

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

or by local primitive recovery from \(u\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g\).

4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for any exponent satisfying

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 7. Dyadic/Vitali refinement

The one-large-source-point proof is the clean mainline. A dyadic source-level extraction is still useful as a robustness fallback. It can improve bookkeeping by selecting a source band

\[
\tau\le |u|\le 2\tau
\]

and extracting an interval where

\[
|u|\asymp\tau
\]

and

\[
\fint_J(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A+B+O(1)}.
\]

But it is no longer needed for the main Gate 2 proof.

---

# 8. Replacement of old D1/D2

The old downstream inputs

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez Propagation},
\]

\[
D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}
\]

are no longer the active Gate 2 route.

They are replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A'}:\quad
\text{source thickening from one large }u\text{ point},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B'}:\quad
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}.
}
\]

So the active Gate 2 dependency is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Remaining proof obligations

The remaining Gate 2 obligations are now precise and local:

1. **Ordinary local complexity for \(u,u'\)**

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

This is near-Green under ordinary zero-separated completed-log-derivative transfer. 

2. **Real scalar normal form**

The \(L^2\)-rigidity proof uses the positivity of

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

after multiplying by \(q\chi_\delta(q)\), so \(q,u,g,h\) must be in a real scalar gauge.

3. **Residual-stable identities**

If

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

then require

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le Q^{-K}|J|^{1/2}
\]

so residuals are absorbed into \(\varepsilon\).

4. **Formal cutoff proof**

Finalize the \(a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)\) multiplier proof.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is locally proved modulo }u'\text{ control and }L^2\text{-input rigidity.}
}
\]

The proof no longer needs Remez, Cartan, pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\)-smallness, or target-smallness interval extraction.
## User (2026-04-27 13:08:51)

go one step further to see if anything extra

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:08:53)

I’ll push one layer deeper on the remaining “primitive bounds” issue. The question is whether the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma truly needs separate \(\|q\|_\infty,\|q'\|_\infty\) assumptions, or whether those can be weakened to \(L^p\)-type controls derived from the identities.

_Thought for 41s_

## Further attack — primitive bounds can likely be weakened to \(L^2/H^1\)-type bounds

The previous Gate 2 proof kept a clean assumption:

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

for the \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity lemma. That is safe, but stronger than necessary. A sharper audit suggests the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

lets us replace most pointwise primitive bounds by **polynomial \(L^2/H^1\)-type bounds**, many of which follow from \(u=q''\), \(g=u-F(q)\), and source complexity. This reduces the primitive-admissibility burden.

---

# 1. What the rigidity proof really needs

Recall:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

The \(L^2\)-input lemma assumes

\[
\|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

The multiplier proof uses:

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q),
\]

where

\[
a_\delta'(q)=O(1),\qquad a_\delta''(q)=O(\delta^{-1}).
\]

In the previous proof, I used

\[
\|q\|_\infty,\ \|q'\|_\infty,\ \|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

But term-by-term inspection shows we can get by with weaker controls:

\[
\|q\|_{L^2},\quad
\|q'\|_{L^2},\quad
\|q'\|_{L^4},\quad
\|q''\|_{L^2}
\]

all polynomially bounded.

---

# 2. Polynomial \(q\)-control from \(F(q)=u-g\)

Since

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

there is a global polynomial inequality

\[
\boxed{
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2).
}
\]

Indeed, for large \(|q|\), \(F(q)^2\asymp |q|^6\); for bounded \(|q|\), the constant absorbs the left side.

Because

\[
F(q)=u-g,
\]

we get

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}.
\]

If source local complexity gives

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

and Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

then

\[
\|F(q)\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/6}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

So \(q\)-control is derivable from \(u\)-control and \(g\)-smallness. We do not need a separate \(\|q\|_\infty\) bound for the main rigidity proof.

---

# 3. Polynomial \(q'\)-control from \(q\) and \(q''\)

In one dimension, interpolation gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
C\left(\|q\|_{L^2(J)}^{1/2}\|q''\|_{L^2(J)}^{1/2}
+ |J|^{-1}\|q\|_{L^2(J)}\right).
}
\]

Since

\[
q''=u,
\]

and \(\|u\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}\), we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Similarly, by Gagliardo–Nirenberg,

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}^2
\le
Q^C|J|^{1/2}
}
\]

in normalized form, or more generally polynomially after tracking the interval scale. This uses \(q'\in H^1\) and \(q''=u\in L^2\).

Thus the primitive \(q'\)-control needed in the transition terms follows from \(q\)-\(u\) interpolation, not from a separate \(\|q'\|_\infty\) assumption.

---

# 4. Kinetic estimate with \(L^2/H^1\) bounds

Use

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q).
\]

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi a_\delta(q).
\]

The main positive term controls

\[
\int \phi q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

Let

\[
Y=\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi q^2(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term is bounded by

\[
\left|\int \phi a_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi a_\delta(q)\|_2
\le
\varepsilon\|q\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi a_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi a_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''a_\delta
+
2\phi'a_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi a_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi a_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The terms are controlled in \(L^2\):

\[
\|\phi''a_\delta\|_2\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|\phi'a_\delta'(q)q'\|_2\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|\phi a_\delta'(q)q''\|_2\le Q^C,
\]

and the transition term satisfies

\[
\|\phi a_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2
\le
Q^C\delta^{-1}\|q'\|_{L^4}^2
\le
Q^C\delta^{-1}.
\]

So

\[
\left|\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
Y=\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi q^2(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}.
}
\]

Since \(q^2\ge4\delta^2\) on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
}
\]

This recovers the needed kinetic estimate without \(\|q'\|_\infty\).

---

# 5. Potential estimate without \(\|q\|_\infty\)

The potential estimate sets

\[
X=\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

The dangerous term after integrating by parts is

\[
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

Now

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2.
\]

So

\[
|F'(q)|(q')^2
\le
C(q')^2+Cq^2(q')^2.
\]

Both terms are controlled:

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3},
\]

and

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi q^2(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\]

for \(\delta<1\).

Thus no \(\|q\|_\infty\) bound is needed for the \(F'\)-term.

The transition term has

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta
\]

on \(|q|\sim\delta\), so it is controlled by the same kinetic estimate.

The cutoff term

\[
\int \phi'\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q'
\]

is bounded by Cauchy–Schwarz:

\[
\le
X^{1/2}
\left(
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\right)^{1/2},
\]

again no \(q_\infty\) needed.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2).
}
\]

---

# 6. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we still have

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta
\]

pointwise, so

\[
|u|^2=|F(q)+g|^2
\le
2C^2\delta^2+2|g|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{|q|\le3\delta}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

This uses no primitive pointwise bounds.

---

# 7. Final \(L^2\)-rigidity with weaker assumptions

Combining:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

The proof needs only polynomial control of:

\[
\|u\|_{L^2},\quad \|q\|_{L^2},\quad \|q'\|_{L^2},\quad \|q'\|_{L^4},\quad \|q''\|_{L^2}.
\]

These follow from:

\[
q''=u,\quad F(q)=u-g,
\]

source \(L^2\)-control of \(u\), and \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\), plus one-dimensional interpolation.

---

# 8. Remaining minimal assumptions

This suggests the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma can be stated with much lighter assumptions:

## Minimal \(L^2\)-rigidity assumptions

On normalized \(J\), assume:

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

and the identities

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then derive:

\[
\|q\|_{L^6},\ \|q\|_{L^2},\ \|q'\|_{L^2},\ \|q'\|_{L^4}
\le Q^C,
\]

and conclude

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This would remove the explicit primitive \(L^\infty\) assumptions.

---

# 9. Caveat: affine primitives

There is one caveat. The interpolation step

\[
\|q'\|_2\lesssim \|q\|_2^{1/2}\|q''\|_2^{1/2}+\|q\|_2
\]

requires \(q\in L^2\), which we derived from \(F(q)\in L^2\). This controls affine drift too, because large affine drift makes \(q\) large and hence \(F(q)\) large except possibly near roots of \(F\).

Could \(q\) be close to a nonzero root of \(F\), namely

\[
q\approx \pm\sqrt3,
\]

with large slope? If \(q\approx\sqrt3+bt\), then \(F(q)\) changes linearly:

\[
F'( \sqrt3)=-12\ne0,
\]

so large slope creates large \(F(q)\) in \(L^2\). Thus \(F(q)\in L^2\) still controls drift.

So affine primitive pathologies appear controlled by \(F(q)\).

---

# 10. Updated Gate 2 local package

Gate 2 may not need explicit primitive admissibility after all.

The minimal route is:

1. Source interval gives

   \[
   |u|\ge\tau
   \]

   and hence

   \[
   \|u\|_2\le Q^C
   \]

   if \(\|u\|_\infty\) is polynomial, or by local source complexity.

2. Gate 2 failure gives

   \[
   \|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le\varepsilon.
   \]

3. Since

   \[
   F(q)=u-g,
   \]

   get \(q\in L^6\).

4. Since \(q''=u\), get \(q'\in L^2,L^4\).

5. Apply \(L^2\)-rigidity.

Thus the proof can replace primitive \(L^\infty\) assumptions by \(L^2\)-derived primitive controls.

---

# 11. Recommended statement

For the paper/proof architecture, I would state two versions.

## Safe version

Assume

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

This is easier to audit.

## Stronger version

Note that the proof only requires polynomial \(L^2/H^1\) primitive controls, and these follow from

\[
q''=u,\quad F(q)=u-g,
\]

under source \(L^2\)-control and \(g\)-smallness.

This can be a strengthening after the safe proof is accepted.

---

# 12. Verdict

The primitive-bound burden is lighter than previously thought.

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }L^2\text{-integral rigidity proof can likely derive its own primitive controls from }u\text{ and }g.
}
\]

The main Gate 2 local assumptions reduce further to:

\[
\boxed{
u=q'',\quad F(q)=u-g,\quad h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^2}\text{ polynomial},\quad \|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le\varepsilon.
}
\]

For rigor, keep the safe primitive \(L^\infty\) version first, but the deeper proof may remove it.
## User (2026-04-27 13:11:26)

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:11:44)

## Continuing attack — prove primitive recovery cleanly in 1D

I’ll push the primitive-recovery improvement into a clean lemma. The objective is to reduce the Gate 2 local assumptions from pointwise primitive bounds

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

to \(L^2\)-level controls that follow from

\[
q''=u,\qquad F(q)=u-g,\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

This matters because the current best Gate 2 route already gives \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\) on a source-large interval, and \(u\) is controlled by source complexity. If primitive controls can be derived inside the rigidity proof, the Gate 2 package becomes substantially lighter. The latest coordinator update identifies this \(L^2\)-input rigidity route as the active Gate 2 mechanism. 

---

# 1. Primitive recovery from \(F(q)\)

The key algebraic fact is:

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

There is a constant \(C\) such that for all real \(q\),

\[
\boxed{
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2).
}
\]

Proof: for \(|q|\ge 2\),

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|
\ge |q|^3,
\]

up to an absolute constant. For \(|q|\le2\), \(|q|^6\le64\), absorbed by \(C\).

Since

\[
F(q)=u-g,
\]

we get

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}.
\]

If

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le M|J|^{1/2},
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

then

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}\le (M+\varepsilon)|J|^{1/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_J |q|^6
\le
C|J|+C\int_J|F(q)|^2
\le
C(1+M^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}
\le
Q^C |J|^{1/6}
}
\]

when \(M\le Q^C\). In particular,

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^2(J)}
\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

No independent \(q\)-bound is needed.

---

# 2. Recovering \(q'\) from \(q\) and \(q''\)

Since

\[
q''=u,
\]

and

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le M|J|^{1/2},
\]

one-dimensional interpolation gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
C\left(
\|q\|_{L^2(J)}^{1/2}\|q''\|_{L^2(J)}^{1/2}
+
|J|^{-1}\|q\|_{L^2(J)}
\right).
}
\]

In normalized \(J\) with \(|J|\asymp1\), this is

\[
\|q'\|_2\le Q^C.
\]

In scale-aware form,

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}
\le Q^C |J|^{1/2}|J|^{-1}
}
\]

if using physical coordinates. In the local normalized proof, this is polynomial and harmless.

For \(L^4\), use the 1D Gagliardo–Nirenberg inequality:

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}
\le
C\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}^{3/4}\|q''\|_{L^2(J)}^{1/4}
+
C|J|^{-1/4}\|q'\|_{L^2(J)}.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^4(J)}^2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}
}
\]

in the normalized scale.

This is exactly what the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof needs to control transition terms involving \((q')^2\).

---

# 3. Kinetic estimate using recovered primitives

We want to prove

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

Use the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q).
\]

Then

\[
a_\delta'(q)=O(1),
\qquad
a_\delta''(q)=O(\delta^{-1}).
\]

Multiplying

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi a_\delta(q)
\]

gives the positive term

\[
2\int \phi q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term is

\[
\left|\int \phi a_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi a_\delta(q)\|_2.
\]

Since

\[
|a_\delta(q)|\le |q|,
\]

and

\[
\|q\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

this is

\[
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

The \(g''\)-term becomes

\[
\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi a_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''a_\delta(q)
+
2\phi'a_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi a_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi a_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

Estimate in \(L^2\):

\[
\|\phi''a_\delta(q)\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

\[
\|\phi'a_\delta'(q)q'\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

\[
\|\phi a_\delta'(q)q''\|_2\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

and

\[
\|\phi a_\delta''(q)(q')^2\|_2
\le
Q^C\delta^{-1}\|q'\|_{L^4}^2
\le
Q^C\delta^{-1}|J|^{1/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\|(\phi a_\delta(q))''\|_2
\le Q^C\delta^{-1}|J|^{1/2}.
\]

So

\[
\left|\int g(\phi a_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi q^2(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

Since

\[
q^2\ge 4\delta^2
\]

on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

This reproduces the needed kinetic estimate with no \(\|q'\|_\infty\) assumption.

---

# 4. Potential estimate with recovered primitives

Set

\[
X=\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

\[
X
=
\int\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is controlled by

\[
\le \|g\|_2 X^{1/2}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}X^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb into \(\frac14X+C\varepsilon^2|J|\).

For the \(q''\)-term:

\[
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

The \(F'\)-term is

\[
\int \phi\widetilde\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

Since

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2,
\]

we bound

\[
|F'(q)|(q')^2
\le C(q')^2+Cq^2(q')^2.
\]

Both are controlled by the kinetic estimates:

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

and

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi q^2(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

The transition term has

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\qquad
|\widetilde\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1},
\]

so it is bounded by

\[
Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

The cutoff term is handled by Cauchy–Schwarz:

\[
\left|\int \phi'\widetilde\chi_\delta F(q)q'\right|
\le
X^{1/2}
\left(\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2\right)^{1/2}
\]

up to \(Q^C\), hence

\[
\le \frac14X+Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
X\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Finish as before

On \(|q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\]

and

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

So

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

On \(|q|\ge3\delta\),

\[
\int |u|^2
\le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

Hence

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J|.
}
\]

After normalizing \(J'\) as a fixed subinterval of \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Minimal \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma

We can now state a stronger lemma.

## Primitive-Recovering \(L^2\)-Integral Rigidity Lemma

Assume on \(J\):

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=u-(6q-2q^3),
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2},
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

No separate pointwise bounds on \(q,q'\) are required, at least in normalized one-dimensional form, provided the interpolation inequalities are applied carefully.

For proof safety, one may retain \(q,q',q''\) polynomial bounds in the first version, but they are not conceptually necessary.

---

# 7. Gate 2 package becomes even lighter

On the source-large interval \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\]

and local source upper bounds give

\[
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_2+\|h\|_2\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Thus the primitive-recovering rigidity lemma applies and gives the same contradiction.

So Gate 2 now needs:

1. real normal form;
2. source thickening from \(u'\);
3. source \(L^2\)-upper bound on \(u\);
4. \(L^2\)-rigidity.

Primitive \(q,q'\) bounds are either removed or demoted to proof-safety assumptions.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primitive admissibility is likely not essential for Gate 2.}
}
\]

The \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma can recover the needed primitive controls from:

\[
F(q)=u-g
\]

and

\[
q''=u
\]

using one-dimensional interpolation.

For a conservative first proof, keep polynomial \(q,q',q''\) bounds. For the sharpest architecture, state the primitive-recovering version above.

## Agent 3 / C — Close the full Gate 2 theorem

I am executing **Agent 3 / C**: combine the current \(L^2\)-input rigidity mechanism with source thickening into the final Gate 2 theorem. I will not use the older dyadic/Vitali or pointwise target-smallness route except as fallback commentary. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 theorem statement

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,\qquad u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Assume the real scalar normal form

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R
\]

on \(I\), and assume the identities for \(g,h\) hold exactly, or with \(L^2\)-small residuals absorbed into the rigidity lemma.

The theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input real rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure

Gate 1:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

Also assume the source Lipschitz bound

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Source thickening from one point

From Gate 1, there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Thus

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

By the \(u'\)-bound, for

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|\le \frac12|u(m_\ast)|.
\]

Hence there is a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}\quad\text{on }J
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
}
\]

This is the active replacement for dyadic/Vitali extraction.

---

# 4. \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on the source interval

On \(J\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2.
\]

Therefore, from Gate 2 failure,

\[
\tau^2\int_J (g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\). Since

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
\tau^2\asymp Q^{-B},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 5. \(L^2\)-input rigidity

Use the real \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|
}
\]

for \(J'\Subset J\).

The lemma uses the real identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

with multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q),
\]

and the optimized scale

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

If the identities hold with residuals \(r_g,r_h\), the same theorem holds provided

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

after adjusting the \(Q^{C_R}\) constant.

---

# 6. Contradiction

On \(J'\subset J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
}
\]

But \(L^2\)-rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Using

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)},
\]

we compute

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Thus the upper bound is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}|J'|.
\]

This contradicts the source lower bound if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}
<
-B-O(1).
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

Therefore Gate 2 failure is impossible for such \(A\).

---

# 7. Final Gate 2 conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for any sufficiently large polynomial exponent \(A\), specifically any

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty
+
L^2\text{-input real rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Required hypotheses made explicit

This theorem depends on four local inputs.

## 8.1 Source Lipschitz

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

This should come from ordinary zero-separated local complexity for

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

## 8.2 Real scalar normal form

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

This is necessary for the coercive kinetic term in the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof.

## 8.3 Rigidity identities

Exact:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Or residual-stable:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

with

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

## 8.4 Local primitive/source control inside rigidity

The safe form assumes

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

The sharper form can recover primitive controls from

\[
F(q)=u-g,\qquad q''=u
\]

using

\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2)
\]

and one-dimensional interpolation. That strengthening is useful but not required for the main closure.

---

# 9. Replacement of old D1/D2

The old inputs

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez Propagation},
\]

\[
D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}
\]

are replaced by this local theorem.

No Remez, no Cartan, no pointwise target-smallness interval, and no pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\) propagation is needed.

The dyadic/Vitali source extraction route is now only a fallback. The mainline proof uses one large source point from Gate 1.

---

# 10. Current status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is closed modulo local complexity and }L^2\text{-rigidity.}
}
\]

The remaining downstream burden now shifts to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 quotient row conversion and row-energy closure.}
}
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem

I am executing the **Agent 3 / C** instruction: combine the real-normal-form/complexity package and the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma into the final Gate 2 theorem, with exact exponent flow. 

---

# 1. Assumptions

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Assume:

1. **Real scalar normal form**

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
\]

2. **Gate 1**

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
}
\]

3. **Source Lipschitz**

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

4. **\(L^2\)-input rigidity**

For every \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This rigidity lemma uses the identities above, with either exact equality or \(L^2\)-small residuals.

---

# 2. Contrapositive setup

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

We will contradict Gate 1 for sufficiently large \(A\).

---

# 3. Source thickening

From Gate 1, there exists \(m_\ast\in I\) such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Hence

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12 Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Using the source Lipschitz bound, for

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\]

with \(c>0\) sufficiently small,

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\le \frac12|u(m_\ast)|.
\]

Therefore there exists a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 4. Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on \(J\)

On \(J\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2.
\]

Hence

\[
\tau^2\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by \(|J|\). Since

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
\tau^{-2}\asymp Q^B,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Absorb the harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor into \(C_R\). Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Apply \(L^2\)-input rigidity

By the rigidity lemma,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Now

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Contradiction

Since \(J'\subset J\) and \(|u|\ge \tau\) on \(J\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
\tau^2 |J'|
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

So Gate 2 failure implies

\[
Q^{-B-O(1)}
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

This is impossible if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)<-B.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

Thus, for such \(A\), Gate 2 failure contradicts Gate 1.

---

# 7. Final Gate 2 conclusion

Under the assumptions above,

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for every sufficiently large exponent \(A\), for instance any

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

So the downstream implication is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
|u'|_\infty\text{ source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input real rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. What this replaces

This theorem replaces the old active inputs

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez Propagation},
\]

\[
D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}.
\]

No Remez, no Cartan, no dyadic/Vitali extraction, no pointwise target-smallness interval, and no pointwise \(\Gamma_G''\)-propagation are needed.

The old routes remain fallback only.

---

# 9. Exact remaining hypotheses

The theorem is closed modulo these local items:

1. **Real scalar normal form**

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
\]

2. **Canonical identity compatibility**

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

If residuals occur,

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

then require

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

on the source interval.

3. **Source Lipschitz**

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

4. **Rigidity local bounds**

Use either the safe primitive version

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

or the primitive-recovering version based on

\[
F(q)=u-g,\qquad q''=u,\qquad |q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2).
\]

The safe version is the recommended mainline.

---

# 10. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is locally closed modulo real/canonical definition audit and }L^2\text{-rigidity.}
}
\]

The remaining downstream blocker is no longer Gate 2 propagation. It is D4 quotient row conversion, especially the order-9 cross-channel correction wall identified in the coordinator brief.

\[

\le

\le

The harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor is absorbed into the rigidity constant \(C_R\).

# 5. \(L^2\)-input real rigidity

Use the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|
}
\]

for \(J'\Subset J\).

This lemma depends on the real identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and is residual-stable: if

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

then it suffices that

\[
\|r_g\|_2+\|r_h\|_2
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

The proof uses the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

and the optimized choice

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

---

# 6. Contradiction

From \(L^2\)-rigidity,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Now

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
}
\]

But \(J'\subset J\), and on \(J\)

\[
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
}
\]

These two bounds are incompatible if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)
<
-B.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 7. Final Gate 2 theorem

## Theorem

Assume:

1. Real scalar normal form:

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
\]

2. Gate 1:

\[
\int_I|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

3. Source Lipschitz:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

4. Exact or residual-stable identities:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

5. \(L^2\)-input real rigidity:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for any

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 8. Classification

\[
\boxed{
D1/D2\text{ are replaced by this Gate 2 theorem.}
}
\]

The dyadic/Vitali extraction route is optional fallback only. The pointwise target-smallness route is historical/fallback only.

The exact remaining Gate 2 dependencies are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real/canonical definition audit}
}
\]

for \(q,u,g,h\),

\[
\boxed{
|u'|_\infty\text{ ordinary local complexity}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
L^2\text{-input real rigidity}.
}
\]

Under those, Gate 2 is closed.

## Real/canonical definition audit

I checked the uploaded definition/repair material for the Gate 2 variables. The audit **mostly closes**, with one remaining definitional item that must be explicit in the paper: the local \(q\) used in Gate 2 must be the derivative of a **real completed critical-line phase/scalar**, not a one-sided AFE/proxy branch.

## Audit verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical curvature convention: closed, if the proposed/updated definition is in the draft.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Anisotropy identities: closed algebraically.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Real scalar normal form: closed conditionally on }q=q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta'\text{ being the real completed-phase variable.}
}
\]

The remaining exact check is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the current draft explicitly define }\Phi_\zeta\text{ as a real critical-line completed phase/scalar?}
}
\]

If yes, the audit closes. If no, add that definition.

---

# 1. Canonical \(q''_{\can}\) convention

The repair material explicitly sets the intended convention:

\[
q''_{\can}(m):=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m),
\]

where

\[
q_\zeta(t)=\Phi_\zeta'(t).
\]

It also states that this is the **full actual-zeta phase-derivative curvature** in the same-point Gram normalization, not a whitened, projectivized, AFE-normalized, or affine-subtracted quantity. 

The same material explicitly distinguishes the complement-source curvature:

\[
q''_{\source,R}(m):=(G^{\new})''(m),
\]

and says it must not be identified with

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m).
\]

So the canonical-vs-complement ambiguity is resolved if these edits are present. 

---

# 2. Canonical decomposition policy

The canonical object is represented, not defined, by zero-side or AFE-side formulas. The relevant uploaded proposition says:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho),
\]

and equivalently, under a smoothed log-derivative AFE,

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\ge1} b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2-im}W(n/X)
+
D_2(m;X,W)
+
E_2(m;X,W).
\]

It explicitly says the canonical object is the full \(q_\zeta''(m)\), not the sign convention or a chosen oscillatory representation. 

This closes the policy question:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
}
\]

must be used as the full real canonical object. \(P_2\) alone, \(D_2\) alone, \(B_2\)-only, or complement-source \(q''_{\source,R}\) are not valid Gate 2 sources.

---

# 3. \(\Gamma_G\) definition

The updated anisotropy definition says that on a centered reduced patch,

\[
q_0=q_\zeta(m),
\qquad
q''=q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m),
\qquad
q^{(4)}=(q_\zeta)^{(4)}(m),
\]

and defines

\[
\Gamma_G^{\can}:=q''_{\can}-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

It then suppresses the superscript and writes \(\Gamma_G\) for the canonical version. 

So:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_0+2q_0^3
}
\]

is closed, provided this updated definition has replaced the older bare-\(q''\) version.

---

# 4. \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) definition

The same updated definition gives:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}^{\can}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16(q_\zeta)^{(4)}.
\]

Again, the superscript may be suppressed once the canonical convention is fixed. 

So:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16q^{(4)}
}
\]

is closed under the same convention.

---

# 5. Corrected identity for \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)

Given

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

differentiate twice:

\[
g''
=
q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

Then

\[
2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16q^{(4)}+q''-2q(q')^2-q^2q''
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
=
(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

Thus the identity

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
}
\]

is algebraically closed once the two canonical definitions are fixed. The uploaded notes also explicitly identify this as the corrected identity used for Gate 2. 

---

# 6. Real-valuedness audit

This is the only remaining definitional condition.

The Gate 2 rigidity proof needs:

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
\]

The current uploaded definition material establishes that \(q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta'\) is the actual-zeta phase derivative used in the same-point Gram blocks, and the same-point Gram formula is written in terms of real-looking scalar entries \(q(t_\pm),q'(t_\pm),q''(t_\pm)+2q(t_\pm)^3\). 

But to **fully close** the real-normal-form audit, the draft must explicitly say one of the following:

\[
\Phi_\zeta(t)\in\mathbb R\quad(t\in I),
\]

or

\[
q_\zeta(t)=\Phi_\zeta'(t)\in\mathbb R\quad(t\in I),
\]

or that \(q_\zeta\) is built from the Hardy/completed real critical-line scalar.

The standard route is:

\[
\Xi(t):=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)\in\mathbb R
\quad(t\in\mathbb R),
\]

or equivalently use the Hardy-normalized real \(Z(t)\). Then any real differential expression in the selected real scalar is real. But I did **not** find a file citation in the uploaded snippets that explicitly states this real-normal-form lemma as an existing paper definition.

So the audit result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Realness is mathematically standard/plausible, but must be explicitly locked in the draft.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Denominator / pole audit

The proposed canonical definition correctly forbids silent replacement of \(q''_{\can}\) by complement-source curvature and says \(q''_{\can}\) is the raw actual-zeta phase curvature, not a quotient/whitened observable. 

For Gate 2, the dangerous forbidden denominators are:

\[
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
\]

I found no evidence in the canonical \(q''_{\can}\) definition that any of these are used. The only denominator risk is chart-level: if \(q\) is chart-dependent, the chart denominator must be named and bounded below by \(Q^{-C}\). I did not find an explicit chart denominator definition in the uploaded snippets.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No forbidden Gate 2 denominator is visible in the canonical convention.}
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }q\text{ is chart-defined, add the chart denominator and }|\Delta|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Residual policy

If the draft uses the exact canonical definitions above, then there is no Gate 2 residual:

\[
r_G=0,\qquad r_{G,2}=0.
\]

If some section uses a represented/proxy object, then the residuals are:

\[
r_G
=
\Gamma_G-\left(q''-6q+2q^3\right),
\]

\[
r_{G,2}
=
\Gamma_{G,2}
-
\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right).
\]

For the current \(L^2\)-rigidity proof, the required bound is:

\[
\boxed{
\|r_G\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_{G,2}\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

But under the canonical definitions, the residuals should be zero.

---

|---|---:|---|

## Real/canonical definition audit — result

I checked the uploaded draft material and handoff snippets for the specific Gate 2 definitions:

\[
q,\qquad u=q''_{\can},\qquad \Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The audit **does not fully close from the current draft material alone**. It closes conditionally if the proposed canonical convention is actually inserted into the draft, but the current accessible draft/handoff material still leaves one finite definitional gap.

---

# 1. What is confirmed

## 1.1 The intended canonical curvature convention is explicit in the repair notes

The strongest available definition says that the canonical source curvature should be

\[
q''_{\can}(m):=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m),
\]

where

\[
q_\zeta(t)=\Phi_\zeta'(t)
\]

is the full actual-zeta phase derivative used in the finite-\(s\) Gram blocks. It explicitly says this is **not** whitened, projectivized, divided by a Gram scale, or defined by an AFE approximation. 

This is exactly the right convention for Gate 2, provided it is now in the draft.

## 1.2 The same-point Gram block uses \(q_\zeta,q_\zeta',q_\zeta''\)

The proposed insertion for the finite-\(s\) Gram block writes the local Gram entries using

\[
q_\zeta(t_\pm),\quad q_\zeta'(t_\pm),\quad q_\zeta''(t_\pm)+2q_\zeta(t_\pm)^3.
\]

That supports the reading that \(q\) and \(q''_{\can}\) are meant to be in the same actual-zeta phase gauge, not unrelated objects. 

## 1.3 The full canonical source is not a one-sided AFE branch

The repair notes say that zero expansions and approximate functional equations are **representations** of \(q''_{\can}\), not definitions. They also state that the source/core decomposition partitions \(q''_{\can}\), while complement-only curvature should be separately named \(q''_{\source,R}\). 

This is important because the real Gate 2 proof must use the full real canonical object, not \(P_2\) or \(D_2\) alone.

---

# 2. What is not fully confirmed in the accessible draft material

## 2.1 I did not find a definitive statement that \(\Phi_\zeta\) is a real completed critical-line phase/scalar

The available files prove/recall that a real completed scalar is available:

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi\left(\frac12+it\right)\in\mathbb R
\]

on the critical line, and likewise Hardy’s \(Z(t)\) is real. They also state that if \(q\) is constructed from such a real scalar by a real differential expression, then \(q,u,g,h\) are real. 

But I did **not** find, in the accessible snippets, the actual draft definition:

\[
\Phi_\zeta(t)=\text{some real completed critical-line scalar/phase}
\]

or

\[
q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta'\in\mathbb R.
\]

So the real-normal-form step remains conditional.

The exact missing sentence is something like:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_\zeta \text{ is the real completed critical-line phase/scalar, so } q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta'\in\mathbb R \text{ on ordinary zero-free intervals.}
}
\]

Without that, the current \(L^2\)-rigidity proof has not been licensed.

---

# 3. Anisotropy identities

The identity package needed by Gate 2 is:

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

The accessible materials support the first two as intended definitions/repair targets. turn73file4

For the second anisotropy, the draft/handoff materials repeatedly use the normalized identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

and derive interval base-locus rigidity from it. 

Algebraically, if

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma_G''=q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q'',
\]

so

\[
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
=
(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Thus the two common forms of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are equivalent, provided the first identity is canonical and all derivatives use the same normalized coordinate.

So the anisotropy algebra closes if the canonical convention is inserted.

---

# 4. Denominator/pole audit

The accessible canonical convention for \(q''_{\can}\) defines it as the raw actual-zeta phase-derivative curvature, not a quotient or projected observable. 

That means I found no evidence that \(q''_{\can}\) contains forbidden denominators like

\[
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
\]

However, if \(q\) itself is chart-defined, the chart denominator is still not specified in the accessible snippets. Then the proof needs a chart condition:

\[
|\Delta_{\text{chart}}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the denominator audit is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}\text{ looks denominator-safe; chart denominators for }q\text{ still need explicit naming if }q\text{ is chart-defined.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Critical-line zero caveat

There is one important caveat: if \(q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta'\) is raw phase/log-derivative data, then a critical-line zero inside \(I^\ast\) is not automatically smooth. The notes explicitly warn that \(q_\zeta\) is not an ordinary \(C^6\) function across a critical-line zero unless phase jumps are regularized or the interval avoids the zero. 

Therefore the real/canonical audit only closes in the smooth ordinary branch under either:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I^\ast,\gamma)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

for critical-line zero ordinates \(\gamma\), or an explicit regularized phase convention with polynomial derivative bounds.

This is not a defect in the real gauge; it is a smoothness/regularization requirement.

---

# 6. Final audit table

| Check | Status |
|---|---:|
| \(q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''\) intended convention | **Supported** by repair text |
| \(q''_{\can}\) is not AFE/proxy/complement curvature | **Supported** |
| \(q\) and \(q''_{\can}\) are same actual-zeta phase gauge | **Supported by proposed Gram convention**, but needs final insertion |

| One-sided AFE excluded for Gate 2 real proof | **Confirmed as necessary** |
| Forbidden denominators in \(q''_{\can}\) | **None visible** |
| Chart denominators for \(q\) | **Need explicit definition if charted** |
| Critical-line zero smoothness | **Requires avoidance or regularization** |

}

The exact missing definition is:

and the Gate 2 variables become real:

## Real/canonical definition audit — deeper check

I checked the actual TeX draft plus the later repair notes. The result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The real scalar part is present in the draft at the abstract phase-kernel level.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual-zeta canonical identification is not fully closed in the original draft unless the proposed repair definition is applied.}
}
\]

So the audit is **partially closed**: the draft already assumes \(q=\Phi'\) for a **real phase** \(\Phi\), but the draft still needs the canonical sentence identifying the actual-zeta phase as \(\Phi_\zeta\) and fixing

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

---

## 1. Real scalar \(q\): closed in the local phase-kernel section

The actual TeX draft defines the local kernel by first taking

\[
\Phi
\]

to be a **real phase** on the local spectral variable \(t\), and then sets

\[
q(t):=\Phi'(t).
\]

That is enough to conclude, at the local phase-kernel level,

\[
q(t)\in\mathbb R,\qquad q'(t),q''(t),\ldots\in\mathbb R
\]

on the real interval. 

So the real-normal-form requirement for the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma is not alien to the draft. It is already built into the local phase-kernel formalism.

---

## 2. Actual-zeta canonical linkage: not fully closed in the original draft

The missing link is not “is \(q\) real?” in the abstract. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the actual-zeta }q_\zeta\text{ used in Gate 2 exactly this real-phase }q?
}
\]

The repair notes propose exactly the needed convention:

\[
\Phi=\Phi_\zeta,\qquad q_\zeta(t):=\Phi_\zeta'(t),
\]

and then define

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(m):=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
}
\]

They also explicitly state that \(q''_{\can}\) is the full actual-zeta phase-derivative curvature, not a whitened, projected, AFE-normalized, or affine-subtracted object. 

So: if that repair is applied, the canonical identification closes. If not, the original draft only has a real abstract phase \(q=\Phi'\), not a fully pinned actual-zeta \(q_\zeta\).

---

## 3. Canonical versus complement-source curvature: repaired, but must be applied

The repair notes correctly separate the full canonical curvature

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)
\]

from the affine-subtracted complement-source curvature

\[
q''_{\source,R}(m):=(G^{\new})''(m).
\]

This distinction is necessary. The Gate 2 proof must use \(q''_{\can}\), not \(q''_{\source,R}\). The repair note explicitly says \(q''_{\source,R}\) is the curvature of the affine-subtracted non-core zero complement and is not the full canonical actual-zeta curvature. 

This part is conceptually closed, conditional on inserting the convention.

---

## 4. \(\Gamma_G\): closed once canonical convention is applied

The repair notes replace the Gram anisotropy definition so that on a centered reduced patch,

\[
q_0=q_\zeta(m),\qquad
q''=q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m),\qquad
q^{(4)}=(q_\zeta)^{(4)}(m).
\]

Then they define

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G^{\can}=q''_{\can}-6q_0+2q_0^3.
}
\]

They also allow suppressing the superscript and writing \(\Gamma_G\) once the canonical convention is fixed. 

So:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
}
\]

is closed under the canonical convention.

---

## 5. \(\Gamma_{G,2}\): closed, with derivation

The proposed repaired definition is

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}^{\can}
=(1-q_0^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16(q_\zeta)^{(4)}.
}
\]

Again, after fixing the convention, write \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). 

Now derive the ODE identity used in Gate 2. Let

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g'
=
q'''-6q'+6q^2q',
\]

and

\[
g''
=
q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

Therefore

\[
2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
=
2q(q')^2
-\frac16q^{(4)}
+q''
-2q(q')^2
-q^2q'',
\]

so

\[
2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
=
(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
}
\]

is algebraically closed once the repaired \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) definition is in place.

Important correction: the derivative identity uses

\[
6q^2u
\]

inside \(\Gamma_G''\), not \(12q^2u\). The repair notes explicitly flag that coefficient correction. 

---

## 6. Canonical representation policy: closed as a repair, not fully in the old draft

The repair notes define the canonical source-curvature representation problem as

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m),
\]

then give both a zero-side representation

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho)
\]

and a prime/AFE-side representation

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with fixed actual-zeta coefficients and all terms in the same normalization. 

This is the correct policy. It prevents replacing \(q''_{\can}\) by \(P_2\) alone, \(D_2\) alone, \(B_2\)-only, or an arbitrary Dirichlet polynomial.

But this again appears in the repair list, not as a confirmed original-draft definition. So the audit says: apply the repair and it closes.

---

## 7. Remaining caveat: critical-line zeros and smoothness

One uploaded note correctly warns that under the repaired convention

\[
q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta',\qquad q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

a critical-line zero inside the smooth interval is not automatically harmless. Raw log-derivative or phase data can have a pole/jump at a critical-line zero unless regularized or avoided. 

So the real/canonical definition audit closes for the **ordinary smooth branch** only under one of these:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I^\ast,\gamma)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

for all unregularized critical-line zero ordinates \(\gamma\), or a stated regularized-jump convention with polynomial derivative bounds.

This is a smoothness condition, not a realness failure.

---

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:36:57)

## Gate 2 theorem

### Theorem

Assume the normalized local derivative convention is fixed on \(I\), and write all derivatives below in that normalized coordinate. Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume the Gate 2 real/canonical normal form is fixed, so \(q,u,g,h\) are real-valued on \(I\), and the above identities hold exactly, or with \(L^2\)-small residuals absorbed into the rigidity constant.

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume source Lipschitz control:

\[
\|u'\|_{\infty,I}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma: for every \(J'\Subset J\subset I\),

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

implies

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2\,dm
\le Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then, for any

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1),
}
\]

Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

## Proof

Assume, for contradiction, that Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

By Gate 1, there exists \(m_\ast\in I\) such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B},
\]

so

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Using

\[
\|u'\|_{\infty,I}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

we can choose a one-sided or two-sided interval \(J\subset I\), centered at \(m_\ast\) when possible, with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|
\]

such that

\[
|u(m)|\ge \tau
\]

for all \(m\in J\). Indeed, for \(|m-m_\ast|\le c\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}\cdot c\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\le c\tau,
\]

and \(c\) is chosen small enough.

On \(J\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2.
\]

Therefore Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\tau^2\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Hence

\[
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Since

\[
\tau^{-2}\asymp Q^B
\]

and

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Set

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2=Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb the harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) factor into \(C_R\), and apply \(L^2\)-input rigidity on \(J'\Subset J\):

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Using the definition of \(\varepsilon\),

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
\]

But \(J'\subset J\), and on \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

The two estimates are incompatible if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)<-B.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

This contradicts Gate 2 failure, proving Gate 2.

---

\[
\boxed{
D1/D2\text{ are replaced by this theorem.}
}
\]

## Agent 3 / C — Final Gate 2 theorem

Executing Agent 3’s instruction: close the Gate 2 theorem from Gate 1, source thickening, and \(L^2\)-input real rigidity. 

---

# Theorem: Gate 1 + source thickening + \(L^2\)-rigidity implies Gate 2

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume the real scalar normal form:

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
\]

and the identities above hold exactly, or with \(L^2\)-small residuals absorbed into the rigidity constant.

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume source Lipschitz control:

\[
\|u'\|_{\infty,I}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume \(L^2\)-input real rigidity: for every \(J'\Subset J\subset I\),

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

implies

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for any

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

---

# Proof

Assume for contradiction that Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

By Gate 1, there exists \(m_\ast\in I\) such that

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Hence

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Set

\[
\tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Using

\[
\|u'\|_{\infty,I}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

there is a one-sided or two-sided interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J
\]

and

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
\]

Indeed, for

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}\cdot c\,\tau Q^{-C_u}|I|
\le c\tau,
\]

and \(c>0\) is chosen sufficiently small.

On \(J\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2.
\]

Therefore Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\tau^2\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_J |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\tau^{-2}Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Since

\[
\tau^{-2}\asymp Q^B
\]

and

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Set

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon^2=Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
Q^{O(1)}\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Absorb the harmless \(Q^{O(1)}\) into \(C_R\). By \(L^2\)-input rigidity,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Now

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-\frac A2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)},
\]

so

\[
\varepsilon^{2/5}
=
Q^{-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)}
|J'|.
\]

But \(J'\subset J\), and on \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge \tau=\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

These two estimates are incompatible if

\[
C_R-\frac A5+\frac{3B}{10}+\frac{C_u}{5}+O(1)<-B.
\]

Equivalently, it suffices that

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

This contradiction proves Gate 2.

---

\[
\boxed{
D1/D2\text{ are replaced by this theorem.}
}
\]

# Summary of what is now good

The updated draft already correctly contains:

\[
q''_{\can}:=\mathcal D^2 q_\zeta=\mathcal D^3\Phi_\zeta,
\]

the canonical definitions

\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta,
\]

and the derived identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]

The new \(L^2\)-Gate 2 theorem is also in good shape. The most important remaining edits are to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{remove/demote the stale Gate 2 hypothesis text,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{make the real completed gauge explicit,}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{make D3/D4 gauge-locking and carrier-quotient assumptions explicit.}
}
\]
